O vos, tres chiers filz, je vos ai acomplit cest livre qui est li derriens de la science de medicine ensamble l’emplissement de lui, et ai fait la fin per ses expositions et par ses declarations.	O you, dear children of mine, I have completed this book which is the final word on the science of medicine as a whole, and I have finished it with its explanations and declarations.
Et m’est venu en vision que je le vos acomplisse avec cest traitier, qui est partie de l’uevre de mains, c’est a savoir «cyrurgie».	And it came to me in a vision that I should complete this treatise with this book, which is part of the work of hands, that is to say "surgery".
Et por ceu que l’uevre de mains est fortraite en nostre region et est etraingie dou tout en tout, si est perie li science et decopee, et n’est riens demorez de li fuers que les petites descriptions en livres des anciens que les mains ont muees.	And because the work of hands is dealt with in our region and is strange to all and every part, it is very rare in science and practice, and is not delayed by the little descriptions in books of the ancient ones that the hands have moved.
Et de ceu est venue li error et li vanitez, et sont closes les ententions et est aloignie li science.	And from this has come error and vanity, and intentions are closed and science is distant.
Or me semble que je la vuel vivifier ensamble l’ordination de cest traitier selonc la voie d’exposition et de declaration et de l’abreviation; et venrai ensamble les formes des ferremens de cautere, et des autres estrumens de l’uevre avec l’ajostement de la declaration et de preparation de li, sicom il est mestier.	Or it seems to me that I should renew this treatise with the order of this book according to the way of explanation and declaration and abbreviation; and I will come together with the forms of the tools of cauterization, and other instruments of the work with the preparation and arrangement of them, as is fitting.
Et por la raison de ceu que nuls boins maistres de mains n’est trovez en nostre tens, est li ars de medicine eslongié.	And for the reason that no good master of hands is found in our times, the art of medicine is diminished.
Et covient celui qui s’en entremet sormonter en la science d’anathomie, si com Galiens dit, tant qu’il saiche la juement des menbres, et les formes et les conjunctions et les separations d’aus, et aient connissance des osses et des nerf et des brais et le nombre d’ous, et le demenement et des voines movans et des reposans, et dou leu de lor issue.	And he who meddles in this should overcome in the science of anatomy, as Galen says, as far as he knows the judgment of members, and their shapes and connections and separations of bones, and has knowledge of bones and nerves and veins and the number of joints, and the movement and moving veins and the resting and non-resting places, and the place of their issue.
Et por ceu dist Ypocras que li nons avec le non est mout, et avec l’uevre est poc; et meismement en l’art de main.	And for this reason, Iopras says that no thing with a thing is bad, and with work it is little; and most of all in the art of the hand.
Nos vos disons en l’introite de cest livre que qui n’est conissans des choses devant dites, si se gart qu’il ne chiece en error et qu’il n’ocie les homes; ensi que j’ai veut maintes fois plusors de ces qui s’entremettent de ceste science et si s’abandonent sen science et sens experiment.	We say to you in the introduction of this book that whoever is not acquainted with the things above mentioned, should guard himself so as not to fall into error and not to hurt men; otherwise I have often wanted many of those who meddle in this science and have abandoned themselves to theory and not to experience.
Car je vis un fol mire qui copa I apostume de scrophules ou col d’une femme, et copa les arteres dou col; por coi tant de sanc issit hors que li femme cheit morte entre ses mains.	I saw a foolish man who cut open an abscess on the neck of a woman, and cut into the arteries of her neck; so much blood flowed out that the woman died in his hands.
Et vis I autre mire qui traït une piere d’un home d’eaige, et li piere estoit grans; si emporta avec li une piece de la vessie, et fut mors li hons dedens III jors.	And I saw another fool who treated a stone in the bladder of a man, and the stone was large; he brought out a piece of the bladder with it, and the man died in three days.
Et je i avoie ja esteit apelez por lou traire, et vis la disposition dou malaide et la grandor de la piere, et soi bien s’on lou tailloit il en morroit.	And I have seen some who were called in to treat the patient and saw the condition of the disease and the size of the stone; and if they treated him, he would surely die.
Et vis I autre mire qui prist en cure I duc de nostre terre qui avoit la jambe brisie, et avec la briseure ot plaie; et li mires plains d’ignorance estraint la brisure sus la plaie as esteles par fort lieure, et ne lassa a la plaie point de xalain, et le lassa ensi I termine; et li comanda qu’il ne la desliast mie; et demora ensi que li jambe fut toute enflee et li piez et vint a perdition.	And I saw another fool who took care of the Duke of our land who had his leg broken, and with the break there was a wound; and the ignorant doctor pulled the break onto the wound with great pain, leaving no scar on the wound, and left it like that; and he ordered that it should not be loosened; and he delayed so that the leg completely gangrened, and the foot came to destruction.
Je fuis apelez por venir a lui, et me hastai por venir deslier la jambe; et quant je l’oi desloie si fut em pais et ne sentit point de dolor.	I was called to go to him, and I hurried to dislocate the leg; and when I did so he was at peace and felt no pain.
Mais toute voie li corruptions estoit ja confermee ou membre, et ne la poi saner; et ne cessa li corrution d’aler par le membre tant que li membres fut dou tout perdus.	But all the ways that the limb is corrupted are already confirmed or the member, and it cannot be healed; and the corruption does not cease to spread through the member as long as the members are all lost.
Et vis I autre mire qui effondra I apostume enchancreit, et puis enflama per le malice de sa signorie.	And I saw another wonder that will destroy the abscess and putrefaction, and then inflame because of the evil of its lordship.
Car chancre, quant il est purs d’umor melancolique, ne covient mie qu’on i(l) touche de fer s’il n’est en teil leu c’on puisse toute oster ce que est corrumpus.	For leprosy, when it is infected with melancholy humor, does not come to an end except that one touches it with iron if it is in a suitable place so that one can completely remove what is corrupted.
Et por ceu, treschier filz, vos est besoig que vos sachiez que oevre de mains est devisee en II divisions: c’est asavoir, huevre ou il a peril en plusors dispositions; et je mostrerai en chescun leu de cest livre ou il a paour et peril.	And because of this, you, gentle son, must know that the work of hands is divided into two divisions: namely, where there is danger in many dispositions; and I will show in each part of this book where there is fear and danger.
Por coi il est besoig que vos vos en gardez, si que li fol mire ne puissent mal parler de vos Si prenez vos armes en cusenson, et entreprenez vos malaides legierement et fermement, et usez de la millor voie si que per la graice de Deu vos venez a salut et soiez loez; et lassiez les maladies espoantables de grief saniteit; et ostez vos armes de ceu que vos fait douter, et aiez foit en vos si que vos puissiez venir de cestui monde a l’autre de gloire.	For so that you keep yourself safe from harm, may the wise man not speak ill of you if you take your weapons with care, and undertake your illnesses lightly and firmly, and use the better path so that, through the grace of God, you come to salvation and are loosed; and leave behind the probable diseases of grief health; and put aside your weapons from him who makes you doubt, and have faith in yourself so that you can come from this world to the other of glory.
Galiens dist en aucuns de ses amonestemens: «Ne prenez mie en cure male maladie, que vos ne soiez apelez fol mire.	Galen provides some of his admonitions: "Do not take on a illness with impatience, lest you be called a foolish person.
» J’ai deviseit cest traitier selonc III chapitres.	I have devised this treatise according to III chapters.
Li premiers chapitres est des cauteres de feu et dé cauteres de medicine ague, et est li chapitres ordenez de lou chief jusques as piez; et des formes des estrumens, et des ferremens de cautere, et de tout ceu qui est necessaire en l’ueuvre.	The first chapters are about fire and medical cauterizations, and the order of the limbs up to the feet; and the forms of tools, and the ironing tools for cauterization, and all that is necessary in this work.
Li secons chapitres si est de taillier et de percier, et des ventouses et des plaies, et des estractions des saiettes, et des semblans choses; et est li chapitres ordenez et les formes des estrumens.	The second chapter deals with cutting, piercing, suction cups, wounds, the extraction of arrows, and similar matters; and it orders the forms of instruments.
Li tiers chapitres est de restorer les dislocations et des torcions, et des semblans choses; et est ordeneiz des lou chief jusc’as piez, et des formes des estrumens.	The third chapter deals with restoring dislocations and torsions, and similar matters; and it orders the forms of instruments as soon as possible, and the shapes of tools.
Ainsois que nos nos remembriens de l’uevre, il covient que je die la qualiteit de l’aide et dou nuisement de chescune complexion.	Thus, let us remember the work; it is necessary that I give you the quality of aid and the harm of each complexion.
Je dis que li qualiteis de l’aide, et dou nuisement, est li plus longe parole et subtilz science et li secrez reponus; et de ceu parlerent li plusors des saiges, et s’acorderent a ceu; et me soffisent poc lor paroles, car je redous la longesce.	I say that the quality of aid and harm is the longest word and subtile science and the most secret answers; and many wise men would speak on it, and agree with it; and I lack words for a long time, because I am short of speech.
Je dis que cautere aide universement a toute complexion ou il a matiere, fuer que II complexions: c’est a savoir complexion chaude sens matere, et complexion seche sens matere.	I say that fire aid is universal for all complexions, except for two: namely, warm-blooded complexions with moisture and dry complexions without moisture.
En complexion chaude et seche ensamble matiere, deviserent aucun et dirent que cautere i est grans aide; et li autre dirent le contraire: que cautere ne vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de sechour.	In hot and dry complexions together matter, they all agree and say that cauterization is great help; and the other say the opposite: that cauterization does not help for sickness which comes from heat and dryness.
Car li nature dou feu si est chaude, et ne doit mie estre cureiz de chaude maladie par chalor, ne per sechour; et dist cil qui dist lou contraire que cautere fait grant aide a maladie chaude et seche que vient en cors des homes.	For the nature of fire is hot, and it should not be cured with hot medicine from heat, nor with dryness; and he who says the opposite that cauterization is great help for hot and dry disease which comes in the body of men.
Car quant tu comperes le cors de l’ome et sa moistor a la complexion dou feu, tu trueves le cors froit.	For when you compare the body of man with the fire's moisture to the skin, you find the body cold.
Et je m’acorde a ceste parole.	And I agree with this word.
Car je l’ai troveit aucune fois per experiment.	For I have never found it by experience.
Et toute voie, ne s’en entremette mie fuers que cil qui l’a esproveit, et qui conoit par lonc usaige le chapistre des cauteres, et la diversiteit des complexions des homes, et les dispositions et les causes de lor maladies, et les sorvenues et l’espaice dou tens; des autres complexions n’avons nos mie paour, meismement em maladies froides et moistes.	And all way, does not interfere but that which has experienced it, and who knows through long use the chaplet of cauterization, and the diversity of complexions of men, and their dispositions and causes of diseases, and the remedies and space of time; of others complexions we have no fear, even for cold and moist diseases.
Et tuit li mire s’asemblerent et s’acorderent au cautere.	And all the hair should come together and agree with the fire cautery.
Et sachiez, filz, que cautere ensamble feu si est des secrez des cures, et de plus grant bonteit que cautere de medicine ardant.	And know, children, that fire cautery together if there are secrets of healing, and much greater goodness than medical fire cautery.
Car li feus est simples, et ne vient mie fuers que au membre qui est cuis, et ne nuit a autre membre se poc nom.	For fire is simple, and comes only to the member that is cooked, and does not hurt any other member at all.
Les medicines ardans vienent de membre a autre en aloignant, et font venir au membre maladies de grief sanation; et par aventure ocit lou malaide Li feus por sa hautece et por la bonteit de sa substance ne fait mie ceu, s’il n’i a superfluiteit.	The burning medicines come from one member to another by removing, and bring to the member sickness of pain; and perhaps fire for its height and for the goodness of its substance does not do this, unless there is an excess.
Et ceu vos ai je troveit par experiment et par la longesce dou servise et de l’estude que j’ai mis en l’art, et esteit sus la verteit des choses; et por ceu je m’escuse de la longesce de la parole, car il ne me plait mie que je vos oste le secreit qui est reponus ou feu, et la qualiteit de l’uevre, coment il deboute les maladies des cors, si com li philosophe le dit en demostrant; or le recevez en vos pensees.	And I have found this by experience and by the length of service and study that I have put into this art, and it is based on the truth of things; and therefore I ask your pardon for the length of the speech, for it does not please me to take away from you the secret that is given to fire, and the quality of the work, how it drives away diseases of the body, as the philosopher says in his demonstration; so accept it in your thoughts.
Et sachiez, fil, que il s’acorderent en quel tens doient estre faites les cauteres, et eslirent prientens.	And know, son, that they should be made in what time they should be performed, and they should be prayed.
Et je dis que cautere est covenable en tous tens, por ceu que li nuisemens sorvenans est desoz mis par l’aide dou cautere; et meismement se li cauteres est por dolors necessaires fors et hastans que ne puent atendre le tens que plus grans malice ne veigne au membre.	And I say that cauterization is appropriate in all times, because the harm that arises is overcome by the aid of cauterization; and most especially, the cauterization is for necessary pains that cannot be delayed until the time when greater harm comes to the member.
Et n’i pensez onques, chier fil, si com font li fol mire; car a la maladie qui est sanee par cautere n’a point de revenue; et il le dient ensi; mais il n’est mie si com il cuident, por ce que cauteres nen est que medicine qui mue la complexion, et seche les humors que sont cause de la dolor, et vaut mues que medicine por le hastement de sa valor, et por la vertut de son oevre et de sa signorie.	And do not think once, my son, as they do; because for the illness that is healed by cauterization there is no return; and it serves so; but it is not like what they think, for cauterization is nothing more than medicine that changes the surface, dries up the humors that cause pain, and is worth more than medicine due to its haste in healing, and because of its virtue and dignity.
Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut; et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie; mais ce avient poc.	Et possans chose est que li maladie viegne aucune fois selonc la complexion dou malaide et lou leu de la maladie et sa vertut; et sont assemblees en lui les superfluitez par l’aquisition des viandes et des semblans choses, se ce n’est cauteres administrez em leu ou il ait poc de superfluitez et de moistor, si com cauteres de dens por la dolor, et les semblans choses, et teil dolor ne revient mie; mais ce avient poc.
Et mout de gens n’entendent mie por coi cauteres est apelez li derriens de medecine, et c’est voir; mais il ne croient mie que cauteres vaille aprés medicine, mais lor ententions est fause, et est cauteres li derriens de medicine por ceu que quant nos aministrons manieres de cures en aucune maladie et elles ne valent, adonc administrons nos le cautere, et il vaut.	And it is possible that the disease will come in accordance with the complexion of the patient and the place and nature of the disease; and excesses are gathered within him by the acquisition of meat and similar things, unless cauterization is administered at the place where there is little excess and moisture, as with deep cauterization for pain, and similar things, and partial pain does not return again; but this happens little.
Adonques apert bien que cauteres est li derriens de medicine, ne mie selonc l’entention des folz mires.	And so open well that the fire cautery is a medicine derived from the entrails, not according to the intention of foolish lookers.
Li ancien dirent que cauteres d’estrument d’or est muedres que de fer, et ne dirent ceu fuers que por la qualiteit de l’or et por la hautece de sa substance; et dirent que li leus de cautere ne fait mie porriture, mais ceu n’est mie voir car je l’ai esprovei, et ai troveit que c’est voir en aucuns homes; et cauteres d’or vaut mues que de fer, si com il lou dirent.	The ancient ones said that fire cautery instruments are made of gold rather than iron, and they said that the metal of the cauterizer does not cause swelling but this is not to be believed because I have tested it, and I have found that in some people it does; and a gold cautery is worth more than an iron one, as they used to say.
Et toutevoie quant tu chaufes estrument d’or, tu ne seis mie quant il est chaus par la color de l’or, et s’est tantost refroidiez; et s’on le chaufe trop; si font au feu; et ensi i a assez d’empechement.	And anyway when you heat the gold instrument, you don't know when it is hot enough because it quickly cools down; and if it is heated too much, it goes out into fire, and so there is sufficient impediment.
Et por ce usons nos de cautere de feir que nos l’avons mues apparilliet a nostre oevre.	And for this reason we use the fire cautery that we have made ready for our work.
Or vos ai ordeneit cest chapitre des lou chief jusc’a piez, por ceu que li voie soit plus legiere a trover.	Or vos ai ordeneit cet chapitre des lou chief jus'à piez, pour ceu que li voie soit plus legiere à trover.
dou cautere olivaire	The olive oil cautery:
Cist cauteres vaut a moistor et a froidor sus lou cerveil, et en i a dous c’on fait par la cause d’une maladie qui est apelee «soda», et par la cause de maintes humors qui dessendent dou chief as eulz, et as oreilles, et por multitude de songes et dolor de dens et dolor de gorge, et meismement a toutes maladies qui vienent de froidor si com paralisie et sode et apoplexie et semblans maladies.	The olive oil cautery is useful for a moist and cold forehead, and also for a multitude of problems in the hair, and in the ears, and for many kinds of headaches and pain in the jaw and throat, and especially for all manner of diseases that come from coldness, such as paralysis, swelling, apoplexia, and similar illnesses.
Li forme de cest cautere si est que li malaides soit espurgiez par medicine solutive mondifiant le chief III nuis ou IIII, selonc ceu que li vertus et li eaige et li acostumance dou malaide le puet soffrir; et puis fai rere lou chief dou malaide.	The form of this cautery is such that the patient is to be purged with a solute medicine that washes the forehead III or IV times, depending on the virtue and lightness and the patient's accustomedness to it so that he can bear it; and then wash the forehead of the patient again.
Et puis le fai seoir croisiet entre tes mains, et mettre ses mains sor som peis; aprés met la racine de ta palme sus la racine de son neis entre ses II eulz; et lai ou venra tes dois moiens, si saigne d’enche puis eschaufe le cautere qui est apelé «olivare», de coi ci est li forme:	And then place the cross between your hands, and put his hands over your palm; after that place the root of your thumb on the root of his index finger; and if it comes to your two sides, let there be a little blood first, and then heat the cautery which is called "oliver", for this is its form:
Et le met sor le leu signiet d’encre, et fai en dessendant et en estraignant ta main poc et poc en trestornant; puis lieve ta main isnelement, et rewarde le leu se tu vois l’os I sol petit; et se tu ne lou vois, si rencomence le cautere tant que tu voies l’os si com je lou t’ai dit; aprés pren I poc de seil, et met en awe et molle coton dedens, et met sor le leu, et li laisse III jors; aprés met sus cotun moilliet en burre; et laisse sus tant que li eschaudure soit ostee; aprés cure la plaie de l’oignement qui est apelez «tetrafarmaçon», tant qu’il soit sanez.	And put it on the signet of ink, and make it descend and extract your hand little by little in torquing; then release your hand, and touch the root again where you see a small bone; and if you do not see it, begin to heat the cautery until you see the bone as I told you; after that take a string, and put molasses and cotton into it, and put it on the signet, and let it be for three days; then put wet cotton into wax; and leave it to be hot until it is ossified; then cure the wound with the ointment which is called "tetrarchafarcion" until it is healed.
Et se dirent li ancien, que quant plus demoure overte li plaie, plus s’espurge; et por ce si aide mues.	And seiden the ancient, that quant plus dure overtli plaie, plus espurgre; et por ce si aide mues.
Et dirent aucun de ces que on doit tant lassier le cautere que partie de l’os soit arse, et puis rese on ceu qui est ars de l’os, et soit curez.	And said the ancient that the longer a wound remains open, the more it will putrefy; and therefore if the fire should burn so much of the bone as to be consumed, then remove what is burned from the bone, and let it be cured.
Et dient li autre c’on doit le cautere tant lassier sus, et bouter si fort c’on abaite de l’os ausi large comme I vertoil que les femmes mettent en lor fusez por ceu que les humors issent mues hors; et doit on lassier la plaie longement overte; aprés le doit on curer et sodeir.	And said the other that one must burn the cauterizing substance so much on top of it, and burn it so hard that the humors come out as far as women put a string in their navels for those who have babies; and one must let the wound remain open for a long time; after which one must cure and patch up.
Et ces II manieres de cauteres ne me semblent mie estre bones dou tout en tout, fuers qu’en aucuns homes ou il ait voie de paor; et mues me semble que je lou doie laissier; car li chiés li est afoiblis par les solutions continuees de nature, si com nos le tesmoignons ens autres membres; et meisme quant li chiés dou malaide est foibles par nature, et li premiere semblance de cautere est plus salve et muedre por moi, et de celi use je oevre en donques emsamble salut.	And these two ways of cauterizing do not seem to me to be good in all respects, except that they are useful in some men where there is a chance of death; and it seems to me that I should let them rest, for the shoulder is weakened by continuous solutions of nature, as we have witnessed with other limbs; and above all, when the shoulder of the sick person is weak from nature, and the first sign of cauterizing seems to me more safe and gentle to me, and from which I use to assemble in a sort of order for healing.
de l’anciainne dolor dou chief	of the old woman's pain with her head
Quant en tout le chief vient dolor croniques, et dure longement, si doit user li malaides yeris et pilules qui sont apelees «cochie», et d’espurgement de chief et d’oiles et d’emplastres; et s’on li fait le cautere que nos avons devant dit, et il ne vaut.	When in the whole head there is a chronic pain that lasts for a long time, one should use herbs and pills that are called "cochier", and head purging, oils, and poultices; and if one does the cautery that we have mentioned above, it will be of no help.
Pren warde se li chiés dou malade est de fort nature, et qu’il ne soit trop froit; adonques le cauterize desoz celui cautere un poc que nos avons dit desus.	Take care that the patient's head is of a strong nature, and that he is not too cold; then apply the cautery to it as we have said above.
Aprés fai cautere sus chescune corne dou chief jusc’a l’os, si com devant avons dit, et fai I cautere ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz»; et est I leus en coi on met ventouses; et alige ta main si que tu ne voises mie jusc’a l’os: li malaides sent trop plus grant dolor en cest cautere que as autres, et je em parlerai aillors; et covient que li cauteres des cornes soient plus subtis que cil dont on cautere la moieneteit dou chief, et c’est li forme:	After you have made the cautery on each horn of the head as we have said above, and have made I a cautery where it is called "vesselz"; and are I to put leech's cups; and arrange your hand so that you do not see them until you reach the bone: the patient will feel much more intense pain in this cautery than in others, and I will speak about that later; and it is necessary that the cornes' cauterizes be finer than those with which we cauterize the hairiness of the head, and this is the form:
dou cautere dou chief	To cauterize the head.
Quant en une partie dou chief vient dolor sodaine, et est estendue li maladie jusc’a l’oil, et li chiés est espurgiez par medicines mondifians, et on a fait les autres cures que j’ai dit en la division des maladies, et tout ceu ne profite mie: adonques li fai cauteres selonc II manieres, c’est a savoir de medicine ague et de feir.	When suddenly there is pain in the head all the way to the oil, and the patient has been feverish as I described in the division of diseases, and nothing else helps: then do the cauterization according to two ways, that is, with water-medicine and fire.
Li cauteres de medicine ague si est que tu preignes une doce d’alz, et oste l’escorce et le recope I poc as II chiés, et puis fent la temple ou li dolor tient en teil maniere que tu puisses reponre la doce d’alz desoz le cuir; et quant elle sera reponuee si le lie et l’estraint bien et le laisse ensi XII houres; et puis le deslie et trait fuers la doce d’ail, et laisse la plaie ensi II jors ou III; puis met sus cotun plongiet en burre tant que porreture en isse.	The cauterization with water-medicine: if you squeeze an ounce of aliz in a bag, peel and ream the root and the bark to II degrees, and then boil it in oil as I have said for the head, and then it holds in the temple or pain is in a part that you can apply the aliz solution on the skin; and when it is applied if you let it rest for 12 hours; and then remove it and treat with an ounce of garlic, and leave the wound for II days or III; then put cotton wadding dipped in ointment onto it as often as possible.
Aprés le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues si fai ceu d’aucunes medicines comburans que j’ai escrites ou dozime traitier des medicines comburans.	After the treatment with ointment until he is well; and if you see that it is good this of some burning medicines which I have written or half-treatiser of burning medicines.
Li cautere de fer si est selonc ceste meniere.	The fire cautery if it is according to this manner.
Chaufe le cautere de coi ci est li forme:	Heat the fire cautery so that it is hot:
Et est apelez «clos» por ceu que li chief est fait a la forme d’un clo ou il ait I poc de corbeure, et em mileu a une petite apparance; et le met sor le leu dolorous, et tien ta main et trestorne le feir un poc legierement, tant que li moitiez de l’espés dou keur soit arse; et lieve ta main que li artere n’arde, que est defuers, et decorre habundance de sanc.	And call it 'clos' for this that the head is made in the form of a 'clo' or hole with a little depression, and place it on the painful spot, and hold your hand and turn the fire slightly, until half of the pain has burned; and remove your hand so that the artery does not burn, which is difficult, and run abundance of blood.
Aprés met coton en awe de seil, et met sor le leu par III jors; puis i met coton moilliet em burre, et puis cure le leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vuelz cauterize ceste emigraine avec le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare», a tout la pointe, et te garde de coper l’artere en ceste emigraine qui n’est mie anciaine.	After put cotton in silk, and place it on the spot for III days; then I put cotton wet with butter, and then treat the spot with ointment until he is well; and if you want to cauterize this migraine with the cautery which is called 'cultellare', all the tip, and keep yourself from covering the artery in this migraine which is not old.
de emigraine	of headache
Quant tu cures emigraine si com nos avons devant dit en divisions des maladies, et ne profite mie, et vois que li cauteres devant dis de la medicine et dou fer ne li soffit mie, adonques covient il que tu eschaufes le cautere qui est apelez «cultellare» tant qu’il soit blans; et seigne ainsois sor le leu doillant une ligne de demi doi de lonc, et oste ta main une fois, et l’estrain que tu ne coper l’artere et que ne viegnes jusc’a l’os; et te warde de la mandibule que muet quant on menjut, et li ners n’ait regart que la muet et que spasmus ne veigne a malaide, et te warde de decorrement de sanc de l’artere quant elle sera copee, ou copement ait grant paour et meismement a celui que ne s’i conoit, et qui n’est estudians et esprovez; et laisse l’uevre em mi voie; mais je vos dirai coment on restainche sanc quant li artere est copee, et je vos mostrerai a leu ou il afiert en cest livre.	For headache As we have said before in the division of diseases, and profit not at all, and see that the cautery before mentioned of medicine and fire does not suffice him, then it is necessary that you heat the cautery which is called "cultellare" until it is white; and sign so on the place where it hurts a line half a finger long, and move your hand once, and hold it so that you do not cover the artery and that you do not come to the bone; and guard against the jaw that moves when he chews, and let the rest be in mid-way; but I will tell you how to stop the headache when the artery is covered, and I will show you at the place where it happens in this book.
Et se tu vois que cist cauteres ne soffise mie a la maladie, et li malaides est soffrans, cauterize le enmi le chief ausi com nos avons dit, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee; et se tu vues, aministre le cautere que nos avons dit ou chapistre de l’estraction de l’artere, avec le cautere qui ait II coutelz; et est cist cauteres millors de celui et plus aidans.	And if you see that these cauterizations do not help the patient's illness, and the patient is suffering, cauterize him on the top of the head as well as we have said, and cure the wound until it heals; and if you see, administer the cauterization that we have said, or the extract of the artery, with the cauterizer that has II knives; and these cauterizations are better than those and more helpful.
de la dolor des oreilles de part froidor	for pain in the ears from cold
Quant en l’oreille vient dolor de froit, et on i a ovreit de medicines solutives et des autres cures que nos avons dit en la division, et li dolors ne se muet, adonques eschaufe cest cautere qui est apelez «poins», de coi ci est li forme:	When there is pain in the ears from cold, and one has applied the liquid medicines and other treatments we spoke of in the division, and the pain does not go away, then heat this poultice that is called "poins," which has this form:
Aprés pointoie tout entor l’oreille malaide, ou entor les II se la dolor tient en ambedous, et t’esloigne un poc ensus de la racine de l’oreille puis que tu as signiet le leu d’enche; et ait X poins entor chescune oreille; aprés cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	After applying the poultice all around the painful ear, or around both ears where the pain is felt at the base of the ear, and keeping it in place for X minutes; then, cure the area until it is healthy.
de la torture de la bouche	of the torture of the mouth
Torture qui doit estre curee par cautere nen est fuers que de celles que muevent de fleume, si com nos avons dit en divisions des maladie; et ne faire point de cautere as semblances que vienent de sechor et de spame de ners.	torture that must be cured by fire is only effective for those that move with fluid, as we have said in the division of diseases; and not to apply fire to similar things that come from thirst and spam of nerves.
Quant tu cures ceste semblance de torture qui muet de fleume d’ydres et d’espurgemens de chief et de gargarisme, et ceu ne vaut, adonc covient que tu cauterizes le malaide de III cauteres: l’une en la racine de l’oreille, et l’autre un poc defuers la temple, et le tier en l’ajostement des II levres; et met le cautere en la partie qui apert saine, et li fai cautere endroit le chief de l’oreille desus un poc desoz la corne dou chief, et un autre en la temple ausi longe com uns poce; et laisse le cautere tant sus que li moitiez dou keur soit arse; et c’est li forme dou cautere:	When you cure this torture of fluid movement in the throat and gargling, and it does not improve, then you should apply three cauterizations: one at the root of the ear, another a little further down the temple, and the third at the junction of the two lips; place the cautery on the healthy part, and let it burn for half the time; and this is the form of the cautery:
Et est li semblance dou cutellaire que nos avons mise devant, mais il est un poc plus subtilz et covient que li coutelz soit un poc plus gros; aprés cure lou leu si com j’ai devant dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	and is the appearance of the scalpel that we have described above, but it is a little more subtle and it is necessary for the scalpel to be a little thicker; after curing the site as I said before, until it is well.
Quant apoplexie est ancieinne et tu la cures ensi com nos avons dit, et il ne profite mie, et li malaides n’ait fievre, adonques li fai IIII cauteres: II sus les II cornes dou chief, et I emmi le chief, et I ou leu qui est apelez «vasselz» si com nos avons devant dit, et lou derrien cautere sus la bouche de l’estomac; et soit curez si com nos avons dit devant.	When apoplexy is ancient and you treat it thus as we have said, then it does not profit, and the patient has no fever, then make four cauterizations: II on the two horns of the head, and I cut the head, and I place it which is called "vesselz" as we have said before, and a fourth cauterization on the mouth of the stomach; and be cured thus as we have said before.
de litargie	of chalk
A cest maladie covient doner au malaide yeres grans et pilules mondifians le cerveil; aprés reis lou chief dou malaide tout, et li met sus l’occipite l’emplaustre de sinapi qui est escrit ou traitier des emplastres; et c’est li maniere dou cautere: si lou fai si com j’ai dit.	For this disease, give the patient great years and pills to clean the brain; then, cut all of the head, and place on the occiput the mustard which is written or used for plasters; and this is the way of the cautery: do so as I have said.
S’il est sanez ensi, boin est; et s’il ne l’est, se li fai III cauteres des emmi le chief en dessendant jusc’a col, et ait d’espaice entre chescun cautere I doi de gros; et le cure si com les autres, et se tu i vues ajoster, et li malaides est soffrans, se li fai I cautere en mileu; et se mestiers est, II autres sus les II cornes, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare», si com j’ai devant dit.	If it is thus, then it is good; and if not, make three cauterizations of cutting the head down to the collarbone, and leave a space of two inches between each cauterization; and heal it as with the others, and if he still writhes, and the patient suffers, then make one cauterization in the middle; and it is necessary, II others on the two horns, and heal it until it is well; and be the cauterization which is called "olive", as I have said before.
de la froidor dou chief	of the cold
Il covient que li chief soit mundifiez de yeres et de ceu que nos avons devant dit; aprés reis le chief dou malaide, puis li fai cautere emmi le chief et sus chescune corne, et I derrier et III sus l’espinee dou col; et se tu en as plus mestier, et li cors est moiste et li malaides est soffrans, et li maladie est fors, se li fai IIII cauteres sus l’espinee dou dos; et li laisse tant que li plus dou keur soit ars, et lieve ta main; aprés le cure tant qu’il soit sanez, et soit li cauteres qui est apelez «olivare» que nos avons devant dit.	the head should be cleaned of years and of what we have just said; then wash the head of the sick person, then do cauterization on the head and on each horn, and behind and III on the spine of the neck; and if you need more, and the body is wet and the patient is suffering, and the disease is severe, then do four cauterizations on the spine of the back; and leave it until the third day is over, and raise your hand; after the cure as long as it is healthy, and the cauterization which is called "olivare" that we have just said.
de l’epilempsie	of epilepsy
Li epilentiques ne doit useir de cautere fuers que cil qui est fleumatique, et covient premier mondifier le cerveil de yeres et d’autres cures que nos avons dites en la division quant li malaides est grans et soffrans de penre medicine.	of the epileptic should only use fire cauterization if it is phlegmatic; first, the brain should be cleaned of years and other cures that we have mentioned in the division when the patient is great and suffering from pain.
Et se c’est uns enfes qui ne lou puisse soffrir, se li fai gargarisme et mastication mondifiant le cerveil sovent avec bones viandes; aprés li reis lou chief em mileu, et i fai I cautere selonc ce que nos avons dit devant, et I cautere sus lou vassel, et sus chescune corne; et se li malaides est fors et soffrans, se li fai cauteres si com j’ai dit a celui qui ait paralisie et mollification de cors, sus l’espinee dou dos et dou col, et soit li cauteres olivier selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if it is an infant who cannot suffer the fire, make gargling and chewing with bone meat; after him put his head in the middle, and do a cauterization according to what we have said before, and a cauterization on his neck, and on each horn; and if the patient is outside and suffering, do cauterize as I said to one who has paralysis and softening of the spine and neck, and let the cauterization be olive according to the way that I said.
Se li malaides est enfes, se li fai I cautere subtil selonc ceste maniere:	If the patient is a child, do a delicate cauterization according to this method:
Quant par la cause de melancolie sunt les superfluitez ou les moistors corrumpues et fleume grosse, adonques lou cauterize de teils cauteres com nos avons dit a celui qui ait paralisie.	When, by reason of melancholy, there are excesses or corrupted wetness and thick fluid, then the cauterization is of parts as we have said to him who has paralysis.
Et se par la cause de melancolie est li superfluitez declinans a melancolie, et est li cors dou malaide moistes, adonc li done a boivre chose par coi li cervelz soit mundifiez, selonc ceu qu’il est devant en la division.	And if, by reason of melancholy, the excess is declining into melancholy, and the patient's spinal fluid is moist, then give him to drink something so that his brain is purified, according to what it is before in the division.
Aprés reis lou chief dou malaide; aprés fai I torteil de lin bien fait, ausi com I cercle, si le met emmi le chief; et li malaides sié croisiez, et soit bien tenus de toutes pars; aprés presente le linement, et vaut mues de burre de berbis ancien; et lou chaufe a feu tempreement, si que li dois s’on li boute le puisse soffrir; aprés vuide le cercle par dedens emmi le chief, et lou laisse refroidier; et fai ce a malaide chescune semaine une fois avec autre governement boin, tant qu’il soit sanez.	After you have cut the head of the patient; then make a well-formed torus out of linen, also as a circle, so that it fits around the head; and sit the patient down comfortably, and hold him firmly on all sides; then present the linen, and rub it with old sheep's butter; and heat the cloth gently by the fire, so that it can be tolerated by the patient; then empty the torus from inside the circle of the head, and let it cool; and do this to the patient every week once with other good governing, until he is well.
Ou se tu vues cauterize lou en faisant poins plusors a tot le cautere.	If you want to cauterize yourself by making many punctures all over the cauterization.
Ceste maniere de cautere amoistit le cerveil igaument; et puis met sus coton moilliet en burre et en graisse de geline.	This way of cauterizing dries out the brain somewhat; and then put cotton that is wet with oil and with grease of goat's milk.
de l’awe des eulz	of the eyes
Quant awe vient premierement as eulz par les signes que j’ai dit en la division, adonques encomence et done boivre au malaide chose mundifiant le chief, et le warde de toutes moistors, et lou fai suer ou bain plusors fois a jeun.	When the hair comes first as long by the signs that I said in the division, then begin and do drink to the patient purifying thing the head, and the ward of all moisture, and let it sweat or bathe many times on an empty stomach.
Aprés li comande a rere son chief, et li fai cautere emmi le chief, et li fai II cauteres sus les II temples se li dessendemens de l’awe est as II eulz ensamble, ou en I se li dessendemens est en I; et cope a tout le cautere toutes les voines et les arteres que sont desoz le keur, et soient li cautere lonc selon lou large de la temple; et te warde de decorrement de sanc, et se tu vois trop de sanc issir, si li estainche de teil pooir com tu as.	After he has let his hair grow long, and he makes a cauterization on the head, and he makes II cauterizations on the II temples where it is shaved, and all the cauterizations of the veins and arteries that are severed, and the cauterization is long according to the width of the temple; and guard against the emergence of blood, and if you see a lot of blood coming out, then stop it with a towel so that it doesn't flow.
Et je t’enseignerai en l’estraction des arteres et a l’incision la cautele coment tu l’estencheras; et aucune fois fait on cautere ou hatereil desoz les II os derrier.	And I will teach you in the extraction of arteries and in the incision how to stop the bleeding; and never do you make a cauterization or an incision behind the II bones.
dou cors des larmes	The tears of the heart
Quant les larmes des eulz sont ancienes et acostumees et sont sus les voines, ou delez les arteres que sont en l’aparance dou chief defors; et on voit que c’est des superfluitez froides fleumatiques, adonques li fai le cautere que j’ai dit en l’encomencement de l’awe dessendant as eulz: I cautere emmi le chief, et II cauteres sus les II temples, et II cauteres ou haiterel desoz les II os; et s’il i a besoigne plus, si le cauterize saigement desus le sorcil a tout I petit cautere.	The tears of the heart are ancient and accustomed, and are in the veins, or take away the arteries that are in appearance at the top of the head; and one can see that it is due to cold, phlegmatic excess, so I make the cautery that I said at the beginning of the work descending into the veins: I cauterize the top, and I cauterize the two temples, and I cauterize where the hair grows on the two bones; and if more is needed, I cauterize it well above the eyebrow with a small cautery.
dou cors des larmes par dedens les eulz	The tears flow from the heart into the veins.
Quant tu le medicines selonc ceu que nos avons dit en la division, et il ne profite mie, adonques done a boivre a malaide III nuis cochies; aprés li reis le chief, et li fai cautere ou mileu dou cautere olivaire; et fai II cauteres dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis» sus les II sorcis, un poc desoz les chevous; et te warde de l’artere que tu ne la coper.	When you treat it according to what we have said in the division, and it does not benefit, then give it three nights' drink of bad wine; after that, he raises his head, and he makes a cautery halfway through the olive cautery; and he makes two cauteries of the cautery called "clavilis" on the two sorces, a little bit from behind the hair; and be careful with the artery so that you don't cover it.
Et c’est li forme dou cautere qui est apelez «clavilis»:	And this is the form of the cauterization which is called "clavis":
Quant li papiere de l’oil est mollifie de maladie et de moistor, adonques la cautarize de cest cautere qui est apelez «olivare».	When the paper of oil is softened by disease and moisture, then the cauterization with this cautery which is called "oliva
de coi ci est li forme:	So that you know how to make this form:
Et se tu vues si fai II cauteres sus les II sorcis ausi lons com li sorcilz sont; et n’i lassiez mie la main fors que tant que li tierce partie de la papiere soit arse, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit.	And if you make two cauterizations on the two wounds as long as the wicks are; and do not remove the hand except that for a third part of the paper is burned, according to the way I have said.
dou poil qui point l’oil	of the hair that drips oil
Aucune fois avient que li poil des oilz sont convertit au pardedens, et poignent l’oil, et i fait on cauteres selonc II manieres: c’est a savoir de feu, ou de medicine ardant.	So that the hair of the oils are converted to the pardons, and they touch oil, and you make cauterizations according to two ways: that is to say, with fire, or with burning medicine.
Ou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals; et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.	For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
