Of certain men some flesh grows red, and covers the apricot and restricts it with paper and turns it back, and looks like a rose of the bush; and the work is such that the patient puts his head in oil, then copes all the flesh, and continues copping little by little until the end, and do not forget to avoid polluting the oil at the work; and be the incision of the spatumile as we have said in the incision of the nail and with small strokes of a chisel on bone like a pearl, as it shows after this chapter. And when the incision is completed and all the flesh is copied, then add to the oil of black seed or you distil red ochre and similar medicines that corrode, and put cotton into the oil for cover with water with the help of wax, so that it be sure of an abscess; and if he does not wait, and the hot foot rises, and you doubt of an abscess, then let go of the oil and treat the abscess with soothing things; then return to your work until it is sound, and in this way do copings of flesh are fitted in oil by this resemblance.
Mais toutevoie il covient que tu aliges la cure de chescun oil foible de la voie natureil; et de la voie accident, en ovraige de fer; et ne bouter mie ta main en aucun de ces ovraiges tant que tu voies que cist membres soit soffrans celui ovraige.	But it is necessary that you equalize the cure of each weak oil of the natural path; and of the accidental path, in the work of iron; and do not put your hand in any of these works as long as you see that this member suffers from that work.
des voines des eulz	of the veins of the hairs
Sebel sont voinnes rouges que sont covertes sus l’oil, et tolent a la veue son ovraige et afoiblissent l’oil toz jors.	are red that are covered on the oil, and endure his work and weaken the oil all the time.
Mestier est donques au premier que tu regardes se li oil, en coi sebel est, est fors, et n’i a autre maladie fuers que lou sebel; adonques le coil en teil maniere: comande au malaide qu’il mette son chief en ton sain, puis sospent celles voines a tout l’oncine selonc sa sapience, et soit li oncines subtilz double selonc ceste forme:	It is necessary therefore that you first see what oil is in the member, and if there are any veins, and if there is no other disease than the disease of the member; then, with respect to his wisdom, suspend those veins entirely for a long time, and make them subtle in some way according to this form:
Et soient dui oncine par degrez en I cors selonc ceste forme:	And are two oils by degrees in one degree according to this form:
puis c’on coil as forces celles voinnes subtilment, et essue lou sanc houre aprés autre, tant que tu voies removoir celles voines fuers de l’oil; et garde que tu ne blecier l’oil as pointes des spatumiles, et fai cest ovraige a houre de midi devant lou soleil, et soies mout fervans en ton ovraige si que tu ne copes fuer que celles voinnes; et quant tu avras ce fait, si distille en l’oil coliere vert et rouge por corrumpre ceu qui est demorez dou sebel.	And then with careful manipulation of those veins, rinse the blood out one hour after another, as long as you can remove the force of the veins from the oil; and be careful not to blister the oil at the tips of the spatulas, and do this work before noon in the sunlight, and be very hot in your work so that you do not get too much heat than those veins; and when you have done this, let it distil into the oil green and red wine to corrupt what is delayed in the soap.
Et se tu n’as pooir de coillir tout ceu en celle houre, si fai emplastre sus l’oil de choses apaisans la dolor des eulz, et le laisse aucuns jors tant que li dolors soit apaisie et soit asseurez d’aposteme chaut, puis rencomence selonc ceste maniere qui est devant tant qu’il soit sanez; et c’est li forme des forces:	If you are not able to carefully manipulate all of that in that hour, then make a paste on the oil from soothing things to relieve the pain of the eyes, and leave it for several days until the pain is relieved and assured by the heat, then begin again according to this method which is described above until it is healed; and this is the form of the treatment.
de la fistule de l’oil	of the pipe
Li mire si nomment «arissati» fistule: quant tu la cures per cautere et par medicine ague ardant selonc ceu que j’ai devant dit, et elle n’est mie sanee, si est engien en li que tu fendes sus l’aposteme, lai ou il doit meurer, et trai toute la moistor que i est, tant que li os soit descovers.	The fistula of the oil: when you treat it with a hot caustic and medicine as I have described above, and it is not healed, then cut through the abscess, because that is where it must die, and remove all the moisture there is, until the bone is uncovered.
Et quant li os iert descovers, et tu verras la corruption et la noiror, si la reis a tout l’estrument de coi ci est li forme; et est apelez «aspre chief», et soit fait de feir inde a I chief reont, et soit pointoiez si com une lime si com il est en la presente forme:	And when the bone is uncovered, and you will see corruption and blackness, then take out all of the instrument with which it is formed; and it is called "spiky chief", and be made from the top to the bottom, and be sharpened as a chisel.
Et met sus lou leu de l’os corrumput, puis le torne entre tes dois, et presse ta main un poc tant que tu saiches que celle corruption est rese; et fai ceu aucune fois, puis restoure lou leu de medicines exiccatives.	And place on the top of the corrupted bone, then turn it between your two hands, and press your hand a little until you feel that the corruption is gone; and do this again, then restore the place with drying medicine.
se li leus est soudez, et char i naist, et li cors de la bowe est soudez, et remaint ensi XL jors, et il ne renovele et n’est mie apostemez, et accidens mavais n’i vient, saiches qu’il est sanez; se ceu non, si n’i a autre engien que de ramener la fistule au pertus dou neif selonc ceste forme: et est que tu descuevre de l’os la seconde fois par fer, et par medicines agues, et quant il iert descovers si prent I foret selonc ceste forme, et soit li chiés de fer a III angles, et li fust soit atenuis jusc’a chief si com tu vois ci:	If his leg is warm, and he has not yet been born, and the iron ring remains in place for XL days, and there is no abscess, and no bad accidents happen to him so that he is healthy; otherwise, there is another reason, which is to bring the fistula to the breach of the navel according to this form: and it is that you should uncover the bone again with iron, and with bitter medicines, and when it is uncovered thus take a ferret according to this form, and let the iron be at III angles, and the ferret be thin up to the top as you see here:
puis le met sus l’os delez lou larmier, et esloigne ta main de l’oil I poc, puis torne a tot le foret tant qu’il perce l’os et le sent li malaides par ceu que li vens en ist s’il tient sa main sus son neif; et pues restoure lou leu de medicines seches, si com je t’ai ensigniet, et quant li char naist et endurcist li leus, si vait li matiere au neif; si est plus legiere chose au malaide.	Then place the iron upon the bone with the chisel, and remove your hand from the oil pot, then turn all the ferret around until it pierces the bone and the patient feels pain through his nose if he holds his hand over his nose; and then restore the position of the dry medicines, as I have taught you, and when the child is born and its leg hardens, so the material goes into the navel. It is a lighter thing for the patient.
de l’issue de l’oil	of the issue of oil
Quant li eulz apert fuer dou tout en tout, et il ne vient point de destorbier au nef, ne amenuisement, si covient que tu lies lou malaide; puis le saine, puis li met ventouses ou haterel sens ferir por succier, puis met sus l’oil I liien fait d’acaice et de aloe et d’encens et de sarcocolle, et puis estrain l’oil, et l’emplaustre sus de bendes et de drapelz; et li maniere des drapelz si est que tu preignes drapelz assez molz, et double chescun en IIII, et puis met l’un sus l’autre selonc la quantiteit que li eulz en ait mestier; puis l’estrain par desus d’un bendeil dur forment, et rencomence les ventouses por succier sens ferir; puis oste les ventouses et laisse l’oil estraint jor et nuit, et se li liiens amolist, si covient que tu l’estraignes mout; puis oste lou liien aprés le jor et la nut, et se tu vois l’oil repairier, c’est boin; se ce non; si rencomence l’emplaustre et les drapelz et lou liien et les ventouses tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the hairs have grown long and even, then command the patient to leave them alone until they are fully grown. For in the working of this chapter, there is often an evacuation of blood when opening a vein, and incising an abscess, and in the treatment of wounds, and in the extraction of arrows, and in cutting into stones, and similar things; where there is doubt and fear, and many die.
dou derrompement de toile uvee	the breaking of a thread from a woven fabric
Quant disruptions vient en la toile uvee, puis apert, et vient fuer des papieres si com I grain de resins, et est espoantauble a veoir; adonques se tu la vues coper, li ovraiges est telz que tu boutes une aguille en la racine des la partie desoz jusc’a celi desus, puis boute une autre aguille ou il ait I fil double des la partie dou larmier; et la fai percier, et laisse la premiere aguille selonc la disposition; puis cope lou leu dou fil double et lie une partie de l’uve entor, et l’estraint bien, puis estrai l’aguille et met sus l’oil lainne moillie en abun d’uef; et le laisse tant que li filz chiece avec l’uve, puis cure l’oil de choses confortans tant que li plaie soit sanee; et aucune fois li plaie est restrainte par l’uve chescune part d’un cercle de drap, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	When a thread breaks in the woven fabric, then it separates and becomes visible as if there were a seed of resin, and is unpredictable to see; so that you cover it up with wax, then you make another hole where there is double thread on the part from the edge up to the top, then you pierce it, and leave the first needle according to its disposition; then you tie the double thread around the weave, and tighten it well, and pull out the needle; and you put a wet wax on the other oil in abundance of resin; and you let it go as long as the thread catches with the weave, then you cure the oil from comforting things until the wound is healed; and never does the wound get constricted by the weave of a circle of cloth, until it is healed.
Et se li eulz done grant apparance, si le perce au spatumile subtil qui viegne em parfont de l’oil, et corre la moistor albuginé et dessende li eulz, et entre ens tantost; puis l’estrai tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the hairs have grown out, let them be cut with a sharp knife that comes completely from the oil, and run the moisture off the skin and dry the hairs, and quickly remove it; then extract it until it is healthy.
de la bowe de l’oil	from the oil
Ceste maladie qui est apelee «alcunnati» nen est fuers que bowe qui est assemblee en l’oil, semblant a aigue dessendant, et ce n’est mie aigue; et li maniere de l’apparance de l’ovraige si est que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege appareilliet et droit, puis prent le chief entre tes mains de II pars, et lou muef tant que tu voies la bowe venir au desus a tes eulz; puis soit ens fichie, et ne dessende et soit descombree li lumiere, et voie li malaides les choses si com il soloit; et s’elle ne dessent desoz, saiches que c’est aigue, et se li dessendemens de la bowe n’est appareilliez si com nos avons dit.	This disease, which is called "alcunnati," is only fur that is gathered in oil, resembling water flowing down, and is not water; and the manner of its appearance in the ovary is such that you put the patient on a chair or table and straightened him, then take the head between your hands from both sides, and move it as much as you see the fur coming up to your hair; then take it off completely, and do not run the moisture off, and let it fall on the ground, and look at the patient's things so as it was alone; and if it does not flow out, know that it is water, and the movement of the fur is not adjusted as we have said.
si fai seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, puis prent le spatumile subtil et fent sus la toile cornee I poc par la continuation de la conjunctive avec la toile cornee et la corone, tant que li bowe isse; et quant elle ert issue, si distille en l’oil aigue chaude mellee a miel, ou aigue ou fenugreic est boillis et miel, puis soit curee d’autre cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If you wish to treat the disease between your hands, then take the subtle sponge and apply it to the cornee cloth with the connection of the cloth and the crown, until the bow is relaxed; and when it has relaxed, pour into hot oil mixed with honey or water or fenugreek that has been boiled and honey, then let it be treated by another cure until it is well.
des aigues de l’oil	of the oil
Nos avons jai les semblances des aigues en la division, et ceu qu’il covient por percier; si en oevre selonc la santeit.	We have made the sounds of the voice in division, and that which is suitable to pierce; if it is done according to health.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains croisiet, fuers de la lumiere por le soleil, et li lie l’oil sain et estreint mout fort; puis met la papiere de l’oil a ta main senestre se li eulz est senestres, ou a ta main destre se li eulz est destres; puis prent en ta main destre, se li eulz est senestres, l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda», ou a ta main senestre, se li eulz est destre; puis met la pointe de l’estrument delez la corone par la groissece d’un rait en celle blenchor de l’oil a la partie dou menor larmier, puis boute l’estrument qui est apelez «almagda» vertuousement, et trestorne ta main tant qu’il perce en la blenchor de l’oil, et sente que almagda viegne a la chose vuide; et covient que li mesure de la voie almagda soit au parfont de la mesure des l’espaice qui est des la prunele jusc’a la fin de la noirour; et c’est li corone de l’oil; si verras l’os en celle papiere por la clarteit de la toile cornee, et pues met l’estrument jusc’a leu ou li aigue est, puis l’espresse desoz une voie aprés autre.	It is necessary that you place the disease between your hands away from light because of the sun, and squeeze the oil well; then take the paper of the oil with your left hand if the fingers are on the left, or with your right hand if the fingers are on the right; and then take in your right hand, if the fingers are on the left, the instrument which is called "almagda", or in your left hand, if the fingers are on the right; and then place the tip of the instrument at the crown by its thickness to a ray in that blenchor of oil in the part of the smaller tear, and bottle the instrument which is called "almagda" well, and turn back your hand so that it pierces into the blenchor of oil, and you will feel that almagda comes to the empty thing; and it is necessary that the measure of the path of almagda be completely in the measure of the space that is from the prunella up to the end of the darkness; and this is the crown of the oil; then you will see the bone in that paper because of the clarity of the cloth cornee, and then place the instrument at the level where the aigue is, then express one path after another.
se li aigue dessent maintenant, si voit li malaides devant lui et l’estrument en son oil.	If he is now sitting down, then see the patient in front of him and the instrument in his oil.
Aprés repose I petit, et se li aigue remonte la seconde voie, met la fuer avec l’estrument, et quant elle est ens fichie et ele ne monte, si estrai almagda legierement en tornoiant ta main poc et poc; et puis remette en aigue un poc de seil gemme, et leive de ceu l’oil dedens.	After rest for a little while, and he rises again, holding the instrument with force, and when it is firmly placed and does not move up, then extract the almagre lightly by turning your hand back and forth; and then put a little gem oil in it, and leave it in that oil.
Puis met par defuer l’oil estoupes ou lainne moillie en oile roset et en abun d’uef, et lie avec l’oil sain.	Then place by the side the oil of spikenard or another moist oil in a cup and in plenty of wine, and mix with the healthy oil.
Nos, et cil qui sont de nostre tens, mettons sus comin broiet avec abun d’uef.	Now, and those who are of our group, let us put on quickly with plenty of wine.
Et se almagda n’i puet entrer en l’oil par sa duresce, car il i a de teilz homes qui ont trop durs les eulz, si covient que tu preignes l’estrument qui est apelez «alberit», de coi ci est li forme:	If the almagre cannot enter into the oil because of its hardness, since there are some men who have very hard hairs, then you must squeeze the instrument which is called "alberit", from which comes this form:
Et perce donques la conjunctive soulement, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, mais fai I leu subtil, puis i boute almagda, si com nos avons dit; et au complissement de l’uevre appareille au malaide I dorteur avenant, en coi il dorme sus son dos en I leu tenebrous; et soit deveez de toz movemens, et preigne legieres viandes, et ne mueve son chief ne a destre ne a senestre, et soit liiez selonc sa disposition jusc’a tier jor; puis le deslie en cele maison meisme tenebrouse, et esprueve sa veue, et lou fai veoir aucunes choses, et puis li remet lou lien jusc’a septime jor; et ne covient mie que tu faices ceu en l’oure de la cure ou aprés l’incision maintenant, mais il covient que tu aliges ceu, por ceu que li aigue monte hastanment.	And so, let us now begin the explanation, and do not grow too impatient, but make it thin, then pour in the albumen, as we have said; and at the completion of the work prepare for the patient the bed approaching, where he sleeps on his back in the dark place; and be careful of all movement, and press only slight meats, and do not move his head to the right or to the left, and bind him according to his disposition until three days have passed; then release him into that same very dark house, and test his sight, and let him see some things, and then bind him again until the seventh day has passed; and it is not appropriate that you do this in the hour of the cure or after the incision at this time, but it is appropriate that you prepare it beforehand, so that what he drinks rises quickly.
se apostemes chaus vient, que tu desliies l’oil devant le septime jor, et l’adrece de ceu qui assouaige aposteme; et quant il est apaisiez, si deslie la veue et met sus sa faice I orilliet por covrir aucun jor, et soit adés en celle maison tenebrouse.	For the abscess, let it slide on the seventh day, and treat it with water that softens the abscess; and when it has calmed down, if it does not slide, cover it with a covering so that no light enters, and remain in that dark house.
Et puis isse de la maison poc et poc, et se convertisse en ses cas; et saiches que nulz deciples ne se doit entremettre en cest cas.	And then take it little by little from the house, and turn it into those cases; and know that no one should meddle in this case.
Et uns vint a nos qui estoit de la Yrach, qui nos dist que en som pais faisoit om almagda perciet, a coi on succe l’aigue, mais toutevoie je n’en vis onques nul en nostre terre, ne je ne lou lis onques en livres des anciens; et par aventure c’est une novele chose.	And one came to us who was from the Land of Israel, who told us that in their country there is a medicine called almagate which sucks out the water, but nevertheless I have never seen it in our land, nor have I ever read about it in the books of the ancients; and perhaps it is a new thing.
Et ce sont les semblances des formes de almagda, por ceu que cil qui ne les conoit les voie; et soient d’arain proprement:	And these are the appearances of the shapes of almagate, so that he who does not know them may see them; and let them be of pure arand:
Et soient li chief d’aus de ceste meisme subtiliteit, et li derriene en III angles ague.	And let the head of this middle substance be, and behind it in three angles acute.
de la char sor le neis	of the nose on the side
Aucune fois naissent ou neis chars ajostees diverses, de coi il i a aucunes qui semblent scorpions a mout de piez; et si i a de telz ou il ait char enchancree de fuxe color, et si a char souef de bone color.	There are times when it is born or does not live up to expectations, of which there are some that seem like scorpions at the base of their feet; and if there are any such ones with a green-colored charm, and if there is a black-colored charm.
En celle donques de ces chars qui est souef, et ne mie enchancree, covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains encontre lou soleil; et oevre ses narines, et giete l’oncine a celles chars, et les trai fuers; pues cope ceu que tu em pues sostenir au spatumile subtil agut d’une part, tant que tu saiches que celle char est toute ostee.	In the case of those charms that are souef and not encrusted, it is appropriate that you make the patient sit between your hands in the sunlight; and open his nostrils, and pour the liquid charm on those charms, and rub them vigorously; for what you pour from the subtle, golden liquid on one side should all be bone.
Et s’il en remaint aucune chose c’on ne puisse coper, si l’ovrez a tout I des estrumens subtil legierement, si qu’il n’i demoure rien; et se sans te sormonte, ou aposteme chaus, si lou secort si com il covient; et se c’est apostemes malignes, si te haste et lou cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez et soient ostees toutes les chars, puis giete ou neis aisil et aigue ou vin.	If there is any remaining that cannot be covered, if you open all the instruments of subtlety lightly, so that nothing remains; and if it does not stay in place, or if it rises, or if it breaks out like an apoplexy, or if it heals like it should; and if it is malignant boils, then hurry and cauterize them until they are fully healed and all the charms are removed, then cut and remove them easily and quickly.
Se li neis oevre, et moistors en vient jusc’a palais, saiches qu’il est sanez; et se moistors ne perce si com il covient, saiches qu’il i a char nee en l’os desus, a coi li estrumens ne vient mie por taillier: adonques covient il que tu i boutes I fil de lin un poc gros, et soit noez de mains nous, et ait entre chescun nout d’espaice I doit ou moins; et mette li malaides lou chiés dou fil en son neif a som pooir, et traie en odorant tant qu’il viegne par lou neif dedens la bouche; et maintes fois font ensi li enfant as escoles, et c’est legiere chose a celui qui le vuet faire; puis tien le chief qui vient par lou neif a une main, et l’autre chief qui vient par la bouche a l’autre main, et saiche l’un aprés l’autre en soiant as nous qui sont ou fil.	If he is sick and moisture comes up to the palace, know that he is well; and if moisture does not pass through as it should, know that there is no room in the bone above, so that the instruments do not fit: then you must insert a thin piece of linen thread, and tie your hands together, and leave a space between each knot of one inch or less; and put the child's fingers around the thread at his power, and pull it gently while it goes through his nose into his mouth; and many times do this to the child in school, and it is an easy thing for him who does it; then hold the head that comes through the nose with one hand, and the other head that comes through the mouth with the other hand, and hold them one after the other as we are holding the thread.
Fai ceu tant que tu saiches que li nout ont corrompue celle char, puis trai lou filz, essue le sanc, et moille lou fil en oignement egiptien, et le remet derechief au neis si com devant; fai ceu III jors ou plus, tant que li oignemens corrode tout ceu qui est demorez de char; et puis met ou neis une caine de plonc aucuns jors tant qu’il soit sanez, et s’il a mestier de medicines sechans, si en use; et c’est li forme de l’estrument por purgier lou chief, a coi on distille les oiles et les medicines ou neis:	Make sure you know that the new has corrupted this char, then try to fix the rope, wash the blood, and soak the rope in Egyptian oil, and put it back in the neck immediately as before; make sure for three or more days, until the oil corrode all who are delayed from the char; and then put a stone of plunk on some days until he is healthy, and if there is need to use dried medicines, do so; and this is the form of the instrument for purging the head, where one distills oils and medicines in the neck:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, semblant a une lampe overte, si com une cainne, et li conduis ausi; et se tu vues, si fai une cainne close, et soit li estrumens plains por espurgier lou chief; et ait I mainche au chief por lou tenir quant on chaufe l’oile ou aucune liquor.	It should be of silver or of gold, resembling a lamp open, like a pipe, and you conduct it so; and if you see, then make a closed pipe, and this instrument is flat for purging the head; and I have many times held the head while oil or any liquid was heated.
de la char sor le neis	from the chest to the neck
Maintes fois naist au chief dou neis une maladie qui est apelee «telul», et croist et devient grans adés, tant qu’il est vis chose au regarder; et por ceu covient que tu lou copes au comencement, et l’oste tout fuer, puis met sor leu lou cautere ou la medicine ardant; et s’on le tarde a coper tant qu’il soit grans, si pren warde s’il est durs, de fuxe color, de povre sens: si ne lou touchier mie de fer car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, car quant on le cope aucune fois, si en vient grant malice au malaide; et se li apostemes est de soef touchement, non mie de fuxe color, et tu vois c’on le puisse tout coper, si vuide le malaide et lou cope sens paor, et cure le leu de choses sechans et restraignans.	several times in the chest to the neck a disease is called "telul", and grows and becomes large enough so that it can be seen; and because of this you need to cut it at the beginning, and the bone completely, then place over it fire or medicine burning; and if you delay to cover it until it is large, so take care if it is hard, dry in color, poor sensation: but do not touch him with iron for it is an abscess inflamed, because when you cover it even once, great evil comes to the patient; and the abscess is soft to touch, not dry in color, and you see that he can be completely covered, so empty the patient and cover him without fear, and cure the place of drying and restraining things.
quant li neis est copez et cosus	when the neck is cut and sewed up
Saiches que quant solutions de continuation vient en une de ces cartillagines ovraiges, i profite poc, fuer que en aucuns homes.	Saiches that when solu[t]ions of continuance comes into one of these ovraiged cartilage, i profit poc, fur that in some men.
Il covient donques cant ceu avient a aucun, si regarde se li plaie est fresche a tout son sanc; et adonques ajoste les II levres a une costure, puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et se les levres sont ja desevrees d’une part et d’autre, si covient que tu escorches toutes les parties de lor keur tant qu’elles sainent, puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et l’estraint, et poudre sus poudre de sanc de dragon, et encens broiet; et met sus les poudres une piece d’emplaustre de fort ou d’autre emplaustre soudant, et le laisse tant qu’il chiece par lui, puis le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	And it is necessary, therefore, that no matter who it is, if the wound is fresh in all its blood, and then insert two blades into a stitch, and then treat as long as he is healthy; and if the blades are torn on one side or the other, you must scrape all the parts of their flesh as long as they heal, and then join the two blades into a stitch, and hold them together, and powder them with dragon's blood powder and burnt incense; and put onto the powders a piece of plaster of iron or any other plaster right now, and let it rest until it bleeds from itself, and then treat with ointment as long as he is healthy.
Li maniere de la costure si est que tu assembles la solution: ou par aguilles, si com nos avons dit en la costure dou ventre; ou par fil, si com je le t’ai fait savoir.	The way to stitch: it is that you assemble the solution: or by needles, as we have said in the stitching of the belly; or by thread, as I have told you.
des apostemes des levres	of the lips
A mains homes avient dedens les levres aposteme dur, semblans a grains de veces, et menor et plus grant; adonques couvient que tu tornes les levres, et fendes sus chescun nout, et le prent as pinceures et le cope en chescune partie; puis emple lou leu aprés l’incision de vitriole broiet, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; et puis lou leive d’aisil, et cure lou leu de choses seches tant qu’il soit sanez.	A home made of the lips, an abscess hard and rough, smaller and larger; then you must turn the lips, cut each hole, and take it into pincers and chop it in each part; then employ the fire after the application of vitriol, until the wound is well healed; and then wash it with water, and cure the place of dry things as long as it is healthy.
de la char des gencives	of the cheeks
Maintes fois naist sus les gencives char ajostee, que li ancien apelent «albulus»; si covient que tu la sostienes as tenailles, et la cope a sa racine, et laisse corre la bowe ou le sanc; puis met sor le leu vitriole broiet, ou autres poudres restraignans et desiccatives; et se celle char revient aprés l’incision, et maintes fois avient, si la cope la seconde fois, et la cauterize: si ne revient mie aprés le cautere; et ce sont les formes des estrumens por coper.	Many times burn on the cheeks of the jaw, which the old man calls "albulus"; if it is necessary that you hold them with pliers, and cut off the root, and let the blood flow; then apply fire to the vitriol, or other restraining and drying powders; and if this burn returns after the incision, and many times happens, if they are covered a second time, and cauterized: if it does not return after cauterization; and these are the forms of instruments to cover.
des sordens	of the ordains
Aucunes fois sont assemblees au chief des dens, dedens la bouche entre les gencives, escorces qui sont laides et aspres; et aucune fois sont li dent noir et citrin et vers, tant que li corruption vient a la gencive, et sont li dent puant; si covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide entre tes mains, et ses chiés soit en ton saint, et reis les dens ou les escorces aperent, tant qu’il n’i demore rien; et ensi fai de la noiror et de la verdor, et de la jaunice et des autres taiches, tant qu’elles soient mondees; et s’on oste ceu que i est a la premiere rasion, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence a rere le secont jor et lou tier, tant que tu aies tout reis; et saiches que li dent ont mestier de diverses formes d’estrumens por reire, selonc ceu que li oevre lou demoustre, por ceu que li raseur dont on reit defuer les dens ont autres formes que cil dont on reit entre les dens; et cestes formes et autres soient avec toi appareillies.	None of the orders should be placed in the teeth, behind the teeth, between the gums, these are ugly and rough; and none of the teeth should be black and yellow and rotten, until the decay comes to the gum, and the tooth is stinky; so that you make the patient sit between your hands, and his teeth are in your hand, and you remove the decay where it appears, without waiting for anything; and in this way do the black and the green, and the yellow and the other stains, until they are all removed; and if one is in the first rasement, it is good; if not, it starts again on the second day and the third, until you have them all removed; and know that teeth must be of different shapes for removal, according to what the work demonstrates, because the rasp with which you remove the teeth has other shapes than the rasp with which you remove between the teeth; and these shapes are to be adapted to you.
Il covient quant tu cures lou dent de sa dolor que tu tardes dou traire tant com tu pues, car ce ne doit om mie faire; car c’est une substance mout haute jusc’a donc c’on n’ait point d’excusation dou raier.	It is necessary that you treat the toothache as soon as possible because it should not be left for so long; for this is a very high substance from which there is no excuse to delay treatment.
Adonques quant li malaides est constrains dou traire, si covient que tu soies certains dou dent doillant.	So then when the patient is in pain, you must be certain of the toothache.
Maintes fois desoit li dolor lou malaide, et cuide qu’elle soit ou dent saint, et fait traire le boin dent; et toutevoie ne se depart mie li dolor per ceu, tant que li malvais estrais, car nos l’avons ja veut faire a ces sainors; et quant tu es bien certains dou dent doillant, si covient que tu escorches entor lou dent a tout i. spatumile fort por warder la gencive de toutes pars; puis le mues a tes dois ou as tenailles subtilz au premier poc et poc, tant qu’il soit bien eslochiés, puis i afferme bien les tenailles; et soit li chiés dou malaide en ton saint entre tes genous, et lou tien bien si qu’il ne se mueve.	Often the pain leaves the patient, and he thinks it is a sound tooth, and makes him pull out the good tooth; but in fact the pain does not go away because we have already made this to these nobles; and when you are certain of the toothache, then you scratch the tooth with a strong spittle so as to ward off the gums from all sides; then you move it to your fingers or small tweezers at one poke and another, until it is well loosened, then you tighten the tweezers; and let the patient's jaw be between your knees, and hold it firmly so that it does not move.
Aprés estrai lou dent droitement sens brisier, et s’il ne saut fuer, si prent aucun de ces estrumens et le boute dedens de chescune part legierement, et lou remuef si com tu as fait premier.	After removing the tooth correctly without breaking it, and if it does not fall out on its own, take one of these instruments and gently place it inside each part, and move it as you did before.
Et se li dens est perciez et mengiez, si covient que tu l’emplisses de drapelz, lai ou li pertus sont; et si l’estraint subtilment as tenailles, que il ne brise a l’estraindre; et covient mout saigement ovrer entor la gencive por deschaucier lou dent.	And if the root is exposed and bleeding, it is necessary that you fill the space where it is with gauze; and if it needs to be extracted gently with pliers, so that it does not break when extracted; and it is necessary to cut the gum very carefully around the tooth.
Et te done bien en warde que tu ne le brises, et en remaigne une partie, et reveigne au malaide par la malice de la racine plus grans dolors de la premiere.	And you must take care not to break it, and if a part remains, and return it to the patient by the wickedness of the root, causing greater pain than before.
Et te warde que tu ne faices mie ensi com font li ignorant sainor, qui par lor haste et par lor hardiesce brisent aucune fois le charreit, et n’i amenistrent mie ceu que nos avons conteit; mais font venir aucune fois par l’oquison de ceu grant maladie por les racines que i demorent, ou por lou charreit qu’il brisent, si com nos avons sovent veut; et quant li dens est trais, si lavez lou leu de vin ou d’aisil et de seil; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, que sovent avient, si emple lou leu de vitriole broiet; et se ceu ne vaut, si le cauterize.	And you must take care not to do as the ignorant surgeon does, who, because of his haste and arrogance, often breaks the jaw by his own hand, and does not provide the patient with what we have mentioned; but rather brings about great disease by the root that he breaks, or by the jaw that he breaks, just as we often wanted; and when the root is drawn out, if you wash the hole with wine or azale or vinegar; and if it does not come out, so that it often comes out, unless you apply vitriol to the hole; and if this does not work, then cauterize.
Les formes des estrumens, a coi om muet les dens premier, soient a longes pointes et a gros mainches, qu’il ne doublent mie quant tu trairas le dent; et ce sont les formes:	The shapes of the instruments, so that they do not mute the teeth at the front, are long points and thick handles, so that they do not bend when you pull the tooth; and these are the shapes:
Et soient de gros membres si qu’il ne ploient mie au traire, et soient de fer inde bien fait, et soient dentez por mues tenir.	And let them be of thick members so that they do not bend when you pull it, and let them be of good forged iron, and let them have teeth for holding it in place.
de la racine des dens	of the root of the teeth
Quant li racine demoure au traire, si covient que tu mettes sor le leu coton moilliet em burre I jor ou ij.,	When the root remains when you pull it, you should put cotton wet with oil or butter on the joint for one hour.
tant que li leus soit amolis, pues i boute les tenailles qui sont apelees «algefri», de coi li chiés semblet bec de soigne; et soient dedens faites ausi com une lime et c’est li forme:	as long as the joints are smooth, because they break the pliers that are called 'algefri', which makes the head look like a beak; and let them be inside made like a file and this is the shape:
Et se les racines ne vuellent issir a tout ces tenailles, si covient que tu descuevre la char tot entor la racine, et i met l’estrument qui est apelez «althali», c’est a savoir palainche, de coi ci est li forme:	And if the roots do not want to come out with all these pliers, then you should strip the flesh completely around the root, and put the instrument that is called 'althali', that is to say file, which is this shape:
Et soit fors et gros si qu’il ne brise mie, et se li racine saut par ceu, c’est boin; se ceu non, si t’aide de toz les estrumens, de coi les formes vienent ci aprés:	And be strong and large so that it does not break, and its root jumps out through it, this is good; if not, if you help with all the instruments, from which the shapes come after:
Et si s’aide on de cest estrument qui ait II rains, de coi ci est li forme:	And if one helps with this instrument that has two heads, from which this form comes:
et d’autres ferremens qui sont devant en la rasion des dens, et de cest estrument qui semble unes grans tenailles, dont ci est li forme:	and other tools that are in front in the rationale of the dens, and from this instrument which seems like a pair of large pliers, of which here is the form:
Et soit cist estrumens fors qu’il ne puisse brisier, et saiches que mout d’estrumens de dens sont; et ausi d’autres estrumens, qui ne sont mie contez; et li saiges maistres subtilz trueve par soi meisme son estrument, selonc ceu que ses ovraiges et li maladie li demoustre, car il i a de teilz maladies ou li ancien n’enseignerent point d’estrument por la diversiteit d’au;s et s’om brise point dou charreit ou des autres os, ou il porrit, si i cerche as estrumens qu’il i covient, que je t’ai dit, et t’aide des gestes, de coi ci est li forme:	and this instrument is strong so that it cannot break, and you know that many tools of the dens are; and also other tools which are not considered; and the master wise men try themselves with their own instruments, according to what their labor and the disease show them, because there are many diseases where the old do not teach the tool; and if it does not break the chariot or the other bones on which he lies, then if you seek the tools that suit him, I have told you, and help you with the gestures, of which here is the form:
Et soient gros et bien tenant por tenir l’os, qu’il n’eschaipe, mais le puisse tenir et oster; et puis restoure lou leu de medicines convenant a ceu, et s’il ait en l’os porriture, et elle est petite, si la reis a tout cest estrument:	And let them be large and firm to hold the bone, so that it does not escape but can be held and removed; and then return them to their place with suitable medicines for this person, and if there is pus in the bone, and it is small, then take all of this tool.
Quant li dent apperent ne mie selonc lou cors natureil, et li forme est laide, et meismement en femmes puceles, si covient que tu saiches se li dens est neis aprés lou dent, et n’est mie en droit leu, et on ne lou puet soier ne limer: adonques lou raie; et s’il est aers avec lou dent, si prent cest estrument dont ci est li forme, et est semblans a I petit bec, et soit de fer inde agut en som:	When the teeth do not appear to be in their natural place in the jaw, and their shape is ugly, especially in young women, you must know that the root may go beyond the tooth, and it does not remain in its right position, and one cannot sew or file it: then pull it out; and if it goes with the tooth, take this instrument whose form is like a small beak, and which is made of iron:
Et lou cope poc et poc em mains jors por la duresce dou dent, et por ceu que tu ne mueves les autres, et s’il est apparans c’on le puisse limer, si lou lime d’une teil lime com ci est li forme:	And the cap fits tight and tight to the tooth's durezza, and so that you do not move the others, and if it seems that it can be filed, then take a file of this shape:
et est ausi com li lime de coi on fait les aguilles; et en lime lou dent poc et poc em mains jors legierement, si qu’il ne se mueve tant qu’il chiece; puis la plaine en la fin a tout aucun raseur, et se li dens est trop trenchans et il blece la lengue, si covient limer l’aspreteit tant qu’il soit igalz, si qu’il ne blece la lengue ne ne corrompe la parole.	and is also like the lime that we use to make needles; and in a lime put and put it in the hand lightly every day so that he does not move until he bites; then the smooth at the end to any razor, and its edge is too sharp and it bleeds the tongue, so it is necessary to polish the sharpness until it is even, so that it does not bleed the tongue or corrupt the word.
quant li dent lochent	when the tooth moves
Quant li dent devant lochent, ou par percussion ou par cheoir, et li malaides ne puet presser sus ceu qu’il menjue qu’il ne chient, et tu les as curez de medicines restrignans, et ceu ne vaut; si les covient restraindre d’un fil d’or, car li filz d’argent devient vert et porrit, mais li ors ne se mue onques; et soit li filz moiens ne trop gros ne trop menus, selonc la quantiteit de l’espaice entre les dens; et se tu vues adrecier les dens, si pren lou fil et lou boute double entre les II dens sains, puis met les chiés entre les dens meus, s’il en i a I ou plusors, tant que tu veignes saigement jusc’au dent sain d’autre part; puis rencomence la coverture jusc’a la partie ou tu encomensas, et estrains ta main subtilment et saigement, tant qu’il ne se mueve point; et soit ta lieeure a la racine dou dent si qu’il ne puist eschaper.	when the teeth move forward due to percussion or chewing, and the patient cannot press on the tooth he is hurting without causing pain, and you have treated them with restraining medicines, and this does not work; so it is necessary to restrain it with a gold thread, because silver wire becomes green and rotten, but gold wire never moves; and let the thread be neither too thin nor too thick according to the space between the teeth; and if you notice any toothache, take the thread and double it between two healthy teeth, then insert the teeth between the gaps, if there are one or more, until you reach the healthy tooth on the other side; then begin again at the covered part and gently and carefully squeeze your hand until it no longer moves; and let your ligature be at the root of the tooth so that it cannot escape.
Puis cope les chiés dou fil a unes tenailles, et les assemble, et les repont entre le dent sain, et le met ensi qu’il ne blece la lengue; et puis le laisse ensi estroit tant com il puet demorer, et s’il deslie, ou li filz ront, si l’estraint d’un autre fil; si demorrait et servira ensi tout son tens, et c’est li forme des dens et li figure de l’adrecement des II dens sains, et des II meus, si com tu vois:	Then tie the ends of the thread to a pair of pliers, and join them together, and put them between the healthy tooth and the tongue so that it does not hurt the tongue; then leave them tight as long as you can, and if they slip or come off, fasten them with another thread; if it holds out and serves this way all its time, and this is the form of the teeth and shape of the fixing of the two healthy teeth and the two molars, just as you see:
Et quant li dent chiet, si lou remet on en son leu, de fres en fres, si com nos avons dit; et ne s’en entremette mie qui n’est saiges et soffrans, et aucune fois fait on la forme d’un dent d’os de vaiche, et lou met on au leu ou li defaute est, et l’estraint on si com nos avons dit, et demore et sert ensi lonc tens.	Then if the tooth falls out, put it back in its place bit by bit, as we have said; and let no one but a clever and patient person attempt this, and never make the shape of a tooth out of bone, and put it back in its place where it has fallen out, and fasten it as we have said, and wait and serve for a long time.
de coper lou liien de la lengue	of copper the ring of the tongue
Aucune fois est cist liiens qui vient desoz la lengue ou naturez, que on naist ensi; ou par accident de plaie soudee; et li ovraiges est telz que tu oevre la bouche dou malaide, et ait sa teste en ton sain, et li lieve la lengue; puis cope lou liien nervous dou large, tant que li lengue soit desloie de son tenement, et se il i a duresce ou nout, et c’est de soudement de plaie, si i boute l’uncine et cope dou large celui liement; et garde que li fendure ne soit mie trop em parfont, por l’artere qui est desoz; et quant tu as fait, si leve le leu d’aigue rose et d’aisil, ou d’aigue froide, puis met desoz la lengue une tente de lin; et la teigne li malaides chescune nuit, que li leus ne puisse soder.	No time is there for the ring of the tongue or nature, that it is not so; or by accident of a sore wound; and the works are such that you open the mouth of the sick person, and place his head on your chest, and pull out the tongue; then take the ring of the nervous large, until the tongue is dislocated from its place, and if there is pain or no, and this is due to a sudden wound, then put the hook and ring of the large, and keep that the cut does not become too perfect, because the artery is behind; and when you have done so, raise the water rose and thus, or cold water, then place on the tongue a piece of linen; and wash the sick person every night, so that the ring cannot close.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si met sor le leu vitriole broiet; et se li sans te vaint, si le cauterize au cautere lentiginout, qui est boin a ceu; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez,	And if the blood comes out, then sprinkle it with Vitriol; and if he does not go up, then cauterize it with the slow cauterizer, which is good for him; then cure it with other cures until it is healthy.
et se tu lou vois de fusse color ou noir ou dur, si que li malaides ne lou sent, si n’i touchier point, car c’est chancre; et s’il est declinans a blenchor, et il i a moistor, si i giete l’oncine, et lou fent d’un spatumile subtil, et lou delivre d’une part et d’autre; et se li sans te vaint a ton ovraige, si met sus vitriole broiet tant qu’il soit estainchiez, puis revien a ton ovraige tant que tu traies tout fuer; puis leve lou leu d’aisil et de seil, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see a dark or black or hard color, then the patient does not feel it, nor touch it, for it is cancer; and if it inclines towards bleached, and there is moisture, then pour the oncine, and make it with a thin scraper, and deliver it from one side and the other; and if he does not go up to your opening, then sprinkle it with Vitriol until it is stained, and then come back to your opening as long as you carry all of it; then raise its head in such a way and tie it, and cure it with other cures until it is healthy.
des apostemes de la gorge	of the throat abscesses
Aucune fois vient dedens la gorge boces qui sont apelees «godath», et les apele on proprement les II amandres, et quant tu les cures, si com nos avons dit en la division, et elles ne sont sanees, si pren garde: se c’est apostemes dur de petit sens et de fusse color, si ne lou touchier mie de fer.	of the throat abscesses come from within the throat, which are called "godath", and they are properly called "amandres"; and when you treat them, as we have said in the division, and they do not heal, be careful: if it is an abscess of small size and light color, do not touch it with iron.
Et s’il est rouges et li racine est grosse, si ne lou touchier mie de fer, ausi por lou decorrement de sanc; mais lou laisse tant qu’il soit meur, et adonques tu lou partiras, ou il rompirait par soi; et s’il est de blainche color reont, et li racine est subtilz, si aies apareilliet l’estrument por coper, mais regarde premierement se li apostemes chalz repose et est apaisiez.	If it is red and the root is large, do not touch it with iron either for fear of its pain or because it may rupture by itself; but if it is a white color, and the root is thin, then you will prepare the instrument to cover it, but first check if the abscess is hot and calm.
Adonques fai seoir lou malaide devant lou soleil, et ses chiés soit en ton sain, et li oevre la bouche et lou preigne li serjans entre ses mains, et presse la lengue desoz a tout l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme; et soit d’argent ou d’arain subtil ausi com uns coutelz:	Then you will make the patient sit in front of the sun, and his shoulders be at rest, and he opens the mouth and puts his tongue between his hands, and presses all the instrument on it, so that this is the form; and let it be of silver or of gold as fine as our knives:
Cant tu presses la lengue a tout cest estrument, et tu vois l’aposteme, si pren l’oncine et lou fiche en l’amandre, et la trai fuer au desus plus que tu pues; et trai aucune chose des toiles avec, puis la cope a l’estrument, de coi ci est li forme, que semble unes forces; et toutevoie li chief sont corbé, et l’un endroit l’autre, et sont molt agut, et est fait de fer inde ou d’andainne:	Press the tongue on all this instrument, and you will see the abscess, if take the hook and put it in amande, and go over it more than you can; and do not include any thread with it, then take off the instrument, for here is the form, which seems a strong force; and yet the heads are curved, and one place to another, and they are very acute, and are made of iron of where or of an iron:
Et se tu n’as cest estrument present, si lou cope as tenailles, de coi ci est li forme:	And if you do not have this instrument present, if you take off the cover with pliers, here is the form:
Et soit trenchans d’une part, et d’autre part nom; et quant tu as copeit l’une des amandres, si cope l’autre selonc cele meisme maniere, et aprés l’incision gargarize li malaides aigue chaude, et aigue et aisil, et se decorremens de sanc avient, si gargarize li malaides aigue, ou escorces de pomes grenates soient cuites, ou fuelles de mirte, et semblans choses, tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois naissent en la gorge autres apostemes que les II amandres, si les cope donques ensi com les II amandres igament.	And be sharpened on one side and the other; and when you have copped one of the mandibles, if you cop the other according to this same manner, and after the incision gargarize the patient with hot water, and often and easily, and let the blood come out if it comes up, then gargarize the patient with water or cooked pomegranate juice, or oak apples, and similar things, until the wound is healed; then cure it as long as it is healthy; and never let there be other abscesses in the throat than the two mandibles, if they are copped just like the two mandibles.
Et je medicinai une femme d’un aposteme que li estoit neis dedens la gorge, c’est a savoir I aposteme de petit sens; et avoit jai bien pres close toute la gorge, si que li femme ne pooit expirer por le conduit qui estoit estoupez, et ne pooit ne mengier ne boivre, et fust morte s’elle demorast ensi I jor ou II.	And I medicated a woman with an abscess that was growing inside her throat, that is to say, a small-sized abscess; and I had closed it up very tightly all around the throat, so that the woman could not breathe through the passageway that was obstructed, and she could not eat or drink, and she would have died if she had not recovered within a day or two.
Et li apostemes estoit jai si montez qu’il avoit fuer mis II rains par les II pertuis dou neis.	And the abscess was so raised that it had risen two inches on either side of the opening where it was growing.
Je hastai donques tantost, et fichai en l’un I oncine, puis lou traï fuers, et en traï grant porcion de bowe; puis refis autreteil en l’autre pertus dou neis, et li ovrai la bouche et li pressai la lengue; aprés fichai l’oncine en ces apostemes, et en copai une partie, et n’en issit fuers que un poc de sanc; et ensi fut destoupez li conduis de la gorge la femme, et comensa maintenant a boivre aigue et puis vin, et ne cessai de taillier de cel aposteme par lonc tens; et li apostemes recroissoit adés, et remplissoit lou leu que je avoie vuidiet, tant qu’il refut mout gros; adonques je l’engignai et lou cauterizai dedens la gorge: ensi demora sens croistre; et me partis de ces parties, et ne soi que Deus fist de li aprés moi.	I hastened and then pierced it with a needle on one side, and then cut it open, and then filled it up again with blood; and then I pierced another one in the opening where the abscess was growing, and pressed the tongue; after that, I filled the abscess with some of the blood, and at that point the passageway in the woman's throat became unblocked, and she began to drink and eat, and did not stop cutting out the abscess for a long time; and the abscess receded, and filled up the place that I had cleared out, until it became very big; then I sewed it up and cauterized it inside her throat: so it stayed still; and I left those parts behind me, and only God knows what happened to them afterwards.
de l’uve	of the eye
Quant reume dessent a l’uve, et elle est enflee et elle est longe, si est apelee «perpendiculaire»; et s’elle est desoz grosse et reonde, si est apelee «uve».	When the vomit comes out of the eye, and it is gone and far away, it is called "perpendicular"; and if it is big and round, it is called "eye".
Quant elle est curee si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, et tu vois que li chaus apostemes est apaisiez, et elle est subtilz, si covient que tu la copes; et celle qui est reonde assemblee et n’est mie longe; et elle est sanguine ou de fusse color ou noire, si covient que tu eschues l’incision de li.	When it is cured as we have said in the division, and the cure does not benefit, and you see that the cheek abscess is softened, and it is thin, then you should cut it; and that which is round and gathered together and is not far away; and it is bloody or of a brown color or black, then you should avoid the incision of it.
Car il i a grant peril sus lou malaide.	For there is great danger with the eye disease.
Il covient donques, quant tu la vois, selonc la maniere que j’ai dit, de sa blenchor et de sa longesce, que tu faices seoir le malaide devant lou soleil, et li presse la lengue a l’estrument dont nos avons fait la remembrance ci devant; puis fiche l’oncine en l’uve, et la trai desoz, et la cope a I des II estrumens que j’ai dit en l’incision des II amandres.	It therefore happens, when you see it, according to the way that I have said, because of its blueness and length, that you make the patient sit in front of the sun, and press his tongue to the instrument which we have mentioned above; then you put the oncine in the eye, and roll it up, and cut with the two instruments which I have said in the incision of the two mandibles.
Et covient que tu ne coper mie fuer que la superfluiteit qui est outre le termine natureil; car se tu en copes plus, si grieves a la voix, et a la parolle; et aprés l’incision, use de ceu que nos avons dit en l’incision des II amandres, et le cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And you must not cover more than the surplus that is beyond the natural term; for if you cover more, it will grieve the voice and the word; and after the incision, use what we have said in the incision of the two testicles, and cure until it is healthy.
Et se li malaides a paor dou coper, si covient que tu i use d’engien a la cauterization de li sens paor.	And if the patient has doubt about covering, then you must use fire cautery on the sensitive part.
Et li maniere dou cautere si est aigue ague.	And the way of fire cautery is sharp and bitter.
Et est que li malaides mette son chief en ton sain, et puis li presse la lengue a l’estrument que nos avons dit ou chapistre de cautere, et confis avec aigue vive chaus, si qu’elle ne soit mie trop espesse ne trop clere; et en emple le chevement de cest estrument, de coi ci est li forme:	And the patient should put his head in your lap, and then press his tongue on the instrument that we have said or fire cautery, and mix it with sharp and vivid water, so that it is not too thick nor too clear; and in using this instrument's shape, from which this name comes:
Et ait ou chief une cheveure ou om met la medecine, si com li chevemens d’une cuillier, et met l’estrument a tout la medicine sus l’uve; et li malaides soit gisans sus son costeit, si que li salive et li muscillaige corre de sa bouche de la medicine dedens, si qu’ele ne dessende a la gorge, et lou blece; puis tien ta main a tout la medicine et la presse sus l’uve, la quantiteit de la moitiet d’une houre, tant que tu la vois nercie et li mordications de la medicine soit apaisie; et se tu vues, pren coton et l’envoloupe sus aucun estrument, et moille lou coton en la medicine, et boute l’estrument a tout le couton en la cainne desus, tant que li coton s’aerde sus l’uve; et fai ceu sovent, tant que li cauteres soit parfais, puis la laisse elle seche, et chiet aprés IIII jors ou V Et se tu as mestier de rencomencier lou cautere de la medicine, si le rencomence, et aprés le cautere l’essue entor l’uve, de couton embut em burre, et mundifie ceu qui est entor de la medicine; et soit arosez d’aigue froide, et soit curez de gargarismes tant qu’il soit sanez.	And let there be a hair on one side of the head, where you will put the medicine, as if it were a spoonful of medicine, and place the instrument over all the medicine on the edge; and let the patient lie on his side, so that he spits out the medicine into the mouth from his throat, so that it does not go down to the throat and choke him; then take your hand from all the medicine and press it over the edge, a quarter of an hour, until you see it turn black and the medicine taste bitter; and if you need to freshen it, do so, and after the cautery, clean it out with warm water, of cotton wadded with water, and wash what is inside of the medicine; and let it be rinsed with cold water, and cure by gargling until it is well.
Ceste cure est plus save de l’incision, ne que li cautere; s’elle est curee de fumigation selonc ceste maniere, pren calament et ysope et origanum et rue et camomille et avronne et semblans herbes, et les assemble toutes ou aucunes d’eles en I pot, et i met aisil, et fai bullir; et li potz soit bien gluez de fort terre, et enmi le pot ait I estrument cheveit selonc ceste maniere:	This cure is more effective than incision or cauterization. If it is cured with fumigation according to this method, take calamus and hysope and oreganum and rue and chamomile and arnica and other herbs, all of which I put in a pot and then pour water on them easily, and make the water boil; and the pot should be well clamped with strong soil, and immerse the pot with a tool according to this method:
Et soit d’argent ou d’arain, et soit li uns des chiés boutez en la bouche dou malaide tant que li vapor monte a l’uve par la caine, tant que li uve soit mortifie; aprés lou rencomence sovent, tant que li uve seche, et garde que tu ne faices ceu au comencement de l’avenement de l’aposteme chaut, car plusors choses i avienent; et ne faire mie ceu fuer que a la declination d’aposteme chaut.	It should be of silver or gold, and let one of the shoulders be inserted into the mouth of the patient until the vapor rises from the vein through the tube until the vein is constricted; then start again frequently, until the vein dries up, and be careful not to do this at the beginning of the arrival of the abscess, for many things can happen; and do not do it except at the decline of the abscess.
Et se cist estrument n’est presens, si pren une caine et met dedens lou chief une craiffe d’uef, si que li bouche au malaide n’ait mie trop chaut; car li craiffe d’uef ne lait mie la vapor grever la bouche, et c’est bone cure ensamble salut.	And if this instrument is not present, then take a dog and put a stick of honey in the mouth of the patient so that it does not get too hot; for the stick of honey will not cause great heat in the mouth, and this is good treatment together with healing.
Maintes fois s’aert a la gorge os ou espinee de poisson, ou aucune chose; si covient donc que tu traies ceu que tu pues veoir, et li presse la lengue au soleil a tout l’estrument, si que tu voies mues la chose; et ceu que ne t’apert mie et est reponus en la gorge, covient que tu faices vomir le malaide ainsois que li viande soit cuite en l’estomac; par aventure si istra li chose aerse par le vomissement; ou li malaides englutisse une piece d’esponge, ou une piece de navel, ou une racine de laitue, ou I morceil de pain sec; et lie a l’esponge I fil, et puis la transglutisse; et quant elle venra au leu, si s’aerdra, et puis trairas fuer; et s’elle ne vient fuer de ceu que nos avons dit, si pren I estrument de plonc selonc ceste forme:	Often times a bone or fish spine comes out of the mouth, or nothing at all; so it is necessary that you draw out what you can see, and press the tongue to the sun with the whole instrument, so that you can see the object; and if what is not drawn out by you is stuck in the throat, it is necessary that you induce vomiting so that the meat is cooked in the stomach; perhaps the object will be vomited up; or the patient will swallow a piece of sponge, or a piece of navel, or a lettuce root, or a slice of dry bread; and you tie the sponge to a string, and then make him swallow it; and when it comes to the place, if it comes out, you draw it out strongly; and if it does not come out by what we have said, then take an instrument of plunk according to this form:
Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu’il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l’epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l’os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l’estrument, por ceu qu’il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l’estrument igalment, tant qu’elle soit fuer.	Et soit li estrumens corbés au chief si qu'il puist plus legierement entrer en la gorge, et ait le chief en haut leveit; et warde que tu ne touchier l'epiglote, que li tous ne li viegne, ne ne bouter mie l'os dedens; et mues vaut que li malaides i boute l'estrument, por ceu qu'il seit mues ou li chose est aerse; si la boute aval, ou il la traie fuer a tout l'estrument igalment, tant qu'elle soit fuer.
de la sansue de la gorge	And make the instrument curved at the tip so that it can enter the throat more easily, and raise the chief [larynx] higher; and be careful not to touch the epiglottis, or else the sound will be blocked, nor should you prod the bone within; and make sure that the patient swallows the instrument, for in doing so he will feel relief or pain; if the fluid is swallowed, or if it is drawn out of the instrument evenly, then let it go.
Aucune fois est medicinee li sansue, si com j’ai dit en la division, par la cure de medicines; et quant ceu ne profite mie, adonques regarde en la gorge dou malaide au soleil, puis que tu li presses la lengue a l’estrument que je t’ai dit.	In no case is medicine effective in this [disease], as I have said in the division of remedies; and when it does not benefit, then look at the throat of the patient under the sun, since you press the tongue towards the instrument that I have told you.
Et se tu vois la sansue, si la trai a tout I petit uncine, ou as tenailles subtilz que valent a ceu.	And if you see the blood, if it runs with a small hook, or with tiny claws that go under him.
Et se ceu ne vaut, si pren une caine chevee, et la boute en la gorge dou malaide, puis boute ou chevement de la caine I fer chaut, et fai ce sovent.	And if he doesn't respond, take a dog's chain, and pour it into the throat of the patient, then pour or pour from the chain's iron, and do this often.
Et se teigne li malaides d’aigue toute jor.	And if the patient's blood is very hot every day.
puis pren plein I voirre d’aigue froide, et oevre la bouche, et la giete ens sens englutir, et la mueve a sa main sovent; et si tost com li sansue sent l’aigue, si chiet.	then take a full cup of cold water, and close the mouth, and pour it into him to swallow, and move it with his hand often; and if soon as the blood feels the cold, spit it out.
Et s’elle ne chiet si com nos avons dit, si subfumige lou malaide d’asefetide, a l’estrument que j’ai dit en la fumigation de l’uve; fai ceu maintes fois, car elle cherra sens targier.	And if it doesn't spit like we've said, then suffocate the patient with the ash of the plant that I mentioned in the smoke treatment of the wound; do this many times, because it will no longer be able to spit.
Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.	Et li maniere de la fumigation si est que tu preignes I pot ou il ait charbons vis, et soit li pos covert d’un coverseil perciet en mileu, et en celui pertus soit li chiés de l’estrument; puis i giete ta fumigation, et li malaides mette lou chief de la cainne en sa bouche, et cloie la bouche, si que li fumee n’en isse mie, mais viegne jusc’a la sansue; et la sansue cherra maintenant, et s’elle ne chiet, si rencomence la fumigation par maintes fois; et soffre li malaides soif, et menjuce choses salees et als, et ne boive point d’aigue; et adonques li iert mestier qu’elle isse fuer par cest governement.
Et li forme de l’estrument a coi on trait la sansue, si est, quant on la puet veoir, semblans a tenailles corbés por mues entrer en la gorge; et ait semblance au bec de soigne, et i ait asperiteit de lime, si que ceu qu’elle prent, elle ne puet lassier; et vez ci la forme:	And the shape of the instrument is such that one can treat the throat, as it appears to be similar to pliers used for holding things in place, with a shape resembling a curbed nail, and it has a roughness like lime, so that whatever it grabs onto does not release; and here is the description:
li chapistres des apostemes	the chapter of abscesses
Mout de semblances d’aposteme sont, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient ci aprés d’un et d’autre en cest livre, et sont diver en perforation et en taille; et c’est en II manieres dont l’une est en sa semblance meisme, et de ceu qu’il tient moistor.	The mouth of an abscess is, according to what this memory comes from a and the other in this book, and are two ways; which one is in its own semblance, and the other is because it has moisture.
Et li seconde maniere si est por les leus ou il sont au cors.	The second way is for the joints where they are on the body.
car li apostemes dou chief est autres que cil dou fondement, et li apostemes dou leu charnut est autres que cil qui vient en jointures, et chescuns ait son jugement en l’uevre.	For the abscess at the top is different from that at the root, and the abscess at the shoulder joint is different from those that come in joints, and each has its own judgment in the work.
Et si a apostemes c’on ne doit mie percier, tant que li bowe est meure selonc son acomplissement; et si a de telz qu’il covient percier quant il sont crut, et ne meurent mie selonc lor acomplissement, si com aposteme qui sont delez jointures.	And if there are abscesses that should not be pierced, as long as the bow is dead according to its course; and if they are of those that should be pierced when they are ripe, and do not die according to their course, as in the case of an abscess at a delusive joint.
Car quant apostemes vient delez jointures, et on le laisse tant qu’il est porris entor, par aventure si sont corrumput li liien et li nerf de la jointure, par coi ce est cause de contraction en celui membre.	For when abscesses come out of the joints, and are left until they rot within, for fear that if the ligament and nerve of the joint are corrupted, then this is a cause of contraction in that member.
Ou li aposteme est delez lou membre principel, et se tu tardes la perforation tant qu’il soit meurez, si nuira au membre principeil; ou il est delez lou fondement, si le perce on ainsois qu’il soit meurs; et ne covient mie que tu perces aposteme crut sens digestion acomplie, fuers que celui qui est delez lou fondement, qu’il ne porrisse em parfont, et soit alongiez dedens, et i viegne fistule; et ne puisse saner en grant termine.	If the abscess is removed from the main member, and you delay perforation until it is dead, then it will harm the main member; or if it is removed from the foundation, so that it is pierced in such a way that it may die completely without healing, so that it does not corrode completely, and it stays inside, and comes to fistula; and cannot heal well.
Et covient que tu saiches l’oure de la perforation de l’aposteme qui est meur selonc l’acomplissement, et c’est quant li dolor est apaisie, et li departemens de la fievre, et l’amenuisement de la dolor et de la roujor, et dou debatement et de l’aguisement dou chief de l’aposteme, et les autres signes; et covient que tu faices seoir la perforation ou plus dependant leu de l’aposteme, et la ou il apert mues; et soit li perforation dou lonc dou cors, et se li apostemes est as mains ou as piez, ou en jointures et au ners et as arteres, et en toz leus igalz ou il n’a point de ploieure.	And you must know the time for the perforation of the abscess which is dead according to completion, and that is when the pain is eased, and the departure of fever, and the decrease of pain and rash, and the sharpening of the tip of the abscess, and the other signs; and it is necessary that you make the perforation where there is most hair, or where it opens, or along the course, and let the perforation run long through the whole body, and be at a distance from the abscess, and from the main roots, and the nerves, and all over the body in even places, where there is no pimp.
En ces que ploient, par selonc celui membre.	In these cases, according to which limb.
Et quant apostemes est en leu charnut, si vaut mues que tu laisses la perforation tant qu’il soit confermez en digestion acomplie, si com nos avons dit.	And when abscesses are in a raised state, if you allow the piercing to remain until it is completely cured, as we have said.
Car se tu lou perces devant ceu, si iert alongiez li cors dou venim de lui, et est plains de mout d’ordure; et par aventure endurcissent les levres et li parfondetez de lui.	For if you pierce it before this, if you allow the body to remain extended in the air of his, and is full of dirty mucus; and by chance hardens the lips and deepens him.
Et si a aucun aposteme que sont perciet selonc le large dou cors, selonc ceu que li membres en ait mestier.	And if any abscess that are pierced according to the breadth of the body, according to which the members have need.
Et covient que tu amenistres em petis apostemes, petis pertus; et en grans apostemes, grans pertus, et maintes fendures selonc la semblance de la grandor de l’aposteme; et si a de tels apostemes ou il covient chever lou keur, et coper; quant il est jai devenus ausi com I drapelz, et est amortis, si covient faire ausi com on fait as bubes: et si a de telz que sont fendut en III angles, et si a de telz dont on cope ausi com la fuelle de mirte, si com apostemes des angres; et si a de telz ou on fait une reonde taille, et autres tailles et semblant copeure.	And you must bring small abscesses, small punctures; and in large abscesses, large punctures, and many slits according to the appearance of the size of the abscess; and if there are such abscesses that they need to be chewed and sealed up: when they have become as thin as drapes, and are softened, do so as you do with bubbles: and if there are any that are split in three directions, and if there are any that you cover as with a fern leaf, like abscesses of the angles; and if there are any that need to be cut into a circle, and other cuts and looks like they have been sealed up.
Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.	Cil qui n’ont point de chief, si com aposteme souef superficial, il covient que tu lou perces plainnement; et covient quant li apostemes est gros, et il a coillit grant bowe, et tu lou perces, si ne traire mie toute la bowe en celle houre, mais en trai une partie; puis estoupe l’aposteme jusc’a l’autre jor, puis en trai aucune chose derechief; fai ceu par maintes fois de greit en greit, tant que li bowe isse toute; meismement se li malaides est de foible vertut, ou femme portans, ou petis enfes, ou viez hons decrepites.
Car li esperis tressaut aucune fois avec l’issue de la bowe, que par aventure muert li malaides, et tu ne t’en persois.	Those who do not have a head, like an abscess on the skin, it is necessary that you pierce it clearly; and it is necessary when the abscess is large, and has a great bulge, and you pierce it, if you do not draw out all of the bulge at once, but only part of it; then stop the abscess until the next day, then draw out nothing more; do this many times from one heavy to the next, until the bulge is completely gone; however, it is a weak person, or a woman carrying, or small children, or old men decrepit.
Eschuez donques cest chapistre par grant cautele, et quant tu as perciet ton aposteme, si essue la plaie, et regarde se li plaie de l’aposteme est petite; et se c’est une tailleure plainne, si amenistre tentes de lin ou de viez coton; et se c’est uns grans apostemes, et il i a mout de pertus, si covient que tu boutes en chescun une tente si qu’ele viegne l’une contre l’autre; et se tu as copeit en l’aposteme une partie dou cuir, et tu l’as cheveit entor, si covient que tu l’emplisses de viel couton ou de rasure de dras de lin sens moistor, et le lie jusc’au tier jor; puis l’oste, et le cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	ESCHuez donc cette chapistre avec grand soin, et quand tu as percé ton apopléi, si essuie la plaie, et regarde si la plaie de l'apopléi est petite; et si c'est une plaie simple, alors met-y des bandages de lin ou de vieux coton; et si c'est un apopléi gros, et il y a beaucoup d'écoulement, alors il convient que tu fasses entrer dans chacun une tente de telle sorte qu'elles viennent l'une contre l'autre; et si tu as enroulé dans l'apopléi une partie du cuir, et tu l'as enduit avec du lin ou de la paille de drôle de lin humide, et le lies jusqu'au troisième jour; puis l'os, et le guérit avec de l'ongement jusqu'à ce qu'il soit guéri.
Et se decorremens de sanc avient a ton ovraige, si amenistre aigue froide et aisil, et moille I drapeil, et met sor le leu decorrant par maintes fois.	And if the pain comes to your head, then bring cold water and quickly, and wet the sheet, and put it on the place where it is hurting many times.
Et se li decorremens de sanc persevere, se i amenistre governement et cure, et les poudres que j’ai dit em mains leus en cest livre, et se c’est ou tens d’iver, et li leus ou li apostemes est est mout nervous, si couvient que tu mettes sus tentes et drapelz moilliez en vin et en oile chaut; et se c’est en esteit, et li leus est charnus, si covient que tu mes sus drapelz moilliez en aigue et en oile, ou en vin et en oile froit, jusc’au tier jor, si com nos avons dit; et puis deslie l’aposteme et l’essue et le cure, si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the pain persists, then bring government and treatment, and the powders that I have said to put in the ears in this book, and if it is a bad ear, and the ear where the aposteme is is nervous, know that you should put on beds and sheets wet with wine and oil warm; and if it is an inner ear, and the ear is fleshy, then know that you should put on sheets wet with water and oil, or with wine and cold oil for three days, as we have said; and then dry the aposteme and wash and treat it, as it should be, until he is healthy.
Et ceu covient il conoistre universement en cures des apostemes: or vos ai dit coment on doit aler avant as cures des apostemes, et vez ci le chapistre.	And this is something that must be known universally in the treatment of abscesses; but I have told you how one should go about treating abscesses, and here is the paste.
des soros	abces
Ou keur dou chief vienent petis apostemes, et sont manieres de nous que sont en toiles, ausi com li josier d’une geline, et mout en i a de semblances.	Or treat the head of the shoulder so that small abscesses are created, and they are treated in such a way that they are like webs, as with the knee of a gown, and many have similar appearances.

Car s’il contient moistor, si lou fent par desus dou lonc.	For if it contains moisture, if it flows from above the long way.
Et quant li moistor est vuidie, si escorche sens rien laissier la peil qui contient celle moistor, car il revient adés quant on i laisse rien; puis plonge coton en oignement egiptien, s’il est presens; se ceu non, en aigue et en seil, et en emple la plaie, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor; et ceu corront ceu qui est demorez dou nit.	Et when the moisture is empty, if you do not leave the hair that contains this moisture, for it returns to its place when you leave nothing; then dip cotton in Egyptian oil, if it is present; and if it is not, in water and linseed, and apply to the wound, and leave until the next day; and let those who are delayed go on.
Et pues rencomence lou coton, si com devant, le second jor, et lou tier, tant que tu saiches bien qu’il ne demoure point dou nit; puis cure la plaie d’oignement a ceu convenauble, tant qu’il soit sanez.
