And when the cotton begins again on the second day, and the oil, as long as you know that it does not remain in place from the night; then cure the wound with ointment suitable for this, until it is healthy.
Et se li apostemes tient I nout gras, si le cope selonc ceste forme, dou lonc; et i giete tes oncines, et l’escorche de toutes pars, et met toute ta cure de traire fuer la cotte ou il gist; et se li artere te fait contraire, si fai ceu que je t’ai dit aprés.	And if the abscess holds a lot of pus, if the wound is shaped like this, then cut off your hair, and burn it all over, and apply all your cure to treat the patch where it is; and if the artery does not go well, do what I have told you after.
Et ausi fai de l’aposteme s’il est pierous, et dou taillier et dou curer si com je t’ai dit.	And so you make the abscess if it is painful, and the barber's and doctor's tools as I have told you.
Et li taille sus l’aposteme pierous et le moiste, si est plus legiere, car il sont de poc de sanc.	And cut on the painful abscess and the wet one, for it is lighter in blood loss.
Et si a aucuns de ces apostemes ou chief ou il n’a point de moistor, et de ces fut I apostemes que je copai ou chief d’une vielle femme; et trovai l’aposteme ausi com une piere xourde, aspre et blainche, et ne pooit brisier; et s’on en eust ferut aucun, on li eust ausi bien fait plaie com d’une piere.	And if any of these abscesses or knots do not have moisture, and the same for those that I struck with an old woman's head; and I found the abscess as a heavy, sharp, and bleached stone, which could not be broken; and had there been any of them, it would have made the same wound as a stone.
En autres apostemes venans ou chief, fuer que ces qui vienent as chief des enfans et as racines des oreilles, li overture si soit toz jors au plus dependant leu, por mues issir la bowe; et les cure si com il covient.	In other abscesses that come out of the head, it should be that those that come out of children' s heads and roots of ears, the opening should always remain dependent, so that the bow can be taken out; and they are treated as needed.
des scrophules	of the scrofula
Maintes fois avienent cist aposteme au col, et desoz les asseles, et ens angres, et aucune fois vienent autre part ou cors, et sont mout, et sont enjanrees l’une avec l’autre.	Many times have there been abscesses in the throat, and they drain, and cause pain, and do not go to any other place or heal, and are rotten, and one is infected with another.
Et chescune scrophule est proprement dedens sa cote, si com li nout et li aposteme dou chief, si com nos avons dit; et les semblances de ces scrophules sont maintes.	And each scrofula is properly inside its rib, as the puss and the abscess of the throat, as we have said; and the appearances of these scrofulas are many.
Il i a de teles que contienent moistor, et si a de malignes qui ne vuellent obeir a santeit.	There are some that contain moisture, and there are others that do not want to obey health.
en celle donques que tu vois de bone disposition au tochier, et est semblans a la color dou cors, et muet de chescune part et n’est mie aerse as ners dou col ne a l’artere ne au conduit, et n’est mie parfonde; si covient que tu la copes par desus, et l’escorche de chescune partie, et estent les II levres dou keur as oncines, se tu en as mestier, si com nos avons dit en apostemes dou chief; et la trai poc et poc, et soies seur que tu ne coper lou nerf ne la voine, et ne soit mie li spatumile agus ne trenchans, que li mains n’eschaipe, et ne voise trop avant, que tu ne coper mie ceu que tu ne dois.	In that one which you see of good disposition in the throat, and is the color of the body, and does not move from any side nor is it deep; if it is that you cut it above, and scorch each part, and are the two lips of the mouth on either side, if you need it, as we have said in the abscess of the throat; and grind little by little, and be sure that you do not touch the nerve or the vein, and do not let it escape, nor go too far forward, that you do not cut what you should.
Et se tu copes la voinne ou l’artere, et ceu ne te laisse ovrer, si met en la plaie vitriole broiet, ou aucunes poudres que restainchent sanc, et estraint la plaie; et la laisse tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et soit amollie li plaie, et encomence a porrir.	And if you cut the vein or the artery and it does not let you sew, then put vitriol brooch on it, or some powders that stop the blood, and extract the wound; and leave it until the abscesses are calmed down and the wound is softened, and begin to rot.
Et quant li sans est estainchiez, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que tu l’acomplisses; puis quier a ton doit indice s’il i demoure nules petites scrophules, si les cope et les munde.	And when the blood has stopped, if you return to your work, as long as you finish it; then examine your index finger for any small pustules, if they are there, cut them and clean them out.
Et s’il a en la racine de la scrophule voinne grant, si ne covient mie que tu copes celle scrophule en sa racine, mais la lie d’un fil double fort, et la laisse cheoir par li, sens nuisement; puis emple la plaie de viel coton plongiet en oignement egiptien, puis la cure.	And if it has a big vein of the scar in its root, then it is not convenient that you cut this scar at its root, but tie it with a strong double thread, and let it hang by itself, without harm; then employ a wound with wet cotton dipped in Egyptian wax, then cure it.
Et se tu copes toute la scrophule, si covient que tu assembles les II levres de la plaie, et les cout maintenant, puis qu’il n’i a point demoreit de superfluiteit por la grandor de la scrophule.	And if you catch the whole plague, it is necessary that you join together the two lips of the wound, and sewed them up, so that there is no delay from the abundance of the plague.
si covient que tu entendes a coper la racine de li, et traire fuer, et la cout si com nos avons dit.	it is necessary that you hear to cover the root of it, and draw it out with force, and sew it up as we have said.
Celles scrophules que tienent superfluiteit, perce lai ou il apert meure; et la perce ensi com celle devant dite, en dependant, puis i amenistre tentes avec oignement et semblans choses, si qu’elle corrompe ceu qui est demorez de la corruption; et quant li plaie est bien mundee, si la cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Those scrofulae that have abundance, pierce them where they open; and pierce them thus, as that which has been said before, depending on it, then add tentes with care and similar things, so that it corrupts that which is delayed from corruption; and when the wound is well cleaned, then cure it with ointment, adding a covering.
de squinance	of squint
Li ancien dirent et parlerent de la tailleure de la gorge; mais je ne vis onques en nostre terre qui la feist, et c’est li escripture de lor parole.	the old people talked about the making of a throat; but I never saw one made in our land, and it is the scriptural word of their speech.
A ces qui ont squinance, il covient que li fendure de la gorge qui est apelee «epiglote» soit eschuee; et c’on ne faice aide par ceu, por ceu que toutes les voines et li pormon dou malaide sont a ces qui ont aposteme chaut en la bouche, ou en la gorge ou en II amandres.	For those who have squint, it is necessary that the slit in the throat which is called the epiglottis be removed; and because of this, no help should be sought from him, since all the veins and the blood of the sick person are at those who have an abscess warm in the mouth, or in the throat or in the two mandibles.
Quant li maladie est en la chenal dou pormon, il covient coper l’epiglote por fuir la perdition qui vient de l’estranglement.	When the patient is in the throat channel, it is necessary to cover the epiglottis to prevent the danger that comes from strangulation.
Il covient donques, quant nos volons fendre l’epiglote, que nos le fendons desoz III cercles ou IIII une petite fendure dou travers, entre les II cercles ou par la quantiteit de la fendure dou syfac, ne mie en la cartillaige; et cil leus si est covenaubles a la section de l’epiglote qu’il n’i a point de char, et li vasseil sont lonc d’enqui.	It is therefore necessary, when we want to split the epiglottis, that we split it with three circles or four small slits from one side to the other, between the two circles or by the quantity of the slit made with a knife, not on the cartilage; and if this is convenient for splitting the epiglottis so that there is no charred part, and the vessel is long of it.
Et se li maistres est paourous, si covient qu’il estende le cuir de la gorge a tout l’oncine, puis fende lou keur tant qu’il viegne a la cheneil; et eschue les vasselz de sanc, se tu vois aucune chose, et puis cope lou syfac, si com nos avons dit; et est demostrez par la section dou fleume de la cheneil ki saut fuer par le leu qui est rompus, et par la defaute de la voix; et laisse la plaie overte une piece.	And if the master is afraid, then it is necessary that he extends the skin of the throat to its entire length, and then splits the larynx as far as it comes to the windpipe; and avoid the veins of blood, if you see nothing, and then cover the wound with a salve, as we have said; and is demonstrated by the section of the flow of the larynx that jumps out by the hole that is broken, and by the failure of the voice; and leave the wound open for a while.
Et quant li houre est passee de coi on doute l’estranglement, assemble les II levres de la plaie dou keur, et la cout toute soule sens la cartillaige; puis aministre medicines qui font naistre char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the hour has passed by which one doubts strangulation, gather the two lips of the wound together, and the whole tongue under the cartilage; then administer drugs that cause char, until it is healed.
Albucasim dist c’on ne faice ce jusc’a tant que li gorge est toute estoupee, et li malaides est jugiez a mort, et li defaut li alaine.	Albucasis says: 'Do not make this cut until the throat is completely closed up, and the patient is judged to be dead, and the fault leaves it.'
Adonques cope on l’epiglote por ceu que li malaides ne puet alener, et il respire par la plaie, et ensi est gardez de mort; et por ce commanderent li anciain a laissier la plaie overte tant que li malice de la maladie soit passee, et elle est passee en III jors ou en IIII Et adonques il comanderent a coudre la plaie et curer, tant qu’elle fut curee; et je vos dirai ceu que je vis.	And then take hold of the epiglottis because the patient cannot raise it, and he breathes through the wound, and so he is kept from dying; and for the command of the elder to leave the wound open until the malice of the disease has passed, and it has passed in three days or four. And then he commanded that the wound be sewn up and healed, until it was healed; and I will tell you what I saw.
Je vis que une damoisele prist I coutel, et le ficha en sa gorge, et copa partie des chenelz dou pormon; et je fui apelez por li curer, et la trovai ausi com morte.	I saw that a damsel took a knife, and put it in her throat, and cut part of the windpipe; and I was called to heal her, and I found her as if dead.
Je descovris la plaie, et trovai le sanc qui en estoit issus, et soi bien qu’elle n’avoit mie copeit voine ne conduit fuer que la gorge, et li vens issoit fuer par la plaie.	I discovered the wound, and found the blood that had issued from it, and I saw well that it had not been cut open by a vein or an artery but was coming out through the throat, and the veins were going out through the wound.
Je me hastai, et cousi la plaie, et la curai tant qu’elle fut sanee; et n’avint a la damoisele fuer qu’elle fut roge de voix, et revint aprés a sa disposition; por ceu di je que en la tailleure de l’epiglote n’ait mie paour.	I hastened, and sewed up the wound, and healed it until it was healed; and there came to the maid only that she became red in voice, and returned after her disposition; for this I say that in the tailoring of the epiglottis there should be no fear.
de la grosse gorge	of the large throat
Cist apostemes est apelez «hernie de gorge», et est uns grans apostemes en color d’une jaisse, et est molt en femmes; et est selonc II manieres: naturez, et accidens; ou natureil n’a point d’engien.	The apostemi is called "hernia of the throat", and it is a large aposteme of a yellow color, and it is common in women; and there are two ways: natural and accidental; but there is no mechanism for natural ones.
Et li accidens est selonc II manieres, de coi l’une est semblans a gras nous, et li autre maniere est semblans a aposteme qui vient de nous d’artere; et il i ait paour, et ne covient mie ovrer de feir fuers que en celi qui est petite, et le prueve et cerche a tout l’intromissoire: se tu le trueves ausi com I nout gras, et ne pent a nulle voine, si le cope, si com on cope les nous, et le trai a tout sa coife, s’il en i a point; et encerche bien tot, et le cure si com il covient, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	And the accidental is according to two ways, of which one is similar to fatty tissue and the other is similar to an aposteme that comes from us through the arteries; and there is fear, and it does not seem right to operate without first proving and searching in all the interior: if you find it like this, as I do with fatty tissue, and you cannot remove any at all, if it curls up and traps itself, cut it off thoroughly so that it is completely healed.
des nous	of us
Maintes manieres de nous sont, dont je dirai toutes les semblances; et or covient que je die toute la difference qui est entre nout et issue.	There are many ways to describe ourselves, which I will now outline; and it is necessary that I make the distinction between our nature and its manifestation.
Je dis que issue est chalors et fievre tenans, tant que li ebulicions est passee, et est acomplie li porriture; adonques repose li fievre et li chalor.	I say that fever and chills persist until the sweating has passed, and the perspiration is complete; then the fever and the chill subside.
Avec lou nout n’a ne chalor ne fievre ne dolor, et contient I syfac, qui est ses propres sac et est selonc la color dou cors, et encomence ausi com une jaisse, et devient gros; et sont selonc ij semblances, ou grais, ou moiste, et mout de color sont si com j’ai dit en la division.	With our nature, there is neither fever nor chill nor pain, and we are dry, which matches the color of the body, and it begins as a seed and becomes larger; and it corresponds to the appearance, whether thin or fat, and its color is very different from that which I have described in the division.
Il covient, quant tu viens a la cure dou nout, que tu esprueves et l’enquier premierement a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «entromissoire», selonc ce que sa forme venra ou chapistre qui est aprés.	When you come to the treatment of our nature, you must first test and inquire about all the instruments that are called "entromissoire", according to what their shape may be or the paste that follows it.
Et li maniere de l’inquisicion des apostemes des nous est que tu preignes ou plus moiste leu que tu trueves en l’aposteme, et torne tes dois poc et poc, tant que tu saiches que li estrumens ait perciet le keur, puis que ce soit selonc la grandor de l’aposteme; puis estrai l’entromissoire, et pren garde en ceu que saut fuer.	And the way of inquiry for abscesses is that you squeeze the most moist place that you find in the abscess, and turn your hands little by little until you feel that the instrument has bitten into it, then, depending on the size of the abscess; then remove the inserter, and be careful to not break it.
Se moistor corrans cort, queil color elle ait, si le fent si com j’ai dit des autres apostemes; et se aprés l’entromissoire nen vient moistor, saiches qu’il est gras, si le fent donques en croix, et le prent as pinceures, et l’escorche legierement de chescune part et warde la cotte ou il gist que tu la traies saine avec le nout; et se tu ne la pues traire saine, si la trai par pieces si qu’il n’i demoure rien.	If the running water is strong, that it be colored, then do the same as I have said for other abscesses; and if after the inserter comes no moisture, know that it is fatty, so then do it in a cross way, and take it with tweezers, and peel it lightly from each side and guard the cotton where it lies so that you take it sound with the thread; and if you cannot take it sound, then take it by pieces so that nothing stays.
Car s’il i demoure rien, si revient li nous par maintes fois; et s’il en demore un poc, et li sans te grieve, si emple la plaie d’aucunes poudres corrosives agues, et estraint la plaie, et met sus choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li nous est grans, si cout les II levres de la plaie, et le cure de ceu qui enjanre char.	For if he does not wait at all, he returns to us many times; and if he waits a little, and does not cause you pain, then employ the wound with some corrosive powders of water, and extract the wound, and put on soothing ointment of chilipe, and cure it with other cures as long as it is healthy; and if we have great pain, then count the two lips of the wound, and cure that which causes the pain.
et se li voine batans t’est contraire ou autre si te haste et emple le leu de vitriole broiet, et lou laisse liiet II jors ou III, tant que li plaie porrisse, et repose li ebulicion dou sanc; puis revien au coper ceu que i est demoreit dou nout.	And if the head is turned against you or another thing, and you hurry and employ the place of vitriolic acid, and leave it for II days or III, until the wound is rotten, and rest the burning of blood; then return to what was delayed from the outside.
Vez ci les formes des estrumens entromissoires, et sont de III manieres: grans et moien et petit; et s’en i a III quarrez qui sont apelez «albaret», et I qui est apelez «breb», et s’en i a de III manieres: grant, moien, et petit, por encerchier les apostemes de fistule; et sont ausi com les aguilles dont on cout les sorceles, et sont d’arain citrin, ou de fer, ou d’argent, et mues valent cil qui sont jaune, et sont plus esprovez de plonc noir por encerchier les corbeures de fistule; et sont de III manieres: grans, moiens, et petis, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce des pertus.	See here the forms of instruments that are inserted, and they are of three manners: large and small and very small; and if there are III quarters which are called "albaret", and I which is called "breb", and they are also like the needles from which they cut sorceresses, and they are of brass yellow, or iron, or silver, and they move those that are yellow, and they are more proven by black mud to encircle the fists of fistulas; and they are of three manners: large, small, and very small, according to the quantity of the largeness of the apertures.
Les formes des oncines sont de mout de semblances, si com tu vois ci: grans, moiens, et petis; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures de III manieres ausi; et si a oncines qui ont III corbeures, et sont ausi de III manieres; et si a oncines qui ont II corbeures, et oncines d’une corbeure soulement, et sont de III manieres; et tuit cist sont necessaire en lor leu.	The shapes of scabs are of many appearances, as you see here: big, small, and medium-sized; and if the scabs have two or three folds in this way; and if the scabs have three folds, and are also of three ways; and if the scabs have two folds, and only one fold, and are also of three ways; and all of these are necessary in their places.
Li chief de ces a coi on fent sont trenchant, et de telz i a qui ne taillent mie fuer que d’une part, dont on escorche les nous, por ceu c’on ne cope la voine ne le nerf; et de ces intromissoires sont les alemeles reponues en mainches, si que li malaide ne s’en persoivent a l’overture des apostemes; et sont de III manieres: grant, petit, et moien, si com tu vois; et n’en use on mie fuer que en leu charnut, si com jambes, et bras, et mameles, et as angres, et en semblans leus; et aucune fois fait on I autre estrument petit, semblant a escorces de fistices, selonc ceste forme, a coi on estainche sanc:	The edges of these are sharp, and some of them do not cut more than one side, from which we scrape the flesh so that the vein or nerve is not cut; and these intermediate ones have many folds, so that the patient does not lose blood at the opening of the abscesses; and they are of three ways: large, small, and medium-sized, as you see here; and we only use one in the place of flesh, like legs, arms, breasts, elbows, and similar places; and we never make any other instrument smaller than these, which look like scabs of fists, according to this form, so that we do not cut blood:
et le met on aucune fois au leu qui saine a copement des voines, et as arteres, et aucune fois reont selonc ceste grant forme:	and put it on no more than once to the place that heals with a comb of veins, and arteries, and never according to this great form:
Aucune fois enflent les mameles d’aucuns homes quant cil encomencent estre corrumput, tant qu’eles semblent mameles de feme; et demorent laides et enflees, et qui les vuet curer, si le covient soier selonc ceste forme des ceste ligne .b. jusques a .g.:	No more than once do you inflame the breasts of some men when they begin to corrumpt, as if they were breasts of a woman; and they remain swollen and enlarged, and who must cure them, so it is useful according to this form of this line .b. until g:
puis escorche la graisse, et emple la plaie de medicine enjanrant char, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie a costure, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee; et se li mamele cline aval, et est amolie por sa grandor si com il avient as femmes, si la fent en II costelz desus, par II semblans fendures; de coi l’une soit tenans a l’autre a la fin de l’une et de l’autre, si que li plus grans ligne conteigne la menor selonc ceste forme, des ceste ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.; puis escorche le cuir qui est entre les II levres, et oste la graisse, et i amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de costure et de poudres, et ceu qui est necessaire en la cure, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, ou li incision n’est mie toute faite, por ceu que li malaides ne vuet reposer, ou por le decorrement de sanc, si covient que tu emplisses la plaie de coton moilliet en oignement corrosif; et le laisse tant qu’il menjuce le remenant et la graisse, puis le cure tant qu’il soit saneis.	Then skin the fat, and apply medicine to the wound by scraping, then join the two lips of the wound together with sutures, and cure it until it is well; and if it does not heal or if the incision is not completely made, so that the patient cannot rest, or for the blood loss, then you must fill the wound with moistened cotton soaked in corrosive ointment; and leave it until the remaining fat and flesh are gone, and then cure it until it is well.
des apostemes des asselles	of the abscesses of the buttocks
Cist apostemes que vienent desoz les asseles sont manieres de scrophules dures ou il ait cotes, et s’en i a que contienent moistor.	which come from sore buttocks are managed like hard scrofula or if it has ribs, and if there is only one that contains moisture.
Cil donques qui contienent moistor covient qu’il soient copez selonc ceste forme, des la ligne .b. jusc’a la ligne .g.:	So those that contain moisture must be cut according to this form, from line. b. up to line. g.:
Et quant toute li bowe qui est en l’aposteme est vuidie, si emple la plaie de viel coton, et la laisse jusc’a l’autre jor, puis oste tout le coton, et cure d’oignement avenant a ceu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when all the bowels that are in the abscess are empty, then plug the wound with wet cotton and leave it until the next day, then remove all the cotton, and treat with ointment as soon as it is healthy.
Et se li apostemes est de semblances de scrophules, si le fent si com nos avons dit en fendures des scrophules, et se li plaie rent bowe, si amenistre cautere si com nos avons dit devant.	And if the abscess is like scrofula, then cut it as we have said in the cutting of scrofula, and if the wound opens bowels, then apply fire cautery as we have said before.
de la routure de l’artere	of the rupture of the artery
Quant li artere est route, et li cuir est soudez qui est sus, si en vient maintes fois apostemes, et tout aussi avient il a la voine enflee et aposteme; et si le conoist on ensi quant c’est por l’artere, si est li apostemes lons em parfont; et quant tu le sens a tes dois, si sens I estraignement; et quant c’est por la voine, si est reons defuer aparans; et c’est folie de coper cest aposteme, et meismement quant il est desoz les asseles et as angres et ou col et em mout d’autres leus, et est mout grans.	When the artery is blocked and the flesh is tightly stretched over it, many abscesses form, both inside and outside; and if you feel for the artery, it is long and complete; and when you feel it with your fingers, it feels like extraction; and when it's the vein, it feels like a path to appear; and it is madness to cut this abscess, and more so when it is stretched over the joints and angles and neck and mouth of others, and it is very large.
Il covient donques eschuir la cure de fer, et celui qui est a chief covient eschuir ausi, et en celui qui est d’enfleure d’artere fent par desus le cuir dou lonc; puis oevre la taille as oncines, et depart bellement l’artere des toiles, tant qu’ele soit descoverte; puis boute desoz li une aguille, et la fai percier jusc’a l’autre costeit, et estraint l’artere d’un fil double en II leus, selonc ceu que je t’ai ensigniet en l’estraction des II arteres qui sont en temples; puis point le leu qui est entre les II liens d’un intromissoire tant que li sans en isse qui i est, et soit deliiez li aposteme; puis amenistre la cure que enjanre bowe, tant que li liien chient; puis cure ceu d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li apostemes est por la taille de la voinne, si covient que tu teignes a ta main ceu que tu pues de l’aposteme a tout le cuir, puis boute l’aguille desoz le leu que tu tiens a ta main, et la fai percier, et i ait I fil double, si que tu le trais de l’autre costeit; puis lie l’aposteme, si com je t’ai dit, ou liien de l’une de II pars as II chiés dou fil; et se tu doutes que li filz n’isse fuer, si i reboute une autre aguille a tout I fil desoz tout l’aposteme a l’incision de la premiere aguille, et estraint les filz en IIII leus; puis cope l’aposteme tant que li superfluitez en isse, puis cope la superfluiteit dou keur et laisse ceu qui est liiez; puis met sus I drapeil moilliet en vin et en oile, puis li amenistre cures de tentes et d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the artery is blocked and the flesh is tightly stretched over it, many abscesses form, both inside and outside; and if you feel for the artery, it is long and complete; and when you feel it with your fingers, it feels like extraction; and when it' s the vein, it feels like a path to appear; and it is madness to cut this abscess, and more so when it is stretched over the joints and angles and neck and mouth of others, and it is very large. So then, the cure of iron should be avoided, and the one at the head should also be avoided, and in that which swells with an artery, stretch the skin from above; then cut the size as one cuts hair, and separate the artery from the threads very carefully, as I have taught you in the extraction of the two arteries in the temples; then take the thread between the two bonds of a double thread until the knot is released which it holds, and then remove the abscess; then apply the poultice as described above, until it heals. And if the abscess is due to the size of the vein, you should rub your hand with the cure as I have told you, so that the abscess can be removed and the skin healed.
des apostemes des ners	of the nerves of the neck
Ausi com aposteme vienent en l’artere et en la voine, vienent aposteme as ners quant il sont ferut, ou par trop grant travail, et semblans choses.	So too do arteries and veins; they come from the nerves when they are hurt, or because of excessive work, and similar things.
Et ceu avient plus sovent as adjutoires et as dois et en toz leus ou il ait jointures, et c’est I grief apostemes, et sa color semble la color dou cors, et est em plusors dispositions sens dolor; et quant on l’estraint forment, si sent li malaides dolor, et n’est mie em parfont dou cors, mais desoz lou keur; et muet bien de toutes pars, et ne va ne avant ne arrier, ne desoz ne desus, et celui qui est en jointures ne covient mie coper par fer: par aventure i vanroit contraction; et cil qui est ou chief ou ou front, fent le cuir au spatumile.	And this often happens to the shoulders and arms and at all joints, and their color seems like that of the body, and they are in many states without pain; and when it is stretched out it feels good, but it does not perfectly close: it moves well on all sides, neither forward nor backward, nor upward nor downward, and the joint does not properly fit: perhaps there is a contraction; and that which is at the top of the head or the forehead feels the scalp to the spine.
Se li apostemes est petis, si le tien a unes tenailles, et le cope en sa racine; et s’il est grans, si le sospent a l’oncine, et l’escorche, puis l’oste et assemble la plaie a la costure, et lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If the abscess is small, then he has a claw at its base, and the cope it; but if it is large, then it hangs from the neck, and the skin boils, then the bone, and the wound is sewn up until it heals.
des grosses boces pendans	of the large bellies hanging down
Aucune fois avient en ventres et ne mie autre part thelul, et est une maladie qui est apelee «funge» par la semblance d’aus, et est li racine subtilz, et li chiez gros; et en i a de petis et de mout grans; et je vis I home qui en avoit II ou ventre qui estoient plus semblans a funges que ai autre chose, et n’i avoit point de difference, et estoient blanc, et avoient menue racine, et estoient jai fendut, et en corroit adés moistor.	There were once in the belly and nowhere else of the boy, and is a disease that is called "fungus" by appearance, and is the subtle root, and the big beard; and there are small and many large; I saw a man who had two or three bellies that looked more like fungi than anything else, and there was no difference, they were white, and had little roots, and they were torn, and came together moist.
Je les copai et trovai en l’un XVIII onces pesant, et en l’autre VI З., et li ovraiges en l’incision si est que tu regardes se li malaides est moistes, et li color de l’artelul est blainche et moiste et de subtil racine; si le cope au spatumile large, et soient en ta presence li cautere au feu.	I took them and found in one XVIII ounces weighing, and in the other VI Z., and the ovraiges in the incision so that you look at it, the patient is wet, and the color of the articol is white and wet and has a subtle root; if you chop with the large spatula, and are in your presence cautery with fire.
Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer; et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors; et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pues bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.	Car au taillier vient maintes fois trop grans decorremens de sanc, et se li sans te vaint, si te haste donques dou cauterizer; et se tu vois le malaide espoanteit et paourous de l’incision dou fer, si prent I fil de plonc bien fait, et en lie l’artelul si com nos avons dit, et le laisse II jors; et puis le restraint, et ne cesser d’estraindre lou fil de plonc tant qu’il cope l’artelul, et chiece par lui sens travail; et se les racines sont grosses, si a paour au coper meismement por le ventre, mais tu em pois bien coper la moitiet, puis le cauterize qu’il ne reviegne; puis cure la plaie, et garde que tu ne coper le thelul qui est de fuxe color et de povre sens et de lait regart.
Car c’est uns apostemes enchancrez, et je venrai a la cure de chancre ci aprés.	For this is an abscess infected, and I will come to the treatment of the ulcer hereafter.
quant li boude ist fuer	when the heat
Se li apparance de la boude vient par cautere de plaie ou de fendure de syfac, et est sus le ventre et en ist aucuns des bouez, si com il avient en autres routures, ou de sanc qui cort de voines ou d’arteres selonc ceu qui est devant, ou de ventositeit; et se c’est par la routure dou syfac et par l’issue dou bouel, si est li color de l’aposteme semblans a la color dou cors, et est legiere chose sens dolor, et apert de diverse issue.	When the appearance of the boils comes by fire cure upon a plague or a cut on the flesh, and it is on the belly and there are some boils, as it happens in other cuts, or blood that comes from veins or arteries according to what is before, or windiness; and if it is by the cut of the flesh and by the issue of the boil, then the color of the abscess seems like the color of the flesh, and it is a light thing without pain, and opening of various issues.
Et se c’est por l’issue de l’intestine, adonques est il plus divers, et quant on le presse a ses dois si se repont, et puis revient, et par aventure si est sarrez, et agrandist mout a l’entree dou bain et por fort travail.	And if it is by the issue of the intestine, then it is more varied, and when one presses it to both sides it turns back, and then comes back again; and perhaps it becomes tighter, and widens greatly at the entrance of the bath and by strong work.
Et se c’est por moistor, c’est legiere chose, et apert bien quant tu le presses a ta main, ne ne constraint mie; et se c’est por sanc, si apert par ces signes li apostemes gros et dur, et est fichiez selonc une quantiteit; et se c’est por ventositeit, si est souef au tochier, et li ovraiges si est que tu regarde se li apparance est por le sanc de l’artere, ou de la voine, ou ventositeit.	And if it is for moisture, that is a light thing, and open well when you press it to your hand, do not constrain; and if it is for blood, if it opens by these signs, the abscesses large and hard, and are inserted according to a quantity; and if it is for wind, if it is hot in the back, and the opening is that you look at its appearance is for the blood of the artery, or vein, or wind.
Si covient que tu laisses la cure.	If you leave the cure.
Car il en a doutance et paor, si com je t’ai dit ou chapistre des apostemes, por l’artere et por la voine.	For in the work of this chapter, there is doubt and fear; if, as I said to you, the chapitre of the abscesses, for the artery and for the vein.
Et se li apparance est por l’intestine ou lou boueil, si covient que tu comandes au malaide qu’il teigne son alaine, et soit estendus tout drois, puis seigne d’enche tout entor la boude; puis le comande a gesir sovin entre tes mains, puis va entor le leu que tu as signiet a tout le spatumile, puis estent la moitiet de l’aposteme au desus a tout le grant uncine; puis le lie entor d’un fil fort, ou d’une corde de fort soie fermement, et soit li nous dou liien assolz; puis oevre la moitiet de l’aposteme estendut sus le liien, et i boute ton doit indice, et quier l’intestine; se tu le trueves pris dou liien, si le deslie, et boute l’intestine au defuer dou ventre; et se tu trueves le boueil, si le prent a l’oncine, et en cope la superfluiteit; et se li artere te fait contraire, ou li voine, si vai belement entor, puis revien a ton ovraige et pren II aguilles, et i boute II fors filz, et boute les II aguilles entor ceu que tu as fait en crois que tu feis percier; puis estrain l’aposteme en IIII leus sus les aguilles, et se tu vues, oste les aguilles, et laisse lou leu tant qu’il porrisse, et chiece li char morte par soi; ou tu la cope quant elle iert subtiliie et porrie, puis le cure de ceu qu’il covient, et cheve l’aposteme si com nos avons dit; et estrai le sanc ou la moistor que tu trueves, puis cure le leu de ceu qu’il couvient, et soude le leu.	And if it is for the intestine or bloat, then command to the patient that he dyes his hair, and is spread out straight, then sign all around the bloated; then order him to walk slowly between your hands, then go around the place where you have signed with the whole hand, then stretch out half of the abscess on top of the large claw; then tie it tightly with a strong thread or a piece of strong silk firmly, and let it hang; then operate on half of the abscess stretched out on the rope, and put your index finger there, and feel for the intestine; if you find it stuck to the rope, let it go, and push the intestine towards the rear of the abdomen; and if you find the bloat, take it to the claw, and cut off the surplus; and if the artery or vein is against you, come back to your work and take two needles, and put two threads, and push the two needles into that which you have made pierce; then stretch out half of the abscess on top of the needles, and if you see it, remove the needles, and leave the place hang until it rot and die, and cut off what is left; or if it is thin and rotten, then cure it from what it needs, and cut off the abscess as we have said; and extract the blood or moisture that you find, then cure the place of what it needs, and soud the place.
dou chancre	 Dou Chancre.
Nos avons dit en la division les semblances de chancre, et coment on i doit ovrer par medicines, et coment on doit eschuer la cure de fer; et disons le chancre enjanreit en la marris, et grant cautele a en la cure, et dirent li ancien que quant chancres est en leu ou on le puet raier si com chancre qui est em mameles, et en la cuixe, et en semblans leus, et le doit tout oster quant il est en l’encomencement; et quant il est grans et anciens, si ne covient mie que tu l’aproches, car je n’en poi onques nul saner; ne nulz n’en sana onques devant moi.	Dou Chancre. There are many treatments for the sore, and how it should be treated with medicine, and how to prevent the cure of iron; and we speak about the chancre that is contracted in the breast, and great care must be taken when treating it, and the ancient man said: "When there is a sore that is in its place, such as a sore on the breasts, or in the milk, and it comes to an end, then all of it must be removed when it is still in its early stages; and when it is large and old, then you cannot approach it, for I have never healed one, nor has anyone ever healed one before me.
Et li ovraiges, quant il est en leu ou on le puet oster, si com nos avons dit, est que tu purge aucune fois le malaide de cole noire; puis le fai sainier s’il ait manifeste repletion, puis afaite le malaide I boin leu por faire l’ovraige; puis giete tes oncines ou chancre, et le cheve de toutes pars, et l’oste de toutes pars sens rien laissier; et laisse corre le sanc tout fuer, et espreint bien le leu a ta main ou a aucune chose, et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire de l’incision de l’artere ou de la voine, si le cauterize tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the openings, when they are in their place and can be removed, as we have said, is that you never purge the malady of black bile; then make it well if it has a manifest repletion, then afaithe the malady to a good place for making the opening; then cast your oncines or chancre, and your hair all around it, and the bone all around it with nothing left; and let the blood run freely, and press it tightly in your hand or in anything, and if the blood recedes from the incision of the artery or vein, then cauterize it until the spot is dried up; then cure it with other cures until it is well.
de ydropisie	About dropsy.
Nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’idropisie, et en queil maniere li assemblee de l’aigue est faite, et les signes de chescune semblance, et la cure qui est faite par medicines, et cele qui est curee par fer: si est eclites soulement; et ne doit on touchier de fer en ces II semblances: c’est a savoir, tympanites et yposarche, car c’est mortelz chose; donques quant tu medicines ceste semblance de ydropisie qui est apelee «eclites» de medicines, et li cure ne profite, si regarde se li malaides est foibles, ou s’il ait autre maladie que ydropisie, si com toust et solution de ventre et semblans choses; si n’i touchier de fer, car il i a doutance; et se tu vois le malaide de fort vertut, et il n’a autre maladie que ydropisie soulement, et il n’est mie trop jones ne trop vielz, si dois ensi ovrer: lieve le malaide droit sus tes mains, et li ministres presse le ventre em boutant l’aigue a la plus basse partie dou pis, puis pren le spatumile espinous selonc ceste forme:	About dropsy. We have already spoken in the division about the similarities of dropy, and how the accumulation of water is formed, and the signs of each similarity, and the treatment that is made with medicines, and what is cured with iron: this is only a last resort; and should one not touch iron in these two similarities - that is to say, tympanites and hypsarche - because it is a deadly thing; so when you treat this similarity of dropy, which is called 'eclites' from medicines, and the cure does not benefit, if you see that the patient is feeble, or if he has another disease besides dropy, such as stomach complaints and similar things; then do not touch iron, because there is doubt; and if you see the patient of great virtue, and he has no other disease but dropy alone, and he is neither too young nor too old, then do so: raise the patient upright on your hands, and the minister presses the abdomen at the lower part of the navel, then take the spatulum with thorns according to this form:
Et soit trenchans de II pars.	And let there be trenching from both parts.
a pointe, et toutevoie ne soit mie si entrans qu’il puist venir jusc’a l’intestine quant on le fiche ens, et ne le puist blecier; puis regarde se li ydropisie est enjanree devers les intestines: si covient que tu fendes ensus de la boude III dois droit desoz sus lou poignil; et se li ydropisie est por la maladie dou foie, si soit ta fendure au senestre de la boude III dois; et se c’est por la miuce, si soit a destre, et ne covient mie que li malaides gise sus la fendure que les superfluitez ne corrent a celui foible leu; puis perce tout le cuir a l’estrument, et le boute, et lieve ta main a tout le spatumile entre le cuir et le syfac ausi com en escorchant a la quantiteit d’une ungle ou enqui entor; puis perce lou syfac tant que li spatumile viegne au leu vuit, et c’est li leus de l’aigue, puis le trai fuer, et i boute cest estrument de coi ci est li forme:	And let there be trenching from both parts. A point, and in no way should it be so deep that it comes up to the intestine when it is put in, and cannot be scraped; then note that the dropsy is running towards the intestines: then you shall make a slash from above the knuckle on the right side; and if it is because of the liver, then your slash shall be on the left side of the bode III; and if it is because of the mucous fluid, then to the right, and it is not necessary that the patient lie down on the slash so that the superfluity does not run into the weak place; then pierce all the skin with the instrument, and pour, and hold your hand over all the sperm from between the skin and the liquid as much as in scraping a finger or half an inch; then pierce the liquid until the sperm comes out at the top, and this is the vein of the water, then draw it out, and pour this instrument out of which there is the shape:
Et est semblans a une caine d’argent subtil, et est d’arain ou d’archaut legier, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus; et ou costeit d’une part, III pertus; et II d’autre part, et I d’autre; et est li chiés tailliez si com une penne, et c’est li forme de l’incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:	Et est semblant à une caenne d'argent subtil, et est d'airain ou d'archaut léger, et a en la partie desoz I petit pertus; et ou coleteit d'une part, III pertus; et II d'autre part, et I d'autre; et est li chiés taiilliez si com une penne, et c'est li forme de l'incision dont li escrivains taille la penne:
au chief desus est li alemele, si que quant li estrumens vient a l’aigue, si dessent maintenant sus l’estrument; vuide la donques la moitiet ou la tierce part, car se tu en vuides plus qu’il ne covient en celle houre, par aventure si muert li malaides por la resolution de son esperit de l’arme, ou il chiet paumez, ou il aproche a la mort; mais en vuide selonc la quantiteit de sa vertut, et selonc ceu que les dispositions de la vertut dou malaide signifient, et ses poulz; puis trai l’estrument et retien l’aigue, et elle est retenue maintenant por le keur qui estoupe le pertus qui est sus le syfac, de coi j’ai parleit, que tu perces selonc ceste maniere; puis rencomence l’estrument l’autre jor, se tu vois le malaide soffrant ceu, et trai de l’aigue une petite quantiteit; fai ce aucun jor, et te garde de foloier tant qu’il ni demore mais c’un poc d’aigue.	It is resembling to an argent subtile dog's tooth, and it is of brass or lightarchal, and has in the part desos a small perforation; and where it costs on one side, there are three perforations; and two on the other side, and one on the other; and the head is tailored as a feather, and this is the form of the incision that the writers cut the feather: at the top of the head is the alemele, so that when the instrument comes to the water, it sprays now on the instrument; drain the half or third part, because if you drain more than it is necessary in that hour, by chance the patient dies because of the resolution of his spirit from the weapon, or he shakes, or approaches death; but drain according to the quantity of its virtue, and according to what the dispositions of the virtue of the sick and his hairs mean, and then turn the instrument and hold back the water, and it is held now by the courage that stops the hole that is on the medicine, which I have spoken about, so you pierce it in this way; then restart the instrument another day, if you see the patient suffering that, and turn the water a little quantity; do not do any more, and keep yourself from fooling around until it does not stop but a little water.
Et se tu doutes sus le malaide, et tu i lais mout d’aigue, si le cure de la sepulture ou sablon chaut, et par mout sueir ou bain et au soleil, et se teigne de boivre; et le cure de medicines desiccatives tant qu’il soit sanez, et cauterize sus l’estomac et sus lou foie et sus l’esplen aprés l’estraction de l’aigue, si com j’ai dit devant.	And if you doubt about the disease, and you leave it with water, so that the cure of the grave or mud is hot, and by sweating or bathing and in the sun, and tanned with wine; and the cure of drying medicines until it is healed, and cauterized on the stomach and on the liver and on the spleen after extraction of water, as I said before.
de l’estopement de la verge	of the stopping of the penis
Aucune fois naissent enfant qui n’ont point de pertus en la verge, ou li pertus est petis, ou il n’est mie en son leu.	No child is born with an imperforate penis, or if it has one that is small, or if it is not in its correct position.
Si le covient tantost qu’il n’aist percier a tout I spatumile molt subtil selonc ceste forme:	If it happens that he does not pierce the most subtle skin according to this form:
puis met ou pertus I clo subtil de plonc, et le lie et le tien ensi III jors ou IIII et quant il vuet faire urine, si soit ostez li clos, et faice urine, et puis li remet; et par aventure nen i couvient point, car li urine qui vient fuer ne lou laisse close.	then place the perforation in a thin skin of leather, and keep it there for three or four days, and when it begins to urinate, if the hole is not closed, let the urine pass through, and then put it back again; and perhaps he will never know it, since the urine that comes out is not kept by him.
Cil de cui li pertus est petis, si est medicinez dou clo de plonc, si com nos avons dit, si s’eslargera.	The piercing of which is painful, if it is medicine of the cloven tongue, if as we said, it expands itself.
Cil qui n’ont mie le pertus en lor leu sont bleciet, car aucun naissent qui ont le pertus au chief de la verge, por coi il ne puient pissier avant s’il ne lievent lor verge en haut; et ne pueent enjanrer por ceu que li matiere ne puet venir jusc’a la marris, et c’est une male maladie.	Those who do not have the piercing in its place are bleached, for no one is born with the piercing at the tip of the penis, so that he cannot urinate until he raises his penis; and cannot ejaculate unless the material can come up to the testicles, and this is a bad disease.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, puies estent le chief de la verge et le cope ausi com la taille d’une penne, si ke li pertus chiece em mileu, si com il covient; et te garde de decorrement de sanc qui i vient maintes fois, et s’il avient, si l’estainche de ceu qui estainche sanc, et cure la plaie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the way of the operation is that the patient lies down on his back, then the head of the penis and the scrotum are cut off as well as the size of a feather, so that the piercing sounds in the middle, as it should; and you must not let blood come out of it, because it often comes out, and if it happens, stop the bleeding of this one who bleeds, and cure the wound until it is healed.
des pustules de la verge	of the penis sores
Maintes fois vienent cist albathe en la verge, et est une apparance de char laide; et en i a malignes et non malignes; si covient que tu les preignes a I oncine subtil, et les cope et munde toutes, puis met sus coton moilliet en oignement egiptien; puis le cure d’oignement diafinicon tant qu’il soit sanez.	Many times there are painful sores in the penis, and it has an ugly appearance; and there are some that are malicious and others that are not malicious; so that you should massage them with a fine oil, and cop them and clean them all up, then put cotton wet with Egyptian ointment on them; then cure them with diafinicon until they are well.
Et se li albathe est maligne, de pute color et depuant, si covient que tu i amenistres cautere.	And if the penis is malignant, of a putrid color and stinking, then you should apply fire cautery to it.
Quant tu l’as copeit, et se li albathe est en som la verge, et en ait partie dedens la peil et partie defuer, si covient que tu oste l’albathe qui est dedens premier; et quant il est soudez, si le cure defuer.	When you have coped it, and if the penis is inside the skin of the scrotum, and there is some part within and some part outside, then you should remove the penis that is within first; and when it is sewn up, then heal the outside.
Car quant tu le cures ensamble, si n’est mie asseurez li chiez de la verge qu’il ne soit perciez, et vient noiror et corruption en son la verge et ou coion; si covient chever tout ceu qui est noir et corrumput, puis lie sus l’emplaustre de miel et de farine qui soit fait d’escorce de poumes grenates et de veces, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	For when you heal it all together, if the head of the penis is not properly secured, then there will be blackness and corruption in his penis and where the foreskin is; so that you should cut off all that is black and corrupted, then put on plaster made of honey and flour, which is made from pomegranate bark and dates, then heal it with other treatments until it is well.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient, si amenistre le cautere lunaire selonc ceste forme:	And when blood comes out, then administer the lunar cautery according to this form:
Li cauteres si aide as II dispositions ensamble: c’est asavoir, au decorrement de sanc, et a la corruption; et se li chiés de la verge est corrumpus et retrais, si covient que tu boutes ou conduit de la verge une cainne de plonc, et pisse li malaides parmi; et quant li pelz iert aerse au chief de la verge qui avient a ces qui n’ont mie esteit circoncis, ou il avient por plaie ou por aposteme, si covient donques que tu l’escorches a I estrument cheveit, tant que li liiens soit desliiez, et soit delivrez li chiez de la verge de toutes pars; et se c’est grief chose de deviser ceu, si covient que tu l’escorches a I spatumile aucun poc dou chief de la verge et de la peil; puis dessevre belement entre II, et i met I subtil drapeil de lin moilliet an aigue froide, qu’il n’aerse derechief.	And if blood comes out when the hymen tears, then administer the lunar cautery in this way: Put together two dispositions; that is to say, when blood comes out and corruption occurs; and the foreskin of the penis is corrupted and withdrawn, so that you put or lead a cord of leather from the root of the penis, and urinate on the patient; and when the hair has grown on the head of the penis which has not yet been circumcised, or it has happened because of an ulcer or abscess, then it is necessary to scrape with the scalpel so that the ligaments are loosened, and the foreskin of the penis is freed from all sides; and if this is a difficult thing to say, then you scrape it with a toothpick at the base of the penis and head, then carefully separate them, and place a thin linen cloth soaked in cold water on top, so that it does not stick anymore.
de la circoncision	of circumcision
Circoncision n’est mie desliemens de continuation si com les autres plaies; toutevoie quant nos faison ceste oevre de nostre volenteit, et proprement as enfans, si est mestier que nos faisiens la millor oevre, et la plus legiere a salut.	Circumcision is not a painful procedure if done like other wounds; however, when we perform this operation on children by choice, it must be done with the greatest care and ease for their benefit and salvation.
Je dis que li ancien ne dirent mie la circoncision de lor enfans, car il n’en usent mie en lor loi, et n’en avons mais que ceu que nos avons aquis par experiment.	I say that the ancient ones did not mention circumcision for their children, because they do not use it in their laws, and we have only learned this through experience.
Car j’ai veut la plus grant partie des maistres et des sainors qui faisoient circumcision entor I dal, et as forces, et a tout une novacule; si fuioit li keurs car il i a II toiles, et par aventure si cope on celi desus et demore celle desoz.	For I have seen most of the masters and wise men who performed circumcision between the shoulder blades, and on the skin, and on all sorts of animals; so that it might be done quickly, because there were two threads, and by chance one might cut above or below them.
Or la recovient coper, et est li dolor double, et a la mundification qui est dou dal n’est mie asseuree li pointe dou membre; et a la mundification de l’ungle par aventure eschaipe li fer, et corront l’uevre, et maintes fois naissent ensi qu’il n’ont mestier de mundification et je l’ai veut.	Or it comes off again, and the pain is doubled, and the washing from the flesh is not certain at the tip of the member; and by chance the nail escapes the iron, and ruins the work, and often happens that there is no need for washing, and I have seen it.
De la mondification qui est faite as forces a tout le liien de fil ai je troveit la bonteit de l’experiment, car les forces taillent justement ausi bien desus com desoz.	Of the washing that is done to all the body with force I have found the goodness of the experiment, for the forces are equally as much above as below.
Car quant tu presses ta main, si tailles igalment en I tout soul tens; mais que li filz soit bien estrois entor lou cuir; et soit li maniere dou premier ovraige si est que tu faices penser l’enfant, s’il entent, que tu ne li fais fuer que liier le fil entor la verge tant soulement, et pues le fai esjoir en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis le fai ester entre tes mains tout droit, et repont les forces entre tes mains ou desoz tes piez que li enfes ne les voie, ne aucun des estrumens; puis boute ta main a la verge et souffle ou keur, et la trai en haut tant que li chiés de la verge soit ens; puis la mundifie bien de l’ordure qui i est assemblee, puis lie le leu signiet d’un fil double, puis la lie desoz I poc a I autre liien; et la tien as II dois par la seconde lieeure au pouchet et au doit indice, et cope entre les II liiens, puis lieve le keur desus hastanment et trai le chief de la verge; puis laisse corre le sanc poc et poc, car c’est li muedres; et met poudre sus et sus la poudre I drapeil glueit d’un moieuf d’uef cuit destempreit d’aigue rose, confit avec oile roset boin et fres, et lou laisse sus jusc’a l’autre jor, et le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	For when you squeeze your hand, if it is cut equally from the skin; but that the thread be well-twisted around the leather; and let the manner of the first work be so that you make the child think, if he hears, that you do not make the thread tight except around the penis so much, and then let it hang in all the ways that you can; then let it rest between your hands straight, and reset the forces between your hands or toes that the child does not see them, nor any of the instruments; then bottle your hand to the penis and blow or heat, and turn it up as far as the head of the penis is set; then wash it well with the dirt that is gathered there, then tie the skin thread with a double thread, then tie it away I thread to another thread; and hold it in place with the second thread at the knuckle and at the little finger, and wrap between the two threads, then let the heat fall gently and turn the head of the penis; then let the blood run and run, for that is the heat; and put powder on and on the powder I draped glue-like from a loaf of baked egg yolk seasoned with rosewater, confited with oil of roses and fresh, and let it rest until the next day, and cure it with other cures as long as it is healthy.
Li forme des forces a la mundification si est ceste: li dui chiés soient tenves et soient trenchans, et soient li chiés ausi grant com li mainche igalment:	The form of the shoulder is thus made firm if it is like this: The two shoulders should be soft and smooth, and the shoulders should also be as long as they are usually.
li error de la mundification si est quant li keurs dedens fuit a l’incision; donques il covient que tu l’estendes a ton ungle, ainsois que li leus faice aposteme; et le cope igalment, et se tu ne lou pues tenir a ton ungle, si le tien as tenailles, et puis le cope.	The error of the washing if it is when the cure is inside the incision; so that you should extend it to your nail, so that the edge makes an abscess; and equal it, and if you do not hold it with a clamp, then hold it with pliers, and then make the cut.
Et s’il trespassent III jors, et ceu qui est desoz la verge est enflez, si le laisse tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et l’escorche legierement; si le cope si com tu pues mues, et te garde de la partie de la verge, ce ne li nuira niant.	If it goes for three days, and what is at the root of the penis is swollen, if he leaves it until the abscess has calmed down, and the skin has peeled off slightly; if you can move it as you can, and keep away from the part of the penis, this will not harm him.
Cure donques le leu de choses soudans plaie de poudre, que nos avons dit ou traitier des poudres, et s’on cope dou keur outre mesure, et il va au desus, si ne nuira point; cure le donques, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	Cure then the powder of things standing wound with powder, which we have said in the treatment of powders, and if the cut goes up, it will not harm him; cure it then, as we have said, until it is healthy.
dou retenement de l’urine	retentlement of urine
Li retenue de l’urine si est d’opilation de piere, ou de sanc congeleit, ou de bowe, ou de char nee, ou de semblans choses, que nos avons dit en la division; et se li urine n’est desliie , et tu vois estre la retenue por la piere qui est jai ou col de la vessie, si covient que li malaides soit corbés sus ses genoulz; et li soient mis li piez sor le dos, et estende son ventre de la partie desus lou dos, et restraigne li malaides s’alainne tant com il puet; et adonques est constrains li colz de la vessie a l’expression de la piere au desus, por coi li urine est desliie e; et s’elle ne vient, si com nos avons dit, et li malaides sent grant dolor, si covient que tu i aministres extraction a tout l’estrument qui est apelez «siringue», de coi ci est li forme: et soit d’argent subtilz legiere chevee, si com li penne d’un oiseil; et soit li caine d’une palme de lonc et demie, et soit subtilz au chief.	The retentence of urine is due to a stone in the kidney, or frozen blood, or bowel obstructions, or similar things which we have mentioned in the division; and if the urine does not pass, and you see it retained because of the stone at the penis base, so it is necessary that the patient be laid on his back; and let him be placed on his back with his feet extended behind him, and stretch out his abdomen from above his back, and restrain the patient so he can remain in this position as long as possible; and then it is necessary to bring the penis up towards the stone's location by means of a tool called a "syringe", which has the following form: and let it be made of fine lightweight silver, like the feathers of an owl; and let its canal be one palm long and half a palm wide, and let it be thin at the tip.
Et li maniere de l’issue de l’urine si est que tu pren I fil double, et lie au chief I poc de laine ou de couton, et boute le chief dou fil dedens la siringue; et cope la superfluiteit de la lainne et le boute jusc’au chief de la siringue, puis oint la siringue d’oile ou de burre et d’aubin d’uef, et fai seoir le malaide sus I siege, et li arose la vessie et la verge d’oile moiste et d’oile d’olive et d’aigue tede; puis met legierement la siringue en la verge, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la verge, puis double la verge desus devers la boude; puis boute la siringue avant jusc’a la vessie, et la sente li malaides venir jusc’a la chose vuide, et ceu n’est mie fait selonc cest ordre fuer que por ceu que li conduis ou elle vait est tors; puis estent le fil a tout la laine poc et poc, et li urine en suit la laine, puis l’estrai fuer, et fai corre l’urine; et rencomence la siringue tant que li vessie soit vuidie, et soit aligiez li malaides.	Et the way of the issue of urine is that you take I double thread, and tie at the end of the yarn a piece of wool or cotton, and bottle the yarn inside the syringe; and cut off the superfluity of the yarn and bottle it up to the end of the syringe, then oil the syringe with oil or butter and egg white, and make the patient sit on a chair, and lift up the bladder and the penis with moist oil and olive oil and water; then lightly put the syringe into the penis until it comes to the root of the penis, then double the penis over the bottle; then bottle the syringe before the bladder, and let the urine come out until it is empty, and this should be done according to this order, otherwise it will go wrong, that the one who leads it goes in a different direction; then are the threads to all the wool tied and tied, and the urine follows the wool, then extract it, and make the urine run; and start again the syringe as long as the bladder is empty, and the patient is calm.
des maladies de la vessie	of the diseases of the bladder
Quant escorcheures ou sanc vient en la vessie, ou porriture i est assemblee, et tu i vues distiller aigues et medicines, si fai a tout l’estrument qui est apellé «clepsedre», et c’est li forme:	When blisters or sores come to the bladder, and it is swollen, and you see there distilling water and medicines, so do for all the instrument which is called "clepsydre", and that is like this:
Elle est close, et si a III pertus: II d’une part, et I d’autre, si com tu vois; et li leus chevez par coi li medicine cort soit telz qu’il estoupe bien la verge sens adition, si c’on em puisse traire la moistor, et bouter quant mestier est; et quant tu vues giter tes medicines en la vessie, met le chief dou keusteur en la moistor, et trai au traiant qui est ens; si trairas la moistor au kesteur, et puis reboute fort le traiant ens; si entrera li moistors ens, et venra a la vessie maintenant, si que li malaides la sentira; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil dont on clisterize la vessie: si est ci:	It is closed, and if it has three openings: one part from one side, and another part from the other side, as you see; and make a hole in the center where the medicine can flow well into the bladder without adding anything, so that you can remove the moisture, and throw when necessary; and when you see your medicines move in the bladder, put the head of the catheter in the moisture, and push while moving it; if you push the moisture into the catheter, and then rebound it strongly from behind; if the moisture enters, and now comes to the bladder, so that the patient will feel it; and this is the form of the thin catheter with which we urine the bladder: it is like this:
Et est d’argent ou d’archaut, et est li chiés plus haut; et desoz a I sein ou li liiens chiet; puis pren une vessie de mouton et i met la moistor dont tu vues clisterizer la vessie, puis la lie entre les II seins forment d’un boin fil double, et chaufe I poc celle moistor sus le feu; puis boute le chief dou clistere en la verge, puis estrain ta main sus la vessie a tout la moistor avenanment, tant que li malaides sente que celle moistor est jai venue a la vessie; et se tu n’as la vessie, si pren une piece de parchemin, et en fai I cercle, et le perce rondement entor; puis boute I fil fort en ces pertus, puis assemble le cercle si com on assemble I dal, et met dedens ceu que tu vues d’oile et de moistor et d’aigue, et le lie en l’estrument; et fai si com tu as fait de la vessie, de presser a ta main tant que li moistor veigne a la vessie.	And it is of silver or bronze, and this is the shoulder higher up; and so to I seater or ligature; then take a bladder of sheep and put the moisture that you have seen to distend the bladder, then lay it between the two breasts formed by a good double thread, and heat the moisture on the fire; then dip the head of the distender into the bladder, then hold your hand over the bladder towards all the moisture, until the patient feels that the moisture has come to the bladder; and if you do not have the bladder, take a piece of parchment, and make it a circle, and pierce it roundly around; then dip a thread firmly in these holes, then assemble the circle as one assembles a dal, and put in what you want of oil and moisture and water, and bind it to the instrument; and do so as you did with the bladder, by pressing your hand until the moisture comes to the bladder.
de la piere	of stone
Nos avons jai dit en la division les manieres de piere, et l’estraction ensamble medicines; et ai dit la difference entre la piere enjanree as rains, et toz les signes, et en queil piere on doit ovrer de taille; et en la vessie, et en la verge; et je le vos dirai apertement et briément.	We have already said in the division the ways of stone, and extraction together with medicines; and I said the difference between stone broken into pieces and all signs, and in what way one must operate on stone; and regarding bladder and penis; and now I will tell you openly and briefly.
Je dis que li piere qui est enjanree en la vessie si avient plus sovent as enfans, et c’est signe que li aigue saut de la vessie semblans a aigue en sa subtiliteit; et i apert harene, et graite li malaides sa verge, et li pent maintes fois, et puis enroidist; et a mout de ces saut li fondemens; et est legiere li sanation des enfans jusqu’il ont IIII ans, et est mout grief en viellars, et est as jones moiene, a ces qui sont entre jonesce et viellece; et est li cure plus legiere de ces qui ont la piere grans, que de ces qui l’ont petite.	I say that the stone which is broken into pieces in the bladder often happens with children, and this is a sign that water jumps from the bladder resembling water in its subtlety; and I open it, and massage the patient's penis, and turn it many times, then renounces it; and the foundations are dissolved much of these leaps; and the cure is lighter for the children until they have four years old, and it is much heavy in the elderly, and it is between the child and the old; and the cure is easier with those who have great stones than with those who have small ones.
Et quant nos venons a la cure, si couvient premier mundifier le malaide per clistere, por traire tout le fiens qui est as intestines.	And when we come to the treatment, if it is necessary first to purify the patient with enemas, in order to remove all the matter that is in the intestines.
Car il encombre aucune fois a querir la piere.	For it never bothers to seek a stone.
Puis prenez le malaide par les piez, et lou deboutez et movez au desoz, si que li piere dessende au parfont de la vessie, et saille aucune fois dou leu haut; puis le fai seoir entre tes mains appareilliet, et ses mains soient desoz ses cuisses, si que li vessie soit toute declinans aval; puis la quier et la touche dedens; se tu sens la piere en l’espaice, si te haste maintenant de taillier sus la piere.	Then take the patient by the feet and move them down so that the stone comes out to the very edge of the bladder, and never goes up again; then let him sit with his legs spread apart, so that the bladder is all turned downward; then examine and touch inside; if you feel the stone in the space, hurry now to cut on top of the stone.
Et s’elle ne chiet au touchier dou tout, si moille ton doi indice d’oile de la main senestre, se li malaides est enfes, ou ton doi moien, se li malaides est jovencelz acomplis; et le boute en son fondement, et quier la piere, et quant tu la sens a ton doi, si l’amoine au col de la vessie; puis presse sus a ton doi, et la boute au defuer lai ou tu vues taillier.	And if it does not come out when you touch it all over, then moisten your index finger with oil from your left hand, if the patient is old, or cut off your second finger, if the patient is young and accomplished; and pour it down its base, and examine for a stone, and if you feel it with your second finger, press toward the bladder's neck; then press up with your second finger, and pour out where you can see the cutting.
Et comande au ministre qu’il presse la vessie a sa main, et li comande qu’il estende a sa main destre les coions en haut, et a sa main senestre oste le cuir qui est desoz les coions en la partie ou on fait la taille; puis i boute le spatumile copant, de coi ce est li forme:	And command the minister to press the bladder in his hand, and he commands that he extends to his right hand the coions up, and with his left hand oste the leather which is desoz the coions in the part where one makes the waist; then i pour the spatumile copant, for this is the form:
Et fent entre ceu qui est entre les coions et le fondement, ne mie em mileu mais au costeit de la naige senestre; et soit drois sus la piere, et tes dois soit adés ou fondement, et soit li taille dou traver si qu’ele soit large par defuer, et dedens estroite, selonc la quantiteit de la piere, ne mie trop grans; par aventure la presse si li dois qui est ou fondement, qu’elle saut fuer sens travail; et saiches qu’il i a teil piere ou il a angles, et marges: si est griés a issir; et si a teil qui est souez, semblans a une glant, et reonde, dont li issue est legiere.	And make space between what is between the coions and the fundament, not in the middle but at the cost of the left side; and let it be right on the stone, and your two be together or at the fundament, and let the size of the travers be so that it is wide on both sides, and narrow inside, according to the quantity of the stone, not too big; perhaps the press if there is a part of it at the fundament, so that it jumps without work; and you know that there are parts where it is hollowed out, like a glade, and round, whose issue is light.
A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole; et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.	A celi donques ou il a angles et marge, fai la taille plus grant; et s’elle ne saut, si covient que tu estraignes sus as tenailles qui sont ausi com une lime au chief, por mues estraindre la piere si qu’elle n’eschaipe; ou tu boute desoz li I estrument subtil corbé au chief; et se tu ne la pues engignier ensi, si eslarge I poc lou pertus, et se li sans decort, si l’estrainche de vitriole; et s’il i a plus d’une piere, si boute premier la plus grant au col de la vessie, puis cope sus, puis le trai fuer, et les petites aprés s’il en i a plusors.
Et s’elle est mout grans, si la covient soier, et faire plus grant plaie.	If the stone is large, then it is necessary to make a larger wound.
Car II choses avienent au malaide: ou il muert, ou li urine vient adés par lai que li leus ne puet souder; mais toutevoie t’efforce dou traire, ou dou debrisier as tenailles, tant que tu la traies par pieces; et quant tu as acomplit ton oevre, si emple la plaie d’encens et d’aloe et de sanc de dragon, et l’estraint, et met par sus I drapeil moilliet en oile et en vin, ou en oile et en aigue rose et aigue froide, por apaisier l’aposteme chaut; puis resovine le malaide sus son col, et ne desliier lou lien jusc’au tier jor.	For two things happen to the patient: he may die, or his urine flows out quickly because the ligature does not hold; but nevertheless you should try to extract it piece by piece with tweezers, until you have finished your task. Then apply warm oil and water, or hot oil and rose water, or cold water to the abscess to heat it up; then tie the patient's neck tightly for three days.
Et quant tu le desliies, si arose mout bien lou leu d’oile et d’aigue, puis le cure d’oignement dyafinicon et d’oignement basilicon, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you release it, so that it returns to its place well with oil and water, then cure it with unguent of honey and unguent of basil until it is healthy.
Et se apostemes chaus vient en la plaie et corrosions, et congelemens de sanc en la vessie, et soit par ceu retenue li urine, qui est conue en teil maniere que sans saut avec l’urine: boutes donques ton doi en la plaie, et estrai celui sanc, car s’il i remaint, si corront la vessie, et la porrit; puis leve la plaie d’aigue et d’aisil et de seil, et li aide en toutes les manieres que tu seis, tant qu’il soit sanez; et covient que toutes les oures que tu le cures, que tu li lie les II cuisses, et assemble les medicines sus le leu.	And if abscesus come into the wound and corrosions, and congealments of blood in the bladder, and it is held back by urine that is conveyed in a certain way so that it does not jump with urine: then you must put your finger in the wound, and extract the blood, because if it remains, it will corrode the bladder, and pour it out; then raise the wound with water and ash and straw, and help it in all ways that you can until it is healthy; and it is necessary that you tie its two legs together, and put medicines on top.
Et se li piere est petite, et ele est ou conduit de la verge, et fichie ens, et li urine ne puet issir; si le cure de ceu que je dis ainsois, que tu lou tailles maintes fois, est on escusez de la taille per ceste cure.	And if the stone is small, and it lies where the penis enters, and is pegged in, and urine cannot come out; then he should cure it as I have said above, that you cut it many times, for this cure excuses the cutting of the penis.
Je ai ja ce proveit ensi.	I have proved this myself.
Pren I foret de fer selonc ceste forme et soit a III angles fichiees en I tison:	Take iron and forge it according to this form, and let it be III angles nailed in one piece of wood:
puis pren I fil et lou lie entor la verge desoz la piere, si qu’ele ne puist venir arrier en la vessie; puis boute le foret en la verge legierement, tant qu’il viegne a la piere; et torne le foret a ta main en la piere poc et poc, tant que tu puisses percier la piere d’autre part; si venra tantost li urine, puis presse ta main sus ceu qui est demorez de la piere qui est dedens la verge.	Then take a file and polish the edge of the iron with a stone, so that it cannot be drawn back in the wood; then tap the file lightly on the edge, so that it comes to the stone; and turn the file little by little in your hand, so that you can pierce the stone from the other side; then soon enough will come the urine, then press your hand on what is delayed in the stone that is inside the wood.
Si est tantost brisie, et saut fuer avec l’urine, et est garis li malaides; et se tu ne pues ce faire por aucune chose qui le deffent, si lie I fil desoz la piere et I autre desus, puis fent la verge endroit la piere entre les II liiens, puis l’estrai fuer, et deslie lou liien, et mundifie lou sanc congeleit qui est en la plaie; et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is soon broken and jumps out with urine and is healed for the patient; and if you cannot do this in any way so that it hurts him, then I file the stone and another above it, then I slide the wood between the two lines, then I pull it out sharply, and wash away the frozen blood that is in the wound; and cure it until it is well.
de la piere des femmes	from the woman's bone
Poc avient que piere soit enjanree en femmes, et s’il avient aucune fois, si est li cure grief, et est deffendut por III choses: l’une est que per aventure li femme est vierge; et li seconde est c’on ne puet trover femme bien saichant qui se descuevre as mires, meismement quant elle est caste.	There is a chance that the bone might be broken in women, and if it is not broken at all, there is a cure for pain, but it is prevented by three things: one is that the woman may be virgin; and the second is that no woman who knows well how to bring forth cannot go on her back when she delivers, even though she is married.
Et li tierce maniere si est que par aventure on ne puet trover femme bien saichant en cest art de mains; et li quarte maniere si est que li piere de la femme si est plus em parfont que li piere de l’ome, por coi il i couvient faire plus parfonde taille, et grant paour i a.
