Et se necessitez semont a ceu, si covient que tu preignes une mieresse bien sachant, et a poines la trueve on, et se tu n’en trueves, point si quier I caste mire subtil; et li presente une baile bien saige en la vie des femmes, ou une femme qui saiche une partie de l’art, et li comande qu’ele faice ceu que tu li comandes de l’inquisicion de la piere; et regarde mout bien se li femme est vierge: adonques li covient bouter son doit ou fondement et querir la piere; et s’ele la trueve, si la constraigne desoz son doit, et li recomande qu’elle boute son doit ou con la malaide, et quiere et presse sa main senestre sus la vessie forment.	And the third way is that there may not be a woman who knows well how to bring forth, when she goes on her back; and the fourth is that the woman's bone is often more perfect than the man's, so that one has to make a deeper cut, and it frightens her very much. And if necessity demands it, you should take a midwife who knows well, and, at most, she may not come near her; but if you don't find one, do not look for a cast-away wife; and the present an able woman in midwifery, or a woman who knows some of the art, and command that she make that which you command her to make in the examination of the bone; and watch well whether she is a virgin: then it is necessary that she put her foot or foundation and try the bone; and if she tries it, she should hold it by the foot, and want and press her left hand on the bladder.
S’elle la trueve, si covient qu’elle la mueve de greit en greit des l’entree de la vessie jusque desoz, tant qu’elle viegne a la racine de la cuisse; puis cope sus la piere en la racine de la cuisse encontre le mileu dou con, lai ou il est mues apparilliet, et sent la piere en celle partie; et ne mueve son doi desus la piere ou desoz, et soit li taille au premier petite; puis boute lou rait en la taille, se tu sens la piere si acroi la plaie tant que li piere puisse issir fuer, et saiches que maintes manieres de pieres sont: c’est a savoir, petites et grans et aspres et souez, longes et reondes, et qui ont rains.	If she tears, so it is necessary that she move slowly from the entrance of the bladder to the anus, until she reaches the root of the thigh; then cut on top of the bone at the root of the thigh towards the middle where it is broken, and feel the bone in that part; and do not move your two legs above the bone or anus, and make a small hole first; then pour boiling water into the wound, if you feel the bone very hot to the wound as long as the bone can come out, and know that there are many kinds of bones: namely, small and large, sharp and smooth, long and round, and some have rain.
si saiches les semblances por savoir l’issue.	If you know the appearances so as to know the outcome.
Et se li sans te vaint, si met au leu vitriole broiet, et li tien une houre tant que li sans soit estainchiez; puis revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer, et aies des estrumens que je t’ai dit en l’estraction de la piere as homes por toi aidier en ton oevre; et se li sans te vaint, et c’est de l’artere qui est copee, si met la poudre sus le leu et l’estrain de tentes et de bendelz, et ne rencomencier plus ceu, et laisse la piere et ne la traire mie, que par aventure morroit li malaide; puis cure la plaie.	And if it does not go away, put vinegar on the wound, and hold it for an hour until the sore is well; then come back to your work, as long as the bone is gone, and have the tools that I told you about in the extraction of the bone to help you in your work; and if it does not go away, and this is the artery that has been cut, put powder on the wound and strain water and salt, and do not re-wound it again, and leave the bone and do not pull it out, lest the patient die; then heal the wound.
Et quant li chalor dou sanc est apaisie, et li leus porrist, si revien a ton ovraige, tant que li piere soit fuer.	And when the heat of the fire has subsided, and the blood has stopped flowing, if you return to your work, let the stone be far away.
de hernie carnouse	the hernia causes pain
Ramice aquouse n’est autre chose que assemblee de moistor ou blanc syfac, qui est desoz lou keur des coions, que contient l’uef; et est apelez «syfac», et aucune fois est proprement en la toile de l’uef, si c’on cuide que ce soit I autre oef; et c’est li cuir dou coion entre lou blanc syfac que nos avons dit; et ceu n’avient se poc non.	The wet substance is nothing other than a mixture of white mud or mucus that clings to the utters and contains the milk; it is called "syfac", and never enters properly into the sack of the utters, if we consider that it is another sort of food; and this same skin between the white "syfac" that we have mentioned; and such an one does not come.
Et li generation de cest ramice si est de foibleteit que vient as coions, et est espandue celle matiere.	And the generation of this hernia is so feeble that it comes from the utters, and that material is spread out.
Et aucune fois si vient de percussion sus les coions, et ceste moistor si a maintes colors: ou c’est color declinans a jaunice, ou c’est sans rouge, ou noir, ou aquous blans, et ce avient plus; et ce sont li signe de conoistre ceste assemblee, car s’elle est ou blanc syfac que nos avons dit, si est li apostemes reons, I poc lonc si com li figure d’un oef, et n’apert mie li coions, car il a moistor tout entor.	And it never comes from the impact on the utters, and this moisture has many colors: or it is yellow-colored, or red, or black, or white water, and such happens more often; and these are the signs of distinguishing this mixture, because if it is white  "syfac" that we have mentioned, it is the sign of a long apoplexy, a long time as the shape of an exercise, and does not open the utters, for there is moisture all around.
Et s’il a moistor en la propre toile, si est li apostemes reons avec une partie de l’uef, et por ceu pense on que c’est uns autres oef; et se li moistor est entre le cuir des coions et le blanc syfac, si le sent om bien; donques quant tu vues savoir la color de la moistor, si esprueve a tout l’intromissoire quarreit, de coi li forme est ci devant.	And if there is moisture in the tissue itself, then the abscesses are with part of the egg, and for this reason it is thought that there is another egg; and if the moisture is between the skin of the scrotum and the white syfac, then it feels very bad. So when you want to know the color of the moisture, try it on all of the inner shell, since its shape is as follows:
Selonc ceu donques qui vient aprés l’intromissoire, juge de ceu qui est dedens.	According to what comes after the shell, judge of what is inside.
Et quant nos la curons par fer, si covient que li malaides soit sainiez selonc som pooir et la repletion de son cors; puis le sovine sus son dos, sus une chose un poc haute, et met desoz lui mout de drapelz; puis sié sus sa senestre, et comande au ministre qu’il sié a destre, et estende la verge a l’un des II costelz dou keur des coions; puis pren le spatumile leit, et cope le cuir des coions parmi leu dou lonc jusque delez lou poignil, et soit ta fendure toute droite en devisant le cuir des coions jusc’a syfac blanc, et l’escorche subtilment selonc tom pooir; puis perce lou syfac plain d’aigue a I large pertus, et estrai toute l’aigue, et puis met tes oncines, et estent lou syfac amont; et ne touchier le keur des coions, mais que le syfac soulement; cope tout ou par pieces meismement le costeit de lui subtil, que se tu ne le copes bien saigement, si revenra li aigue; et se l’uef saut fuer a ton oevre, si le ramoinne en son leu quant tu avras acomplit l’uevre dou syfac; puis assemble les II leivres dou keur des coions a une costure, puis le cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when we treat it with fire, so that the patient is healed according to his power and the repletion of his body; then he sits on his back, on something a little high, and spreads out some sheets for him; then he sits on his left side, and orders the minister to sit on his right, and extends the wand to one of the II ribs from between his legs; then he takes the spatula, and scrapes the skin among them all the way up to the top; and let it be cut all at once in a straight line, cutting off the skin of the scrotum little by little; and let the blade pierce the white syfac with water, and let him draw out all the water, and then put on the gloves, and let him cover the syfac up high; and do not touch the keur des coions, but only the syfac itself; cut it apart piece by piece smoothly, so that if you don't cut it well enough, the water will return; and if the egg was escaped to your work, take it back to its place when you have finished working on the syfac; then join the II leivres des coions with a seam, then heal him as you would other wounds, until he is healed.
Et se tu trueves l’uef corromput d’autre maladie, si covient que tu lies les vasselz que sont suspensoire, en doutant le decorrement de sanc; puis cope le coion a tout le suspensoire, et estrai l’uef, et le cure si com nos avons dit.	And if you find the egg corroded by some other disease, then it is necessary that you lay the eggs that are suspended, in doubt of the decay of blood; then take out the egg and treat it as we have said.
Et se aigue est assemblee en II parties ensamble, saiches que ce sont II ramices; si cope l’autre partie si com tu as fait la premiere igalment, puis essue lou sanc, et met en la plaie lainne moillie en oile roset; et met defuer autre laine moillie en vin et en oile, et met sus les II coions, et met desus drapelz doublés, et le lie sus a tout le liien qui est selonc ceste forme:	And if the egg is assembled into two parts together, knowing that these are two ramises; then cut out the other part as you did with the first one evenly, then wash the blood away, and put on the other part wet with oil of roses; and put another piece of wool wet with wine and oil, and put on the two eggs, and put double sheets over them, and bind it all together according to this form:
Puis pren II drapelz, et les emple de laine charpie selonc ceste semblance et soient assemblez par cousture en la gorle des braies, et li uns des chiés preigne sus le fondement jusc’au dos, et li autres a la partie dou poignil; et li autre dui chief sus les II angres, et soit toute assemblee li restreinture en la boucle dou braier; et aucune fois est medicinee ceste ramice de cautere en leu de taille de fer, et est que tu preignes I cautere cultellaire subtil, et cope le cuir des coions, et soit eschaufez si com nos avons dit, si que li syfac blanc que contient l’aigue est descovers; si pren lou cautere selonc ceste forme, et perce celui syfac as oncines, et l’escorche a cest subtil cautere chaut:	Then take two sheets, and fill them with wool cotton according to this form and join them together by sewing in the girdle of the braies, and let one of the shoulders rest on the foundation up to the back, and the other to the part of the arm; and let the other two heads rest on the two angles, and let all be joined together by a strap around the girdle; and never is this ramice of cautery used in place of a iron bar, but you must use I cautery of the color of milk, and cut off the skin of the eggs, and scorch it with this fine cautery as we have said, so that the white syrup that contains the blood comes out; then take the cautery according to this form, and pierce that white syrup with little needles, and burn it with this fine cautery:
Et lou cope en toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que tu esraiches tout; et garde que li feus ne touche l’uef; et saiches que ceste oevre est plus salve; et mues gardans de decorrement de sanc, et muedres que li ovraiges de taille; et se nulle chose te fait contraire, ou aposteme chaus ou decorremens de sanc ou autre chose, si cure ce qui te fait contraire, selonc ceu qui est devant dit.	And heat the cup in all ways that you can, as long as it is scorched completely; and guard so that the fire does not touch the yolk; and know that this work is more safe; and be careful of the burning of the blood, and be careful that the incisions of the size do not; and if anything makes you contrary, or an abscess or a burn of the blood or another thing, heal what makes you contrary, according to what has been said before.
Et se li malaides est paourous, et ne vuet atendre cest ovraige por son horribleteit, si amenistre perforation, si com je te di, et est que quant tu es bien certains par les significations que nos avons dit que ramice aquouse est lai, si fai seoir le malaide sus I siege leveit; pues perce l’aposteme an la partie desoz a tout le spatumile large, et met la perforation dou lonc dou cors; et soit larges li pertus, si que toute li aigue corre fuer; puis met coton sus le leu, et le lie, et laisse por corre le remenant de l’aigue, puis le cure tant que li plaie soit sanee; et se li blainche toile ne laisse issir l’aigue en la bouche de la plaie, si covient que tu i boutes une penne ou l’estrument dont on trait l’aigue des ydropiques, de coi li forme est ci devant; et eslarge I poc la plaie, et saiches que li aigue revient, et est assemblee aprés VI mois ou enqui entor, et quant elle est assemblee si com devant, et ensi passera li malaides ses jors.	And if the patient is afraid and will not wait for this procedure because of its horror, then make a perforation as I have said, and it is that when you are sure by the signs that we have said that the ramose water is there, then place the patient on one raised seat; for the abscess comes in the part of the nose to all the spatumile large, and put the perforation in the long of the hole; and make the holes wide, so that all the water runs out; then put cotton in the place, and bind it, and let it run out the remaining water, then heal it as long as the wound is healthy; and if the white cloth does not allow the water to come out of the wound's mouth, then you must put a feather or the instrument with which they treat the water from the hydropses, so that it takes this form as described above; and widen the hole slightly, and know that the water returns, and is joined after VI months or more, and when it is joined in the same way as before, and so the patient's time will pass.
de l’aposteme des coions	from the appendix of the colon
Saiches que en la section de ceste ramice a paor em plusors dispositions, por coi il me semble que mues vaut c’on la laisse; et je vos dirai l’ovraige et les semblances de l’aposteme.	I know that in this part of the text there are many interpretations, so it seems better to leave it alone; and I will tell you about the work and the appearances of the appendix.
Je dis donques que maint aposteme vienent ou cors, et meismement as coions; et c’est par mout de cas.	I say that most appendicitis come from the bowels, and least often from the intestines; and it is by chance.
C’est a savoir par superfluiteit aigre et ague, qui est espandue as coions, ou de percussion; et est li color de l’aposteme selonc la color dou cors; et ne trueve point de dolor, et est aposteme grief; et par aventure est uns apostemes griés paourous et pierous, et de fuxe color, et aucune fois vient de nout d’artere, ou d’enfleure de voine.	It is to be known that by acrid and bitter superfluity that spreads into the intestines, or by percussion; and the color of the appendix depends on the color of the bowels; it does not cause pain, and is a grievous appendix; and sometimes an appendix becomes painful, piercing, and discolored, and never comes from a blood vessel, or swelling of a vein.
Quant c’est par nout d’artere, si est conus par la disposition d’aposteme chaut, quant tu la presses a tes dois; et ne covient mie que tu i touches.	When it is by a blood vessel, if you know the warm position of the appendix, then when you press it with your fingers; and it only deserves that you touch it.
Cil qui est fais d’enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition a l’expression dou touchement des dois, et puet om bien faire la taille sus ceste semblance, et sus les autres chars; et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l’uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l’uef.	Cil qui est fais d'enfleure de voine est conus par sa disposition à l'expression du toucher des deux, et puet on bien faire la taille sur ceste semblence, et sur les autres chars; et est que tu cope lou keur des coions, puis estent l'uef en haut, et le trai fuer dou blanc syfac, et delivre lou suspensoire de toutes pars de l'uef.
Se li uef est ja sodez avec ces chars nees, si covient donques que tu traies l’uef, et lou cope; et s’il est aers au syfac, ou en ceu qui est dedens les vasselz, si covient que tu delivre toute celle tenve, et la cope reondement.	The structure of the body is known by its arrangement in relation to the expression of touch on both sides, and it can be done well in terms of size on this appearance and on other characters; and that you remove the cause of the wound, then the flesh rises up high, and the white fluid is strong, and deliver the suspension from all parts of the flesh. The flesh has already been joined with these raised characters, so it is necessary that you draw the flesh and the cope; and if it is elevated towards the white, or in that which is inside the cases, it is necessary that you deliver all that is held, and the cope repeatedly.
Et se li naissance de la char est ou leu derrier, si covient que tu la copes toute, et estrai l’uef, si com nous avons dit.	And if the birth of the horse is from behind, then you should cut it all, and remove the membrane, as we have said.
Et quant tes ovraiges est acomplis, si emple la plaie de laine moillie en oile roset et en vin, puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when your work is completed, then employ the wound with wet wool in oil and wine, and then cure it with other remedies until it is healed.
de l’aposteme des coions	of the abscess of the testicles
Cis est uns apostemes envoloupez d’un envoloupement semblant a I borjon, avec le mollifiement des coions, et se muet li malaides griement quant il vait; et li cure de ceste maladie si est bien pres ausi paourouse com ceste ci devant, et toutevoie nos vos dirons l’ovraige de li, selonc ceu que li ancien firent.	This is an abscess enveloped by a wrapper resembling a bag of cheesecloth, with the softening of the testicles, and the patient grumbles much when he goes; and the treatment for this disease is so well concerned with fear as this above, and we will tell you the work of it, according to what the ancient one did.
Il covient que tu faices seoir lou malaide sus I siege aleveit, puis li boute le suspensoire des coions aval a tes dois, a tout le vasseil qui sont prochien a la verge, et les teigne li maistres, et les estende forment; puis cope au spatumile trenchant large dou traver endroit les vasselz, tant qu’il soient descovert, et puis escorche de chescune part, si com nos avons dit en l’estraction des arteres qui sont en temples; puis i fiche une aguille ou il ait I fil double, et le lie au premier leu ou li vis est venue, et le lie derechief a l’autre chief; puis les cope em mileu droitement, selonc la longesce dou cors, et en trai les moistors corrumpues; puis cure la plaie si com les autres ou on enjanre bowe, si que aucun vassel chiecent que norrissent l’un des coions; car par ceu n’i vient point de mal, et se a toz les vasselz vient vis, si covient traire les coions a tout les vasselz; si que li oes ne perde son norrissement por l’incision des vasselz, et sechent et ne se puient aidier.	It is necessary that you make the patient sit on a soft seat, and then dip the suspension of the testicles in water at your feet, to all the vessels which are near the penis, and dry them carefully; then cut off each part with a sharp spatula, as we have said for the extraction of arteries which are in temples; then he fixes it with a double thread of thread, and ties it to the first place where the vein has come, and quickly ties it to the other end; then he cuts it straight, according to the length of the body, and removes the corrupt humors; then cure the wound as the others where one bowels are not moved that they do not nourish a testicle; for by this there will be no loss of nourishment, and all the vessels come out, so that you do not need to worry about the incision of the vessels, and they dry up and do not want to help themselves.
de la routure dou syfac	about the surgery of the sick
Li avenemens de ceste ramice si est par la section que vient ou syfac, ou l’estension sus le ventre en la partie des angres, por coi li intestine dessendent de celle routure a l’un des coions; et ceste routure est ou dou syfac, ou de l’estension de li, et vienent ces II manieres de mout de causes: ou de percussion, ou de saut, ou de braire, ou de levement de grief faix, et par semblans choses; et li signes quant c’est de l’estension dou syfac, si est qu’il avient poc et poc, en lonc tens, et ne vient mie soudainnement; et est li apostemes igalz jusque vers le parfont, por ceu que li syfac apresse l’intestine.	About the surgery of the sick: If it is a section that causes the problem of syphilis, or an extension on the abdomen in the part of the angles, so that the intestines descend from that section to one of the loins; and this section is due to syphilis, or to the extension from it, and these two ways are caused by different means: either by percussion, or by jump, or by roar, or by pain caused by some thing, and similar things; and the signs when it is an extension from syphilis, if it is little by little, for a long time, and does not suddenly arrive; and the apostemes are even until near the end, so that the syphilis urgues the intestine.
Et li signes est quant c’est de la section dou syfac, qu’elle fait venir a l’encomencement dolor soudaine, et est li apostemes divers apparans, desoz le cuir pres, et c’est por l’issue de l’intestine et le cors au defuer dou syfac.	And the signs are when it is a section of syphilis that sudden pain comes, and the apostemes are different appearances, dislodging the skin; and this is due to the exit of the intestine and the body away from syphilis.
Et aucune fois dessent li cirbes avec l’intestine, et est retenus enqui, et fait grant dolor soffrir au malaide, meismement quant il est pressez.	And never do cut the circumcision with the intestine, and is held in-quest, and causes great pain to the patient, even when it is pressed.
Et en ces cures de fer a paor, por coi il s’en covient eschuir.	For in these treatments of iron, for fear of which they must be avoided.
Et li maniere de l’ovraige si est que tu comande ou malaide qu’il ramoine l’intestine a sa main au dedens en la plaie, s’il i puet rentreir; puis soit sovinez sus son col. entre tes mains, et lieve les cuixes; puis estent le keur au desus, et cope tout le cuir des coions dou lonc; puis boute dedens les leivres de la taille uncines selonc ceu que tu en as mestier por ovrir la plaie, et soit telz que li oes em puist issir; puis escorche lou syfac que est desoz lou cuir des coions, tant que li blans syfac dur soit descovers de toutes pars; puis boute ton doi indice en ceu qui enseut lou coion, en ceu qui est entre lou blanc syfac qui est desoz lou cuir de l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac, et depart ceu qui est derrier l’uef, et entre lou secont syfac; et pues muef a la main destre dedens lou keur des coions, et estent lou blanc syfac en haut a ta main senestre, et lieve l’uef a tout lou syfac devers la taille; et comande au ministre qu’il estende l’uef en haut, et deslie ceu qui est aers derrier le liement; et quier a tes dois s’il a point de l’intestine envoloupeit ou blanc syfac dur, et se tu en trueves aucune chose, si le boute au ventre desoz; puis pren une aguille ou il ait I gros fil fait de X filz, et la boute en la derriere partie dou syfac, qui est aprés lou cuir des coions; aprés la taille, puis cope les chiés qui apperent des filz, tant qu’il i ait IIII filz; puis les assemble l’un sus l’autre en maniere de croix, et en lie lou syfac, dont nos avons dit qui est desoz lou cuir des coions, d’un fort liien de II pars; puis envoloupe les chiés des filz, et les lie forment de II pars, si que nuls des vasselz que les norrissent ne puissent entrer en ous, que aposteme chaus n’i viegne; et met derechief le liien selonc le premier liien lonc II dois de celui, et aprés ces II liiens laisse dou syfac qui est desoz lou keur des coions le grant d’un doi; et aprés tout l’autre selonc la rondesce que li euf porte; puis cope en la partie qui est desoz le cuir des coions, tant qui li sans corre, et li bowe, si com nos avons dit ci devant; puis amenistre laine moillie en oile, et met em plaies, et i amenistre le liien que nos avons dit.	And in these treatments of iron, for fear that they must be avoided. For the way of the incision so that you command the patient that he keeps the intestine to his hand inside the wound, if he can enter; then is soft on his neck between your hands, and take care of the sutures; then is pulled above, and kop the skin of the scars long; then pour in the bile of the liver of a cow into the wound, and let it come out; then skinned the skin from all sides; then pour in the bile of the liver of a cow inside the scar, as much as the white skin is hard that covers the bile from all sides; then pour in your index hand into the incision between the scar and the bile, and between the second scar, and depart from behind the belly, and between the second scar; and with your right hand move it down inside the wound, and hold the bile up to your left hand, and pour out the bile on all the skin; and command the servant that he extends the bile above, and leave what is behind the loop; and look with your two hands if there is any involute or hard white skin, and if you do not find anything, then pour in the belly inside; then take a needle that has a thick thread made of XX threads, and pour it into the back part of the skin, which is behind the scar; after the liver, then kop the threads that appear from the wire, until there are IIII threads; then assemble them on top of each other in a cross shape, and bind the skin, which we have said is skinned from the skin of the scars; then wrap the threads around, and tie them together, so that no thread can enter that nourishes the scar, so that no chafing comes; and above all, the other one according to the circumference that the belly carries; then kop in the part which is behind the skin of the scars, until it is firmly bound, and let it bend, as we have said before; then pour molasses oil into the wound, and wrap it up with the thread that we have said.
Et aucune fois est cauterizez li blans syfac que nos avons dit, aprés l’incision, par doutance de decorrement de sanc.	And never is cauterized the white blood that we have said, after the incision, for doubt of decay of blood.
Car ce avient maintes fois, et laisse le liien tant qu’il chiece per lui; et s’il tarde au cheoir, si soit arosez d’aigue chaude, et met sus ceu que nos avons dit, tant qu’il chiece; puis cure la plaie d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez parfaitement.	For this often happens and leaves the ligature as long as it leaks itself; and if it delays at the leak, let it be raised by warm water, and put on that which we have said, until it leaks; then cure the wound with another cure, until it is completely healed.
de hernie carnouse	of hernia carnous
En ceste ramice ne vis je onques nul qui osast faire la cure par fer.	In this recipe I have never seen anyone dare to try to make the cure with fire.
Et li ancien dirent qu’ele est faite si com li ramice qui est ensamble la vis, en teil maniere que tu lie les vasselz, aprés la taille sus ous legierement au desoz; puis cope em mi, et cure l’aposteme de ceu qui oevre, tant que li vasselz chient; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the ancient ones said that it is done so as the ramie is joined together, in a certain way that you tie the chains, after cutting them lightly on the leg; then cut off and cure the abscess of him who has it, until the chains leak; and cure it as we have said, until it is completely healed.
Aucune fois vient routure ens angres, si com nos avons dit, et apert li leus; et ne dessent nulz des intestines as coions, et s’il en i dessent, c’est poc, et repaire toutes houres; et toutevoie s’il demoure trop en cest point, si croit li plaie ou syphac, tant que li intestine dessent; et ceu avient par l’estension dou syfac qui est as angres, si com nos avons dit, car il est estendus, puis est mollifiez et enflez li leus et apert; et li cure si est par cautere, si com nos avons devant dit; et aucune fois est curee par fer en ceste maniere: et est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos entre tes mains, puis cope le leu de la routure enfleit dou large selonc la quantiteit de III dois; et puis estrai le syfac qui est desoz le cuir que l’ensuet, puis pren lou rait et lou met sor le leu apparant dou syfac; et lou presse au parfont dou ventre, puis cout les II leus apparans dou syfac sus lou chief dou rait, et cout l’un et l’autre; puis estrai le chief dou rait, et ne coper point dou syfac ne n’estendre l’uef n’autre chose, si com je t’ai fait savoir en la cure de la ramice des intestines; puis le cure par la cure des plaies.	No time comes when the arteries burst, as we have said, and open their channels; and let no entrails flow into the bowels, and if they do flow, it is a little, and repair every hour; and yet, if he lingers too long in this place, he believes that the wound or syphac [syphilis] will come, as we have said, so that the intestines flow; and what happens by the extension of the syphac which is in the arteries, as we have said, for it is stretched, then it softens and swells their channels and opens them; and the cure is by cautery, as we have before said; and no time is cured by iron in this way: and it is that the patient lies often on his back between your hands, then cope the place of the burst with the large amount of III pieces; and then draw out the syphac which is under the skin that covers, then take a thread and tie it over the place of the burst syphac; and press it perfectly hard against the belly, then cut the two appearing channels of the syphac on his head of the thread, and cut the one and the other; then draw out the head of the thread, and do not cover the syphac or stretch the uvula [uterus] or any other thing, as I have told you in the cure of the ramose intestines; then cure it by the cure of wounds.
Et quant tu copes les filz, si le mundefie et cure la plaie, tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And when you cut the hair, if it is infected or healing the wound, until it is healed.
Li syfac est constrains, et n’a point d’apparance en la routure, et li cauteres est muedres en cest leu, et plus prochiens a salut.	The ointment is constant and has no appearance in the rupture, and the cauterization is moist in this place, and closer to salvation.
de l’amollissement dou cuir des coions	of the softening of the leather of the crotch
Maintes fois est amollis li cuirs des coions en aucuns homes, por ceu que les chars que sont dedens sont mollifiees, et est lait a veoir; et est mestier, quant on le vuet curer, c’on faice gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li cope le cuir qui est mollifiez sus le cuir natureil; puis assemble les II levres a une costure, et se tu vues, cout premier la superfluiteit dou cuir mollifiiez a III costures ou IIII fermement; puis cope entre les costures, et lou cure si com les autres plaies, tant qu’il soit sanez, et chient li fil.	Several times the leather of the scrotum is softened in some men, because the balls that are inside are softened and can be seen; and it is necessary, when you treat him, to make him lie on his back, and to cut off the soft leather over the natural leather; then join the two lips with one seam or three solid stitches; then cover between the seams, and treat him like other wounds until he is healed, and remove the thread.
dou chastrement	Dou cautere de feu comande au malaide qu’il laisse les poilz tant qu’il soient lons et igals; et s’il le poignent a lor nassance, se li estraint les eulz qu’il ne se muevent tant qu’il naissent.
Saiches que chastremens est escomeniez en nostre loi, et por ceu il me plairoit que je n’en parlasse mie en cest livre; et n’est necessaires fuer que por II manieres: dont l’une est que li mires en saiche respondre quant on li demandera, et en saiche la cure; et li autre, por ceu que nos avons sovent mestier de chastrement d’aucunes bestes por nos aidier, si com de bouc et de mouton et de chait et d’autres bestes.	For the fire cautery, instruct the patient to let the hairs grow long and even; and if they prick at their base, hold the eyes steady so they do not move until they grow.
Je dis donques que chastremens est fais selonc II manieres: ou par atraction, ou par fendure.	I say therefore that chastement is done in two ways: either by attraction or by a cut.
En celle que nos faisons par attraction, faisons nos seoir la beste en aigue chaude, tant que li coion soient mollifiez et pendant; puis les preing a ta main, tant qu’il soient remis et que tu ne les sentes plus.	In that which we do through attraction, let us sit the beast in warm water until the testicles are softened and still; then grip them with your hand, until they are set and no longer felt.
Du chastrement de taille: covient que tu teignes la beste, et li presse le cuir des coions a ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et cope sus chescun oef a I cop, quant tu les avras bien escorchiez; et i laisse aucun poc dou syfac et lou subtil syfac qui est sor les vasselz; et ceste maniere de chastrement est muedre que cele qui est faite par attraction, por ceu que a l’atraction demoure par aventure aucune chose des coions, par coi li beste desire luxure; puis cure la plaie tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Du chastement de taille: Il convient que tu t'enduites la bestiale, et presse le cuir des côillons à ta main senestre, puis lie le suspensoire, et couve sur chaque oie à je ne sais combien d'oies; laisse aucun petit pou du si-fac et du soub-tifac qui est sur les vasselins; et cette manière de chastement est mûre que celle qui est faite par attraction, pour ceu que à l'attraction demeure par aventure aucune chose des côillons, par coi la bestiale désire luxure; puis guéris la plaie tant qu'elle soit saine.
des hermofrodites	Of the chastisement of size: It is fitting that you anoint the bestial, and press the skin of the hoglets to your left hand, then tie the suspender, and cover each hoglet with I know not how many; leave no small poultice of the si-fac and sub-tifat which is on the vasselins; and this mode of chastisement is mature that which is done by attraction, for thisu that to the attraction remains by adventure nothing of the hoglets, by coi the bestial desires luxure; then heal the wound as long as it is healthy.
Hermofrodie est selonc II manieres as homes: l’une si est que entre les II coions apert ausi com li figure de la nature d’une femme, ou il ait poil, et aucunes fois en cort li urine.	Hermaphrodite is according to two ways like men: one is that between the two testicles are open as the shape of nature of a woman, or it has hair, and sometimes in urination.
Et li autre maniere si est en femmes, et ait sus lou poignil ausi com une verge et II coions.	And the other way is in women, and has on the breast as a penis and two testicles.
Et li cure de l’ome et de la fame si est que tu copes les chars ajostees toutes, et les cure si com autres plaies; en la seconde maniere, des homes dont li urine saut par lou cuir des coions, si n’a point de cure.	And the cure of the man and the woman is that you copulate the joined ones all, and the cure is so as other wounds; in the second way, from men whose urine jumps out through the skin of the testicles, there is no cure.
de la tentigene	of the tentacle
Tentigene est une chars ajostee sus la partie natureil, tant qu’elle est trop laide a veoir; et aucunes femmes l’ont ausi grant com une main, et c’est li cure.	is a joined one on the natural part, so much that it is too ugly to see; and some women have it also great like a hand, and that is the cure.
Il covient que tu teignes la superfluiteit de la tentigene a ta main ou as oncines, et la cope legierement; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que decorremens de sanc n’i viegne, puis le cure d’autre cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et a une autre char que naist a la bouche de la marris, et l’emple, et par aventure saut fuer, et est selonc la semblance d’une kowe, et por ceu l’apelerent li ancien «maladie kowee».	It is necessary that you take the superfluity of the tentacle to your hand or oncines, and copulate lightly; and do not go too completely perfect, that runs away of blood there is none, then the cure of another cure as long as it is sane; and at another joined one that comes out of the mouth of the married woman, and uses it, and perhaps jumps out, and is according to the appearance of a cow, and because of this they called it the "old cow disease".
Si covient que tu la copes, si com nos avons dit la tentigene, et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	If you need to cut it, as we have said about the tongue, and treat it until it is healthy.
de erratique	of irregular
Erratique si est quant li nature de la femme n’est mie percie, ou li pertus est petis; et est naturez par naissance, ou accidens par maladie que venue i est; ou c’est par char ajostee, ou dou syfac subtil ou espés, et est fais em parfont en la marris, ou en costez, ou desoz, ou que soit; et deffent le concevoir, et l’enfantement, et par aventure les flors a avoir; et li connoissance de ceu si est par le regart de la baile.	of irregular if the nature of the woman is not yet perceived, or the hole is small; and is characterized by birth, or accidental due to disease that has come; or it is by char (chastity) or subtle medicine or spice, and is perfect in marriage, or coast, or seed, or whatever; and prevents conception, and childbirth, and possibly flowers to have; and the knowledge of this one is through the gaze of the ball.
Se li estoupemens est prochiens apparans, si quier a tes dois ou au rait.	For if the stoop is close and apparent, whether it is at your two sides or above.
S’il est dou syfac subtil, et il est prochiens as II leivres, si te haste, et la ront ensi: met tes II dois indices ensamble, et li femme soit sus son dos, espandues ses jambes; puis estent les II leivres forment, tant que li subtilz syfac soit rons, et soit overs li estoupemens; puis pren laine, et la moille en oile, et la met sus le leu, et gise li femme a home chescun jor, si qu’il ne puist souder.	If it is subtle medicine, and it is close as the leaves, if you hurry, and turn them inside: put your two fingers together, and the woman is on her back, spreading her legs; then form the two leaves, until the subtle medicine is wet, and the stoop is overcome; then take wool, and moil it in oil, and put it on the spot, and lie the woman on her back every day, so that he cannot hold.
Et se li syfac est dur et espés, si covient que tu lou copes au spatumile semblant a foille de mirte.	And if the remedy is harsh and thick, then it is necessary that you take a kind of spa water resembling a mint leaf.
Se li estoupemens est de char nee, si la sospent a l’oncine et la cope; et aies les medicines estainchans sanc, si com acaice, sanc de dragon, encens, ensamble abun d’uef; puis amenistre une caine de plonc large, si que li plaie ne puisse souder; et ensi soit longement, et li amenistre une tente de lin sec; puis soit curez d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the stinging is of fire, then you should hang it on a chain and dip it; and add medicines that stop pain, like dragon's blood, incense, and glue mixed with alum; then put a large cloth, so that the wound does not heal; and let it be for a long time, and then add medicine until he is well.
Et quant en la marris vient char nee, si la covient coper selonc ceste maniere, se ce n’est apostemes enchancrez.	When the woman is pregnant, and you cover her according to this method, unless it is an abscess.
Car a l’aposteme enchancreit qui est en la marris, ne doit on touchier de feir.	For in the case of an abscess that is in the womb, one must not touch fire.
des emorroides	hemorrhoids
Emorroydes sont overtures de voines dont sans cort acostumeement, et quant les emorroydes sont vielles si devienent thelul; et nos avons jai dit en la division les semblances d’aus, et les signes, et je dirai ci celles qui resoivent curation.	are openings of veins, from which, without the use of a knife, and when the hemorrhoids are old, they become inflamed; and we have already spoken in the division about the appearance of arrows, and signs, and I will say here those that bring about healing.
Je di que les emorroides et li thelul, quant il sont em parfont en la marris, et il n’aperent au sentir, si n’est mie li cure par fer.	I say that hemorrhoids and the thump are perfect in the marriage, and they do not appear in feeling unless it is cured by fire.
Cil qui sont a la bouche de la marris, c’on puet sentir, sont cil c’on puet curer.	Those who are at the mouth of the vagina can be felt, and those who can be cured are cured.
Il covient donques que tu mettes la femme en une maison froide, puis estent l’altelul as tenailles, et le cope en ses racines, puis poudre sus medicines restraignans sanc, si com acaice et sanc de dragon et encens, et semblans choses; puis boute ses piez a la paroit une houre, puis la met en aigue froide; et se decorremens de sanc i vient, si la fai seoir en une decoction de sumac et d’escorce de pomes grenates et de gales et de semblans choses, et puis pren farine d’orge, et la confis avec miel et aisil, et en fai I emplaustre sus son dos.	Therefore, you should put the woman in a cold house, then tie the thump with a rope, and cut it at its roots, then sprinkle medicines that restrain blood, as we have done, and blood of dragon and incense, and similar things; then pour water on her feet for an hour, then put her in cold water; and if the blood comes out, you should make her sit in a decotion of sumac and bark of pomegranates and gall and similar things, and then take barley flour, and confound it with honey and so, and make an ointment of it and put it on her back.
Et se il estainche, c’est boin.	And if it stops, that's good.
Se ceu non, se li fai aerdre ventouses au dos et as mameles sens ferir; puis pren lainne, et la moille en jus de plantain ou en jus d’aglentier avec vin viel, et fai aerdre au leu.	And if it does not stop, blow on the back with ventilators without hurting them; then take another, and the juice of plums or of hawthorn with old wine, and blow at the place.
Et quant li aposteme repose, si cure lou leu d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez; et celle qui est apelee «albathir» est rouge, et est semblans a I chief aspre, si le covient coper si com j’ai dit le thelul; et puis lou cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when the abscess has healed, keep the place oiled until it is well; and that which is called 'albatyr' is red, and resembles a sharp chief, so cover it as I have said in The Book of Simple Remedies; and then oil it until it is well.
des apostemes de la marris	the abscesses of the married woman
Maintes manieres d’aposteme vienent en la marris, si com chancre et aposteme pierous et herpes et estiomenes et fistules et emorroides et aposteme chaut, et plusors autres maladies que j’ai dit en la division.	Various kinds of abscesses come in the married woman, such as plaguey and piercing abscess, herpes and estias and fistula and hemorrhoids and hot abscess, and many other diseases that I have mentioned in the division.
Il covient donques que je die en cest traitier l’aposteme chaut qui vient en la marris, qui n’est mie des apostemes que coillent bowe; et se tu vues savoir l’ovraige de fer, si regarde se li apostemes est agus en l’encomencement de sa venue, et plain de chalor et de fievre, et s’il devient rouge se tu le pues veoir.	It is therefore necessary that I say in this treatise about the chest that comes with the wife, which is not an abscess that boils; and if you know the work of iron, then look at the abscess is hot when it begins to come out, and full of heat and fever, and if it turns red you can see it.
Adonques ne te haster mie de percier, mais lou fais meurer tant que li dolor soit apaisie; et puis fai seoir lou malaide sus I siege, et ait II petis sieges ou il se cline, et apoie sus son dos et assemble ses piez as parties defuer la jambe; et soient ses cuixes espandues, et mette ses braz desoz ses genous, et les lie bien d’un boin liien; puis succe li baille devers lou destre costeit, et i amenistre l’estrument dont on oevre la bouche de la marris, de coi ci aprés vient li forme; et covient que quant tu i vues amenistrer cest estrument, que tu fiches le rait premier ens por savoir la parfondeté de la marris, si que ceu qui entre ens de l’estrument n’i viegne plus em parfont qu’il ne doit, et qu’il ne blece la malaide; et se li estrumens est plus grans, si covient covrir la parfondesce de la marris de drapelz, si que li estrumens ne li grieve; et covient qu’il mette le cornet de l’estrument au desus, et qu’il teigne l’estrument.	So then you should not hurry to pierce it, but let it die until the pain is relieved; and then have the sick person sit on II small chairs or beds where they lean their legs away from the leg; and let their knees be spread, and tie them well with a good rope; then bring the mouth of the instrument that is used for the mouth of the wife to here afterwards comes the form; and it is necessary that when you introduce this instrument, you stick the rod first by to know the depth of the wife, so that what enters through the instrument no longer comes in as deeply as it should, and does not wound the sick person; and if the instrument is larger, then cover the depth of the wife with cloths so that the instrument does not hurt her; and it is necessary that he put the cone of the instrument on top, and dunk the instrument.
Et quant li apostemes apert, et on lou fent a la main mol, si le covient coper au chief, au spatumile leit; et quant li bowe est vuidie, si covient que tu mettes en la plaie tentes moillies en oile roset, ou en oile vert sec; et met la tente fuer de la plaie au parfont de la marris, et met par defuer sus la marris et sus le poignil lainne nette moillie en aigue ou malves soient cuites; puis le cure aprés II jors d’oignement avenant a ceu, tant qu’il soit sanez; et aucune fois leve on la marris et la plaie par clistere d’aigue et de miel, et puis d’aigue ou racines de lis et aristologe longe soient cuites; puis reveigne a l’oignement.	And when the abscess is opened and the hand is wet, if it is convenient that you cover the head with a cloth, lead the sputum away; and when the bowels are empty, if it is convenient that you put wet tents in oil of roses or green oil, dry them outside the wound, and place the tent completely over the wound and over the other hand and moisten it well with water or cooked mallows; then cure him after two days of ointment coming before this, as long as he is healthy; and never raise the wound and the skin with an alcohol sponge and honey, and then with water or roots of licorice and aristolog long are cooked; then remember to the ointment.
Et se li plaie est reponue en la marris, si covient que tu te gardes de cuire de fer, mais cure la si com nos avons dit en la division.	And if the wound is healing in the scar, you must keep yourself from cooking with iron, but cure it as we have said in the division.
de l’enfantement	of birth
Mestier est premier a la baile qu’elle conoisse la figure de l’enfantement natureil, et li signes si est quant tu vois la femme apresser aval, et desire odorer l’ar: adonques se haste li enfes de fuer issir; adonc saiches que cil enfantemens est selonc la figure natureil, et est li issue soz son chief, et li secondine avec lui; et quant tu vois ces signes, si covient presser legierement son ventre, si que li enfes isse tost; car quant il dessent sus son chief, si ist li secondine avec lui, et est mondee li marris de ses superfluitez par bone mundification; et cist qui vient autrement ne vient mie naturelment.	For the art of midwifery, it is necessary that she knows the natural figure of childbirth, and the signs when you see a woman hurry down there, and desires to smell air: then the baby is soon coming out; so you know that these births are according to the natural figure, and the issue is from her head, and the second with him; and when you see these signs, so it is necessary to gently press her belly, so that the baby comes quickly; for when he descends on his head, so does the second with him, and the married man purges his excesses by good purification; and what comes otherwise does not come naturally.
Car il vient aucune fois sus ses piez, et vient fuer li cors ou li chiés, et les mains, ou il vient sus son ventre, ou sovin, et est convertis par aventure sor son col, et par autres figures malvaises; si est mestier a la baile qu’elle soit saige et subtilz en ces choses, et se warse d’error et de decevement, et je vos mostrerai toutes les figures coment on li doit aidier.	For it does not come once on its feet, and comes from the chest or shoulders or hands, or comes on its stomach, or often, and is turned around by accident on its neck, and in other evil shapes; so it is necessary for midwifery that she be wise and subtle in these things, and guard against error and delusion, and I will show you all the figures how to help them.
Se li enfes vient sus son chief par issue natureil, et li femme enfante griement, et li vertus de li est foible, si la fai seoir sus une selle, ou les femmes la tienent; et arose sa nature d’oile ou fenugreic soit cuit, et puis boute li baile entre ses dois le petit spatumile dont ci est li forme:	If a man falls upon his head by a natural fall, and the woman gives birth with great pain, and the virtue of him is weak, so let her sit on a saddle, or the women hold it; and then extract his seed with oil or fenugreek that has been cooked, and then pour it between his two little sputums, of which this form is made:
et fende la secondine, et cope a son ungle tant que li moistors qui est ens corre fuers; et preint lou ventre de la femme tant que li enfes dessende, et s’il ne dessent, si covient clisterizer la femme de muscillaige de fenugrec avec oile de sisament; puis la fai preindre et esternuer de condisi, et tien sa bouche et son neis une houre: si istra maintenant l’enfes.	If a woman sits on a saddle, or the women hold it; and then extract his seed with oil or fenugreek that has been cooked, and then pour it between his two little sputums, of which this form is made: and split the second one, and chop off his nail as much as the moisture that is inside comes out; and squeeze the woman's belly until the baby pees, and if she doesn't pee, it is necessary to massage her with fenugreek oil with sesame oil; then make her squeeze and shake for an hour: now the baby will come.
Et se les II mains issent fuer, si covient que tu les ramoinne legierement poc et poc; et s’elles n’i puent entrer, si met la femme sus I siege, et li lieve les piés en haut; puis deboute le siege sus terre, et teigne on la femme, qu’elle ne chiece au deboutement; et se li mains n’i puet entrer, et li enfes muert, si li cope les mains au couteil qui est ci devant mis, et estrai l’enfant, et ramoine igalment.	And if the two hands come out, then it is necessary that you pull them gently little by little; and if they cannot enter, then put the woman on a chair, and raise her feet up; then take off the seat from the ground, and tie the woman so that she does not fall down; and if the hands cannot enter, and the child dies, then cut the hands with the knife that is placed in front, and pull out the child, and pull them both evenly.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses piés	in the delivery of the child on its feet
Quant li enfes vient sus ses piez, si lou covient bouter en haut; et puis le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit igalz; puis preigne I des piez et l’estende poc et poc.	When the child comes out on its feet, then it is necessary to turn it upside down; and then pull it little by little until it is even; and then spread its legs apart and stretch it slightly.
Cant il saut jusc’as cuixes, si la comande a preindre, et la fai esternuer de condisi; si saut fuer, se Deus vuet.	Can't he jump just as high as his knees, then he is to be commanded to bend, and made to tremble by wind; if he jumps, then God will help him.
Et s’il n’ist fuer si com nos avons dit, si le torne poc et poc, tant qu’il soit selonc la figure natureil.	And if it does not turn out as we have said, then let it be turned little by little, until it is back in its natural position.
Car adonques ist il legierement.	For now it is light.
Et s’il ne vient fuer si com nos avons, dit si pren muscillaige de altee, et oile de sisament, et gomme fondue, et broie tout en I mortier; et met sus la nature de la femme dedens et defuer cest oignement, puis la fai seoir en aigue tede jusque desoz les costelz; et quant elle est moillifie desoz, se li fai I coliere de mirre, et li met desoz, et li laisse une houre; puis la fai seoir sus I siege, puis la fai esternuer et estraint sa bouche et son neis, et li preint le ventre legierement, car li enfes saut maintenant.	For now it is light. And if it does not come out as we have said, then take musk of aloes, and oil of sesamum, and gum melted, and grind them all together in a mortar; and put on the nature of woman within and make this ointment; then let her sit in water till she is soiled; and when she is moist, let her sit in mirrrow-water, and let her stay, and then let her sit in a chair; then let her jerk and strain her mouth and nose, and squeeze her belly lightly, because the cure is now ready.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus ses genous	of the delivery of the child between his legs
Quant li enfes vient en ceste forme, si i mette li baile ses mains poc et poc; puis soit sovinee sus son col, et li pendent li piez aval, et soit gisans sor I lit; et plie ses mains poc et poc, et puis li preint les mains sus lou ventre, et li oste les cussins desoz, tant qu’elle soit appareillie aval; et se li enfes ne saut, si pren ses piez et li muef forment, puis li muef lou ventre amont, puis i boute tes mains; et ewe l’enfant poc et poc; et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse.	When the child comes in this form, if I put the bail its hands poky and poky; then be Sovinee on his neck, and let him hang down his feet, and let him lie on my bed; and bend its hands poky and poky, and then take its hands on his belly, and let him tie the cussins behind, until it is stripped down; and if the child does not jump, so take its feet and move them, then move his belly upstream, then I pour your hands; and give the baby poky and poky; and command the woman that she prays as the child is going.
de l’issue de l’enfant qui vient dou large une main pendant	When the child is born with one hand extended,
I covient engignier a ramener la main: s’on ne la puet ramener, si fai lever la femme, et aler; s’elle ne puet aler, si la fai gesir sus I lit, et li deboute les jambes forment; puis amenistre lou muscillaige que j’ai conteit; et s’elle n’enfante, si la fai seoir sus I siege, puis estudie au rameneir la main; et ewe l’enfant selonc la figure natureil, et la fai esternuer, et li comande qu’elle se preigne tant que li enfes isse fuer.	When the child is born with one hand extended, I come to bring back the hand: if it cannot be brought back, let the woman get up and go; if she cannot go, let her lie down on the bed, and stretch out her legs; then put the muscle-twister that I have mentioned; and if she does not give birth, let her sit on a chair, then try to bring back the hand; and according to the natural form of the child, make him sneeze, and command her to pray until the child is born.
de l’issue de l’enfant sus son col, et ait espandues ses mains, et sa faice tornee devers lou dos sa mere	of the baby's delivery through its mother's groin, and it spread its hands, and its face turned towards her back
I covient que li baile teigne sa main, puis le torne poc et poc, et l’ewe legierement; et quant il est igalz, si met sus la nature muscillaige de altee et oile, si com nos avons dit, puis li comande qu’elle se mueve poc et poc; et quant tu avras ce fait, si la fai seoir sus I siege, et li comande k’elle se preigne; et la fai esternuer.	I command that the boy grasps his mother's hand, then he turns it little by little, and lightly rubs it; and when it is even, if you put it on the muscled nature of a high place and oil, as we have said, then order him to move it little by little; and when you have done this, if you make her sit in a chair, and order her to lean; and she will shiver.
de ceste meisme maniere a tout la secondine	of this same method for all the second part
Quant il vient fuer en ceste maniere a tout la secondine, si cope la secondine a ton ungle, tant que li moistors soit vuidie; et se li enfes pent sus sa faice et sus son col, si la cope des la boude, qu’elle ne soit retenue, et muere li enfes; puis boute l’enfant dedens, tant que tu l’aies mis si com il covient, et comande a la femme qu’elle se preigne aucune fois: adonques si istra legierement.	When it comes in this way for all the second part, if the water is empty, order the woman to lean back, and keep her like that; then put the child inside, as it should be, and order the woman not to lean back at all: then she will turn lightly.
de l’issue des gemelz	of the twin's issue
Saiches que gemeil naissent maintes fois, et aucune fois en naissent III ou IIII; et ceu n’est mie estrainge chose, et poc avient.	That twins are sometimes born with three limbs and sometimes with four, which is not an unusual thing, and that this has never been a strange thing and does not happen often.
Dui sont estrainge chose, et ne vivent mie, se poc nom; je sai ceu, qu’il soient multipliiet, et sont desevrez par lou syfac qui les devise, qui est liiez a la boude; et aucune fois issent ausi naturelment com uns tous sous, si com nos avons dit.	Two are strange things, and they do not live long, unless one of them is dead, for which I know the cause, namely, that they have multiple limbs, and they are defective because of the leech who devises them, who is tied to the bouge; and they are not born naturally as all others, but rather by a method like ours, as we have said.
Et s’il issent griement, si la cure si com nos avons dit, et soit li baile subtilz, et faice tost et legierement ceu qu’elle fait; et faice ensi com il vaut mues a salut.	If they are born with pain, if the cure is as we have said, and if the doctor is subtle and does it quickly and lightly, then he should do so in such a way that it saves them from death.
de plusors enfans	of many children
Aucune fois sont formez en la marris I ou II ou III ou IIII ou V ou VI ou VII, ou plusors jusc’a XV, et sont tout formeit en forme d’enfant par le mesurement dou saige glorious, et couvient que li baile saiche tout ceu, car par aventure semblans chose li avient; si faice selonc ceu qu’il covient.	That many children are sometimes formed in the womb one or two or three or four or five or six or seven, or more up to XV, and they are all formed in the form of a child by the measurement of the wise glory, and that the doctor knows everything about them, for there may be strange things; so he should do as he wants.
de l’enfant mort	of the dead child
Quant tu cures la femme de l’enfant mort ou ventre, si com j’ai dit en la division, et il ne vient fuers, et tu es constrains d’ovraige de mains; si covient que tu saiches se li femme est de saine vertut, et n’ait accident ou elle ait paor de mort; si covient que li femme soit sovinee sus son dos, et soit ses chiés enclins aval, et les jambes levees; et li ministre la teigne de II pars, ou elle soit liie au lit si qu’elle ne soit traite au dessendement de l’enfant; puis frotez la bouche de la marris d’oiles moistes avec muscillaige de altee et de fenugrec et semence de lin, puis oigne li baile ses mains de ces oiles et de ces muscillaiges; puis les boute en la marris legierement, puis quiere I leu ou elle boute les oncines que soient covenaubles a ceu, et pren warde se li enfes est apparilliez qu’il dessende sus son chief; si fiche les oncines en ses eulz ou en son col ou en sa bouche ou en som palais ou desoz la barbe ou en la forcele ou pres des costez, et se li dessendemens est sus piez, se li fiche ou poignil et as costes moienes; et covient qu’il teigne l’oncine a sa main destre, et mette la corbeure entre ses dois de la senestre main, et li boute a tout sa main legierement, et fiche l’oncine en aucun de ces leus que nos avons dit, tant qu’il viegne a la chose vuide; et c’est li forme de l’oncine:	When curing the wife of a dead child or stomach, as I have said in the division, and it does not come out, and you are compelled to work with your hands; if it is necessary that you know that the woman is of sound health, and she has no accident or from which she could die; if it is necessary that the woman is loaded on her back, and her knees are bent forward, and her legs are raised; and the minister bathes her from both sides, where she lies in bed so that she can be treated for the falling of the child; then rub her mouth with moist oils with althaea and fenugrec and flax seed, then oil her hands with these oils and these muscillaiges; then pour them into her mouth lightly, then wants I to let it or he pour the onions that are appropriate for this, and take care that the child is dressed that he falls on his head; then puts the onions in his hair or in his neck or in his mouth or in his palace or cuts his beard or in the forelock or near the ribs, and the falling is on the feet, then he pierces it or sticks it and cuts it at the cost of; and it is necessary that he bathes the onion in his right hand, and puts the basket between her two hands with his left hand, and pours it lightly with all his hand, and puts the onion in any of these places that I have said, until he comes to the empty thing; and this is the form of the onion:
puis fiche encontre I autre oncine, ou le tier se tu en as mestier, si que li estractions soit igalz; et puis l’estent igalment en movant d’une part et d’autre, por mues issir, et soit li oncines dentez por mues tenir, si com ci est li forme:	and here comes the second sentence.
Et s’il en demoure une partie, si oigne li baile aucuns de ses dois d’oile, et les boute en celle partie, et traie l’autre partie; et s’il en i demoure point, si met cest oncine ou plus haut leu, et fai ceu tant qu’il s’en isse tout fuers.	And if a part of it remains stationary, then anoint some of its two sides with oil and press them together, and pull the other side; and if no part of it remains stationary, then place this oncine higher up or lower down, and make it like this until it comes out completely.
Et se l’une mains vient devant l’autre, et il ne puet ramener por l’estreignement, si covient que tu envoloupes sus I drapeil, tant qu’il isse tote; puis la cope en la jointure de la plante ou au coute, et ensi covient que tu faices en l’autre main, et as II piés.	And if one hand comes before the other and cannot be brought back by restriction, then you must wrap it in two sheets until it comes out completely; then put the cap on the joint of the sole or at the wrist, and do the same to the other hand, and to the feet.
Et se li chiés de l’enfant est gros et il est estrois en l’issue, ou il ait ou chief aigue assemblee, si covient que tu boute le spatumile espinous entre tes dois, et fent le chief et estrai l’aigue; ou tu la ront a l’estrument qui est apelez «almidach», de coi li forme vient avec les estrumens ou chapistre qui est aprés cestui; et ensi meisme faice se li enfes a grant chief naturelment; et puis traie fuer les osses as tenailles, et se li chiés saut fuer et il estraint a la forcele, si soit fendus, tant que li moistors qui est ou pis issue fuer; et s’elle ne puet issir, si le cope par pieces au mues que tu pues; et s’il est enflez au ventre ou desoz les costez, si covient que tu lou perces tant que li moistors corre.	And if the child's pelvis is large and it is stuck in the birth canal, or if there is a sharp accumulation of head, then you must press the thorn-like spur between your two hands, and make the head come out and draw out the sharp point; or you put it on with the instrument called "almidah", so that the shape comes out with the instruments or paste after this one; and in the same way I make the child's birth naturally large; and then pull the bones with nails, and if the pelvis is forced and stuck, so it is split into pieces until the moisture runs; and if it cannot come out, then cut it off piece by piece that you can; and if it swells in the abdomen or comes out of the sides, then it is necessary to pierce it until the moisture flows.
Et se li enfes est sus ses piez, si est li attraction legiere, et li adrecemens a la bouche de la marris est legier.	And if he falls on his feet, then is the light आकर्षण, and the treatment is at the mouth of the wound.
Et s’il est estrois au ventre ou au pis, si couvient que tu l’estraies a I drapeil envoloupeit sus la main; et fent le ventre ou le pis, tant que li moistors qui i est corre; et se li autre membre sont osteit, et li chiez demoure, si boute li baile sa main em parfont de la marris, et le traie jusc’a la bouche de la marris; puis i boute I oncine ou II, et le trai fuer; et se li bouche de la marris est retrecie por aposteme chaut qui i est venus, si n’i covient mie travillier, ains covient amenistrer choses moistes et grasses; et li amenistre emplaustres, et siece en aigue mollifians et amoistans.	If he falls on his stomach or back, then you shall draw it with the cloth wrapped around your hand; and cut the stomach or back until the moisture which is there comes out; and if another member is dislocated, and the joint remains, then bind the limb firmly with a bandage, and treat it to the mouth of the wound; then bind one or two more times, and treat it harder; and if the mouth of the wound has become constricted by an abscess which has come out hot, you shall not work it, but apply moist and greasy things; and apply poultices, and chop in water that is warm and moistening, and let it drip on the poultice.
Et se li enfes est sus son costeit, et tu le pues mettre igal, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit en l’enfant vif; et s’on nen ait pooir, si lou trai fuer par pieces, et n’i laissier rien de la secondine.	And if it is stuck on his rib cage, and you can make it even, then administer what we have said about the live child; and if one has no power, then let him be torn into pieces, leaving nothing of the second.
Et quant tu avras ce fait, se li amenistre ceu que nos avons dit ens apostemes chaus que vienent en la marris; et se decorremens de sanc vient, si soit mise en aigue restraignant, et li amenistre autres cures.	And when you have done this, administer what we have said about the cut-off feet that come in the mare's; and if the blood comes out, then it is restrained with water, and other cures are administered.
Et je vis une femme en cui ventre uns enfes avoit esteit mors, puis consut I autre sus celui, et refut mors li autres.	And I saw a woman in whose womb an infant had been killed, then consult another on that one, and kill the others.
Aprés lonc tens li vint uns apostemes en la boude, et enfla tant qu’il ovrit, et comensa a grant porreture.	After a long time, the twenty feet came out of the boat, and they began to grow large.
je fui apelez a la cure, et i pensai lonc tens, et ne pot soder li plaie.	I was called to treat it, and I thought for a long time, and I could not close the wound.
Je mis sus emplaustre de fort attraction, et en issit uns os, et aprés aucuns jors uns autres.	I put on a strong plaster, and after a few days more.
Je me mervillai mout, por ceu c’ou ventre n’a point d’os.	I marveled much, for this belly has no bones.
Si pensai que c’estoit des os d’un enfant mort.	I thought that it was the bones of a dead child.
Je quis la plaie, et en traï mains os, tant que li femme fut em millor point; et vesquit li femme lonc tens ensi, et issoit adés un poc de bowe dou leu; et je n’ai recordeit cest chapistre fuer que por ceu que, quant li maistres trueve une estrainge chose, qu’il i saiche mettre aide.	I wanted to examine the wound and, with my hands only, while the woman was in a better state; and I waited until the woman had been well for some time, and there was a little bow of hair at the place; and I do not remember this chaplet being used before except that, when the master tried an unfamiliar thing, he knew how to help.
dou ramener la marris a son leu	to bring the wife back to her bed
Ci aprés vient li forme dou pressor, a coi on ewe les livres; et a II tornans as II chiés des II liiens.	Then comes the form of tying up, so that we tie the limbs; and after two turns there are four ties.
Toutevoie, li cornes soit plus subtilz dou restrictoire, et soit fais de ebene ou de bux; et soit li bouche dou fust I doi de large, et li marge des arbres I doit, et de lonc une palme et demi; et enmi les II liemens soient dui ajostemens de cest meisme fust, qui soient fermeit en l’un et en l’autre, de demi palme de lonc ou un poc plus; et cist dui ajostement sont bouteit en la bouche de la marris por ovrir quant on torne les II cornes.	However, the rope is thinner than the restringent, and it is made of ebony or box; and the mouth of the tube must be wide enough, and the margin of the branches I must, and a long palm and a half or a little more; and these two ties are threaded through the mouth of the wife so that they open when the two horns are turned.
Une autre forme, a sa semblance plus subtilz et plus legiere, soit faite de fust de ebene ou de bux, selonc la semblance des tenailles; et ait as II chiés II ajostemens, si com tu vois, d’une palme de lonc, et II dois de large; et quant tu vues ovrir la marris a tout l’estrument, si fai seoir la femme sor I lit, les piez pendant et les jambes overtes, puis boute les II ajostemens ajostez ensamble en la marris, et tien le chief de l’estrument desoz entre ses cuixes; puis oevre ta main a tout l’estrument, si com tu as fait as tenailles igalment, selonc la quantiteit que tu vues ovrir la bouche de la marris, tant que li baile faice ceu qu’elle vuet.	Une autre forme, à sa ressemblance plus subtile et plus légère, soit faite de fuste d'ébène ou de buis, selon la ressemblance des tenailles ; et ait aux deux chiennes deux ajoutements, si tu le vois, d'une paume de long, et deux pouces de large ; et lorsqu'tu vois ouvrir la main à tout l'instrument, si fait de sier la femme sur le lit, les pieds pendant et les jambes ouvertes, puis bouttez les deux ajoutements ajoutés ensemble en la main, et tien le chef de l'instrument dosé entre ses cuisses ; puis ouvrez ta main à tout l'instrument, si tu l'as fait aux tenailles uniformément, selon la quantité que tu vois ouvrir la bouche de la main, jusqu'à ce que le balais fasse ce qu'elle veut.
Cist estrument sont tuit sormontez, et sont multiplies lor semblances; et quant li mires les ait apareilliez, tant est plus hastans li oevre, et plus haute as homes por lor quantiteit.	This is a medical instrument used for delivering babies. It is designed to facilitate the birth of a baby by providing a means to open and close the woman's hand, allowing for the delivery of the baby's head. The instrument consists of two long, slender handles connected at one end by a flexible joint, resembling a pair of tongs or pliers. At the other end of each handle is a large, flat surface, resembling a palm tree frond or leaf. When opened wide enough to accommodate the baby's head, the instrument can be placed around the mother's hand and used to gently pull the baby out. The shape and size of the instrument are tailored to the woman's hand, with the aim of making the delivery faster and easier for both mother and child.
Si ne despire mie l’estrument que tu ne l’aies apparelliet, car lor necessitez n’est mie escusauble.	If I do not despair of the instrument, you have not prepared it well, for its necessity is not excusable.
Quant li secondine est retenue a l’enfantement, si covient que tu comandes a la malaide qu’ele reteigne son alaine, et puis la fai esternuer de condisi, et li estraint tes mains a la bouche et au neis; et s’elle saut per ceu, bien est.	When the second is retained at birth, it is necessary that you instruct the patient to hold her tongue and then make her sneeze with a spray of water from a sponge, and keep your hands away from her mouth and nose; and if she spits because of this, it is good.
Se ceu non, si prent I pot, et fai I pertus ou cuvercle, et i met herbes que puissent ovrir la bouche de la marris, si com calament, rue, anis, camomille, cassialigne et centoire; toutes ces herbes, ou aucunes d’eles, soient cuites ou pot en aigue sus le feu; puis met une caine ou pertus dou pot, et l’autre chief en la bouche de la marris, et la teigne tant que li vapors viegne dedens la marris; puis la fai esternuer, si com nos avons dit.	If she does not spit because of this, I can take it, and make a cup or cover, and put herbs that can open the mouth of the mother, as calamus, rue, anise, chamomile, cassialine and centaury; all these herbs, or any of them, are cooked or made into a drink with water on the fire; then put one tube or cover with the pot, and the other in the mouth of the mother, and keep it until the vapors come out of the mother's mouth; then make her sneeze, as we have said.
Si saut li secondine hastanment.	If a person has had surgery.
Et s’elle remaint aprés ceste cure, et n’ist mie fuer, si comande a la baile qu’ele moille sa main senestre en oile de sesement ou en muscillaige de altee, et puis la boute en la nature, et quiere la secondine; et quant elle l’avra trovee, si la preigne et l’estende poc et poc droitement, si que li marris ne chiece a l’estraction; mais la covient movoir legierement a destre et a senestre, et puis traie; si venra et se desaerdra.	If, after this treatment, the person does not recover and continues to feel pain, order that he immerse his left hand in oil of sesame or in muscle extract [muscillaige] for a long time, then let it air out, and if he wants to use it, and when he has found it, if he twists and extends it little by little correctly, so that the joints do not ache during movement; but he should move it gently from side to side, and then stretch it; then he will unclench it.
Et se li bouche de la marris est jai estrecie, nos avons dit la cure d’esternuer, et de fumigation des herbes; et s’elle n’ist de tout ceu que nos avons dit, si garde que tu ne foloies au traire; mais il couvient que ceu qui est a la bouche de la marris, que tu le lies a la cuixe de la femme, puis la clisterize d’oignement tetrafarmaçon; si la porrira et remettra, et venra fuer; mais toutevoie, quant elle porrist si en vient male odor au stomac et au chief, et blece la malaide.	And if the patient's jaw is stiff and painful, we have mentioned the treatment of stretching and vaporizing herbs; and if it only responds to these treatments, you must take care not to follow the advice of those who recommend oiling the jaw; but it is necessary that he who has the jaw problem should lie on his back, then apply hot poultices; if so, she will loosen and recover, but nevertheless, when she will stretch herself, if there comes a bad smell from the stomach and head, and bleeds the disease.
Si covient donques fumigations covenaubles a ceu: aucun des anciens ont esproveit fumigation de cresson et de figues seches.	If it is necessary, then there are appropriate fumigations for him: no one has ever experienced a fumigation of nettle and dried figs.
Li forme de l’estrument a coi on fumige la femme a la retenue des flors et de la secondine si est ceste:	The form of the instrument to which you will add the smoke of the flowers and the second one if this is it:
Et est de voirre semblant a une caine, et met on le chief subtil en la nature, et les chiés larges sus le feu; et soit li fumigations sus les charbons, et la teigne tant qu’elle soit gastee, et rencomence une autre.	And it is like the smoke of a dog, and put the head in the middle, and the shoulders wide by fire; and let the fumigation be on the coals, and the skin until it is spent, and start another.
de percier lou fondement	to pierce the foundation
Maint enfant naissent qui n’ont mie le fondement perciet, ains l’ait estoupeit uns subtilz syfac: si covient donques a la baile qu’ele perce celui syfac a son doit, et ne lou perce mie de spatumile agut, et garse le lacement qu’elle ne le touche; puis met sus lainne moillie en vin et en oile, puis la cure d’oignement tant qu’il soit sanez.	For many children are born who have not had the foundation pierced, but a skilled surgeon pierces it for him: if it is necessary at the ball to pierce that skilled surgeon on his right, and does not pierce him with a spatulum, and protects the lancing so that he does not touch it; then put on another moistened cloth in wine and oil, and then cure the wound until it is healthy.
Et se tu doutes qu’il ne restoupe, si met ou pertus une caine de plonc, et li laisse mains jors, et soit ostee quant li enfes vuet aler en chambres.	And if you doubt that it will not recover, put a splint on the leg, and let it hang by the hand, and be careful when it walks upstairs.
Et aucune fois vient cist estoupemens de soudement de plaie ou d’aposteme; si covient coper celui soudement: si soit curez, si com nos avons dit de la caine de plonc.	And there is no risk of sudden death from a wound or abscess; if it is necessary to cover the wound: if it is treated, as we have said, with a splint.
de la fistule dou fondement	from the fistula at the foundation
Fistules qui vienent desoz le fondement sont nodation, et groissor que vienent delez lou fondement defuer, ou en l’espaice des II parties, si a une fistule ou plusors; et quant celle nodation est anciene, si aoeuvre, et encort moistor awouse blainche ou subtilz bowe, et aucune fois sont ces fistule persans; et sont conues par ceu qu’il en ist ou egestion ou ventositeit quant li malaide fait egestion, et par aventure en saut uns vers.	Fistulas that come from the fundament are a nodulation, and more painful than those that come from the fundament, or in the space between the two parts, if there is one fistula or more; and when this nodulation is old, if it is opened, and then moistened with a white or subtle liquid, and never does this fistula persist; and they are caused by the person who has an emission or wind, sometimes towards.
Et si a fistules que percent jusc’a la vessie, et jusc’a la moitiet de la verge; et parvienent jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, et jusc’a nout de la kowe.	And if they piercing through reach the bladder, and just to half of the penis; and come up just to the junction of the scrotum, and just to the nape of the neck.
Et ensi conoist on la fistule persant au fondement, et ne mie persant: et est que tu boutes ton doi indice ou fondement, et boute une aguille subtil d’arain ou de fer en la fistule quant il n’i a tortuositeit.
