And thus know you when the fistula pierces to the foundation and not further; and it is that you stick your second finger or foundation, and stick a fine needle of bronze or iron into the fistula when there is no twist.
Et s’il ait tortuositeit, si i boute une tente de plonc subtil, ou I poil de cheval, tant que tu sentes la tente ou le poil a ton doit; et se tu ne le sens, et il ne vient dou pertus egestion ne ventositeit ne ver, si com nos avons dit: saiches qu’elle ne perce mie; si te haste dou curer.	And if it has a twist, if you stick a tenet of thin string, or I hair of horse, as long as you feel the tenet or hair on your finger; and if you do not feel it, and no perforation or emission or vision comes, so as we have said: know that it does not pierce; and if you hurry to cure.
Et quant li fistule est persans jusc’a la vessie ou jusc’a conduit de l’urine, si en saut li urine, et ne puet soudeir par medicines.	And when the fistula reaches just to the bladder or just to the urinary conduit, if then the urine jumps out, and cannot be held back by medicines.
S’elle est percie jusc’a la jointure de la cuixe, si est li tente venans jusc’au leu; s’il n’i a tortuositeit et li invention de la dolor entor, si est qu’il en ist adés bowe, et n’i vaut medicine ne soudement par oignement; et en ces fistules persans n’a point de cure fuer que labor, et vaniteit des folz mires qui s’en entremettent.	If it is pierced just to the join of the loins, then he must try going up to the right place; if there is no twisting and the pain does not come from the entrails, then he is already bowing and should not expect a cure by medicine or sudden remedy through touch; and in these persistent fistulas there is no cure except toil, and the vanity of foolish people who meddle with them.
En celle qui n’est mie persans et n’est mie anciene, a esperance de saniteit par fer, si com j’ai esproveit, et est que li malaides gise entre tes mains sus son dos; et li lieve les jambes jusque sus ses cuixes, et ait ses cuixes enclinees a son ventre; puis boute une tente d’arain, ou de plonc s’il i a tortuositeit, tant que tu saiches ou li tente vient.	If it is not persistent and is not old, there is hope for health by iron, as I have experienced, and that is that the patient lies between your hands on his back; and he raises his legs up to his loins, and bends his loins towards his belly; then pour a pitcher of rain, or of water if there is twisting, as long as you know where the piercing comes from.
Se li malaides la sent entor le fondement, si covient que tu i boutes ton doi indice, se sens adonques que li tente l’ait perciet; et soit descoverte ou tu sens entre ton doit le syfac ou la char, adonques saiches qu’elle est persans; si n’i travillier mie c’on ne la puet saner.	If the patient has pain in the foundation, then it is appropriate that you put your index finger there, so that you can feel the pulse beat; and if you cover or uncover between your thumb and the syfac or char, then you know that it is persisting; if not, then it will not be cured without working on it.
On dist toutevoie c’on em puet bien saner aucuns, mais ce avient poc; et li aide c’on i fait, si est c’on eschaufe le cautere subtil selonc la largesce de la fistule, si com il est devant dit; et le boute tout chaut en la fistule, tant qu’il viegne delez le fondement; et faice ceu II fois ou III, tant que tu saiches que ces chars fautrees soient arses, qui sont semblant a une penne d’oiseil; et puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre, tant que celle chars isse fuer, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char et soudant.	If the patient has pain at the base, then it is appropriate that you place your index finger there so that you can feel the pulse beat; and if you cover or uncover between your thumb and the syfac or char, then you know that it is persistent; if not, it will not be cured without working on it. Now, for those that can be well healed, but this only happens sometimes; and the help that is given to them, is that the subtle fire is heated according to the width of the fistula, as it has been said above; and pour it directly into the fistula, until it comes out at the base; and do this twice or three times, until you know that these chars made are burned, which look like a bird's feather; and then treat with wet tar, until those chars come out, and then bind them together.
S’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If he is healthy, then that is good.
Se ceu, nom autrement ne puet estre sanez; et se li tente entre, et ne perce jusc’au doit qui est ou fondement, et a entre ton doi et la tente une coverture espesse de char ou de syfac, et tu vois la fistule a ceu qui enseut la coverture dou keur; si le cope des l’encomencement de la fistule, et boute adés avant la tente, et pues le cautere aprés, tant qu’il viegne au chief de la tente; et sera delivré li tente, et cherra; puis mondefie celles chars fautrees que semblent une penne d’oisel, et n’en remaigne niant.	If not, otherwise he cannot be healthy; and if he is pricked, and does not pierce to the root that is at the foundation, and there is between his two sides a thick covering of cloth or of silk, and you see the fistula at this end of the covering from where it comes out; then take off the covering of the encumbrance of the fistula, and bottle it up immediately before the tent, and then cauterize it afterwards as soon as it has come to the head of the tent; and it will be delivered from the tent, and it will heal; then I will tell you what silk-made covers seem like a swan's feather, and there will remain none.
Et si li sans te vaint, et cort entre toi et l’uevre, si le cauterize de feu ou de medicine ague.	And if the blood does not come out, and you cut between yourself and the work, then cauterize with fire or with bitter medicine.
Car li cauteres de feu assemble II bones choses: c’est a savoir, l’arsure de ces chars ajostees, et l’esteinchement de sanc et la sechor de la moistor; puis le cure de tentes moillies em burre ou en choz broiez, tant que li leus giete bowe, et isse fuer li chars arse en la bowe; puis cure la plaie des oignemens soudans enjanrans dure char, et sont les medicines seches.	For the fire cautery brings together two things: namely, the burning of these joints that are heated up, and the drying out of blood and the evaporation of moisture; then he treats the wet tents with sawdust or hay, as long as the earth is dry, and he burns the joints in the earth; then he treats the wound with dried garlic, which is used to treat hard, rotting joints.
Car quant il est restoree, si est sanee et ne revient mie.	For when it has been reset, if it has healed properly and does not come out again.
Et se fistule vient jusc’a parfont dou fondement, et est esloigniez dou cors, se li boute ton doi ou fondement, et enquier ceu.	And if a fistula comes up to the very foundation of the body and is separated from the chest, then it should be cut off at the root, and such things should be dug out.
Se tu sens la tente, et entre II est li toile ou li syfac ou chars, ou il est pres a percier, si n’i ait fuers que voie de fiance et d’esperance, par l’aministrement de l’une des III manieres: ou tu le cauterizes si com nos avons dit, ou tu le cope jusc’a fons, ou se tu pues si i met tentes et cure si com premier; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, que tu ne coper le tenement qui tient le fondement, et viegne li egestions par lai sens volenteit; puis le cure, si com nos avons dit; par aventure si sera sanez, ou tu esloigne celle coverture et la munde puis qu’elle est copee delez lou fondement, ou par tente ou par autre estrument apointé; puis mondefie cele char fautree qui est en la plaie, tant com tu pues; puis estudie a restorer la plaie, et a demorer la fistule en la partie defuers le fondement: si iert plus legiere chose au malaide.	If you feel the tent, and between the two there is linen or Stoff or joints, or it is ready to pierce, then there are only three ways to deal with it: either cauterize it as we have said, or cut it back to the root, or if you can, put some tents on it and treat it as we have first mentioned; and do not go too far in the healing process, so that you cover up the foundation, and let the discharge come out by its own will; then treat it, as we have said, with garlic, or any other medicine; then study to restore the wound, and delay the fistula in the part farther from the root: this is a lighter thing for the patient.
Et aucune fois sont fistules selonc ceste maniere: et est quant tu boutes la tente en la fistule, et elle est ou costeit dou fondement delez lou cuir desus, si pren une tente percie au chief selonc ceste forme:	And there are no times when these are made according to this way; and when you plug the tent in the fistula, and she is or lies on the foundation of your leather above it, then take a tent pierced at the top according to this form:
Et i boute I fil tort en II, et boute la tente a tout le fil en la fistule tant qu’il soit au chief.	And I pour in water into it in two, and plug the tent into all the thread in the fistula as long as it is at the top.
S’elle est persans en la marge dou fondement dedens, adonc estrai lou fil de celui pertus, ensi que tu boutes ton doi ou fondement; et trai le chief dou fil, et assemble les II chiés ensamble, et estraint l’un a l’autre, et le laisse I jor ou II; et le restraint aucune fois, tant que li filz cope ces chars que sont entre dous, et chiecent; puis cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit soudee et sanee.	If it is pierced in the margin of the foundation inside, then remove the thread from that pierced, so that you plug your two foundations; and tie the head of the thread together, and pull them apart, and leave them one day or two; and do not restrain them at all, until the thread covers these gaps that are between two, and chatters; then cure the wound as long as it is healed and well.
Se li fistule ne perce, si la fai percier en toutes les manieres que tu pues, s’ele n’est trop em parfont.	If the fistula does not pierce, if you make it pierce in all the ways that you can, if he is not too deeply imbedded.
Car il ne covient mie faire por le lacement coper si em parfont, et puis le cure, si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	For it does not fit to make a cover with a perfect seam, and then heal, as we have said, until it is healthy.
Li forme dou spatumile espinous dont on fent la fistule si est mout agus d’une, part et trenchans; et d’autre part non, por ceu c’on ne cope mie ceu c’on ne doit mie copeir, si com tu vois ci:	The form of the spout with thorns from which one makes a fistula is very sharp and penetrating on one side; and on the other side not at all, because it does not fit to make a cover which should not be made, as you see here:
des emorroydes	hemorrhoids
Emorrydes sont selonc II manieres: ou elles sont dedens le fondement, ausi com grain de resin, et s’en i a petites et grans, et en cort adés sanc, et s’en i a une ou plusors, et sont defuer le fondement et au chief dou fondement; mais celles qui sont defuer si ont poc de moistor, et encort adés ou un poc d’aigue citrine ou un poc de sanc, et ont la color dou cors; et li cure de ces qui les ont dedens le fondement, si est que tu comandes au malaide qu’il s’espreigne por aleir en chambres, tant que li fondemens li isse fuer, et c’aperent li filz; si te haste, et le pent as tenailles, ou tu le tien a ton ungle, puis le cope en ses racines; et se li uncine ne les pueent tenir por ses moistors, si les prent a I drapeil, ou a couton, ou d’une piece de chamelot; et les estrai a tes dois, puis les cope, et poudre desus aucunes chaudes poudres que soient en leu de cautere; ou tu les cauterize si com il est dit ou chapistre de cautere, pues les cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li fondemens ne puet issir, si clisterize le malaide de clistere mordant et aspre por laver ceu qui est ou fondement, si qu’il puist issir apertement; cant li malaides se preint, et se li fil sont fuer dou fondement, si est li cure legiere; et est que tu les preignes a ton ungle ou as tenailles, et les cope, puis les cure si com nos avons dit, tant qu’il soit sanez, et qu’il redoute l’incision par fer.	Hemorrhoids are of two kinds: those which are within the fundament, as grains of resin, and small and large, and flow together without pain, and there is one or more; they are far from the fundament and at the top of the fundament; but those which are far away have a little moisture, and then suddenly dry up, and are of the color of the body; and the cure for those who have them within the fundament is this: you should command the patient to strain himself so that the blood comes out in chambers, until the fundament comes off, and the thread comes out; if you are in a hurry, and hold it with tweezers, or you hold it with your fingernail, then cut it at its roots; and if it does not stick because of moisture, take it with a piece of cloth or cotton or a piece of cambric; and extract them with your fingers, then cut them, and powder them with hot powders that are for cauterization; or you can cauterize them as we have said in the chapter on cauterization, for other cures until they are healthy; and if the fundament does not come out, then clisterize the patient with a clisterizing fluid and sharp, so that it comes out freely; when the patient is stretched, and the thread has fallen from the fundament, the cure is light; and you should hold them with your fingernail or tweezers, and cut them, then cure them as we have said, until they are healthy, and avoid incision with iron.
Si covient que tu amenistre la costure selonc ceste maniere: pren I fil tort, et le boute en une aguille, et puis trai le fil au desus et fai percier l’aguille d’autre part, et torne les II chiez dou fil desoz l’aguille, et si soit dou large; et estraint le fil forment, puis noe le fil, et estrai l’aguille, et fai ensi de toz les autres, et en laisse I por corre la superfluiteit dou sanc; puis met sus le fondement I drapeil moilliet en oile roset ou en cerote, et met sus le fondement, et comande au malaide k’il repose; et puis le laisse tant qu’il chiecent, et quant il seront cheut, si les cure d’oignement et d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	If it is necessary for you to introduce the stitch in this way: take a twisted thread, and pour it into a needle, then bring the thread over the top of the needle and pierce the needle from the other side, then twist the two ends of the thread around the needle, and if it is wide; then pull the thread tight, then remove the needle, and do the same with all the others, and leave one for draining blood; then put a wet cloth on the foundation soaked in oil or lanolin, and put it on the foundation, and command the patient to rest; and then leave him until he stops dripping, and when he has stopped, treat him with ointment and other treatments until he is well.
dou sechement dou fiens ou fondement	to dry at the end or foundation
Maintes fois avient sechement de fiens en l’intestine, et par constrignement de nature, et quant li maladie est vielle et medicine n’i vaut.	Many times there is drying out in the intestines, and by necessity of nature, and when the disease is old and medicine is no good.
Si covient que tu reses a la point d’un spatumile ou a ton ungle l’escorce desus, qui ne le laisse a moistir; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sodez si com il covient; et s’il ne puet soder, si rencomence la rasure plus fort que devant, tant qu’il saine mout, et soit escorchiez; puis le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	Si it is necessary that you rub at the spot of a splinter or your nail the bark above, which does not leave it wet; then treat it as long as it is soft as it should be; and if it cannot be treated, then start to scrape it more forcefully than before, until it heals, and is peeled off; then treat it as long as it has healed.
dou fremit	Do not sweat.
Formice est une petite apparance fautree antor le cors, et va mout em parfont; et aucune fois la trueve li frois, et le sent on ausi comme mort de fremit, et vient en tout le cors, et plus as mains que autre part.	The formicle is a small thing that appears before the wound, and it goes away completely; and one does not feel it tickle, and one feels it like death, and it comes all over the body, and more in the hands than anywhere else.
Et li cure si est que tu pren une cainne d’une penne d’oie, ou une penne de vultul fort, et met celle caine sus le fremit, tant que li cercles porpreigne le fremit tot entor; puis torne ta main a tout la cainne tant que tu copes tout entor le fremit, et le met em parfont, et esraiche le fremit de ses racines.	And the cure is that you take a feather from an owl or a strong vulture, and put that feather on the tickle as long as the purple ring surrounds the tickle completely; then turn your hand around all of the feather as much as you can completely surround the tickle, and put it away completely, and peel the tickle from its roots.
Et se tu vues, si fai ceu d’une caine d’arain ou de fer selonc ceste forme, et soit subtilz desoz et traians desus:	And if you see, so make this of a dog's head or iron according to this form, and be subtle and run on top:
ne mie perciet, por mues tenir au doi, et mues presser Et se tu vues, si cauterize lou fremit, si com il est devant ou chapistre de cautere.	And if you see, so make this of a dog's head or iron according to this form, and be subtle and run on top: do not pierce, lest it cause pain, and press
de la forme dou clistere	of the form of the cautery
Aucune fois fait on clistere d’argent ou d’archaut, ou d’arain fondut ou mailliet; et aucune fois fait on de ces estrumens petis et grans, selonc ces a cui il sont amenistrez.	No time made on the cautery of silver or iron, or of melted lead or salt; and no time made on these instruments small and great, according to those who use them.
Cil donques c’on amenistre en la cure des enfans et qui sont foible et dolorous, sont petis.	This is used therefore in the cure of children and who are weak and painful, are small.
Li forme dou clistere petit et grant si est desus large, ou li ventres est liiez selonc ceste maniere:	The form of the cautery small and great is above wide, or the belly is tied according to this way:
et i ait une desevrance ou li ventres soit liiez, si com tu vois, et li chiez soit dedens perciez; et ait a l’un des costez II pertus, et en l’autre I; et soit li ventres ou om met les medicines d’une vessie de beste ou de parchemin, et soit perciez tout entor de menus pertus, et ait entre chescun pertus I doit d’espaice, puis boute en ces pertus I fil fort de fil crut tort en X ou enqui entor, et assemble le ventre si com est une chievre; et quant li medicine est dedens, si la lie a l’estrument devant d’un fil fort, puis clisterize; et c’est li forme dou cercle:	and I say here is a lack of space where the belly is tied up, so that you see it, and where the chaps are inside, and one of the sides is broken, and in the other there is; and let the belly be put with medicines from a bladder of sheep or parchment, and pierce all around the small breaks, and leave between each break a space of I measure, then pour into these breaks a strong thread twisted X-shaped or string around, and bind the belly as if it were a shepherd; and when the medicine is inside, if the instrument is before a strong thread, then clisterize; and this is the form of the circle:
Et soit li medicine ne trop chaude ne trop froide, et oint le chief dou clistere d’oile ou d’aubun d’uef, ou de semblant chose, puis le boute ens legierement; puis l’espreigne li ministres a ses II mains ensamble, tant qu’il soit toz vuis, puis estrai lou clistere, et lieve li malaides ses jambes a la paroit, et se li medicine vuet issir, si la teigne tant com il puet; et s’il dort une nuit atot, si est plus grans aide.	and let the medicine not be too hot or too cold, and oil or beeswax or something similar be spread on the head of the clister, then pour it lightly; then the minister will hold it with his two hands together until it is completely filled, then remove the clister, and put the legs of the patient against the wall, and let the medicine flow out as much as it can; and if he sleeps a whole night, it is greater help.
Et se tu le clisterizes em maladie de decorrement de ventre, et li medicine se haste d’issir, si le rencomence tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you cauterize him with fire because of a disorder of the belly, and the medicine hastens to come out, then wait until he is well again.
Et se li emorroide sont ou fondement, ou aposteme, si soit li clistere ausi subtilz com por I enfant; et c’est li forme dou clistere subtil sus coi li cuir soit estraint:	And if the hemorrhoids are at the root or an abscess, then let the cauterization be as small as for a child; and this is the form of the small cauterization on which the skin is stretched.
des plaies	of wounds
Nos avons jai dit en la division la cure des plaies; or vos dirons les cures de mains et de medicine, selonc l’acomplissement.	We have already spoken about the treatment of wounds; but now we will tell you about the treatment of hands and medication, according to the achievement.
Je dis que les plaies sont diverses selonc ceu qu’elles sont faites, et selonc les leus ou les plaies sont faites, et de coi elles sont faites.	I say that wounds are various according to what they are, and according to the places where they are made, and according to how they are made.
Les choses par coi plaies sont faites sont par gitement de piere, et taille d’espee et de couteil, ou de lance ou de fust ou de siette, ou de semblans choses; ou que sont faites selonc les leus dou cors, si com plaie que chiet sus le col, ou sus le chief, ou le peis, ou le ventre, ou le foie, et semblans membres; et je vos dirai la cure de chescune plaie, et encomencerai as plaies dou chief simples, car li remenbrance venra en son chapistre.	The things by which wounds are made are by hitting with a stone, and cutting with an axe or a knife or a spear or a lance or a fust or a staff or similar objects; or that are made according to the places of the body, such as a wound that comes on the neck, or on the head, or on the back, or on the belly, or on the liver, and similar limbs; and I will tell you about the treatment of each wound, and I will begin with simple wounds, for his remedy will come in his chapter.
Je dis que quant simple plaie vient ou chief, et li os n’est brisiez, si pren garde se c’est de gitement de piere ou de semblans choses, et li cuir est toutevoie rompus et est li plaie grans, et tu doutes levement d’aposteme chaut: si le fai tantost sainier de la cephalique meismement s’il vient poc de sanc de la plaie, et soit li sainie au contraire de la partie navree; et eschuisse li malaides repletion de vin et de viandes grosses.	I say that when a simple wound occurs from which the bone is not broken, take care if it is due to stone or similar things, and the skin is always broken and the wound is large, and you doubt the warmth of an abscess: if you do so soon, save the patient's life from death, and let the wound be hot at first; and avoid the patient's repletion of wine and fatty meat.
Et s’il ne vuet sainier, si soit amenuisie sa viande, et ne boive point de vin, ne ne menjuce point de char; et met sor la plaie, se apostemes chaus i vient, coton moilliet en oile roset soulement, ou en vin stiptice; et s’il n’i a aposteme chaut, si met sus la plaie, s’elle est fresche a tout son sanc, et elle n’est muee par l’air, poudre, que je dirai un poc ci aprés; et se li ars l’ait muee, si met sus aucuns oignemens, tant qu’il soit sanez.	I say that if he cannot be saved, his meat will diminish and he will not drink wine or eat cheese; and put on the wound, if it is hot, with cotton wet in oil and astringent, or with wine of rubies; and if there is no heat, put it on with herbs until he is well.
Et se li plaie est grans si com de tailleure d’espee et de semblans, et les levres ne se pueent assembler par tentes, si les assemble par cousture, si com je dirai as plaies dou ventre, de la costure.	And if the wound is large, as from a sword or similar weapon, and the lips cannot be joined by stretching, but must be joined with sutures, just as I say about abdominal wounds, from the stitch.
Se li plaie est descoverte de l’os, et pent, et ne tient mais que a un poc, si le cope; puis cure la plaie de medicine, et restoure char dure en leu de cuir, et comande au malaide a mengier grosses viandes, si com testes et froment cuit, ausi com poulz, et semblans choses.	If the wound is exposed to the bone and is small, and only holds together with one stitch, then patch it and cure the wound with medicine, and replace the skin with hard leather, and command the patient to eat thick meat, such as roasted beef or poultry, and similar things.
Et se tu trueves ou cuir porriture, et il n’aert a l’os, si cope lou porrit tot, et giete fuer, puis le cure; et se il ait artere en la plaie ou voine, dont sans cort, et il ne puet estainchier par medicines, si quier l’artere, et se tu la trueves desloie, si la lie d’un fil; et se ceu ne profite mie, si la cauterize.	And if you find that the rot has reached the bone, and it is not held together with a stitch, then patch it and cure it; and if there is an artery in the wound or vein, cut it off, and if it does not benefit from being cauterized, cauterize it.
Et se ces plaies sont petites et simples, si est li cure legiere: et est que tu mettes ens ceste poudre qui soude ainsois que li ars l’ait muee.	And if these wounds are small and simple, then the treatment is light; and that you put this powder in them so that fire moves them.
Et li maniere de la poudre si est: pren encens une partie; sanc de dragon II parties; chalz vive III parties, et le poudre subtilment, et emple la plaie, et l’estraint forment, tant qu’elle s’aerse bien et se joigne a tout son sanc; et puis la lie bien, et la laisse sens desliier, s’elle n’enfle; car on n’oste la madicine tant qu’ele soit sanee.	And the method of this powder is this: take incense one part; dragon's blood two parts; live charm three parts, and powder it finely, and apply the wound, and bind it tightly, until it has healed well and joined together all its blood; and then bind it firmly, and leave it undisturbed, if it swells; for we do not remove the medicine until it is healed.
Et aucune fois fait on ceu de chalz soulement, quant on n’ait l’encens ne lou sanc de dragon, mais que li ars n’ait muee la plaie.	And never does one use only live charm when incense or dragon's blood has moved the wound; but that fire has moved the wound.
Et se li ars ait mueit la plaie, meismement en esteit, si n’i met om mie ceste poudre; mais met sus aucuns oignemens digestis, ou poulz de farine d’orge faites d’aigue et de miel, tant qu’ele giete bowe; puis le cure d’autres cures tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if fire has moved the wound, it is better to put this powder on it; but put on some digestible ointments, or flour of barley made with water and honey, until it heals; then treat it with other remedies until it is healed.
Et se li brisure d’os vient avec la plaie, et elle est petite, si l’estrai as pinceures subtilz; et je vos dirai ci aprés les brisures dou chief.	And if the fracture of the bone comes with the wound, and it is small, then extract it with tiny tweezers; and I will tell you later about the fractures of the head.
de la plaie dou col	of the wound at the neck
Se plaie vient ou col et elle est simple, si n’a point de difference entre li et celi dou chief, mais se li ners dou col ou li artere est copee.	If the wound is at the throat and it is simple, there is no difference between it and that of the head, but the artery at the throat is severed.
Se c’est li ners, si n’i a autre engien que laissier la cure, et n’i mettre nulle chose restraignant, car il nuit as ners et les fait retraire; et ne mettre sus la plaie rien froit, car li substance des ners est froide, et li continuation d’aus si est avec le cerveil, qui est li plus haus membres; mais soit li medicine souez, si com chalz lavee en aigue douce, et mellee avec oile roset, et cucie lavee ausi en aigue douce, et autres pieres de mine selonc ceste maniere, et oignemens moistes.	If it is the neck, if there is no other way to let the cure happen but to leave it unrestrained and put nothing in its way that might hinder it, for it will damage the neck and cause it to retreat; do not put anything on the wound, for the substance of the neck is cold, and its continuation with the skull, which is the highest bone; but be it as a warm bath, as hot water mixed with oil, and as cool water too, and other stones of different sizes according to this way, and wetting with oils.
Et se li plaie est grans, si la cout et lie de bendes, puis la cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the wound is large, then bind it with bends, and then treat until it is healed.
Et se les plaies sont parfondes et ele est chevee et pleinne de bowe, si la perce ou plus bas leu; et se li artere est copee, et decorremens de sanc en vient, si la desoivre, et la loie, et la cauterize se mestier est; et se li espinee de la gorge est copee, ou li keurs, et li conduiz est gardez, par coi la viande va, si cout le keur sus la cainne de la gorge, et ne touchier la gorge mais la remet selonc sa figure naturel; et puis l’estraint avenanment, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le cure d’oignemens desechans tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li plaie a fait empression en l’os, si la quier; et s’il i a pieces d’os, si les trai fuers toz se tu pues, et ces que tu ne pues avoir, si laisse tant que li plaie porrisse, et soit desevree et aligie li issue; et se li plaie est fresche, si poudre sus la poudre que j’ai dit.	And if the wounds are deep and the bowels are full of blood, then the piercing or deeper it is; and if the artery is cut, and blood comes out, coming from the throat, then it is cauterized, and the spitting is stopped, and the cure is done; and if the pain in the throat is cut, and its conduct is kept, so that the meat goes well, if the cut is higher on the chin of the throat, and does not touch the throat but adjusts it naturally; and then he holds back a little, and leaves it for some days, and then treats with ointments that are discarded until it is healed; and if the wound has made an impression on the bone, then it is sought; and if there are pieces of bone, then they are torn hard, and those that you can't have, let them be until the wound rots and comes out in its own way; and if the wound is fresh, then powder on the powder that I said.
Et s’il a en la plaie os et il i a fistule, si la cure ensi com j’ai dit en son chapistre.	And if there are bones in the wound and it has a fistula, then treat it as I said in my chapter on the ointment.
de la plaie de lance ou de coutel	of the lance or knife wound
Se c’est cop de lance ou de coutel, et li plaie est parfonde, si regarde se de la plaie saut ventositez cant li malaides alainne: saiches adonques que li plaie est mortelz; et s’elle n’est parfonde, et elle est fresche a tout son sanc, si n’i mettre mie a la premiere houre la poudre, ne ne la liier mie por le sanc que ne demorse em parfont, et reviegne au cuer, et ocie lou malaide; mais i met oignement atractif, et le lie II fois le jor; et se tu n’as oignement, si met en la plaie viel coton por succier fuers la moistor, et fai dormir le malaide sus la plaie III jors, ou IIII, ou plusors; si n’i venra mie spasme, ne tremor male de cuer n’estraingnemens d’alainne; et quant tu vois les bones dispositions, si saiches que li plaie est sauve.	If it is a lance or knife wound, and the wound is deep, then look out for wind that might come from the wound, because then the wound will be fatal; and if it is not deep, and the wound is fresh in every part of the body, then do not put on the powder at first, nor bind it so as to prevent movement until it has healed completely, and let the patient rest; but if you have no poultice, put wool in the wound to absorb the moisture, and let the patient lie down on the wound for three days, or four, or more; if then you do not get spasms or a bad tremor from the body or strange movements; and when you see that the bones are in order, know that the wound is saved.
Cure la donques de tentes et d’autres cures, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’elle ne puet saner, et oevre, adés saiches que il i a fistule; si la cure si com on doit.	Treat the pustules and other ailments until they heal; and if they cannot heal, then sew up that which has become a fistula; do so as one should.
Et se li plaie est d’incision d’espee ou de coutel, et elle est simple, ou pis ou au dos, si la cure de ceu qui est devant; s’elle est grans, de cousture; et s’elle est petite, de poudre, et s’elle est empressee en l’os, et en a copeit pieces, si quier la plaie, et les trai fuers s’il sont desevrez; et s’il ne sont desevrez, si laisse porrir la plaie, si aligera li estractions; et des autres plaies as autres membres est li jugemens si com nos avons dit.	If the wound is from a knife or sword and is deep, sew it up; and if it is shallow, use powder, and if it has penetrated bone and broken into pieces, clean the wound, and treat the foreign bodies carefully if they are stuck in; and if they are not stuck in, let the wound fester, so that the extractions will be easier; and for other wounds to other limbs, there is judgment as we have said.
dou derrompement dou ventre	Dou derrompement du ventre
Li derompemens dou ventre est grans et moiens et petis; de la grant plaie saut aucune fois li intestine, ou li ners des intestines, par coi li intromission d’aus; et li costure est plus malaisie, et aucune fois vaut pis li petite plaie que li grans, por ceu c’on remet plus a poinnes les intestines en, s’on ne les i remet de chaut en chaut; por ce que li intestine enflent tantost qu’il sentent le froit, si rentrent plus a poinnes, et por ceu vaut mues li moieinne plaie, por ceu c’on ramoine mues l’intestine a son leu que as autres II Et saiches que li routure dou ventre est selonc IIII manieres: les II costures communes avienent en la costure dou ventre, et li costure des autres plaies dou cors et II autres costures propres sont communes as autres plaies; et toutevoie elles sont plus propres avec la costure dou ventre, et je dirai une chescune et declairerai.	The rupture of the abdomen is great and small; from this a lot of intestines may come out, or the intestines may be torn away from one another, for which the incision is more difficult, and a small wound is harder to deal with than a large one, so that if we do not put the intestines back together piece by piece, they will swell up sometimes so much that they feel cold, then we will have to put them back together again; and it is to be known that the rupture of the abdomen is according to three ways: the common sutures are those which are in the incision of the abdomen, and the common sutures of the other wounds of the body and the other proper sutures are common to the other wounds; and yet they are more proper to the incision of the abdomen, and I will say one thing and declare another.
Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l’intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l’une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.	Je di que quant li plaie est petite, et aucune chose de l'intestine ist fuer, et griés chose est dou remettre, ceu est par l'une des II manieres: ou por la petitece de la plaie, si com nos avons dit, ou por ce que li intestine est enflez por le froit.
Et quant il est frois, eschaufez lou en teil maniere: moillie une esponge ou I mol drapeil en aigue tede soulement, ou tu cuis en aigue squinant et cipre et spique, et arose l’intestine tant que li enfleure soit ostee; et aucune fois fait ce vins restraingnans, et est muedre que awe soule por desenfler.	I say that when the wound is small and nothing from the intestines comes out, and there is something to be done, it should be done in one of two ways: either because the wound is small, as we have said, or because the intestines are swollen with fever. And when it is swollen, heat it in a third way: wet a sponge or a soft cloth with cold water, or cook it in warm water and saffron and cumin, and roast the intestines until they swell; and never stop doing this, and make it sweet so that it swells again;
Et quant tu vois l’enfleure departir, si amoiste l’intestine d’aigue ou altee et malves soient cuites, car par ceu est aligie li entree a poc de chose; et s’il n’i puet entrer, si fent un poc la plaie a l’estrument de coi on cope les emorroydes; et li premiere cure est muedre que li taille, que nus n’i doit taillier sens grant necessiteit n’i ait; et c’est li estrumens por le fendre: si trenche dedens en la corbeure et defuer non, et vez ci la forme:	And when you see the swelling subside, if you moisten the intestines with water or boil and dry them, for that way it is more difficult for anything to enter; and if it cannot enter, then cut a small hole in the wound with the instrument used to cut hemorrhoids; and the first cure is to make it sweet, so that it can be cut, which we should not do unless there is great need; and this is the instrument for doing so: if you cut into it from within and don't slice off any, and do this:
Et quant li plaie est enlargie, et li intestine saut fuer, si le remet arer selonc la forme naturel en son leu propre, se tu en as pooir, car ce vaut mues.	And when the wound is enlarged, and the intestines are protruding, if you can put it back in its natural place in its own proper place, for that is what needs to be done.
Quant li plaie est large, et elle est en la partie desoz lou ventre, si covient que tu faices gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et met ses jambes plus haut que son chief; et s’elle est en la partie desoz le ventre, si met le chief et le pis plus haut que les parties desoz, et ausi se li routure dou ventre est en l’une des II parties si met t’entente en ceu que li partie navree soit plus haute que li autre; et ensi covient amenistrer ceu que je dis en plaies grans et moienes.	And when the wound is large, and it is in the lower part of the belly, so that you make the patient lie on his back, and raise his legs higher than his head; and if it is in the lower part of the belly, so that you raise the head and the chest higher than the lower parts, and also, if the stomach has been torn, you should pay attention to which side the tear is on, so that you make that side higher than the other; and in this way, I have said, one should deal with large and painful wounds.
Es plaies petites met ceu que t’est apparilliet, puis aies entre tes mains I ministre pitous ki teigne toute la routure a sa main, et assemble les levres; et c’est la maniere commune de costures, et est que tu preignes une aguille ou plusors, selonc la quantiteit de la largesce de la plaie, puis laisse des le chief de la plaie I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une aguille ou il ait I boin fil fort; et perce les II chiés dou cuir avec les II chiés dou siphac, qui est desoz le cuir dedens, tant que tu la faices percier de celle partie, et assemble les II chief dou siphac les IIII ensamble; puis l’estrain d’un fil double entor l’aguille de II pars, puis assemble les II chiés de la plaie avenanment, et puis laisse I doi d’espaice, et i fiche une autre aguille; puis la lie dou fil si com tu as fait la premiere aguille, et ne cesser de ceu faire selonc ceu que tu as mestier des aguilles, tant que toute li plaie soit restrainte; et soient les aguilles moienes, entre subtilz et grosses, car les aguilles subtilz copent toute la char, et les trop grosses si ne pueent mie bien entrer: por ceu covient qu’elles soient moienes; et ne covient mie bouter les aguilles trop au defuer de la char et dou cuir, k’elles ne copent et oevrent la plaie devant la soudure; et puis cope les chiés des aguilles, qu’elles ne blecent lou malaide au dormir, et i met tentes ou drapelz au chiés des aguilles por mues tenir, et les laisse tant que li plaie soit soudee; et ceste maniere de costure as aguilles est plus covenauble en petites plaies, car il i soffist une aguille ou II Li seconde costure si est commune, et est que tu assemble les II chiés dou cuir et les II chiés dou syfac ensamble a une aguille ou il ait I fort fil moien; et quant tu avras perciez ces chiez toz IIII ensamble, si ramoinne l’aguille a la partie ou tu as encomenciet, en la maniere c’on cout les dras; et met d’espaice entre chescune costure la grossece d’un menor doi; ceste costure sevent li home, et je cousi une plaie c’uns hons avoit ou ventre, qui estoit navrez d’un coutel, et estoit li plaie plus d’une palme de grant, et issoit des intestines bien II palmes de grant, et estoit li plaie enmi le ventre.	For small wounds, one should prepare the patient in the manner described above; then, between your hands, you should hold the thread that will cover all of the tear and secure it with a knot; and this is the usual way to sew up, and it is because you take an needle or more, according to the size of the wound, then leave a little space at the head of the wound, and insert a needle there with good strong thread; then pierce the two pieces of skin together with the two pieces of cloth, which are inside the skin, as far as you can make them go, and join the two ends of the cloth together; then draw one double thread through the needle from both sides, then join the two edges of the wound together, leaving a little space between them, and insert another needle; then draw it through in the same way as the first needle, without stopping to do this for each needle you use, until all the wound is sewn up; and the needles should be medium size, because small needles will not hold the skin tightly, and large ones will not go well into the skin; therefore, it is necessary that they be of average size; and you should not push the needles too far from the edge of the wound or the skin, so that they do not break open the wound before it is completely sewn up; and then you should cut off the ends of the thread, leaving about a thumb's width between each knot. This second sewing is more suitable for small wounds, because the first one holds the skin together while the second one finishes the work; and this second sewing is done with a needle and strong thread; when you have pierced both pieces of cloth and skin together with the needle, as far as they will go, then join the two ends of the cloth to each other, leaving a little space between them, and make another needle from there, which will be about half an inch long; then pierce the two pieces of skin and the two pieces of cloth together with this small needle; then take your double thread and insert it through the small needle from both sides, so that it passes under both pieces of cloth; then tighten this thread as much as possible, so that it pulls the two pieces of cloth tightly together; then cut off the ends of the thread, leaving about a half inch between each knot. Je li ramenai l’intestine puis k’il ot esteit XXIIII houres fuer, et fut li plaie soudee jusc’a XV jors, et le curai, et fut sanez.	I took him into my care when it had been ## hours since the injury, and the wound was well-healed after fifteen days, so I treated it, and he recovered.
Et li mire l’avoient jugiet qu’il morroit, et ce fut miracle; et ne le curai mie d’oignement, car je estoie en I leu ou on n’en trovoit point, ne nule medicines; et metoie sens plus sus la plaie coton viel II fois le jor, et le lavoie d’aigue de miel tant qu’il fut sanez.	And the people said that he was dying, and it was a miracle; I did not treat him with ointment, because I was in a place where there was none to be found, nor any medicines; so I put cotton wool on the wound twice a day, and washed it with honey water until he recovered.
Or vos dirai les II propres manieres de cousture: pren l’aguille, et la boute des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens; quant elle a perciet le keur de droit en droit, si lai le chief dou siphac ou cousteit ou tu as bouteit l’aguille, et la fai percier d’autre part des la partie dedens jusc’a celi defuer; et li entendemens de ceste costure si est que tu cous ausi com li peletier font les pelz, et que tu laisses une fois le syfac d’une part, et le reprent d’autre, tant que li costure soit toute acomplie.	Or I will tell you the two proper methods of sewing: take the needle and thread from the outside edge all the way to the center; when the thread has gone through, bring it back out again from the inside edge to the outside, and tie it off; this is how you should sew, just as the furrier does when he sews fur, and so that the stitch remains in one place while the skin moves around on the other side.
Li seconde maniere de costure, que Galiens dist proprement, si est si com aucun font, qui assemblent les II parties ensamble naturelment, et apploient l’un des chief dou syfac a l’autre chief, en teil maniere: fiche une aguille ou chief dou mirach prochiene, et fai percier celui leu soulement, et laisse les II chiés dou syfac; puis torne l’aguille, et la fai percier des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, as II chiés dou syfac; puis fai percier l’un et l’autre des la partie defuers jusc’a celi dedens, en II autres chiés dou mirach que sont on l’autre costeit; et c’est li muedre maniere de costure et li plus commune. Galiens si dist ceste parolle, et aucun le tesmoignent, c’on doit coudre le ventre a II aguilles, ou il ait fil en chescune; et doit on bouter l’une aguille d’une part, et l’autre d’autre, en la maniere de ces qui cousent corroies; et saiches que quant li routure est enmi lou ventre, si est li cousture plus griez que des autres leus dou ventre.	Galiens say this word, and no one testifies against it: the abdomen should be sewn with two needles, each with its own thread; one needle should be driven from one side, and the other from the other, in the manner of those who sew shoes; and know that when the rupture is in the middle of the abdomen, the sewing is more painful than others.

If the wound is fresh and bleeding, as well as if it has been moved by heat, then place the intestine back inside, and stitch it up; then put on the powder of calamine, and if the heat has moved it, apply any ointment that is available, until the wound heals; and if you do not have medicines, place cotton cloth on it, often turning it over, until it is healed.
Car tu n’as mestier d’autre medicine en plusors dispositions cant les plaies sont simples; et se tu doutes que li plaie ne faice communiteit as membres principelz, si covient ke tu moilles lainne legiere en oile de tempree chalor, ou en oile roset, et la met entor les angres, et desoz les asselles; et s’il sent dolor ou porriture en bouelz, et maintes fois avient, si les clisterize de vin noir tede, et meismement se li porriture vient jusc’a l’intestine; et le perce dedens, et saiches que quant c’est li gros intestines, si est plus legier a saner que li petis. Li intestine qui est apelez «jeun» ne puet saner quant il est navrez, et c’est por la planteit des voinnes que i sont, et por la subtiliteit de tout le cors, et l’aprochement de sa nature des ners.	Since you have no need of other medicine in the various preparations where the wounds are simple; and if you doubt that the wound will connect with the main members, then it is convenient that you wet another light one in oil of tempere or hot rose oil, and put it around the ankles, and clean out the blisters; and if it feels pain or corruption in the balls, and often happens, if the clisterize of black wine soothes, and more often the corruption comes up to the intestines; and pierce them inside, and know that when this large intestine is, it is lighter to heal than the small one.

And if the piece of flesh jumps out of the wound, put it back in place as with the intestine while it is fresh; and if it has become old and has turned black, you must find the place that is black, from which blood should not flow, because there are veins and arteries; then cut off what is between the two joints, and hang them up by the sides of the wound until it stops bleeding when the piece jumps out, and the wound heals.
de la routure dou boueil	Of the rupture of the blister
Quant li intestine est rons, et li plaie est petite, si la puet on restorer en aucuns homes, por ceu que je vis que uns hons fut navrez ou ventre d’une lance; et estoit li plaie au destre de l’estomac, et fut envillie et devint fistule, et en issoit li egestion et li ventositez; je i mis cure selonc ceu que je poi, et ne cessai de subtilier tant qu’il fut sanez, et li leus soudez.	When the intestine is torn and the wound is small, I have seen some men restored by cutting off a part of it, as if they had been stabbed or wounded with a lance; and the wound was on the right side of the abdomen, and became gangrenous and turned into a fistula, and there was gas production and pus discharge; so I treated it according to what I could find, and did not stop trying until it was healed, and the wounds closed up.
Et quant je le vis souder, je doutai que li malaides n’eust mal en son ventre; et il n’i ot point de mal, mais demora en millors dispositions, et menjans et bevans; et dirent aucun experimentors que quant il a petite plaie en l’intestine, qu’il doit estre liiez en teil maniere: pren fremis a grans testes, puis assemble les levres de la plaie, et quant li fremis ait overte la bouche, si la met sus les II levres, si qu’elle estraigne sa bouche sus; et puis li cope la teste, et ce se tient si qu’il ne puet desliier, puis met I autre fremit aprés en celle maniere que devant, tant que li plaie soit toute porprise; et cout la plaie.	Et when I saw him sewed up, I doubted that the patient had done himself harm in his belly; and he was not ill, but delayed in better dispositions, and feasting and drinking; and no experimenter said that when he has a little wound in the intestine, he must be bound in some way: take frissons from great testes, then gather together the lips of the wound, and when the frisson has opened the mouth, then put it on the two lips, so that it estranges its mouth above; and then he copes his head, and this remains so that he cannot unsew it, then puts another frisson after in that way as before, until the wound is all taken; and let the wound.
Cil chief si s’aerdent en l’intestine, et ne vient nulle nuisance au malaide, et se puet on liier l’intestine d’un fil subtil qui est copez de l’intestine d’une beste, en teil maniere: pren le chief de cest fil d’intestine que soit mout descharnez, et puis lie au chief de cest fil I fil de lin subtil tort, puis boute le fil en l’aguille, et en cout l’intestine, et le ramoinne en la routure; et ceste maniere de costure de fremis nen est fuers que selonc la voie de fiance et d’esperance; et se li plaie est grans et large, meismement quant elle est en l’un des grailes intestines, si n’i a engien ne santeit, fuer que subtiliteit.
