de fistule ou qu’ele soit	of the fistula, whether it is
Saiches que toute plaie ou aposteme, quant il enveillist, si est apelee universement «fistule», et meismement quant elle est chevee et rent bowe.	are that all wounds or abscesses, when they heal, are called 'fistula' in general, and most when they have gone through the body and come out at the other end.
Et fistule est selonc la verteit nodation fautree dure et blainche, ou on ne sent dolor, et est ausi chevee com li penne d’un oiseil; et aucune fois en saut clere bowe, et autre fois espesse; aucune fois poc, et autre fois assez; et je en ai jai parleit en la division des plaies, que toute plaie que n’est sanee, et il n’i a char, ce n’est fuers que par une des VIIII causes: c’est a savoir, par la petitece dou sanc ou cors; ou por sa malice; ou por ceu qu’il i a char dure dedens, et sus les levres, que n’i laisse naistre char; ou il i a trop de bowe; ou li leus est porris, et li matiere est de male qualiteit; ou li medicine n’est mie bone en la cure; ou por ceu que li corruption est maniere de pestilence; ou por la proprieteit en la region est tardive li digestion, et tarde li santeit, et enflee par nature; ou il i a voinnes ou os: et j’ai ja mostreit toutes ces causes, et les signes, et les cures de medicines en la division.	And the fistula is according to the green, dry and white nodulation, where there is no pain, and it is also chewed like the feather of a bird; and never clear bowels, and sometimes thick, sometimes thin, and never a hole, and I have already spoken in the division of wounds that all wounds that are not healed, and there is no cure, this is not done except by one of VIII causes: namely, by the smallness of blood or corruption; or because it is malicious; or because there is something hard inside, on the lips, which does not allow birth to occur; or there is too much bowels; or the leus is rotten, and the matter is of poor quality; or the medicine is not good in the cure; or because what corrupts is according to a pestilence; or because digestion is late in that region, and health is late, and it escapes by nature; or there are wounds or abscesses. And I have already shown all these causes, and the signs, and cures of medicines in the division.
Or covient que je te faice a savoir la cure de fistule qui est faite par oevre de mains.	It is necessary that I make you aware of the treatment of fistulas, which is done by manual labor.
Saiches que fistule avient en tous membres dou cors; car il i a fistules que vienent as grans voines, et as arteres, et as ners, ou au syfac, ou a l’intestine, ou a la vessie, ou a aucunes des costes, ou a l’espinee dou dos, ou a aucune jointe des mains ou des piez; et si a teil que vient a la proprieteit dou membre principeil, et as semblans leus.	Fistulas can occur in all limbs of the body; for there are fistulas that come from great veins, and arteries, and nerves, or to the sinus, or intestine, or bladder, or some of the ribs, or spine of the back, or any joint of the hands or feet; and if one part that comes from the principle limb, and similar things.
Et toutes les fistules que sont de ceste maniere sont de grief sanation, et n’i a fors que labour, et ignorance; et se il i a aucune fistule que ne veigne mie jusc’a leu que j’ai dit, et tu as fiance de la cure, et tu la vues conoistre, si pren une tente d’arain ou de fer, se li fistule est droite, si la quier; et se li fistule est torte, si la cerche d’une subtil tente de plonc, car li plons se ploie mues entor la tortuositeit; et se li fistule a mains pertus et tu ne la pues mie bien cerchier par tentes, si la clisterize par l’un des pertus, car la moistors si cort d’un pertus a autre, et la mundifie; puis la quier saigement a ton pooir, que tu conoisses s’il i a os ou nerf, et est chevee em parfont, et demande bien au malaide de la dolor qu’il sent au presser de ta main, et le leu ou il la sent; et quant tu savras vraiement le leu ou elle est, et s’elle est loing de jointure, ou de nerf, ou d’artere ou de voine, ou en aucuns des leus que je t’ai dit, si la cope selonc ceu que je t’ai dit, et oste fuer la fautreure et les chars corrumpues que sont dedens; et puis la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee, et se li fistule est bien parfonde de droit endroit, si covient que tu copes em parfont, tant com tu pues, puis i met tentes moillies en medicine ague, et les boute jusc’au chief de la fistule, tant que li medicine corrode la superfluiteit qui est demoree au fons; et puis i met oignemens enjanrans sainne char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez par ceu, si le cauterize si com nos avons dit, et se li os est corrompus de la fistule, si le cope.	And all the Fistulas that are of this manner are of great difficulty in treatment, and there is only labor, and ignorance; and if there is any fistula that does not come from the principle limb, and similar things. All such Fistulas are of grievous sanitation, and there is nothing but work, and ignorance; and if there is any Fistula that does not come from a certain part, and you have engaged to cure it, and you see it clearly, then take a tent of rawhide or iron, if the Fistula is straight, then seek it; and if the Fistula is twisted, then seek it with a slender tent of pliers, for the pliers bend themselves in accordance with the tortuosity; and if the Fistula has broken hands, and you cannot find it well with tents, then you shall open it with care, so that you may know if there are bones or nerves, and it is completely removed, and ask the patient of pain that he feels when you press your hand on it, and the place where he feels it; and when you truly know the place where it is, and if it is far from a joint, or nerve, or artery, or vein, or in any of the places that I have said, then you shall treat it according to what I have said, and you shall take care not to leave any foulness or corrupting bones inside; and then cure as long as it is healthy, and if the Fistula is very deep from the right side, then it is necessary that you treat it completely, as much as you can, then put moist tents in a medicine of water, and pour them on the top of the Fistula, until the medicine corrodes the excess that is reserved at the bottom; and then put embalmings in janrainings of healthy oil, as long as it is healed; and if it is not healed by this means, then cauterize it as we have said, and if there are corrupted bones from the Fistula, then treat them.
Se voinne ou ners ne te greve ou membres principelz, si com nos avons dit; et se li os est descovers, et il i a corruption et noiror, si lou reis tant que li corruption soit toute ostee, puis le cure de choses enjanrans char tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’il n’est sanez, et rent bowe si com devant, saiches que tu n’es mie alez jusc’a font: si descuevre et quier tant que tu soies au fons, et oste toute la corruption, puis restore le leu; et s’il est ensi sanez, c’est bien.	If a vein or an artery is cut in the principal members, as we have said; and if the bone is uncovered, and there is corruption and blackness, so long as the corruption remains whole bone, then cure of dislocated bones as much as it is healthy; and if it is not healthy, and it comes back bowing as before, know that you have not yet gone far: uncover and examine as long as you are at the bottom, and then restore the place; and if it is healthy there, it is well.
Se ceu non, saiches que la corruption est trop en parfont, que tu n’i pues avenir; si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier a nature; et s’il i a i petit os corrumput, et tu le pues traire as tenailles, si l’estrai a I estrument covenauble a ceu, et s’il i a maint os, si les trai trestoz, ne n’en laissier nes un; et se li moistor te fait contraire, et il n’i a error ne paour, si cope et moistor et char, et delivre les os.	If not, know that the corruption is too complete, so you cannot come; if there is no other way than to loosen by nature; and if there is one small bone corrupted, and you can pull it with pliers, if you extract it with the right instrument for this, and if there are many bones, if you loosen them all, do not leave one; and if moisture makes it opposite, and there is no mistake or fear, then cut and moisten and heat, and deliver the bones.
Et se tu ne les pues oster a une houre, si met sus la plaie chose enjanrant porriture, et laisse tant que li leus soit porris entor les os, et adonc si avront plus legierement les os; et se c’est uns grans os, si com de jambe ou de cuisse, si reis tant soulement la corruption tant que li noiror soit toute ostee, puis restoure la plaie; et s’il en i a grant partie dou corrumput, et vient jusc’a mole de l’os; si le covient soier et coper tout jusc’a la corruption, et puis le cure tant qu’il soit soudez; et je te dirai d’une fistule qui avint I home en sa jambe, si que tu i preignes exemple et aide en ton ovraige.	And if you cannot remove them in an hour, then place on the wound something that causes putrefaction, and let it remain until the pus is between the bones, and then the bones will be looser; and if it is a large bone, such as a leg or thigh, then wait until the putrefaction has turned the whole bone black, then cover the wound; and if there is a great deal of corruption and it has reached only half the bone, then it is fitting to patch and cover everything up to the corruption, and then treat it until it is healed; and I will tell you about a fistula that happened to one man in his leg, so that you may take an example and help in your work.
Il fut I jovencelz entor XXX ans, qui ot une dolor en sa jambe d’une cause que vint dedens le cors, tant que les matieres vinrent a la jambe, et fut enflee d’un gros aposteme, et n’ot point de cause defuer por ovrir; mais li mire par lor folie ovrerent tant sus que li apostemes ovri, et en corroient mout de matieres, et devint fistule, et i vint mout de pertus que tuit gitoient bowe et moistor dou cors; et maint mire i mirent cure entor II ans, et n’i ot nul saige en l’art de mains, tant que je i fui apelez, et vi sa jambe et les medicines dont on le curoit, et ceu que corroit par les pertus a grant cors; et devenoit rouges li cors dou jouvenceil, et avoit color citrine.	He was a young man of thirty years who had a pain in his leg from an unknown cause that spread to the bone, so that matters came to the leg and caused a large abscess, and he had no reason to operate; but by his folly he operated so much that it corroded much matter, and became a fistula, and it came to such a degree of harm that all were wet with sweat and moisture from the body; and many times he was treated for two years, and there was no skill in the art of hands until I was called, and I saw his leg and the medicines by which he was being cured, and that which was corroded through the fistula; and the color of his body became red, and had a yellow tint.
Je boutai une tente en l’un de ces pertus, et puis cerchai toz les pertus, et trovai que li uns venoit encontre l’autre de toutes les parties de la jambe.	I pitched a tent in one of those clefts, and then I searched all the clefts, and I found that one came against the other on all sides of the leg.
Je me hastai donques, et copai en l’un des pertus tant que je descovri une partie de l’os, et le trovai corrumput et perciet, et venoit li corruption jusc’a l’os dedens; je soiai ceu qui m’aparissoit de l’os corrumput, et cuidai qu’il n’i eust autre corruption, fuer que celi que je ostai; et comensai a restourer la plaie de medicines sodans par lonc tens, et ne pot souder; et puis rencomensai, et descovri l’os si com devant, et trovai la corruption continuee en l’os, et la soiai, et puis l’ostai, et me penai de souder le leu; mais je ne pou tant que je copai entor une palme de l’os, et le traï fuer a tout son mole, puis le restourai de medicines; et il fut sanez et soudez hastanment, et ne covint plus rencomencier l’ovraige fors por la foibleté dou malaide, qui ne pooit soffrir, et por la paour de mort que je avoie de lui.	I quickly started, and I dug in one of the clefts as far as I discovered part of the bone, and I found that it was腐れた and broken, and it came against the other on all sides inside; I recognized what appeared to me from the bone corrumpted, and I took care that there was no corruption beyond that which I held; and then I started again, and uncovered the bone as before, and I found the continuing corruption in the bone, and I recognized it, and then I held it, and then I dug a hole for the bone; but I could not hold it, because I dug into one palm of the bone, and I removed it completely from all its mold, then I restored it with medicines; and it was healed and firmly bonded, and there was no need to dig again beyond the weakness of the disease, which could not stand, and for the fear of death that I had for him.
Car por l’evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l’os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n’ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l’aleir ne a venir.	Car por l'evacuation sanglotoit sovent, mais il fut sanez entierement, et nasquit en leu de l'os une char dure, et fut de bone disposition et n'ot point de nuisement ne de contraire dou tout en tout, ne a l'aleir ne a venir.
Et se li os est brisiez en aucun leu dou cors, si le covient soier en ceste maniere: pren I liien, et l’estrain au chief de l’os qui apert, et comande aucun k’il l’estende en haut; et met I autre lien de lainne plus gros dou premier liien, et le lie sus la char qui est desor l’os, et estent le chief, si que tu traies la char corrumpue au desoz, et descuevre la char sus le leu ou tu vues soier, que li soie ne blece la char; et met I tison ou une tauble desoz l’os por mues coper la char corrumpue; et covient tant soier com on puet veoir et sentir la corruption, et soier ancor autre fois.	Because often there was a bleeding evacuation, but he was completely healed, and gave birth to the bone in place of the skull, and was of good disposition and had no harm or opposite from all this in everything, nor in air nor in coming. And if the bone is broken in any place of the spine, then it should be done in this way: Take a thread, and pull at the head of the bone that is open, and command anyone to extend it upwards; and put another thread, thicker than the first, on the other side, and tie it to the bar that is beyond the bone, and uncover the head, so that you remove the decayed bar, and cover the bar with a skull, that the bar does not harm the skull; and put a piece of wood or a covering over the bone for protection; and it should be done as often as one can see and feel the decay, and again.
Et se li os est corrumpus, et n’apert mie, et li corruptions est en mileu ou en une partie, si descuevre la char toute; puis met I tison desoz, et puis soie des l’une partie a l’autre la corruption, et soit li soieure dou lonc de la corruption I poc, si com nos avons dit; et se li corruptions est en la jointure, si cope la jointure corrumpue, et soie l’os ou elle contient de l’autre part; et se li corruptions est en la continuation des II jointes, si n’i a autre angien que dou coper; et se li corruptions est ou poignil de la main, ou ou poignil dou piet, si est mout fort celle chose, mais toutevoie il covient que tu enquieres celle corrosion, coment elle t’apert; et la mundifie en toutes les manieres que tu pues, mais que li voine ou li nerf ne te faicent contraire; et saiches que li incisoire et les soies por coper ces os sont maintes, selonc l’assise des os et l’aparance d’ous, et lor grossece et lor subtiliteit, et lor grandor et lor petitece, et lor duresce; et por ceu covient il apareillier a chescune semblance d’ovraige son estrument; et saiches que l’uevre te moustrera l’estrument dont tu avras mestier, selonc la conissance de cest art, et le tesmoignaige des manieres des maladies; si porpense l’estrument dont tu as mestier selonc ceu qu’il le covient.	And if the nose is corrupted and does not open at all, and the corruption is in the middle or in one part, then uncover the entire nose; then set fire to it with a torch, and then sew it together from one side to the other of the corruption, and let the thread run along the length of the corruption, as we have said; and if the corruption is in the joint, then cut off the joint that is corrupted, and sew the bone on either side; and if the corruption is in the continuation of two joints, then there will be no other pain than that of the joint; and if the corruption is at the knuckle or at the foot, it is very painful, but all the same you must inquire about this corrosion, how it opens; and clean it in all ways that you can, but so that the vein or nerve does not oppose you; and know that the saw and the sutures to cover these bones are many, according to the shape of the bones and the appearance of them, and their thickness and subtlety, and their greatness and smallness, and their hardness; and for this it is necessary to prepare each instrument for each kind of operation, and know that the work will show you the instrument that you will need, according to the knowledge of this art, and the signs of the ways of diseases; so assume the instrument that you have need of according to what is appropriate.
dou feu	of fire
Li chiés porrissent ou par cause dedens, ou par cause defuer; et quant tu avras medicinee celle corrosion par la cure des medicines, et il ne profitent mie, si covient coper celui membre jusques au leu ou li corrosion vient, si que li malaides eschaipe par ceu de la mort, ou par la malice, qui est plus grans, de la defaute dou membre; et li signes si est que li membres devient noir, si qu’il semble qu’il soit ars dou feu, et porrist aprés la noiror, pues va celle corrosions de membre em membre, et prent par tout le cors; si te haste dou coper, et se c’est par la percussion d’aucunes venimouses bestes, si com scorpion de mer et wivre et semblans, se li corrosion est au chief dou doi, si le cope, et ne li doner mie espaice de venir jusc’a la main.	In case of swelling or pain; and when you have applied medicine to the corrosion by way of cure with medicines, and it does not benefit, then cover that member up to the place where the corrosion comes, so that the patient escapes from this one death or the other, which is greater, from the fault of the member; and the signs are that the members turn black, as though they were burned by fire, and after the blackening, it follows that the corrosion takes hold of one member after another, and permeates all the body; if you hurry to cover it up, and if it is due to the percussion of certain poisonous animals, such as sea scorpions and adders and others, then cover the head of the member, and do not give it space to come up to the hand.
Et s’elle vient jusc’a la main, si la cope a la jointe, si que la corrosion ne viegne jusc’a bras; et s’elle vient au bras, si le cope au coute; et s’elle passe le coute, c’est li mors, et n’i vaut amenistremens fuers que li quantitez de sa vertut; et tot ensi fai quant li corrosion vient ou piet: s’elle vient en la premiere jointe, si la cope aprés l’autre jointe; et s’elle vient ou piet, si cope tout le piet; et s’elle monte en la jambe, si cope a la jointure dou genoil; et s’elle vient desus le genoil, si n’i a autre engien que dou lassier le malaide a mort; et li maniere dou coper ou dou soier le membre si est que tu le lie desus et desoz, et estende uns menistres l’un des liiens aval, et uns autres ministres l’autre liien amont, et tu dessevre la char qui est entre les II liiens a I spatumile large, tant que li os soit descovers; puis le cope ou soie, et met de chescune part I drapeil de lin, si que li soie ne touche le leu sain, et viegne au malaide autre lesion et aposteme chaus.	And if it comes up to the hand, then cover it at the joint, so that the corrosion does not come up to the arm; and if it comes to the arm, then cover it at the shoulder; and if it goes beyond the shoulder, it is death, and there is no remedy except the quantity of its virtue; and do all this as soon as the corrosion appears, whether it is in the first joint or later; and if it appears at the foot, then wrap the whole leg; and if it comes up the leg, then cover the knee joint; and if it comes above the knee, there is only one thing to do for the sick person to die; and the way of covering or soaping the member is that you tie it on top and bottom, and extend one minister a length of linen thread on either side, and you unravel the cloth which is between the two threads to the size of a large spatumile, until the bone is uncovered; then cover or soie it, and put a piece of linen cloth on each side, so that the soie does not touch the joint health, and comes to the patient another injury and abscess.
Et se decorremens de sanc vient quant tu oevres, si cauterize le leu hastanment, ou tu met sus aucunes poudres restraignans; puis revien a ta medicine tant qu’elle soit acomplie, puis lie le membre navreit d’un liien covenauble, et le cure tant qu’il soit sanez; et je te conterai k’il avint a I home en som piet: il li avint une noiror qui sembloit arsure de feu, et celle corrosion vint premier en son doi dou piet, tant qu’elle porprist tout le piet; et quant li hons vit la corrosion, si se hasta de coper le piet, et fut sanez; et lonc tens aprés li revint li corrosion ou doi de la main, et il vint a moi, et je li mis sus choses repercussives aprés la mundification dou cors, et ne pot cesser li corrosions; et il vot que je li copasse la main, et je ne vou, que je avoie esperance de repercuter la matiere; et doutai ausi que se je tailloie sa main, qu’il ne morist, car li vertus de l’ome estoit foible; et il se despera toz, et revint en sa terre, et se hasta de coper sa main, et fut sanez; et je n’ai ceu conteit fuers que por ceu c’on faice autreteil, s’on en a mestier.	Et si the decorremens de sanc comes when you operate, if you cauterize the area thoroughly, or you put on some powders to restrain it; then return to your medicine until it is completed, then bind the injured member with a convenient bandage, and treat it until it is healed; and I will tell you what happened to the man at home in some detail: he got a blackening that seemed like burning from fire, and that corrosion came first in order from the foot, so much so that it discolored all of the foot; and when the man saw the corrosion, if he covered his foot with copper, it was healed; and a long time later the corrosion returned to its place on the hand, and it came to me, and I put things that rebound after purification of the body, and could not stop the corrosions; and he said that I should cut off his hand, and I would not, that I had hope of rebounding the material; and I also doubted that if I were to shave his hand, he would not die, for the man's virtues were weak; and he despaired completely, and returned to his land, and covered his hand with copper, and was healed; and I only told this because it might be useful to do something different if necessary.
Aucune fois vient aposteme en leu charnut, et demore si longement qu’il fait grant assemblee de bowe; et puis ront et perce, et en saut li bowe, et demoure li leus vuis, ausi com uns vasselz; et li cuir qui est desus est ausi subtilz com I drapelz deliiez, et ne corront mie jusc’a l’os, ne jusc’au nerf, et telz maladie si est apelee «sain», et n’est mie apelee «fistule»; mais s’elle est si alongie qu’elle viegne jusc’a l’os em parfont, si est apelee «fistule»; et li cuire si est que tu cope celui cuir tout entor, et meismement quant il est subtilz, ausi com uns drapelz; et ne s’aert mie por sa corruption.	No one time comes an abscess in the flesh, and it remains so long that it makes a great gathering of bowel; and then rot and pierce, and spring the bowel, and remain the viscera as ours, and the skin which is above is also fine like sails, and do not corrode until the bone, nor until the nerve, and such disease is called "healthy", and is not called "fistula"; but if it is so long that it comes to the bone completely, then it is called a "fistula"; and the skin is such that you cover all the skin with it, and most especially when it is fine like sails; and does not rot for its corruption.
Et se tu as fiance que li cuirs s’aerde, et li corruption n’est mie en parfont, et li cuir est espés de char, si le cure de clistere ensi: regarde se li seins est grans, et li bowe qui en ist est de puant odor, adonques le clisterize de medicine egiptiaine qui est ensi faite: prenez aisil, et oile, et litargire, igalment, et metez cuire en I vassel au feu, tant que li medicine soit rouge, et deviegne ausi espesse com miel; et puis pren de ceu selonc ta necessiteit, et le font en aigue et en miel, et en clisterize lou sein, et estraint le pertus; et laisse la medicine ens par II houres, puis l’estrai en espreignant; fai ce mout de fois, tant que li seins soit mondefiiez, et soit ostee li puor; et aucune fois est clisterizeis d’aigue de cendres, quant ceste medicine n’est presens, et est que tu preignes cendres de fust de vigne, et giete aigue desus, puis la coule, et en clisterize, tant que tu saiches que li seins est bien mondez; et se li malaides ne le puet soffrir, ne la medicine egiptiaine ne l’aigue de cendres, si le clisterize d’aigue et de miel ou il ait un poc de litargire broiet; ou tu la clistirize de miel et de vin melleit, que li mielz ait proprieteit de mundifiier et de laver, et li vins fait aerdre le sain; et quant tu as ce fait, et tu as fiance que li seins est bien mundifiiez, si le clisterize de ceu que fait naistre char en li, et est que tu preignes emplaustre diafinit, et le font avec oile roset et en vin; ou tu le clisterize d’aucunes medicines et d’oignemens, dont j’ai dit les proprietez ou traitier des oignemens; et se li pertus dou sein est petis, et li cainne dou clistere n’i puet entrer, si l’eslarge d’un fer un poc, et met ens une tente de l’oignement egiptiein, ou oignement basilicon, tant k’il soit eslargiez; et se li plaie est trop large, si la cout et i laisse tant soulement I leu ou li clistere puisse entrer, et se li pertus que giete bowe est au desus, si le cope ou plus bas leu que i est.	And if you are sure that the skin will rot, and the corruption is not complete, and the skin is like a carriage cover, then wash it with Egyptian medicine made like this: take oil, and turpentine, and equal parts, and put the skin in a vat to cook on the fire, until the medicine turns red, and thickens too; and then take some of that according to your need, and make it into water and honey, and clisterize the breast, and extract the pus; and leave the medicine there for two hours, and then strain it out by squeezing; do this a hundred times, until the breast is very red, and the pustule has come out; and never clisterize with water of ashes when this medicine is not present, but if you squeeze ash from a vine, and pour water on it, and let it run, and clisterize it, until you know that the breast is very red; and if the patient cannot bear the medicine or Egyptian water of ashes, then clisterize with honey and wine, which has the property to cleanse and wash, and the wine makes the disease come out; and when you have done this, and are sure that the breast is very clean, then clisterize it with char, and make it like plaster, and cook it with oil of roses and wine; or clisterize it with some medicines and ointments, whose properties I have described in treating of ointments; and if the breach in the breast is small, and the catheter for the clisterize cannot enter, then enlarge it a little with iron, and put an ointment of Egyptian or basilicon ointment, until it is enlarged; and if the wound is too wide, then leave it open so that the catheter can enter, and the breach where the bowels come out is above, then cut off or lower the breast where it is.
Car quant li bowe est en parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char; et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si appareille en tel maniere que li bowe corre au plus bas leu que i est, car quant li bowe est parfont, si n’i laisse enjanrer char et se tu ne pues coper lou sein desoz si com tu vues, si apareille en teil maniere: que li bowe corre legierement aval, et n’i lassier rien de la bowe; et pren medicines consolidatives por mettre sor le sain, et estent sus I drapeil de lin que cuevre tout le sain; puis cope as forces endroit le pertus dou sein I poc plus large dou premier, pues estent oignement souef sus I autre drapel selonc la quantiteit dou pertus, et le met sus le pertus dou sain por aligier la bowe, et n’oster mie le grant drapeil fuers que aprés maint jor une fois; et celui qui est sor le pertus dou sein, oste sovent por oster la bowe, et saiches ceu que corra de la bowe, se c’est venin ou poc ou assez, ou digeste, ou indigeste; et pren warde se li patiens sent dolor ou nom, et s’il i a aposteme ou non, et quant ta medicine s’est en teil maniere estendue et tu vois la nature que saut sus le pertus dou sain, si saiches que li seins s’aert ja, et aproche li santez; et puis le deslie le matin, ou le tier jor, et quant tu delies la plaie, si chainge I autre drapeil, et renovele l’oignement.	Car when the bowels are in perfect health, then one should not let them become constipated; and if you cannot cover the anus properly as you see fit, then prepare it in such a way that the bowels run down to the lowest part that they can go, for when the bowels are in perfect health, then one should not let them become constipated and if you cannot cover the anus properly as you see fit, then prepare it in such a way: that the bowels run lightly downward, leaving nothing of the bowels behind; and take medicines that consolidate to put on top of the wound, and place them on I lin-cloth that covers all the wound; then cover with force at the area of the anus where it is wider than the first, since ointment is applied according to the quantity of the opening, and place it over the wound to ease the bowels, and do not remove the large cloth except after many days once; and that which is on top of the opening should be removed often to remove the bowels, and know what runs from the bowels, whether it is venom or pus or enough or digested or undigested; and take care that the patient feels pain or no pain, and if there is an abscess or not, and how far the medicine has spread in such a way that you see the nature that rises over the opening of the wound, then know that the breasts are beginning to work again, and come closer to them; and then remove them in the morning, or on the third day, and when you remove the wound, if you change another cloth, and renew the ointment.
Et se li seins giete bowe indigeste aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie.	And if her breasts are swollen and painful after many days, because her breasts do not ache.
Et se venins subtilz cort aprés lonc tens, si ne te desperer mie de la santeit, car li santez aproche.	And if subtle poisons run long after the spring, so that you are not desperate for health because healing is close.
Car il i a homes cui tarde enjanremens de char en ses plaies, et de ces que font le contraire; et se bowe indigeste saut dou sein aprés maint jor, saiches que li seins ne s’aert mie; et se li seins tarde d’aerdre, et est porloigniez, si ajoste medicines sechans moistes en substance et seches en vertut, si com oignement diafinit, car il i a grant partie de vitriole, et c’est li derriene medicine; pren oignement dyafinit, et le font avec oile roset, et l’arose de viel vin igal en substance; puis le confit et en use; et ceu meisme fait mielz cuit engroissiez, quant oignemens dyafinit n’est presens, ou tu pren mirre et aloen et encens, et le broie, et le poudre sus le miel quant il est sor le feu; et puis en glue I drapel, et l’estent sor le sein, et aucune fois i aministre on aristologe longe, et racines de lis celeste, qui est ausi com farine de veces et centoire; et en use de simples ou de compostes: broie les, et en fai poudre, et met sus le miel que j’ai dit, et en use; et se li cure est alongie, et n’est curez par ceste cure, adonc saiches que la corruptions est em parfont, et fait empression en l’os, ou as membres durs, ou as liemens; si le cure de la cure de fistule, si com nos avons dit ci devant.	For there are some who late in their recovery from heat in the wounds, and from that which makes them opposite; and if her breasts are swollen and painful after many days, because her breasts do not ache; and if her breasts delay in healing, and are enlarged, so that medicines that dry out moist substances and dry out useful substances, as it were, are necessary because healing is slow, for there is a great deal of vitriol, and that is the opposite medicine; take the opposite of it, and make it with oil, and sprinkle it with fair wine that is equal in substance; then confit and use it; and this also makes better honey cooked and increased when dried on fire; and then glue it in a cloth, and put it on the breast, and never administer it with an aromatic drug, or with roots of the heavens, which is also like flour of times and centore; and use them of simple or compound medicines: grind them, and make powder, and put on honey that I have said, and use it; and if the cure is long, and is not cured by this cure, then know that corruption is complete, and makes an impression in the bone, or in hard members, or in joints; if the cure of fistula, as we have said before.
de l’aposteme de l’ungle	of the nail of the toe
Panarice est un aposteme que naist desoz l’ungle dou pouchiet de la main, ou dou piet, ou par aventure naist en autres dois; et quant il est envielliez, et on n’i prent garde, si i vient I aposteme chaus, et corront et giete bowe tant qu’elle corront la racine de l’ungle, et par aventure la corront toute; et vient li corrosions jusc’a l’os, tant qu’il i vient dolor puant, et est li chiés dou doi larges, et est li color fuxe.	A bunion is a growth that develops at the base of a toe or, on occasion, in another part of the hand; and when it has broken out, and one does not pay attention to it, then it comes to an ulceration, and hurts and makes one sneeze so much that the root of the nail comes off, and perhaps even the whole nail, and there is a burning pain until it reaches the bone, so much so that there is a strong pain, and the two toes are wide apart, and the color turns blue.
Quant tu le cures si com nos avons dit en la division, et li cure ne profite mie, si covient que tu copes a i. fer toute la superfluiteit qui est demoree de l’ungle, puis cauterize la plaie aprés.	When you treat it as we have said in the division, and the cure does not benefit, then you must cut off all the excess that has accumulated under the nail, and then cauterize the wound afterwards.
Li cauteres est mout grans aide se li os est sains, et li ungle est sainne; et se li ungle apresse la char ens, et l’encomence a poindre, et la blece, si covient que tu mettes lou rait desoz l’ungle que point la char, et la boute en haut, et cope celi char subtilment et legierement, et met sus le remenant de la char medicines ardans et corrosives por oster tout; puis le cure d’oignemens tant qu’il soit sanez.	The cauterization is a great help if the bone is sound, and the nail is healthy; but if the nail presses upon the flesh and causes it to ache, then you must cut off the toenail with care, and cut back the edge that presses upon the flesh, very lightly and carefully, and place burning and corrosive medicines on top of it in order to destroy all of it; then treat with ointments until it is healthy.

des vils	of evil
Vis sont voinnes grosses envoloupees pleines de superfluitez melancoliouses, que vienent em plusors membres dou cors; et plus avient en jambes de ces qui vont a piet et qui travaillent et portent, que a autres. The cutting according to this way: arise the first the leg of a hot water very strongly, until the thick blood is thinned out, then extract the leg of the sick from above the knee up to the part between the thigh and the calf; then cut the vein in one place, or two, or three, of a wide size, then drain and drive out the black blood by your hand, from one head to another, until as much blood comes out as the virtue of the sick can bear; and then bind it, and order him that he fastens himself of meat in rubbing black blood; and then begin the evacuation and the washing again when the veins are empty, and keep doing this to the sick.

des vers qui naissent entre cuir et char	vers that hatch between leather and cart
Ceste maladie est apelee en nostre terre «maladie de buef», por ceu qu’elle avient maintes fois as bués, et est un petis vers qui naist entre cuir et char, et va par tout le cors montant et dessendant, et le sent om bien a l’aler de membre en membre, tant qu’il desront le cuir ou il vait, et saut fuer; et est enjanrez de porriture d’aucunes humors, si com vienent vers et serpens et lumbris et ascarides ou ventre; et doute on de son malice, car quant il va par le cors, et il monte au chief, et il vient a l’oil, par aventure rentre, et destruit l’oil; et ceu avient maintes fois. This disease is called in our land "vacir," and it is a pain that comes in some members, and then moves from member to member; and I have seen this one that I told you.

Je me mervillai mout coment elle se movoit ensi de membre em membre, car je n’avoie onques veut ceste maladie selonc ceste maniere.	I marveled how much this woman was moving her member from one to the other, for I had never seen such a thing with this disease.

Je la quis a tout une subtil tente, et ne la sentis mie; et il sentoit pointure et dolor desoz sa destre oreille.	I left it under a sutured tent for a long time, and I did not feel it; but he felt pain and ache on his right ear.
Je pensai que c’estoit de la pointe de la saiette Je mis sus lou leu emplaustre atratifet digestif, por ceu que li leus n’enflast; et m’aparut li leus de la saiette.	I thought it was from the tip of the arrow. I put on the plaster of the Arrow-head, to prevent it from getting swollen; and I saw the arrow-heads.
Je i mis l’emplaustre mains jors, et resouda li plaie derechief, et demora ensi li malaides lonc tens, tant qu’il sentit la saiette I jor dedens son neis; et il le me dist.	I put on the plaster right away, and resolved the wound immediately, and delayed it for a long time so that the patient could feel the arrow-head inside his neck; and he told me.
Je mis sus la plaie medicine ague corrosive par mains jors, tant qu’elle fut overte, et la tentai, et sentis le chief de la saiette qui s’aerdoit au leu; puis ajostai en l’overture de la plaie par celle medicine ague, tant que li chiés de la saiette m’aparut visablement; et trespassa bien li termines entor IIII mois, et puis eslarja si li plaie que je i boutai les tenailles, et le meus d’une part et d’autre, et ne pot issir; adonques ne cessai de subtiliier et d’engignier de manieres d’estrumens, tant que je la pris I jor as tenailles bien faites, selonc ceu que sa forme venra en la fin de cest chapistre, tant que je la traï, et restourai la plaie.	I put on the medicine that burns acutely right away, until it was opened, and tested it, and felt the head of the arrow which was burning at its place; then I added to the opening of the wound with this medicine, until the head of the arrow appeared clearly to me; and three months later, and then the wound spread so much that I had to use tweezers from both sides, and I could not get it out; therefore I ceased not to try and invent ways of tools, until I took it out with well-made tweezers, according to what its shape will be at the end of this chapter, until I took it, and healed the wound.
Et li mire jugent que li cartillaige dou nez ne puet restorer: je la restourai adonques, et fut soudee li plaie, et fut sanez li malaides entierement.	And I saw that the cartilage of the nose could not be restored; but I restored it then, and the wound was healed, and the sick man was completely cured.
Or t’ai dit la qualiteit de l’estraction d’aucunes saiettes, si que tu mettes ta cure sus ceu que je ne dis mie, car li livres ne puet mie tout porprendre; mais li saiges maistres compere sus bien poc grant chose, et sus ceu que li est present et defaillant, trueve nueve oevre, et nuef estrument, au dessendement des choses estrainges qui avienent en cest art.	Do you wish to speak of the extraction of certain arrows, so that you should apply your remedy to those things which I have not spoken of, for the book cannot do all; but master surgeons work on a few small things and on those that are present and failing, trueve with nine ouvres and neuf instruments, at the dismemberment of foreign things which come in this art.
Je dis que les saiettes n’issent des membres ou elles sont fichies fuer que selonc II manieres: ou par lou leu ou elles entrent, ou par d’autre part; et celle que saut fuer par lai ou elle entre, c’est saiette entrans en leus charnus, et saut fuer aucune fois maintenant.	I say that arrows are in the members or they are stuck except for two ways: either by the place where they enter, or by another part; and that which jumps over into them, it is an arrow entering into their flesh, and never jumps any more.
Et s’elle ne saut maintenant, si la laisse tant que li chars soit porrie entor, et soit alegie li issue; et ausi s’elle est fichie en l’os, et elle ne puet issir, si la laisse ensi aucuns jors, et la muef chescun jor; et adonques elle saut, et s’elle ne saut, si perce entor a tout I foret subtil, tant que li leus entor soit eslargiez, et puis la trai.	And if she doesn't jump now, let her be as long as the bones are rotten inside, and the issue is clear; and likewise if she is stuck in the bone, and cannot come out, let her be so for some days, and then she will jump, and if she does not jump, then pierce all the tiny bones inside until the bones inside are widened, and then take it out.
Et se li saiette est fichie en l’os dou chief, et vait jusc’a l’un des ventres dou cerveil, et aucuns des accidens que j’ai dit apert au malaide: si ne la traire mie, mais la laisse tant qu’elle soit igalz aprés aucuns jors, car se li saiette vient jusc’a syfac, c’est li mors.	And if the arrow is stuck in the neck bone and goes to one of the head's ventricles, and some of the accidents that I have said above happen to the patient: do not pull it out, but leave it as long as it remains even after a few days, for if the arrow comes to the syfac, it is death.
Et se li saiette n’est fichie fuer qu’en l’os soulement, et ne vient jusc’a syfac, et demoure li malaides aucuns jors sens mavais accident, si l’engigne dou traire.	And if the arrow is stuck only in the shoulder bone, and does not come to the syfac, and the patient remains for some days without any bad accident, then use the device to pull it out.
Et s’elle est mout fichie ensi et ne puet issir fuer, si i aministre tareres entor, si com je t’ai dit; puis cure le leu tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if it is stuck like this inside and cannot be taken out, then you should administer tar water to it, as I told you; then cure the joint until it is healthy again.
Et se li saiette est reponue en leu dou cors si c’on ne la puisse veoir, si la quier a tout la tente; et se tu la sens, si la trai a aucun estrument covenauble; et se tu ne pues por l’estrecement de la plaie, et por la parfondesce de la saiette, et il n’i a os ne nerf ne voine, si la fens tant que li plaie soit grans; et trai la saiette se tu pues, et s’il ait en la saiette oreilles a coi elle tient, si oste la char qui est ens fichie de II pars au mues que tu pues, et puis brise ou ploie les oreilles de la saiette, tant que tu la puisses traire; et subtilie bien que tu ne brisier la saiette, que tu la trairoies plus griement.	And if the arrow is stuck in the middle of the neck so that it cannot be seen, even after a thorough search; and if you feel it, take care to use a suitable tool; and if you are not able to extract it because of the pain, depth, or thickness of the arrow, and there are no bones, nerves, or veins nearby - break or bend the arrow until you can pull it out; and be very careful so that you do not break the arrow, but pull it out roughly.
Et se tu ne pues a une fois, si la lai jusque li leus entor soit porris, puis la trai, car li estraction iert alegie.	And if you cannot hold it once, then let it go until it is no longer painful, for extraction will be easier.
Et se li decorremens de sanc te fait contraire, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit de la cure en son chapistre; et te warde de l’incision dou nerf et de la voinne, et met engien coment tu pues mues traire la saiette sens peril, ou tost ou tart, ou fermement ou belement; et met le malaide selonc la forme qu’il estoit quant li saiette li chut ens, car c’est li plus grans aide que i soit, et se tu ne pues, si lou met selonc ceu que li signe lou te mostrent.	And if the pain from the extraction makes you lose your temper, then apply what we have said in the chapter on this paste; and be careful when cutting the nerve and opening the vein, and do not extract the arrow too quickly or slowly, or firmly or gently; and set the patient according to the form he was in when the arrow entered, for that is the greatest help there is, and if you cannot do that, then follow what the signs show you.
Li saiette que vient fuer d’autre part, ou il apert aucune chose de li, ou li cuir est enflez endroit si c’on le voit ou sent aparamment: taille donques sus, tant que les tenailles i puissent prendre, et puis l’estrai: si saut fuer maintenant.	The arrow that comes from another direction and does not pierce anything, or the wound is swollen in one place only if it can be seen or felt: cut it off as much as the scissors can take hold of it, and then extract it: do not wait any longer.
Et s’elle est retenue en l’os, si tornoie ta main rondement, tant qu’elle entre en l’os, et eslarge l’os, puis la trai.	And if it is held in the bone, turn your hand round, as far as it enters into the bone and broadens the bone, then remove it.
Et s’elle ne puet issir, si la laisse encor, et puis rencomence l’estraction tant qu’elle isse fuer; et se li fust de la saiette i est, se le boute a tout le fust; et se li fust chiet, et tu vues aministrer boutement, si i aministre I estrument cheveit, si que li pointe de la saiette entre en la cheveure de l’estrument; et puis boute fuer, et se li saiette est chevee, se i boute I estrument a pointe entrant ens, por alegier l’estraction.	And if it cannot be taken out, keep it still for a while longer, and then begin the extraction again as far as it will go; and if there is any doubt about whether it has come loose from the arrow or not, hold it with the tool, so that the point of the tool enters into the wound of the extraction; and then push on, and if the arrow has become loosened, push the tool against the head entering the wound, so as to ease the extraction.
Et se li saiette est entouchie, si covient que tu copes toute la char entor ou li venins est, se tu pues, puis cure la plaie si com il couvient.	And if the arrow has touched something, it is necessary that you cut away all of the flesh around where the poison is; if you can do so, then treat the wound as it should be treated.
Et se li saiette chiet ou peis ou au ventre ou a la vessie ou au costeit, et elle est prochiene, et tu pues coper sus, se i cope; et te garde de coper la voinne et lou nerf, et puis l’estrai, et puis cout la plaie, se mestier est; et la cure tant qu’elle soit sanee.	And if the arrow hits anywhere in the abdomen or bladder or ribs, and it is close, then you may cover it, if you can. And be careful not to cover the vein or nerve, and then extract it, and then patch up the wound, if that is your trade; and treat until she is well.
Li forme des tenailles dont on trait les saiettes sont semblans au bec d’oiseil, et vez ci la forme:	The form of the clamps used to treat arrows are similar to an owl's beak, and here is the form:
Et en sont mout de manieres: grans, moienes, et petites, selonc la quantitei de la saiette.	And there are many ways: large, medium, and small, depending on the size of the arrow.
Li forme dou boutant cheveit est ausi com li penne d’un oisel, por bouter a la pointe de la saiette, si com ci est li forme:	The form of the piercing knife used is similar to an owl's feather, to pierce the tip of the arrow, as here is the form:
li forme des tenailles por bouter et por sachier si est ci:	The form of the clamps for piercing and for extracting, if it is this, is:
des voinnes dou cors communes	Of the veins of the torso, common:
Des voinnes dont on se saine sont XXXI, de coi il a ou chef XVI, c’est a savoir: II batans qui sont aprés les oreilles, qui sont apelees les dous «herbech»; et les II arteres qui sont en II temples apparans; et II voines que sont en II larmiers des II eulz, que sont apelees «aspires»; et li voine que est emmi le front; et li voinne que est au chief dou neis; et les II guindeges qui sont ou col; et les II voinnes que sont en levres desus de la bouche, et ce sont les voines que sont apelees «augeherich»; et II voinnes que sont desoz la lengue.	XXXI veins from which one heals are XVI, that is to say: the two batans (ear lobes) called dous herbech; the two arteries in the two temples apparent; the two veins on the two cheeks of the two eyes, called aspires; the vein at the forehead; the vein at the top of the head; the two jugulars at the neck; the two veins on the lips above the mouth, which are called augerich; and the two veins that are behind the tongue.
Les voinnes dont on saine communement sont V en chescun bras: l’une est li cephalique, et est dou senestre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou chief»; et li moiene est apelee «faste», et est composte de la cephalique et de la basilique, et l’apelent li laie gens «voinne dou cuer»; et li basilique si est ou destre costeit, et l’apelent li laie gent «voinne dou ventre», et est sus le foscile, et est celle dont on saine, qui apert manifestement sus le pouchet.	The veins from which one commonly heals are V in each arm: one is the cephalic vein, and it runs along the left side of the chest, and is called by common people 'vein at the head'; its partner is called 'fast' and is composed of the cephalic and the basilic, and is called by common people 'vein at the wrist'; and the basilic lies on the right side of the chest, and is called by common people 'vein at the belly', and is on top of the shoulder blade; and this is the one from which one heals, opening clearly on top of the elbow.
Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l’auriculaire et l’anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l’une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet dou senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville dou destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee «nesse», que est en la cheville de l’autre costei; et en l’autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.	Et li salvatelle est li voine qui est entre l'auriculaire et l'anulaire, et si a II rains; et en la jambe et ou piet sont III voinnes: l'une si est desoz la corbeure dou pochet du senestre costeit, et li seconde sophene qui est a la cheville du destre costeit; et li voine qui est apelee "nesse", que est en la cheville de l'autre costei; et en l'autre jambe sont III voinnes desoz celles.
Li sainie des voinnes que sont aprés les oreilles si aide as catharres anciens, et a emigraine; et li qualiteis dou sainier, si com je te dis, et est que tu reises lou chief dou malaide, et frote lou leu ou les voinnes sont d’un drap aspre; puis estrigne li malaides son col a une vis, tant que les II voinnes aperent derrier les oreilles en II leus dependens dou chief: quier les donques a ton doi, et ou tu sens lou poulz desoz ton doi, si seigne d’enche; puis pren la lancette, et la boute par desoz la voine jusc’a l’os, puis lieve ta main a tout la voinne amont, et cope et lou cuir et la voinne bien II dois dou traver, et fai issir dou sanc tant que tu vues; puis l’estrain et lie, tant qu’ele soit sanee; et j’ai ja dit l’incision et le cautere ou premier livre.	The salvatrice is the vein between the index and middle fingers, and if it is inflamed; and in the leg and where the foot are three veins: one is dislocated from the flexor of the little finger of the left side, and the second, which is at the ankle of the right side; and the vein called "nesse", which is in the ankle of the other side; and in the other leg there are three veins dislocated from those. The salvatrice of the veins that are behind the ears helps with old catarrh and emesis; and the quality of the salve, as I told you, is to return the chief of the disease, and rub it where the veins are with a rough cloth; then extract the disease by a vis with its head, until the two veins open behind the ears in two places: feel them on your side, and wherever you feel a pulse moving, sign with your finger; then take the lance, and pierce through the vein up to the bone, then lift your hand towards all the vein upstream, and cut and strip the vein well, and make it bleed until you see it; then extract it and bind it tightly until it is healed; and I have already spoken of the incision and cauterization in the first book.
Li sainie des II arteres que sont en II temples, si vaut a emigrainne anciene, et sode, et obtalmie acostumee, et au cors des larmes agues as eulz; et li qualitez dou sainier si est si com je dis: et est que li malaides estraigne son col, tant que les II voinnes aperent apertement; et sent lou polz desoz ton doi, et puis seigne d’enche; puis lieve lou keur sus la voinne en haut a ton doi indice, et boute la lancette desoz, et lieve la voine en haut, et la cope, si com tu as fait en II autres voinnes, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit; puis deslie lou malaide, et met ton doi sus la voine une houre, puis met sus coton; et puis la lie forment, et la laisse tant qu’elle soit sanee; et nos en avons jai parleit et de lor copement et de lor estraction, ou comencement dou livre.	The two arteries that are in the two temples, so it is said, and the old, accustomed to being dry, and at the base of the eyes, used to the tears flowing there; and the quality of the eye so is as I say: and this is that the patient draws out his neck, until the two veins appear openly; and feel the little pole on your two fingers, then sign the end; then lift up his cure on the vein at the top of your index finger, and bottle the syringe from there, and lift up the vein above, and wrap it, so as you did in the other veins, and make a correction of the blood according to your need; then remove the patient, and put your two fingers on the vein for an hour, then put cotton on it; and then let it form, and leave it until it is healed; and we have spoken about their wrapping and extraction, or beginning of the book.
Li sainie de la voine dou front si vaut autant com li sainie de la cephalique as maladies de la faice ancienes, et a emigraine, et a roujor; et li qualitez si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant, tant que li voine apere; puis pren l’estrument qui est apelez «fosseur», dont ci est li forme:	The treatment for the headache at the front is as effective as that for the cerebral diseases of the old face, and for migraines and jalap. And the quality is such that the patient twists his neck until the vein appears; then take the instrument called a 'fosseur', whose form is:
Et met la pointe sus la voinne, et fier sus de ta main, ou d’autre chose, et laisse dou sanc issir selonc la quantiteit que tu vues; puis delie au malaide le col, et lie la voine tant qu’elle soit saneel et aucune fois l’uevre on d’un flaime large.	And place the point onto the vein, and hold it firmly with your hand or something else, and let blood flow according to the quantity that you see; then loosen the patient's neck, and tie the vein until it is healed, and never use a wide flame.
Toutevoie, il ne covient mie que li flaimes soit trop agus; et le saine de travers, car li os est pres, et par aventure brise li flaimes quant il est subtilz.	However, it is not appropriate that the flame be too hot; and the treatment for the spine should be from side to side, because the bone is close by, and the flame might break out if it is too small.
Li sainie des II voines que sont en II larmiers si aide as eulz, et a la tigne, et a la roujor, et a l’oriuel en l’oil, et as maladies de la faice; et li qualitez de lor sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col en tordant d’aucun liien, si com devant; puis le saine, et soit li sainie dou traver, un poc dou lonc dou flaime un poc large, car il n’i a point de char.	The treatment for the two veins in the two limbs helps with the itch, and with the jalap, and with the inflammation, and with oil in the face; and the quality of their treatment is such that the patient twists his neck without tying it, as before; then treat, and do the treatment from side to side, a little of long flame, a little of wide flame, because there is no fire.
Et se li flaimes est subtilz, par aventure si brise; puis fai corre dou sanc, tant com tu en as mestier, et puis lie sus couton, et le lie bien.	And if the flames are subtle, because of this break it; then make run blood, as much as you need, and then put on wool, and bind it well.
Li sainie de la voine dou neis si vaut a ague, et a sode forsenee, et a maladies de faice, si com emigraine et roujor que vient en la faice, et meimement quant elle est anciene; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estrigne son col, puis estrain son neis a ta main senestre, et pren lou flaime subtil lonc, et le fiche emmi la levre en l’espaice qui est entre les II narines, car li voinne n’apert mie bien enqui, et li sans comencera maintenant a corre; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, et fai corre dou sanc selonc ta necessiteit, puis la lie une nuit, car elle est mout tost restoree; et c’est li forme dou flaime:	And if the blood from the vein is running, and immediately stops; and with sudden fever, and diseases of the face, as if it is migraine and redness that comes on the face, even when it is old; and the quality of the blood is such that the patient strangles his throat, then draw his nose toward your left hand, and take a subtle long flame, and put it between the two nostrils because the vein does not open well, and now the blood will start to run; and don't go too far in perfection, and make the blood run as much as you need, then tie it for a night, because it is quickly restored; and this is the form of the flame:
Li sainie des II guindeges si aide a l’estrecement de l’alainne, et a l’encomencement de meselerie, et a mout de maladies, et a empetigine, et a corrodens, et a herpes, et estiomenes; et li qualitez de la sainie si est que li malaides estraigne son col desoz l’une et l’autre, si com nos avons dit; et soit li maistres estans sus lou chief dou malaide, et li malaides siece sus I siege, puis saine la voine dou lonc un poc largement, puis trai dou sanc tempreement, ou tant com mestier est; puis refai autreteil en l’autre voinne, puis deslie lou liien, et estraint andous les voines moienement, que li malaides n’estrangle; et le laisse jusc’au matin, que li plaie soit sanee.	The doctor should instruct the patient to let their hair grow long and even, and to avoid pricking or irritating them. 
de la sainie des leivres	of the health of the animals
Li sainie des voinnes des levres desus si aident a cole en la bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et fendures de levres, et dou neis et entor.	Of the health of the lips, that they may not hurt themselves when eating in the mouth, and do not corrode the gums, nor tear the lips, nor cause pain or disease in them.
Et li qualitez de la sainie si est de faire seoir lou malaide devant toi, et estraint son col si com j’ai dit; puis torne la levre, et regarde as II voinnes, dont l’une est a la destre levre et li autre a la senestre, et les conoist on par ceu qu’elles sont noires, et par ceu que entor elles a voines menues noires: cope donques l’une et l’autre, et se tu ne les conois, et tu en es en doutance, si cope la plus grosse de chescune part, et tout ausi fai des II voinnes que sont desus et desoz, car c’est une meisme maniere.	And the quality of the health is that it places the patient in front of you, and holds his neck as I have said; then turn the lip, and look at the veins, one on the right lip and the other on the left, which are known by this that they are black, and by this that they ache a little: so take the biggest of each, and do the same to the two veins that are above and below, because it is a similar method.
de la sainie desoz la lengue	of the health of the tongue
Li sainie des voinnes que sont desoz la lengue si aide aprés la sainie de la cephalique, et c’est a l’estrecement de la gorge, et as maladies de l’uve, et as maladies de la bouche; et li qualitez dou sainier si est que li malaides siece entre tes mains devant lou soleil, et li lieve la lengue, et regarde desoz en chescun costeit une voinne noire: saine donques l’une et l’autre, et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car desoz sont les arteres.	The doctor should instruct the patient to keep the tongue in place after treating the cerebral vein, as it is connected to the strangulation of the throat, and the diseases of the eye and mouth; and the quality of the doctor is that the patient should bite between his hands before the sun, and he should let the tongue fall, and look up at each side a black vein: so heal both, and do not cut too much perfectly, because the veins are there.
Les voinnes dou coute dont on saine communement sont sainies selonc II manieres: ou em poignant a tout I flaime mirtin large, ou olivaire subtil si com coutez trenchans, et est apelez «anesil»; et sont large et subtil selonc la largesce et l’estrecement des voinnes.	The veins of the neck that are commonly treated are healed according to two methods: either with a sharp, thick blade, or with a small, thin blade as if cutting vegetables, and it is called 'incision'; and they are wide and fine according to the width and strangulation of the veins.
Li forme dou flaime mirtin si est mout renommee, et est large si com tu vois:	The shape of the sharp, thick blade is called a 'flame', and it is wide as you see it.
Et ait mestier por ovrir les voinnes chevees plaines de gros sanc apparent, et que contienent gros sanc et trouble; et c’est li forme dou flaime olivaire:	And it is a craft to open the veins that are flat with great blood appearance, and which contain great blood and turmoil; and this is the form of the flame of olive:
et est plus subtilz apointé, et est por sainier les voinnes subtilz, ou il a subtil sanc citrin.	and it is more subtle pointed, and is to save the veins that are subtle, where there is subtle blood citron.
Li sainie de la basilique, qui est une de ces voinnes, si aide as maladies que sont desoz la gorge, et ou col, et ou peis, et ou ventre; et covient au sainor qu’il saine saigement, et qu’il se warse de l’artere qui est desoz.	The relief of the basilica, which is one of these veins, so help diseases that are destroyed in the throat, and where the neck, and where the chest, and where the belly; and it comes to the healer that he heal bloodletting, and that he warse the artery that is desoz.
Et s’il cope l’arterre, et decorremens de sanc vient, si le covient estainchier, si com j’ai dit; et ne doit mie estre poignans li flaime, mais taillans si com anesil.	And if he stop the artery, and the blood comes out, if it is necessary to stop bleeding, as I said; and should not be grasped the flame, but cut off like an animal.
Et se li basilique n’apert manifestement, si covient que tu l’estrainges, et chainge une autre; ou tu quieres aucun rain de li, ou tu saine en leu de li la voinne emmi le bras: elle apert manifestement; et la cope au flaime anesil, si com nos avons dit.	And if the basilica does not open manifestly, if it is necessary that you extrude it, and change another; or you want any rain of him, or you heal in its place the vein cutting off the arm: it opens manifestly; and it stops at anesil flame, as we have said.
Et se tu vues conoistre le leu de la sainie, si covient ainsois que tu estraignes lou bras, que tu touches le leu tant que tu conoisses le poulz; puis signe le leu d’enche, et puis lie lou bras, et cope la voine dou flaime anesil; et warde que tu ne ferir en l’artere quant tu vois le leu enfleit, car c’est de l’artere: eschui la donques.	And if you know the place of the vein, then it is also necessary that you extract the arm, that you touch the place as much as you can feel the pulse; then mark the place with your hand, and then tie the arm, and cut off the blood vessels under the flame carefully; and be careful not to injure the artery when you see the place of the vein, for it is an artery: avoid it.
Et se tu vois saillir en haut ausi com l’urine d’un enfant, et li sans est rouges et subtilz, saiches que c’est sans de l’artere: haste toi donques, et met ton doi sus longement, puis oste ton doi se li sans estainche, que maintes fois avient; se lie lou bras, et laisse ensi, et ne lou mueve li malaides; et soit sus paour, et ne lou mueve tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if you see it coming out on top as if the urine of a child, and the veins are red and thin, know that it is an artery: hurry up then, and place your thumb on it for a long time, and then remove your thumb so that it does not hurt, which often happens; tie the arm, and leave it like that, and do not move the patient; and be afraid, and do not move it until it is healed.
Et se li sans n’est estainchiez, et il te vaint, et li medicine ne t’est presens, si cope l’artere s’elle apert, car li chief de li retraient; et estainche li sans.	And if he does not stop bleeding, and you go, and the medicine is not there, if you cut the artery, because the head of the retort stops it; and stop the bleeding.
Et pren une escorce de fistice, et la fent, et pren l’une des moitiez et lie sus bien jusc’a l’autre jor; se li sans estainche, c’est bien; se ce non, si le cure, si com nos avons dit, des poudres qui estainchent sanc; et li estainchemens n’est mie griés em plusors dispositions por le petit leu de la plaie, et la possance dou liien dou bras.	And take a piece of fig tree, and bind it, and take one of the halves and put it well up to the other day; if the bleeding stops, it is good; if not, apply the powder that stops blood, as we have said, in various preparations for the small size of the wound, and the power of the vein of the arm.
Li sainie de la voinne em mileu si aide qu’elle trait sanc dou chief desus, et dou cors desoz, por ceu qu’elle est composte de la basilique et de la cephalique, si com nos avons dit; et covient au sainor qu’il se warse por lou nerf qui est desoz, et s’il point trop em parfont, et il trueve lou nerf, et il enfle et li santez soit griés, et par aventure ne puet saner; et cist nerf apert mult de fois, et s’il n’apert en aucuns homes por sa subtiliteit, si covient que tu lou saines de l’estrument anesil; et eschui lou nerf a ton pooir.	The healing of the vein in the middle, so that it stops bleeding from the head and the vein at the base, because it is composed of basilicum and cephalicum, as we have said; and it is up to the patient who hurts himself by warping the nerve which is at the base, and if he cuts it too much in perfection, it will bleed, and it swells and its healing is damaged, and perhaps it does not heal; and this nerve opens many times, and if it does not open in any man because of its subtility, then you must cut it with an anesthenic; and avoid wounding the nerve at your power.
Et se il a voinne entre les II ners, si la fent dou lonc.	And if there is a vein between the two necks, then cut it short.
Li sainie de la cephalique si aide, qu’ele atrait sanc dou chief, et aide as eulz; et covient sainier em poignant au flaime olivaire ou au flaime mirtin, car c’est li plus sauve de toutes les voinnes, car il n’a desoz li ne nerf ne artere.	And the cure for a headache is to draw blood from the head, and to let it flow; and it should be done by pricking at the olive flame or the merkurial flame, since this is the safest of all veins, because it does not damage the nerve or artery.
Toutevoie, covient querir lou plus legier leu, et ne grieve rien s’on faut la premiere fois, et on rencomence; et par aventure enfle li leus a aucuns homes, cant on faut la premiere fois, mais il ne grieve rien.	However, it is necessary to choose the easiest way, and do not grieve anything if it fails the first time, and start again; and by chance, the blood flows in some men, when it fails the first time, but it does not grieve anything.
La qualitez de la sainie si est selonc ta pensee.	The quality of the bloodletting is according to your thought.
Li premiere chose que tu dois savoir de sainier, si est que sainie n’est amenistree fuer que por garder santeit, et por eschuir les maladies a venir; et soit li sainie faite en l’une des III voinnes que sont ou coute: c’est a savoir, cephalique, faste, et basilique; et se doit on sainier en l’encomencement de prientens a geun, et en autompne et en yver aprés mengier, quant li signe de repletion aperent; et se doit on sainier le premier jor ou le tier, aprés II houres ou III dou jor.	The first thing you must know about bloodletting is that it should be done only to maintain health and avoid future diseases; and it must be done in one of the three veins: cephalic, facial, and basilic; and it should be done at the beginning of a fast, or in autumn or winter after eating, when the sign of fullness appears; and it should be done on the first day or the third day after every two hours.
Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n’a point d’oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc’a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc’a septime.	Li sainie qui est aministree as maladies n'a point d'oure determinee, mais que quant besoing est de jor ou de nut, en toutes houres et en toz tens; et ne covient mie sainier les enfans jusc'a XIIII ans, ne femme portant fuer que des lou quart mois jusc'a septime.
Ne ne se doient mie sainier li viel qui ont passez LX ans.	The patient who is free from disease does not have a determined time limit, but when it comes to eating or drinking, it is in all hours and at all times; and one should not heal children until they are 12-13 years old, nor women who have been pregnant for less than four months until they are seven months pregnant. One should not heal the elderly who have passed 60 years of age.
Et quant aucuns se vuet sainier, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient k’il mondefie les intestines d’un clistere legier, s’il a mout de fiens retenut, si que les voines n’atraient des intestines les superfluitez porries nuisans as membres principelz; ne ne se saine mie cil qui est trop saolez de viandes, ne qui est yvres, tant k’il en soit fuer, ne ydropiques; et se warse on de sainier aprés colique passion, et vomissement, et decorrement de ventre, et multipliement d’abiter a femme, et de traval, de veiller et de juner, et ceu que tot la vertu, ou par chose de l’arme ou dou cors; puis subtilie les humors, se li sans est gros, par viandes et par bevraiges et par medicines, se tu en as lou poir; puis entre ou bain, s’aucune chose ne lou deffent, por subtiliier lou sanc, et te saine de la voinne dou pis entor la tierce, si com nos avons dit; et te garde celui jor de travail, et de poinne, et de luxure, et de semblans choses; et soies liez et joians, et soit li sainieres plus haut que cil cui on saine, et li frote lou bras II fois ou III, puis estraigne lou liien desus moienement, car quant il est trop estrois ou poc, si ne puet corre li sans; et puis le frote le leu as mains, tant que les voines enflent, et les sente on; puis moille li sainieres le flaime d’un poc d’oile viel, puis mette son doit de sa main senestre sus celle voinne desoz lou leu un poc ou il vuet sainier, que li voinne ne fue et faille au ferir.	And when someone is to be healed, in whatever way it is done, it is necessary to make a light enema, if there is a blockage, so that the intestines do not draw out the superfluous rubbish that is harmful to the main organs; and one should not heal him who is too much affected by meat, or wine, as long as it lasts, nor urines; and one should not heal after a colic, vomiting, abdominal pain, excessive menstruation, travelling, staying up late, eating and drinking, and using medicines, if there is any harm to them; then let him bath or swim, unless something hurts them, so as to subtilize the blood, and let him be healed from the vein at the base of the penis, as we have said; and guard yourself that day from work, and from hunger, lust, and similar things; and be moderate and prudent, and let the healer who heals you be higher than the one who heals you, and rub his arms twice or three times, then draw the ligature away with ease, because when it is too constricted or tight, it cannot be unfastened; and then rub the healer with his own hand on the base of the penis, as long as the veins swell, and one can feel them; then moisten the healer with a little old oil, then put his thumb of his left hand on that vein where he is to be healed, so that the vein does not hurt or cause pain.
Car il i a voinnes que fuient ausi com cordes au sainier, et si a de telz que sont plainnes de ventositeit, si que quant on met sus le flaime, si retrait a flaime, et ne puet ovrir li voinne, et ensi est on de ceus; et s’il aoevre la voinne, si est li plaie trop estroite, por ceu si covient que li sainieres soit avisez en ces choses.	Car il y a des veines qui fuient comme des cordes au tailleur, et si elles sont de telles que sont plates de ventitude, si que quand on les met sur le feu, si on les retire du feu, et ne peuvent être ouvertes la veine, et ainsi sont-elles de ce genre; et si on ouvre la veine, si est la plaie trop étroite, pour ce que il convient que le tailleur soit averti en ces choses.
Et se li voine oevre la premiere fois, c’est boin; se ceu non, si rencomence ancor un poc desoz celui leu ou sus hastanment, se li leus n’est enflez.	For veins that flow like strings on the tailor, and if they are of such that they are flat with windiness, so that when you put them on fire, if you remove them from fire, and cannot open the vein, and so are they of this sort; and if you open the vein for the first time, it is good; but if not, then again begin a little bit at a time those legs or under hospital, if their lees are not swollen.
Et se li leus est enflez, et li malaides s’espoante, se li laisse I jor ou II, et ne liier mie le bras: par aventure i venra apostemes chaus; ne n’entre ou bain, puis rencomence la sainie s’elle li plait; et se li pertuis est petis, ou li sans cort subtilment et tu doutes qu’il n’isse mie tant de sanc com tu vues, si fier en celui pertuis meisme a tout le flaime droitement; et l’uevre un poc hastanment, ainsois que li leus soit enflez; car ceu avient maintes fois, quant li plaie est petite.	And if their lees are swollen and the patient hopes, let him rest one day or two, and do not bind his arm: perhaps it will come an abscess; nor go into a bath, then begin again the operation if it pleases her; and if the breach is small, or the skin is thin, and you doubt that it will not bleed as much as you see, so put all your fire directly on it; and work a little bit in hospital, so that their lees are swollen; for this happens many times, when the wound is small.
Se tu vois le leu enfleit, si ne rencomencier mie la sainie, et met sus un poc de lie d’oile, car elle alige lou cors dou sanc, et est muedre en cest leu li lie que li oile; et ensi aministre la lie de oile en chescune sainie que tu saines les voines, por estanchier lou cours dou sanc; et ceu meisme fait triaicle et bowe d’eus, quant on le met sus le leu; si subtilie li sans et s’espart quant il est trop gros.	If you see a wound that is infected, do not put anything on it yet, but put a little oil on it, for it dries up the blood in this place and makes it soft with the oil; and so administer the oil to each wound you treat, to stop the flow of blood; and if you do this it will make a small hole and burst when it is too large.
Et s’il i vient uns apostemes gros, qui avient maintes fois, meismement quant il n’est sainiez fuer que a celi fois ou li overture de la voinne est petite, si te haste, et met sus le leu esponge moillie en aigue et en seil un poc chaut, et l’estraint une houre; et covient que tu faices ceu aprés l’issue dou sanc de la voinne, et s’il demoure au leu aprés aucuns jors aucune noiror ou verdor, si ne li nuist mie; et se tu vues, met sus aucune chose de aloes ou de mirre remise en jus de calament, monstastre, ou semblant.	If there is a large abscess that happens many times, most especially when the opening of the vein is small, you must hurry and put a wet sponge in water and tie it around for an hour; and it is good that after the blood goes out of the vein you do this, and if it stays at the place after some days there is no harm to it; and if you see it, put something of aloe or myrrh applied with calamine juice, marjoram, or similar.
Et maintes fois avient aposteme et aparance a la sainie de la basilique: met donques ta main sus, et se tu trueves le leu mol a la compression de la main, si est celle aparance male.	And many times there is an abscess and an appearance in the temple of the basin: so put your hand on it, and if you find the place soft to the pressure of the hand, then this appearance is bad.
Eschui donques que tu ne mettes sus aucune chose de ceu que nos avons dit, car par aventure en cort sans de l’artere; mais li fai I emplaustre sec por endurcir le leu, puis le cure d’autre cure, tant qu’il soit sanez.	I do not want you to put your hand on anything of what we have said, for perhaps in the cut without an artery; but he makes it dry with patch, so he cures it with other cure, as long as it is healthy.
Et trai a chescun dou sanc selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu, et de la color dou sanc.	And each person should be treated according to the quantity of his virtue and the color of his blood.
Car se li sans est noir, si en laisse issir tant qu’il soit rouges; et se tu lou vois gros, si lou laisse tant qu’il soit subtiliiez; et s’il est trop chaus, si le laisse refroidier.	For if the person's blood is black, let it come out until it is red; and if you see him sweat a lot, let him cool down; and if he is too hot, let him cool down.
Et covient a celui qui est plains et fors, et ait mestier d’estraction de sanc, c’on li faice plus large plaie, et soit li flaimes larges; et a celui qui est foibles, fai le contraire, et le covient sainier poc et sovent, et le doit on sainier en taillant de travers, ne mie en poignant; et ceste maniere de sainie est sauve de decorrement de sanc et de copement de nerf, et vaut mues que li sainie dou lonc ne dou large.	And for those who are weak and have a need to extract blood, let them make a larger wound, and have the flames wide; and for those who are feeble, do the opposite, and it is better that the person who is long in health and often should be cured by cutting across, not by piercing; and this way of curing is saved from the decay of blood and the melting of the nerves, and it is better than the long cure.
