Et a celui cui li cors faut a la sainie, covient doner pain moilliet en jus de pomes grenates; s’il est eschaufez, si trai dou sanc III fois ou IIII Et s’il est de froide complexion, si menjuce devant la sainie pain moilliet en sirop muzé, ou en sirop de miel aromatique avec espices, si com poivre, canelle, gingibre, et chiches, et sirop bien odorant.	And for those whose course is to the sea, it is right to give moist bread in grape juice; if it is heated up, eat three times or four times and if it is of a cold complexion, before eating the moist bread, make a syrup with muscatel grapes, or honey with aromatic spices such as pepper, cinnamon, ginger, and fennel seeds, and well-smelling syrup.
Et s’il paume a la sainie, aprés l’issue de mout de sanc, si covient qu’il hume brouet de char, et sirop odorant subtil, et use des autres choses que nos avons dit en la division ou chapistre de sincope, por l’evacuation de voinne.	And if it is the case that one has had a bout of diarrhea after eating bread made with three or four times the normal amount of grape juice, then it is right to drink beer and subtle, fragrant syrup, and use other things that we have mentioned in the division or chapter on syncope for the evacuation of the vein.
Et s’il vuet esventer som bras, et sainier autre fois, si covient, quant il est afoiblis par grant sainie, k’il se saine poc et poc, selonc la quantiteit de sa vertu continueement.	And if one farts with the arms raised up and then begins to vomit at another time, when he is weakened by great vomiting, that he heal little by little, according to the quantity of his continuing virtue.
Et qui vuet esventer som bras aprés la premiere sainie, et il a cors fort, si se saine VII houres aprés la premiere sainie, ou aprés la nuevime houre.	And who wants to vent his arms after the first wound, and he has a strong cord, so that he heals seven hours after the first wound, or after the ninth hour.
Et qui se vuet sainier d’autre part, si se doit sainier lou secont jor ou le tier.	And who wants to be wounded elsewhere, should be healed in two days or three.
Car il a mout de sanc dedens le cors qui est ja eschaufez, et fait venir fievre; si en covient traire grant quantiteit, et eslargir le pertus tant qu’il chiece em pameson; puis que tu rewardes toutes les conditions de sainie, et met ta main sus som poulz quant il saine, que li mors ne viegne en leu de pameson, et ceu avient maintes fois, quant li sainieres est negligens; et ne covient mie quant tu vues desliier lou bras, et faire issir sanc la seconde fois, et li pertus est clos, que tu presses forment sus; ne s’il est corbes, qu’il estende lou bras hastanment, car ce seroit malz; mais le laisse tant qu’il saine la seconde fois; ou tu i point a la pointe dou flaime, tant que li sans qui est congelez a pertus de la voinne isse fuer, et met sus I poc de seil remis en aigue, et presse sus legierement.	For he has a lot of pain in his body, and the fever comes; so that a great quantity needs to be drained, and the opening is widened as much as possible; then you should reward all the conditions for healing, and put your hand on his pulse when it heals, so that death does not come from the pus, and this happens many times, when the wounds are neglected; and you do not deserve to break the shoulder, and make the wound again, and the opening is closed, then you press firmly; but if it is broken, he should extend his arm smoothly, because it would be bad; but leave it until it heals for the second time; or you pierce the point of the flame, as much as the opening frozen by the vein is forced, and put a little rope soaked in water on it, and press lightly.
Et se li voine est enflee, si la laisse et ne l’estreindre mie, tant que li aposteme soit apaisiez.	And if the vein has burst, let it go and do not tighten it, as long as the abscess is calm.
Et se necessitez est dou traire dou sanc la seconde fois, si le saine en celui leu meisme, ou en un autre voinne, ou en l’autre bras.	And if necessity requires to drain the blood a second time, if it is in the same place, or in another vein, or in the other arm.
Li voinne emmi le bras est sainie en leu de la voine dou chief por ceu qu’elle est composte.	The vein that runs through the arm is attached to the vein from which blood comes out.
Et li maniere de la sainie si est que li malaides boute sa main en aigue chaude, tant que li foscile soit rouges; puis soit liiéz moienement, si que li voinne apere bien, puis le saine maintenant dou travers, ne mie dou large ne dou lonc; et soit li pertus larges, et soit sainiez bien pres de la jointe de la main, et se sans n’en puet issir, si remet la main en aigue chaude, et laisse corre lou sanc en l’aigue, tant que tu en aies assez; et se c’est en esteit, si ne rebouter mie la main en aigue chaude, car on l’i met plus en yver que en esteit; et li sainie de ceste voine est plus sauve de toutes autres voinnes, qu’il n’i a ne artere ne nerf.	And the way of the vein so is that the patient holds his hand in hot water, until the pulse is red; then let it rest gently, so that the vein appears clearly, then sew it now across, not wide nor long; and if it is too wide, sew it well near the joint of the hand, and do not pull it out again, unless it comes loose, then put the hand in hot water again, and let the blood run in the water until you have enough; and if it is in this state, do not re-wrap the hand in hot water, for we use it more for healing than for anything else; and the vein of this vein is the most saved from all veins, since it does not involve an artery or a nerve.
Li sainie de la salvatele de la main destre si vaut a toutes les maladies dou foie, et c’est li maniere: estrain la main, et boute en aigue chaude, tant que li voinne soit enflee, si c’on la voie; et se la saine de travers, et se tu la copes dou tout en tout, si ne grieve rien; et n’aler mie trop em parfont, car li nerf sont desoz toz desnuez de char, et puis remet la main en aigue chaude, se li sans est congelez en la plaie, et n’en puet issir.	The treatment for diseases of the liver with salve from the right hand is this: take the hand, and soak it in hot water until the vein is gone, if you see it; and then cut the skin, and remove all of it completely, without causing any harm; and do not cut too much perfectly, because the nerves are all bare and exposed; and then put the hand back into hot water, if it has become frozen in the wound, and cannot be removed.
Et quant tu avras trait dou sanc tant com mestier t’est, si met sus la voinne oile et seil por souder hastanment, et ensi fai de chescun rain.	And when you have treated the blood as much as necessary, put oil and wax on it to make it strong; and do the same for each arm.
Li sainie de li en la main senestre si vaut a la maladie de la mice, et fai tout ausi com je t’ai dit devers destre.	The salve for the left hand is good for the disease of the heart, and do the same as I told you before for the right hand.
Li sainie de la sophene si vaut a toutes les maladies que sont desoz le cors, si com maladies de la marris, et retenement de flors, et maladie des rains, et des cuixes et des jambes ancienes, et semblans maladies.	The salve for the foot is good for all kinds of diseases that come from the body, such as diseases of the bride, and restraining of flowers, and old diseases of the feet and legs, and similar diseases.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides boute som piet en aigue chaude, et frote sus la voinne tant qu’elle pere, et lie desus la jointure dou piet; et li voinne si est a la cheville, et par desus lou piet en vont mout de rains; saine la donques ou plus large rain, ou a la cheville, que mues vaut.	And the quality of this medicine is that the patient puts some water in hot water and rubs on the vein until it stops, and ties up the joint of the foot; and if the vein is at the ankle, and above the foot goes more rain; heal then or broader rain, or at the ankle, that it moves.
Et se tu la saines sus lou piet, si te warde des ners qui sont desoz, et la saine de traver ausi com en copant; et soit li flaimes anesil.	And if you heal on the foot, be careful of the nerves that are exposed, and heal it with a transfixion as when you are drilling; and let the flames go out.
Et se li sans n’en puet issir, si remet lou piet en l’aigue, et laisse bien vuidier la voine.	And if he cannot get it out, put the foot in water, and leave the vein well open.
Et se li sainieres faut la premiere fois, si rencomence la seconde au desus un poc, car li leus est salz; ne ne douter de nerf, si com nos avons dit, et ensi fai de la sophene de l’autre piet igalment.	And if you heal it the first time, start the second time above a little hole because the blood is salty; do not doubt about nerves, as we have said, and so do the same with the other foot evenly.
Li leus de la voinne sciatique est a la cheville de fuer, et sa sainie vaut a la dolor de la hainche, quant c’est por sanc chaut.	The blood vessels are at the ankles, and the pain in the knee joint is due to the blood leaving the leg when it is cut off.
Et li qualitez de sa sainie si est que li malaides entre ou bain, et estraigne desus la cheville IIII dois en tordant, car autrement n’apert li voinne; et s’elle apert, si le saine en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et en traversant; et vaut mues que tu la copes, car li leus est saus, et elle est mout reponue a mains homes.	And the quality of this vein is that the patient goes in or out, and removes it from the ankle with four twists, because otherwise the vessel does not open; and if it opens, then do all the cutting you can, and cross it; and it will break more easily than you cut it, for the blood is out, and it is very much swollen.
Et se tu ne la trueves, si saine aucun rain de li qui apert ou dos dou piet, et vers lou petit doi, et te warde des ners; et fai tant corre dou sanc que tu vues, et puis deslie lou lien, et met sus coton et l’estraint; ele est maintenant sanee.	And if you do not open it, if the blood flows or stops from the foot, and turns towards the little toe, and keeps away from the nerveless parts; and do so much as you can to turn the blood, and then unthread the leg, and put cotton on it and tie it up; now he is healed.
des sainies de ventouse	ventose
Ventouses sont fait de cornes, ou d’arain, ou de voirre; et ventosation si est faite selonc II manieres: ou par ferir et atraire sanc, ou sens ferir.	Ventouses are made of horns, or horn, or glass; and the application is made in two ways: by piercing and drawing out blood, or without piercing.
Et ceste ventosation qui est sens ferir si est selonc II manieres: ou elle est a tout feu, ou sens feu; et ventosation qui est faite par ferir et par estraction de sanc si est faite en XIIII leus dou cors, de coi li uns est tout en som le chief; et li autres est emmi le col; et II autres en II costeis dou col; et li ventouse desoz lou menton; et li ventouse des II espaules; et li ventouse sus les crupies; et les ventouses emmi les II bras; et les ventouses des II jambes; et les ventouses des II chevilles; et li ventosation ne trait point de sanc, fuer que des menues voinnes que sont esparses en la char, et por ceu n’en afoiblist om mie, si com on fait de sainie de voinne; et ne covient mie qu’elle soit aministree, ne a tout feu ne sens feu, en aucune maladie qui vient de repletion, tant que toz li cors soit vuidiez.	And this ventosity that is made without piercing, it is applied in twelve places of the body, for which there are two ways: hot and cold. And the application that is made by piercing and drawing out blood, is applied in twelve ways in the body, to which one is at the top of the head; and another is under the chin; and another is on the neck, between the two sides; and another is on the shoulders; and another is on the arms; and another is on the legs; and another is on the feet; and this application does not treat bloodletting, unless it is small venations that are spread throughout the body, and for this reason it should not be applied hot or cold in any disease that comes from overloading, until all the body is voided.
Et se par necessiteit de maladies covient ventoser, ou por acostumances, si l’amenistrons chescune houre en l’encomencement dou mois, ou en la fin, et emmi et en chescun tens; car il i a de telz qui, quant il ont mestier de ventoser, si ont pesant chief; et si a telz qui truevent repletion et roujor en lor faice, et en lor chief, et au col, et tenebrour as eulz; et telz qui truevent une goute de sanc en lor bouche, et ont enflee la lengue, et raichent sanc; et si i a de telz qui songent, et voient par nut sanc et navrez et mors et semblans choses.	And if, because of necessity due to disease, or because of habits, we must treat each hour during the beginning of the month, or at the end, and in between; for there are some who, when they need to belch, become very heavy; and those who experience regurgitation and redness on their face, and their throat, and darkness in their eyes; and those who belch a drop of blood from their mouth, and have lost their tongue, and thirst for blood; and if there are those who dream, and see with no food or drink or death or similar things.
Et quant nos voions ces signes, et meismement quant c’est emmi lou mois, nos lou commandons a ventoser aprés III houres dou jor.	And when we saw these signs, and in particular when it is the middle of the month, we order them to belch after three hours from day.
Li sainie de la muze si aide a la grieteit dou chief … que vient as eulz, et ne covient mie que ce soit aprés l’evacuation de tout lou cors; et ceste ventosation si est en leu de la sainie de la cephalique, et ne covient mie que cil qui est de froide complexion en use, ou qui ait chatharre, car ce lor fait mout grant nuisement; et por ceu ne covient mie que li veillart en usent, ne qui ont ou chief froides maladies.	The doctor will explain to the patient that if there is a buildup of gas in the stomach, it should be released after three hours from the beginning of the day. This belching should occur when the patient's head feels better ... and comes with the evaporation of all the body's fluids; and this belching is in the place of the head's health, and does not apply to those with a cold complex, or those who are depressed, because it causes them much harm; and for that it only applies to those who work at night, or who have a cold-related headache.
Et cil qui s’en saine sovent, si devient oblious, et por ce covient mettre la ventouse un poc plus aval par la doutance d’obliance.	And those who are recovering from it often become confused, and for this reason the suction cup should be placed a little further downstream due to the doubt of confusion.
Li ventosation emmi le col est en leu de la sainie dou chief et de la basilique, et por ceu vaut elle a l’estrecement dou pis, et a fendure de la chenal dou pormon, et a toust, et a repletion; et la covient poc bouter, car s’elle tient trop fermement, si enjanre obliance ou stomac et ou cuer.	And the suction should be applied to the throat at the level of the recovery of the voice and the base of the tongue, and for this reason it helps in extraction from the pit and from the channel of the tonsils, and for all this, and for repletion; and one must push a little, because if it holds too tightly, confusion or stomach or wherever.
Li ventosations as II costelz dou col si vaut as dolors dou chief, et obtalmie et emigrainne, et a l’estranglement, et a la dolor as racines des dens, et est en leu de la sainie de la basilique; et covient que tu comandes au sainor qu’il espresse sa main au mettre, qu’il ne cope l’artere, et ne veigne decorremens de sanc.	And the suction should be applied to the back of the throat at the level of the recovery of voice and the base of the tongue; it causes pain in the neck and eyes, and stinging and strangulation, and pain at the roots of the teeth, and is at the level of the treatment of the base of the tongue. And you should instruct the doctor that he press his hand without hurting, so as not to hurt the artery, and not cause movement of blood.
Li ventosations desoz lou menton si vaut a maladie de bouche, et a corruption de gencives, et semblans maladies qui sont en la bouche; et est en leu des sainies des II levres.	The wind-puctions of the mouth cause diseases of the mouth and corruption of the gums and similar diseases that are in the mouth; and are in the place of the roots of the teeth.
Li ventosations des espaules vaut a maladie que vient de chalor et de remplissement.	The wind-puctions of the shoulders cause a disease that comes from heat and swelling.
Li ventosations des coutes si vaut autant com des III voinnes dou bras, car elle atrait sanc de ces grosses voinnes; et comande au sainor qu’il ne fiere mie trop em parfont, car li leus est nus de char, et sait desoz ners et arteres.	The wind-puctions of the arms cause as much pain as three veins in the arms, for they draw blood from these large veins; and instruct the patient that he not cut them too deeply, for their tendons are exposed and their arteries run close by.
Li ventouse qui est sus la croupe si vaut as emoroydes dou fondement, et as maladies desoz, et covient que li ventouse soit grans, et soit d’arain, qu’elle a mestier de bien traire; et par aventure, s’elle estoit subtilz, si briseroit; et i fai grans plaies.	The wind-puctions that are on the back are as painful as the emoroid veins, and as similar diseases; it is necessary that the wind-puckings be large and of air, for they have the duty of well draining; and perhaps, if they were too fine, they would burst, and would cause great wounds.
Les ventouses des jambes si sainent apertement, car elles atraient sanc de tout le cors, et valent as dolors ancienes des rains, et de la marris, et de la vessie, et ramoinnent les flors; et sont en leu des II sophenes, et des II chevilles, et toutevoie elles afoiblissent lou cors aprés lonc us, et font venir paumison em plusors dispositions.	The ventouses of the legs if they are opened up, because they draw away blood from all over the body, and they resemble the ancient pains of the rain, and of the marris, and of the bladder, and they renew the flowers; and they are in place of the two sophenes, and of the two ankles, but nevertheless they weaken the body after a long time, and bring death to many different dispositions.
Li maniere de mettre la ventouse si est que tu la mettes premier vuide, et succe tempreement, et la met hastanment, et remue igalment, et ne cesser de ceu faire, tant que tu voies lou leu rouge et enfleit, et apere li roujor dou sanc; puis fier, et remet les ventouses, et pren warde en la disposition des cors, car il i a telz qui ont tanre char, et clers porez: si covient ferir une fois soulement, et covient faire larges plaies, et un poc parfondes; et suce legierement.	The manner of putting the ventouse is that you put it first empty, and suck promptly, and put it in place, and move evenly, and do not cease to do so, until you see the red and inflamed place, and appear the color of the blood; then firm, and remove the ventouses, and take care in the disposition of the bodies, for there are some who have great pain, and clear pores: it is therefore necessary to injure once only, and to make deep wounds, and a little bit deep; and suck lightly.
Et se li sans est gros, si couvient ferir II fois: la premiere fois por subtiliier la voie dou sanc gros.	And if it is without a belly full, if he comes to kill twice: first time to soften the path of blood thick.
Et se li sans est tres espés, si covient ferir la tierce fois; et quant nos volons traire dou sanc poc et poc, si nos soffist soulement une fois.	And if it is very thick outside, he comes to kill for the third time; and when we want to squeeze blood little by little, we suffocate it just once.
Et se nos volons mout de sanc, si rencomensons sovent; et se li sans est espés, si fier em parfont, et li termines si est que li keurs soit perciez soudement, et couvient a celui qui a gros cuir et dur, et qui ont estrois porelz, que tu oignes les leus des ventouses d’oile aperitif et dissolutif: se c’est en esteit, d’oile violet, ou d’oile d’amandres douces, ou d’oile de semence de cucurbite; et se c’est en yveir, d’oile de cresson, ou de lis, ou de camomille, ou autre semblant.	And if we want to squeeze blood, let us do it frequently; and if the outside is thick, he comes to kill completely, and the end is that the curse is suddenly perceived, and covers himself with a strong and hard skin, and has a stink that drives one away; that you wet the leeches with oil that opens and dissolves: if it is in summer, with violet oil, or sweet almond oil, or cucurbit seed oil; and if it is in winter, with watercress oil, or lily oil, or chamomile oil, or another kind of oil.
Et se li superfluitez est grosse et froide, si pren oile amaratin, ou de balsamite, ou oile d’anet, et les semblans.	And if the overflow is thick and cold, then take oil of almonds, or of balm, or oil of anise, and the like.
Et se cil cui on saine a tendre char et larges porelz, se n’i covient mettre point d’oile, mais le covient laver aprés la ventosation d’aigue rose, ou d’aigue froide, ou d’aigue de morelle, ou d’aigue de cucurbite, ou d’aigue de porcelainne, ou autre semblant.	And if the patient's skin is very dry and scaly, then one should not use oil, but it must be washed after the wound has healed with rosewater, or cold water, or water from mulberries, or water from cucumbers, or water from porcelain, or something similar.
Et cil qui a mout de moistor, si se leve d’aisil, ou d’aigue de mirte, et de sumac, et de semblans choses.	And for those who have too much moisture, if it comes out like this, or with water from myrtle, and sumac, and similar things.
Et cil qui ont grosses superfluitez se levent de vin viel, ou d’aigue de seuc, ou de decoction d’anet ou de camomile, ou d’autres semblans; et ne se covient mie sainier de ventouse devant le bain ne em bain, mais aprés lou bain une houre ou II; et ne dorme mie aprés la ventosacion, et covient k’il se warse, quant il se doit ventoser et quant il est ventosez.	And for those with thick overflows, they should be made to stand in old wine, or water from oak tree, or a decoction of fennel or chamomile, or similar things; and one should not treat with suction before the bath or in the bath, but an hour or two after; and one should not fall asleep after the wound has been treated, but when it is necessary to apply suction, so that when it is applied, the patient lies down.
Et warde se cil qui se saine est coleriques, et se li sans est trop agus et enflamez; si covient qu’il preigne choses froides, si com pomes grenates et endives et laitues a l’aisil, et semblans choses; et menjuce pucins, et char de chastron, et viandes moistes.	And guard those who are sickly, and whose bile is too thick and inflamed; it is necessary that he drink cold things, such as pomegranates and endives and lettuces with the apple, and similar things; and little sweets, and horse meat, and moist meat.
Et cil qui a froide complexion, si preigne syrop de miel, et vin odorant moien, qui est entre viel et noveil, et menjuce poc, et menjuce pucins et petis oiselz et pijons; et lou jor qu’il se ventousera, si doit plus boivre que mengier; et covient doner a aucuns homes aucune fois triaicle ou muscate devant la ventosacion, ou aprés, por conforter les membres principalz; et soit subtiliiez li sans, mais il ne covient mie que cil qui sont chaut le boivent.	And those who have a cold complexion should drink syrup of honey, and fragrant wine that is between old and new, and little sweets, and little birds and pigeons; and on the day when he will breathe, he must drink more than eat; and it is necessary to give some men triple or muscat before breathing, or after, in order to strengthen the main members; and soften the bile, but it is not right for those who are hot to drink it.
Les ventouses que sont mises sens ferir sont celles que sont mises sus lou foie, et sus la mice, et podagre, et sus lou ventre et la boude et les rains et la hainche, car cil membre ne soffrent mie ferir sus oulz, et ne le fait on fuer que por atraire sanc de membre em membre, si com nos mettons sus les mameles quant li neis sainne; por oster la viscositeit qui est au membre, si com nos metons ventouses sus le ventre et sus la boude por amenuisier le membre; et oste la dolor, quant il i a opilation ou piere, si oste par sa vertu atractive par aventure l’opilation, ou desaert la piere de son leu; et ensi fait ele quant on le met sus lou foie et sus la mice quant il i a ventositeit retenue, et ces ventouses sont aministrees vuides por sucier tant soulement; et aucune fois sont aministrees ensamble feu, et aucunes fois plainnes d’aigue tede, si com em maladies dou pleuresin, et en tel maniere c’on emplisse la ventouse d’aigue chaude soule, ou d’aigue ou il ait cuit herbes covenaubles a ceu.	The suction cups that are not likely to hurt are those put on the liver, and on the kidney, and podagra, and on the belly and the bowels and the rain and the hernia, for this member does not suffer to be hurt on the outsides, and it is done only in order to attract blood from one member to another, as we put on the breasts when the person is not well; in order to remove the viscous substance that is in the member, as we put suction cups on the belly and the bowels in order to reduce the member; and thus it is done when it is put on the liver and on the kidney when there is repressed wind, and these suction cups are emptied only for sucking so little; and they are never empty together, and plain water is never used, as in the pleurisy, and in this way the suction cup is filled with hot water or water in which herbs have been boiled suitable to that.
Li forme de la ventouse aministré a feu si est ci:	The shape of the suction cup is administered to fire as such:
Et ait II dois de large et demi palme de parfont, et ait ou costeit entor lou mileu I petit pertus, ausi com por bouter une aguille, et soit d’arain, souef devant si qu’ele ne blece lou malaide au mettre sus lou membre; et ait em mileu une verge de travers d’arain ou de fer, por mettre une chandoile emprise, et en soient et grans et petites selonc les maladies et l’eaige de ces qui les prenent; car les ventouses des enfans sont autres que des vielz, et des maigres que des gras.	The shape of the suction cup is administered to fire in this manner: It should be two handsbreadths wide and half a palm deep, and it should have an opening at its center about as large as a pin, just as for threading a needle, and it should be made of leather or skin before use so that it does not hurt the patient when placed on the limb; and in the middle there is a crossbar of leather or iron to hold a grip, and they are very large or small according to the disease and age of those who take them; for the suction cups of children are different from those of old people, and those of the thin are different from those of the fat.
Et doit on ensi mettre ceste ventouse sus lou membre: empren la chandoile de cire ou I linement, et le met emmi la ventouse au traver de la verge qui est emmi la ventouse, si que li clartez soit au fons de la ventouse qu’elle ne brule le malaide; et puis la met sus lou membre, et tes dois soit sus lou pertus que nos avons dit, si que quant on vuet, si en va li vapor, et oste on la ventouse; et emprent on le linement si com devant, et le rencomence sovent, se tu as mestier.	And it should be placed on the limb like this: Take the grip of wax or linen and place it over the top of the suction cup so that the clarity is at the bottom of the suction cup so that it does not burn the patient; and then place it on the limb, and those two should be on the opening that we have said, so that when you release them, if there is steam, and then remove the suction cup; and take linen like before, and renew it often, if you need to.
En la ventouse donques qui est aministree em maladie de pleuresin, a tout aigue, n’a point de verge ne de pertus, et n’est amenistree fuer que quant ele est plaine d’aigue, et est mise sus lou membre tant soulement; et c’est li forme:	En the ventouse donques qui este aministree em malade de pleuresin, a tout aigu, n'a point de verge ne de pertus, et n'este amenistree fuer que quant el est plaine d'aigu, et este mise sus lo membre tant soulement; et c'est li forme:
Sansues ne sont amenistrees fuer que en membres ou on ne puet mettre ventouses por lour petitece, si com levres et gencives, et semblans leus; et en leus desnuez de char, si com doi ou neis, et autres semblans; et li qualitez de l’user si est que quant tu trueves sansues que sont en aigues douces nettes sens porreture, si les pren; et les met une nut en aigue douce, tant qu’elles soient famillouses, et n’aient rien en ventres; et puis soit sainiez de voinne et de ventouse, puis frote le membre tant k’il soit rouges, et met sus les sansues; et quant elles seront plainnes, et cherront, se c’est leu ou on puisse mettre ventouse, se li met, car ce vaut mout aprés.	The text describes the treatment of pleurisy, a lung inflammation, using suction cups (ventouses) applied to affected areas. It mentions that the patient should not use suction cups on certain parts of the body due to their sensitivity, such as lips and gums. The text also provides instructions for preparing the patient before applying the cups, including ensuring the cups are placed in a clean, gentle way and that the person's breath is free of moisture.
Se ceu non, si leve le leu d’aisil, et puis d’aigue, mout bien, et puis l’espreint; et se li leus saine trop aprés lou cors des sansues, si moille I drapel de lin en aigue froide, et met sus, tant que li sans soit estenchiés; et se li sans est multipliez, si met sus vitriole broié, ou gales, et semblans choses, tant qu’il soit estenchiez; ou tu met sor le leu moitiez de feves pelees, et les laisse tant qu’elles s’aerdent au leu, si estanchera maintenant; et se tu en as de plus mestier, si pren autres sansues.	If so, raise the bed, and then water, very well, and then press it; and if the bed is too high after the heart of the sick person, dip a linen cloth in cold water, and put it on, until the blood is stopped; and if the blood flows again, put vitriol powder, or gall, and similar things, until it is stopped; or you put half a dozen peeled beans on the bed, and leave them until they are hot to the touch, then they will stop the bleeding now; and if you need more, take another set of veins.
Et se les sansues ne se vuellent prendre, si frote le leu de sanc fres, ou tu i fiche une aguille tant que li sans en isse, et puis les met sus, et tantost com elles sentent lou sanc, si s’aerdent; et quant tu vues qu’elles chieent, si poudre sus un poc d’aloen et de seil broiet, ou de cendre, si cherront maintenant.	If the veins do not want to take, then rub the bed with fresh blood, or you put a needle in it until the blood flows, and then put them on, and soon as they feel the blood, they will heat up; and when you see that they are burning, if you powder a little aloe and seel, or ash, they will cool now.
Ci comence li livre des brisures	Here is the translation of the text line by line:
Cist chapistres est maintes fois necessaires en l’art de medicine, et est restorement de brisure et de desaluement.	The chapters on this chapter are many times necessary in the art of medicine, and is a remedy for fractures and dislocations.
Saichiez, chier fil, que li fol mire se gietent de cest chapistre, qu’il ne virent onques nul des anciens livres, ne lettre n’en lurent; et por ceste cause est estraingie li science en nostre terre, car je n’en trovai onques nul boin; et n’en sai nient, fuer que par la science des anciens livres, ou j’ai tant estudiiet que je en ai traite la science, et par experiment, et par l’acostumance de ma vie; et je vos ai jai descrit en cest chapistre ceu qui est contenut, et l’ai abregié en la fin, et ai mostreit clerement les formes des estrumens que sont amenistrez, si com j’ai fait en ces II chapistres ci devant.	Know, son of a bitch, that the fine men of old cast this chapter on , which was never read in any of the ancient books or letters; and for this reason the science is extraneous to our land, because I have never found one good; and I know nothing of it, except by the science of the ancient books, which I have studied so much that I have treated the science, and by experience, and by habit of life; and I have described to you in this chapter the contents thereof, and have abridged them at the end, and have clearly set forth the forms of the instruments that are used, as I did in the two chapters preceding.
Il covient donques que nos disons ou prologue de cest livre les sommes de la parole et les chapistres ou li saiges met son entendement, et demore sus la verteit, si que cil qui sont esproveit saichent et aprenent cest art noble, et l’aprenent a autrui.	It is therefore necessary that we say in this book the sums of words and the chapters where the sage places his understanding, and delays on truth, so that those who are proved may know and learn this noble art, and teach it to others.
Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d’une part et d’autre, s’aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n’est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c’est a savoir froides joutes, et char d’oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne menjuce nules grasses chars, et ne s’emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sanc, tant que tu n’aies doute d’aposteme chaut, ne d’espandement de matiere au membre; si reviegne li malaides a som premerain governement k’il a useit.	Je dis que quant brisure ou dislocation ou torsions ou quasseure vient a aucun, si covient que tu te hastes de sainier lou malaide d'une part et d'autre, s'aucune chose ne lou te tot, si com foiblece de cors, ou enfes, ou viellars; ou se li tens n'est tres chaus, ou trop frois; et menjuce cholz frois, c'est a savoir froides joutes, et char d'oiseil et de chevril, et ne boive point de vin, ne mijuche nules grasses chars, et ne s'emplisse mie trop de viandes qui remplissent les voinnes de sang, tant que tu n'aies doute d'aposteme chaut, ne d'expansion de matiere au membre; si revient li malaides a som premerain gouvernement qu'il a useit.
Et quant li os brisiés comence a restourer, si covient que on norrisse le malaide de viandes que font gros norrissement, ou il ait viscositeit, si com froment cuit en aigue, et ris, et testes, et piez, et pance de vaiche, et oefz, et poissons fres, et gros vin, et semblans chose.	And when the broken bones begin to heal, it is necessary that the patient be fed with meat that is very fat, or with viscous food, such as cooked wheat in water, and rice, and beans, and pies, and porridge made from veal, and eggs, and fresh fish, and strong wine, and similar foods.
Car a teil norrissement se reprent mues et plus tost li brisure.	For a slow healing will be delayed and slower the break will heal.
Et saichiez que li os brisiez des vielz et des decrepites ne se pueent mie bien reprendre ne souder selonc lor nature por la sechor des membres, ne cil ausi qui sont trop tendre, si com os de petis enfans; mais n’a cure, ramoinne sus l’os brisiet I gros tenrons qui s’aert et joint le membre ensamble, tant qu’il enforce si com il fut devant; et ne li tot point de son oevre, et por ceu le covient norrir de grosses viandes, si com nos avons dit.	And know that the broken bones of old and decrepit people cannot properly heal or be joined together by the sinews according to their nature, nor those which are too soft, as is the case with the bones of small children; but do not stop at that, go on to the broken bone and join it with large tendons which bind the member together, as strong as possible; and do not quit your work, and for this it is necessary to feed them with large meat, as we have said.
Et saiches que les briseures sont diverses em maintes manieres.	And know that breakers are various in many ways.
Car li brisure dou chief est autre que li brisure dou pis, ou de la jambe, et je vos dirai en cest chapistre toutes manieres de brisure.	For the break in the head is different from the break in the foot or leg, and I will tell you in this chapter all the ways of breaking.
Car il i a brisure que vait a arvol, et autre en aguisant, si com li taille d’une penne por escrire.	For there is a break that goes to the root, and another in grinding, as when one trims the tip of a feather to write with it.
Et si a brisure avec plaie, et brisure a tout une petite fendure.	And if a break is with a wound, and a break is all a little crack.
Et a chescune maniere ait son engien, et son estrument propre en la restauration, selonc ceu que li remembrance vient en son leu; et est conue li brisure de l’os par ceu que li leus est tors, et apert bien par defuer, et sone au presseir de la main; et quant il n’i a tortuositeit ne son au tochier, et li malaides ne sent mie grant dolor, se n’i a point de brisure; mais il puet bien avoir tortuositeit, ou fendure, ou petite brisure.	And to each way there is an instrument, and a special tool for restoration, according to what comes to mind in its place; and it is known the break of the bone by what turns its edge, and opens well from the side, and presses with the hand; and when there is no tortuosity or bump, and the patient feels no great pain, there is no fracture; but it can have tortuosity, or a crack, or a small fracture.
Si ne covient mie que tu lou mueves a la main, mais met sus medicines que vienent ci aprés, et puis l’estraint maintenant subtilment.	If it is not necessary for you to move it with your hand, but put on the medicines that come after this, and then now restrain it gently.
Et saiches que li brisure que vait en arvol, et sont les II parties desjointes, il les covient maintenant mettre a point igalment, ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne; et se apostemes chaulz i vient, si lou laisse aucun jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez; puis le met igal au mues que tu pues legierement et saigement, et saiches que li restauration de li est plus legiere que li restaurations de celi ou il ait pieces; puis l’estraint, si com il covient ci aprés.	And know that the fracture that has happened in the shoulder, and the two parts are separated, you must now put them together smoothly, so that the chest goes out and comes back in; and if the chest comes out again, let it rest for a day, as long as the chest is calm; then put it equal to the muscled part that you can move easily and firmly, and know that the restoration of this is easier than the restoration of the one where there are pieces; then restrain it, as it is said hereafter.
Et se en l’os a piéces brisies, si l’estent de II pars, se c’est mains ou piet, ou a ta main se c’est uns petis membres, ou a II cordes, ou a une corde et a ta main; et met le membre selonc sa figure natureil, si que quant les parties dou membre brisiet sont desevrees, si ramoinne par toz engiens les additions en lor leus au mues que tu pues, et garde que par ton ovraige ne viegne au malaide lesion ne doulor; et ajoste bien les II chiés des os selonc les millors formes.	And if there are pieces of bone broken, and the two parts are between the hand or foot, or at one's side, or at two strings, or at a string and at one's side; and set the member according to its natural shape, so that when the broken parts of the member have healed, you may move them by all means in their places by the muscles that you can move, and guard against your work causing pain and injury to the patient; and fit the two bones together well according to their best shapes.
Et le sent bien a la main s’il te semble k’il ne soit mie bien: si la dresce bellement, et ne l’estraindre mie trop, ne presser si com font cil qui i font venir par lor ovraige aposteme chaut et contraction au membre, si com nos avons veut maintes fois.	And the hand feels right to you if it seems not to be well: if the dressing is done well, and you do not tighten it too much, do not press as they do who, by their over-zealous treatment, cause pain and contraction of the member, as we have often seen.
Et quant li membres est a point, si chastie bien lou malaide qu’il ne lou mueve, ne en veillant ne en dormant, ne en tornant, ne en autre maniere; et warde bien que li membres soit si asseurez qu’il ne sente nule dolor.	And when the member is healed, teach the patient to keep it still, neither watching nor sleeping, turning or in any other way; and guard well that the member be so secure that it feel no pain.
Car quant il sent nulle dolor, si n’est mie a point, et le covient mettre en teil disposition qu’il ne sent nule dolor; et te garde k’il soit mis droitement, que tortuositez n’i veigne quant il iert restorez; et li qualitez dou membre brisiet est selonc ceu que je te dis.	For when there is no pain, it is not yet healed, and the appropriate disposition is that there be no pain; and guard well that it be set straight, so that there is no twistedness when it is restored; and the quality of the member is according to what I have told you.
Saiches que li membre brisiet sont divers em petitece et en grandor et en forme.	You know that broken members are different in smallness and greatness and in shape.
Car il i a petis membres, si com brais et dois et semblans: si covient envoloupeir drapelz de lin molz et subtilz; et cil qui sont gros, si com cuixe et jambe: si covient envoloupeir d’un liien large et dur, car li larges liiens embraice tout le grant membre, et l’estraint de toutes pars igalment, si qu’il n’i a nule taiche; puis lie entor estoupes legieres, III tours ou IIII selonc lou membre, et estraint ta main un poc a tout le liien, puis vai au desus de la brisure et l’estraint moins, que la brisure puis esloigne un poc la brisure; et mollifie lou liien poc et poc, tant que tu preignes grant partie dou leu sain, puis repren I autre liien, et torne entor derechief sus lou leu brisiet; puis revai a la partie desoz de la brisure, et l’estraint moienement, ne mie trop fort ne trop molement, si com nos avons dit en la premiere lieure desus; puis met entre les liiens estoupes de lin ou drapelz, tant qu’il soit toz igalz, puis lie tout par desus I bendeil, et puis met tes esteles bien faites sus, s’il n’i a aposteme ou enfleure.	Car il y a des membres petits, si comme les bras et les jambes et les semblants: si convient d'envelopper des draps de lin doux et fins; et ceux qui sont gros, si comme le cuisse et la jambe: il convient d'en envelopper avec un lien large et dur, car les liens larges embrassent tout le grand membre, et l'entraînent de toutes parts uniformément, sans aucune taché; puis lie dans une entorse légère, III tours ou IV selon le membre, et étire la main sur tout le lien, puis va au-dessus de la rupture et l'étire moins, que la rupture puis s'éloigne un peu la rupture; et adoucis le lien petit à petit, jusqu'à ce que tu ressentes une grande partie du lieu sain, puis reprends un autre lien, et retourne entourer très étroitement sur le lieu brisé; puis reviens à la partie en saillie de la rupture, et l'étire avec modération, ni trop fort ni trop doucement, comme nous avons dit dans la première lieure au-dessus; puis met entre les liens enveloppés de lin ou de draps, tant qu'ils soient tous égaux, puis lie tout par-dessus le bandage, et puis met tes étais bien faites, s'il n'y a pas d'abdication ou d'enflure.
Et s’il i a enfleure ou aposteme, si met sus chose apaisant aposteme chaut, et qui oste l’enfleure, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors; puis estrain sus tes esteles, et soient de moitiet d’une large cainne rese saigement, ou de fust dont on fait les clives, ou de rains de palme, et soient selonc ceste figure:	And if there is an abscess or a sore, put something soothing onto the abscess and let it be for some days; then draw it out with your thumbs, and make a half-inch square hole clean, or from a branch from which they make cleats, or from palm leaves, and make it according to this figure:
mais il covient que li estele que om met sus la brisure soit un poc plus grosse et plus large que les autres; et soit ausi longe com il covient au membre de petitece ou de grandor; puis estraint sus les esteles ausi com tu as fait a la premiere lieure, puis lie desus un fil avenanment, si com en la premiere lieure sus la briseure; plus estroit est ensus, adés moins; et covient que li fil soient moien, ne trop gros ne trop menus, et soient de lin mol; car se li fil sont gros, si com j’ai veut des oevres des folz qui font lor lieures des cordes de linement tort, et c’est grant error, car li lieure ne puet estre igal s’il est trop subtilz, et ne covient mie qu’il ait entre chescune estele moins dou doi d’espaice.	And the thump that you put on the break should be a little thicker and wider than the others; and it should also be as far away from the member's smallness or greatness as it needs to be; then draw it out on the thumps just as you did in the first lieure, then tie it up forward, like in the first lieure on the break; the tighter it is, the better; and the thread should be medium, not too thick nor too thin, and made of linen; for if the thread is thick, like the work of foolish people who make their lieures with rope-like linen, and that is a great mistake, because the lieure cannot be equal if it is too tight, and it only needs to have less than two inches of space between each thump.
Et se li malaides est navrez par les chiés des esteles aprés l’estrignement en leus sains, si met desoz elles estoupes de lin, ou lainne charpie, si qu’il ne se blece.	And if the patient is stabbed by the chisels of the stiles after the extraction in their healthy places, then set them with a linen patch or another clean cloth so that they do not bleed.
Quant li plaie est avec la briseure, et li keurs est rompus, je en dirai la cure ci aprés.	When the wound is with the bruise, and the suture is broken, I will describe the treatment hereafter.
Et saiches qu’il ne covient mie estraindre d’esteles toz les membres brisiez le premier jor.	And know that it is not convenient to extract all the members of the broken limb on the first day.
Car quant li membres est grans, se n’i covient mie mettre esteles fuer que aprés V jors ou VII, ou plus selonc ta seurteit d’aposteme chaut sorvenant; et vez ci la maniere des emplaustres anciiens por restorer brisure, dislocation, et torsion: et est que tu pren de la farine que se tient as parois dou molin, et la confis avec abun d’uef, et met ceste confection, ne trop clere ne trop espesse, et en use, et c’est li commune maniere de l’emplaustre restorant la brisure a plusors dispositions, et meismement as femmes et as petis enfans, car il n’est mie ne trop chas ne trop frois.	For when the limbs are large, it is not convenient to put spails on them before five or seven days or more according to the urgency of the abscess, and follow the ancient method of splinting to restore the break, twist, and twist: and that you take flour which clings to the walls of a mill, and confound it with plenty of flour, and put this conflation, neither too thin nor too thick, and use it, and this is the common way of the plasterer restoring the break in many conditions, especially in women and small children, for it is not convenient to do it too often or too hard.
Autre maniere d’emplastre restorans la brisure et la dislocation et la torsion: pren З abareis et ladani et enule et asefetide et gomme arabique et mugat, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana V З.; alechil VIIII З.; et en fai poudre, et les melle avec aubun d’uef; se li complexion de l’ome est chaude, si use de cest emplaustre, car il est de bone composition, et restoure les os brisiés hastanment, et vaut a plusors homes.	Another method of plaster for repairing breaks, dislocations, and twists: take honey, turpentine, resin, asafetida, Arabian gum, and myrrh, in the proportions of X Z; aloes, in V Z; angelica, in VIII Z. And reduce them to a powder, and mix them with egg yolk from an eagle; if the complexion of the wound is hot, use this plaster, for it is well-composed and quickly repairs broken bones, and is useful to many people.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a torsion: pren mugat et vismalve, ana X З.; mirre et aloes, ana VIIII З.; acaice VI З.; bolic armenic X З., et broie bien, et confit avec aigue ou abun d’uef, et l’aministre.	Another method of plaster for treating twists: take myrrh and resin, in the proportions of X Z; aloes, in VIIII Z.; akkah, in VI Z.; Armenian bole, in X Z., and grind it well, and mix it with vinegar or egg yolk, and administer it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a jointes et as os desevrez de lor leus, et apaise la dolor sorvenant, et le taille usent de l’os, et la briseure: pren lainne novele, et la moille en aisil et en oile cuit, et met sus lou leu.	Another method of plaster for joints and bones that have come out of place, to soothe the pain gradually, and to fix the size of the break: take a young cow's horn, and reduce it to a paste with water and baked oil, and apply it to the joint.
Cist emplastres ne restoure mie, mais il est boins por apaisier d’aposteme chaut, et oste proprement les dolors.	Do not return to bed until they have healed completely; it is good for soothing an abscess, and properly relieving pain.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre qui restoure les os brisiez: pren foilles de figuier seches, et foilles de pavol terrestre, et broie ensamble, et fai emplaustre.	Another way to make an ointment that heals broken bones: take dry leaves of the fig tree and leaves of the holly tree, grind them together, and make an ointment.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre a la restoration de la brisure de l’os et por amenusier lou remenant de l’aposteme.	Another way to make an ointment for healing bone breaks and alleviating pain left over from abscesses.
Pren racine de vismalve, camomille, flors de violettes, farine de veces, de chescune une partie; et broie, et confis avec vin, et se li membres est eschaufez, se le confis avec aigue de coriandre moiste, ou d’aigue, et en use.	Take one part of root of mallow, chamomile, violets, wheat flour, and each of them; grind them together, and confound them with wine, and heat the members, and apply them with water of coriander or water, and use it.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre plus fors que li premier, quant aposteme dur vient a la restauration dou membre.	Another way to make an ointment that is stronger than the first one, which is used when the pain from the abscess lasts for a long time and needs to be healed quickly.
Pren racines de vismalve, et semence de lin, balauste, mellilote, et sansuce, et flors de violetes et de camomille, de toutes ana une partie; et broie, et confit avec aigue de salz, ou aigue douce, ou avec vin, selonc la chalor du membre, et son repos.	Take roots of chamomile, and of violet, and of melilot, and of fennel, and of lin-seed; and flower of melilot, and of violetes, and broie them well with water, or with wine, or with salt water, according to the heat of the member, and to his rest.
Ypocras dist en son livre c’on ne mette sus lou membre brisiet por restorer fuer que cerote fait de cire et d’oile, et nulle autre chose plus, et dist qu’il soit entre dous ne trop molz ne trop durs.	In his book, Ypocras says that one should not put anything on a broken member before the scar tissue is formed, except for a wax and oil cerote, and nothing else, and he says that it should be neither too soft nor too hard.
Et il semble galien c’on doit mettre sus lou membre brisiet, por restoreir, choses seches un poc chaudes, si com mirre et aloes et encens et semblans choses, si com nos avons dit.	And it seems to me that one should put on the broken member, to restore it, dry things that are a little warm, such as mirr, and aloe, and incense, and similar things, as we have said.
Autre maniere d’emplaustre que vaut a lesion et a dolor: pren mugath et chevolz d’omes decopez, ou pennes d’oiseil, et vismalve, et seil igalment, et les broie, et en fai emplaustre et lou lie.	Another method of making plasters that is good for lesions and pain: take wool from sheeps' backs, or feathers, and honey, and cotton equally, and grind them, and make a plaster with it and apply it to the wound.
Et puis lou deslie un poc aprés, et pren garde se li malaides ne sent nule dolor, ne ne s’est meus li os de son leu; si ne lou deslie par mains jors Et se dolor vient au leu, ou prurite, sens repos ou enfleure, si te haste, et le deslie, et oste l’emplaustre maintenant; et pren drapeil legier, et esponge de mer moiste, et plonge en aigue, et en leve lou leu, tant que li prurite cesse, et soit apaisie li dolor; puis laisse reposer lou membre une houre, puis met sus lainne seche, moillie en aigue ou en oile roset, et lie sus une nut, tant que tu soies seur d’aposteme chaut; et repose li enflammation dou membre, et soit ostee li dolor, puis rencomence la lieure subtil, et un poc d’emplaustre, et ne l’estraindre mie si fort com devant; et subtilie tant qu’il soit sanez.	And then wait a little after, and take care that the patient feels no pain, or does not move his jaw from its place; but if pain comes to its place, or itchiness, or lack of rest or swelling, then hurry and dislocate it, and apply the plaster now; and take a light cloth, and a sea sponge moistened, and dip into water, and raise up the jaw, until the itching ceases, and the pain is eased; then let the member rest for an hour, then put on another dry cloth, wet with water or oil and tie it onto a nut, until you are sure that the abscess is warm; and alleviate the inflammation of the member, and ease the pain, then restart applying the plaster gently, and a little bit of plaster, and do not extract it as strongly as before; and apply gently until he is well.
Et se tu vois que aposteme chaus et roujor et dolor et enfleure sont jai osteit dou tout, et tu as mestier d’emplaustre et de liien, si le rencomence, si com tu a fait premier igalment.	And if you see that the abscess is warm and red and painful and swollen all over, and you need to apply ointment and bandages, then if it starts again, as you did at first.
Et s’il ne vient au membre nient de ceu que nos avons dit, si ne le desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou IIII ou V ou VII; et aucune fois le laisse XX jors, selonc ce c’on voit, tant que li briseure s’aert, et aproche li ajostement de la char sus; adonques lou restraint plus que premier, et li engroisse sa viande, si com j’ai dit devant; et se tu vois lou leu sechier plus que mestier n’est, saiches que norrissemens n’i puet venir; arose lou donques d’aigue chaude tede, toutes les fois que tu lou deslies, et ce soit chescun tier jor, et eslaiche un poc la lieure; par cest ovraige donques cort li norrissemens au membre, et esmende hastanment ceu que font li fol mire, que restourent le membre tortement: c’est malvais, et si est ovraiges paourous, et je n’i voi autre chose que dou lassier et de l’ovrer droitement.	And if the limb does not respond to any of the above said, but only after III days or IV or V or VII; and never more than XX days, according to what is seen, until it breaks through, and approaches the joint with the bar; then restrain it more than before, and make it fatter with meat, as I have said before; and if you see that it dries up more than it should, then you must bathe it every day with hot water, and let it dry up a little bit each time, that is every third day, and wash it well with wine; by this work therefore stop the swelling at the limb, and carefully remove what is wrong, that restores the limb properly: it is painful, and if it is severe, I do not see anything else but to let it rest and work correctly.
des diverses manieres de brisure	Of the various ways of breaking.
Maintes manieres de brisures sont, et diverses figures, et les causes sont destintees; car il a brisures que sont faites de percussion d’espee, et li colz oste tout l’os jusc’a syfac qui est desoz l’os, si com fait haiche ou fust; et por ceu est apelee ceste maniere de briseure «haichure».	Of the various ways of breaking. There are many different ways and figures, and the causes are distinct; for there is a breaking that is done by the percussion of an axe, and the whole bone is broken from the socket, as if it were done by a stake or a staff; and this is called "haichure" in this manner of breaking.
Ou li espee cope l’os par desus sens percier, et est apelee ceste maniere de brisure «absolue»; et est li plaie de ces II brisures grans ou petite.	For the sword breaks the bone from above by piercing it; and this is called "absolute" breaking in this manner of breaking; and the wound of such great or little breaking.
Et s’il i a percussion emboee, ou fendure ou de colz de piere, ou de cheoir sus piere, ou d’autres semblans.	And if there is a percussion within, or a split or a collar of stone, or a fall on stone, or similar things.
Et s’il a brisure persant, qui aproiche jusc’a la toile qui est desoz l’os, ou elle est sus l’os, et est ceste plaie ou grans ou petite.	And if there is a piercing breaking, which approaches to the tendon that is out of the socket, or which is upon the bone, and this wound is great or little.
Et si a plaie qui est reponue en l’os ausi subtil com uns chevous, et est li fendure petite, et por ceu est apelee ceste brisure «capillaire»; et si la plaie qui est faite ou par ferir de piere, ou par cheoir, ou par semblant chose, et fait entrer la piece de l’os aval, et est li leus chevez si com font li chaudelier quant il fierent sus les chaudieres; si entre li piere dedens.	And if a wound that has entered the bone is as fine as a hair, and for this reason it is called a "capillaire"; and if the wound is caused by stone, or by falling, or by a similar thing, and causes a piece of bone to enter the body, and the head of the bone is as though it were forged in a cauldron when it is placed on a cauldron; if it enters the stone.
Et ceu avient plus a sous qui ont ou chief moistes os, si com chief d’enfant; et avient a toutes ces manieres de brisure que pieces menues en sont desevrees si com esteles; et je em parlerai en son leu.	And if there is too much moisture in the bone below the jaw, so that it resembles the head of a child; and if all these types of fractures are caused by small pieces being broken off, just like in the case of tiles; and I will talk about this in its place.
Et conoissons toutes manieres de briseures par la detraction sus elles, et l’inquisition a tentes, et par la char corrumpue qui est sus.	And let us know all the ways to break it by pulling on them, and by the investigation, and by the rotten cart which is above.
Li semblance capillaire est conue par ceu que quant on a descovert l’os, et on frote enche sus, si apert li brisure noire.	The hair appearance is caused by the fact that when we uncover the bone, and we rub it from above, if we open the black break.
En la cure de la brisure, pren garde as accidens dou malaide, et se tu vois nul malvais accident, si com vomissement de cole, et amission d’entendement, et estension, et paumeson, et fievre ague, et les eulz issir fuer et rougir, et autres semblans em plusors dispositions, si ne puet saner sens doute.	In the cure for a fracture, take care of the accidents of the patient, and if you see no bad accident, such as vomiting, loss of feeling, stiffness, palms, fever, hair becoming long and red, and other similar signs in various dispositions, so cannot be cured by doubt.
Et se tu ne vois accident espoantauble, et tu esperes salut, si comence la cure.	And if you do not see a possible accident, and you expect salvation, begin the cure.
Et quant li navrez vient premier a toi, et c’est en yver, si covient oster l’os devant lou quatorzime jor au mues que tu pues.	And when the break comes first to you, and it is in winter, so it is necessary to remove the bone before the fourth day at most.
Et se c’est en esteit, si te haste d’oster l’os devant lou septime jor, ainsois que li toile desoz l’os soit corrumpue, et vienent li accident que nos avons dit.	And if it is in summer, so you hurry to remove the bone before the seventh day, so that the bone's thread does not corrode, and the accident that we have mentioned comes.
Et se li brisure de l’os vient jusc’a la toile que cuevre lou cerveil, si covient que tu fendes la partie fendue ensi: et est que tu preignes lou chief dou malaide navreit, et descuevre sus l’os en toutes les manieres que tu pues, et sus la figure de la plaie plus souef que tu pues, et se decorrement de sanc vient au descovrir l’os, ou aposteme chaus, se li aide de ceu qu’il covient, et est que tu emplisses lou leu de drapelz moilliez en oile roset; et fai reposer la plaie tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et soies asseurez de decorrement de sanc; puis comence entor l’os a oster, et c’est fait selonc II manieres d’ovraige: l’une manieres si est que tu copes au taillement estroit devant, et c’est li forme:	And if the fracture of the bone comes only to the membrane that covers the skull, so it is convenient that you split the split part in this way: and it is that you press the head of the patient with pain, and uncover the bone in all ways as you can, and on the shape of the wound more sorrows than you can, and if the breaking of blood comes to uncover the bone, or an abscess, help him with what is convenient, and it is that you fill the place with wet towels soaked in oil; and let the wound rest until the abscesses are calmed, and be sure of the breaking of blood; then begin to open the bone, and this is done according to II ways: one way is that you chop the narrow end before, and this is its form:
Et puis i boute I autre taillement plus grant que lou premier.	And then another way is more grant than the first.
Et li seconde maniere si est que tu aies nombre de taillemens divers, les uns estrois et les autres larges, et soient a pointe, et soient de fer inde; et en oevre legierement, que tu ne bleces le chief.	And the second way is that you have many different taillements, some are thick and others are wide, and they are pointed, and they are made of iron; and do it lightly, so that you do not bruise the head.
Et se li os est fors et durs, si covient que tu lou perces entor, ainsois que tu i aministres taillemens avec tareres, ne mie parfont qu’il ne percent outre l’os dou test, et doit avoir desus la pointe une marge ou I cercle, que ne laisse passer la pointe outre l’os; et t’en covient avoir plusors, si que chescuns viegne en son leu de l’espés de l’os, si que tu aies tareres por toz test; et c’est li forme des III manieres de tareres:	And if the bone is strong and hard, it is necessary that you pierce it at the back, so that you bring the taillements with bars, not entirely cut through so that they do not go beyond the bone's end, and it must have on top of the point a margin or a circle, so that it does not let the point go beyond the bone; and you will need several, so that each one comes to its place at the end of the bone, so that you have bars for all the test; and this is the form of the three ways of bars:
Li qualitez por percier entor l’os brisiet est que tu mettes I tarere sus l’os, et torne a tes dois tant que tu saiches que li os est perciez; puis remet lou tarere autre part un poc aprés, et ensi fai tout entor, puis cope as incisoires l’espaice de l’os qui est entre les pertu, et fai ceu plus subtilment que tu pues, et legierement, si com nos avons dit, tant que tu en traies l’os a ta main, ou a aucun des estrumens que tu as si com tenailles, pinceures; et garde que tu ne touchier au cerveil ne au syfac.	The quality for piercing inside the bone is that you put the bar on top of the bone and turn it two times until you know the bone is pierced; then move the bar a little bit further, and so do all around, then cut off the space of the bone which is between the holes, and do this more finely than you can, and lightly, as we have said, until you hold the bone in your hand, or at any of the instruments that you have such as pliers, pincers; and be careful not to touch the skull or the syphac.
Et quant tu avras l’os perciet, et trait, si couvient que tu reses l’apreteit qui est demoree de l’os a tout I autre estrument semblant a un incisoire, mais il covient qu’il soit plus tenves et plus subtilz que li autre incisoire; et s’il demore rien des petis os, ne nulles escailles, si les oste legierement a I des estrumens; puis cure la plaie de tentes et d’oignemens que nos avons dit.	And when you have cut and treated the bone, if it is understood that you extract the marrow which is delayed in the bone with all other instruments resembling an incisor but it is necessary that it be more tender and more delicate than the other incisor; and if it does not lag behind any small bones or scales, if the bone is lightly attached to the instrument; then cure the wound of tenderness and ointments that we have said.
Et li autre maniere d’ovraige si est cil que Galiiens dist, qui est plus saus; et le loa molt fort, et c’est sa parole.	And the other way to treat it is as Galen says, which is more effective; and to press it very strongly, and this is his word.
Il covient premier que tu descuevres une partie de l’os, lai ou li brisure apert mues, si que quant tu avras descovert celle partie, si metras desoz lou chief de cest incisoire lenticulaire, de coi ci est li forme:	It is necessary first that you discover a part of the bone, where the break opens, so that when you have discovered that part, you put on the end of this lens-shaped incision, from which it takes its form:
Et ne trenche mie d’une part, et est li partie ague en II costez, si que li trenchans est devers l’os; puis fier d’un petit maillet sus, si que tu copes legierement l’os tout entor, et te done bien en garde de la toile que est desoz; s’elle est aerse a l’os, si l’oste legierement, car on l’oste bien sens nuisement, et sens paor.	And do not cut it from one side, and the part is wet in two sides, so that the cutting is beside the bone; then set it with a small mallet on top, so that you hit the bone lightly all around, and take good care of the thread that is desos; if she is stuck to the bone, so gently hit the bone, for the bone well feels pain, and without fear.
Et se li brisure de l’os ne perce jusc’a la toile, et li os est copez tant soulement par desus, et il i a petites pieces, si couvient rere celle asperiteit, et oster les escailles au raseur subtil dont tu dois avoir diverses quantitez, por amenistrer en chescun leu le plus covenauble, selonc l’ovraige et la figure de la brisure.	And if the bone does not break through the skin, and the bone is cut so little from above, and there are small pieces, then cover them with a thin rasper, of which you must have various quantities, to apply in each place the most suitable, according to the work and the shape of the break.
Si reis devant de grant raseurs, et aprés de plus subtilz, et ne cesser de ceu faire tant k’il soit bien.	If you have several thin rasers, and then more fine ones, and do not stop doing this as long as it is well done.
En chescune des autres tailleures capillaires et brisure subtil, covient que tu amenistres cause selonc son adrecement; et c’est chose que n’est mie reponue a celui qui a mis son estude en cest art.	In each of the other haircuts and delicate cuts, you must bring the reason according to its adjustment; and this is something that has not yet been answered to the one who put his study in this art.
Et se li syfac est descovers, si covient que tu preignes I drapeil de lin, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et le moille en oile roset, et le mete sus la plaie; puis pren I autre drapeil doublé en II ou en III, et le moille en vin et en oile roset, et le met sus le premier drapeil; et fai ceu plus legierement que tu pues, que tu ne grever lou syfac, puis aministre par desus I autre liien, et ne l’estraindre mie fuer que tant k’il teigne la plaie soulement; et le laisse ensi I jor ou II, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, puis le deslie, et i aministre medicines si com racines de lis, et farine de veces, et poudre d’encens, et aristologe, et semblans choses; et de ces choses fai poudre, et met sus la plaie, et i aministre adés medicines mondefians sens mordication; et warde que li plaie soit adés nette, que tu n’i laissier mie l’oignement, ne n’i laissier mie assembler bowe, car quant bowe s’asemble sus la toile dou cerveil, si la corront et porrist, et avient au malaide grans malice; car quant on met sus lou syfac chose mordant, si nercist par desus.	And if the wound is uncovered, you should bring the fabric according to its size; and this is something that has not yet been answered to the one who put his study in this art. And if the wound heals slowly, take a linen cloth, according to the quantity of the wound, moisten it with oil, and place it on the wound; then take another doubled cloth, wet it with wine or oil, and place it over the first cloth; and do so more lightly than you can, that you do not hurt the wound, then bind it up, and do not tear it unless it is completely dry; and leave it like this for a day or two, until the abscesses have healed, then unbind it, and administer medicine to it as roots, flour of times, powder of incense, and aromatics, and similar things; and make these things into powder, and put it on the wound, and administer medicine to it immediately with deadly poison without bitterness; and guard against infection, so that you do not leave it, nor allow bowels to gather there, for when the bowels come together on the cloth of the skullcap, if they corrode and corrode, they bring great harm to the patient; because when something biting is put on the wound, if it is removed quickly.
Pren warde donques, se nulz mavais accidens vient au malaide, si com nos avons dit, si est doutable sens doute.	Watch out therefore, so that no bad accident happens to the patient, as we have said, if it is doubtful without doubt.
Et se noiror n’i vient fuers que por la medicine c’on a mise sus, que teil vertu ait, si covient que tu preignes une partie de miel, et III parties d’oile roset et en glue I drapel, et lou met sus lou syfac; puis lou cure de manieres de cures qu’il couvient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if blackened it comes only because of the medicine that has been put on, which has virtue, let you press a part of honey, and III parts of oil and in glue I drapel, and he puts it on his wound; then he cures by ways of cures that he knows, as long as he is healed.
Saiches que aucune fois sont brisies les II parties dou neis desus, ou li une par li soulement, car ce sont II os; et cil desoz est cartillaginous, et ne brise mie, si ne fait fuer k’enbower ou tordre, et puis saine.	You know that neither of the two bones above is ever broken, or if one falls out by itself, for these are two bones; and that bone is cartilaginous, and does not break unless it bends or twists, and then heals.
Et se l’une des II parties est brisie, si covient que tu boutes ton petit doi ou pertus dou neis, et met igal cele brisure dedens a ton doi indice, et au pouchet par defuer, tant que li neis reveigne selonc sa figure natureil; et fai ce legierement, et warde que li malaides ne sente dolor par ton ovraige.	And if one of the two bones is broken, let you put your little finger or a hole in the bone, and make equal that break inside your ring finger, and at the back by the side, as long as the bone regains its natural shape; and do this gently, and watch that the patient does not feel pain from your work.
Et se li brisure est en la partie desus lou neis, et ne puet venir li dois au leu, si couvient que tu lou mettes igal au chief d’un rait un poc gros.	And if his break is in the upper part of the neck and cannot return to its place, know that you put it equal to the head of a stick a little thick.
Et se li brisure est de II pars, si refai autretel, et te haste de restorer lou premier jor, se tu pues; se ce non, aprés lou septime ou le disime, quant li apostemes chaus est apaisiez, puis bouthe au chief dou neis tentes de drapelz de lin, se li brisure est en une partie.	And if his break is in two parts, do this other way, and hurry to restore the first day, if you can; if not, after the seventh or ninth, when the abscess has calmed down, then bind to the neck with strips of linen cloth, if the break is in one part.
Ou tu boutes I autre d’autre part, se li brisure i est; et soient les tentes si grosses qu’eles emplissent les pertus dou neis.	Or you bind the other to the other, if it breaks; and let the strips be so thick that they fill the openings of the neck.
Et dirent aucun restorour c’on doit moillier les tentes em burre, et muer chescun jor.	And say that one must dampen the strips to make them soft, and change them every day.
Il ne me semble mie que ce soit bien, mais covient qu’elles soient moillies en confection d’aubun d’uef, et de poudre de molin; puis laisse la tente, tant que li os soit fers, et li cartilaiges endurcis.	I do not think that this is good, but it seems that they must be wet with oak bark and mortar powder; then leave the strip, until the bone is hard and the cartilage is hardened.
Et aucune fois boute on ou neis pennes d’oie en leu de tentes, et si a I souef drapeil entor, et se tient la briseure, et soffle li malaides parmi; or fai lou kel ke tu vues.	And never put goose feathers in place of tents, and if it is a large draping cloth, hold the edge down, and let the wind blow on the patient, or make a small cage as you can see.
Et se apostemes chaus vient au neis tandis com tu i oevres, si i met cerote ou coton moilliet en oile roset, ou en I poc de dyaquilon.	And if an abscess forms while you are operating, put cotton soaked in oil or a poultice of blood-root, or a small patch of dyak.
Et se apostemes chaus n’i vient, si met emplastre par defuer, de farine de sisament, et de poudre d’encens, confites avec aubun d’uef, puis met sus estoupes legieres, et ne liier mie lou neis; et se li brisure dou neis est petite, et il est brisiés em menues pieces, si l’estrai as estrumens covenables a ceu, puis cout la fendure, et la cure de choses enjanrans char, et soudant, si com emplastres et oignemens covenables a ceu; et s’il n’a dedens lou neis nule plaie, si lou cure de tentes, et i met cainnes de plonc, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if an abscess does not form, put plaster on the outside, of flour made from sorghum and incense powder, cooked with egg white, then place it over light splinters, and do not tie the cloth; and if the dislocation is small, and it is broken into small pieces, then extract them with suitable instruments, then cut off the fracture, and cure the other injured things, and with suitable plasters and ointments; and if there is no wound inside the cloth, then cure the tents, and put cowhides on it, until it heals.
de la routure de la mandibule	From the rupture of the jaw.
Quant li mandibule est route desoz, et il n’i a point de plaie defuer, et li brisure est defuer tant soulement, et n’est mie brisiez en dous, fuer que corbelz dedens, si le conoist on legierement.	When the jaw is broken and there is no wound, and the break is not too large, and it is not broken into two pieces, but rather bent inside, then one must take care lightly.
Il covient, se li brisure est en la destre partie, que tu boutes ton doi indice en la bouche dou malaide; et se li brisure est en la mandibule senestre, si boute ton doi indice de la main destre, et boute la brisure dedens legierement, et l’afaite a l’autre main par defuer, et met igal.	If the break is on the right side, you should put your index finger in the mouth of the patient from the right hand; and if the break is on the left jaw, put your index finger from the left hand inside, gently pushing it back into place, and make it equal with the other hand from the outside.
Et se li brisure de la mandibule est desevree en II, si covient que tu aministres extension de II pars, tant qu’il soit igalz.	And if the break of the jaw is in two parts, then you should bring them together with two extensions, until they are equal.
Et se commovemens des dens avient, ou routure, si les estrain d’un fil d’or ou d’argent ou de soie, puis met sus la mandibule brisie cerote, et met sus I drapel double; et met sus lou drapel une grant estele bien faite, ou une piece de cuir igal, longe et large selonc la mandibule, et la lie sus au mues que tu pues, et comande a malaide qu’il se repose, et menjuce viandes legieres.	And if there is movement from the inside, or rupture, then tie it with a cord of gold, silver, or silk, then put wax over the broken jaw, and put a double cloth on top; and put a long and wide piece of leather, equal to the jaw, on top of the cloth, and fasten it with knots that you can, and instruct the patient to rest, and eat light food.
Et se tu vois que li figure se chainge, si le deslie au tier jor, et puis remet a point ceu que c’est chaingiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d’uef ou farine de sisament, aprés ceu que tu as osteit lou cerote; et met sus l’emplaustre lainne legiere, et se li emplaustres s’aert, et li disposition dou malaide ne se chainge, laisse le tant k’il soit sanez; maintes fois est sanez en III semainnes.	Et si tu vois que la figure [de la plaie] se change, si le désalage au tier jour, et puis remet à point ceu que c'est changiet; et met emplaustre sus, de la poudre dou moulin avec abun d'uef ou farine de sisament, après ceu que tu as ostéit lou cerote; et met sus l'emplaastre lainne légière, et si li emplaustres s'aert, et la disposition du malaide ne se change, laisse le tant qu'il soit sainz; maintes fois est sainz en III semainnes.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si amenistre ceu que nos avons dit maintes fois.	And if you see that the figure [of the wound] changes, if you desalinate at the third day, and then put back to place what has changed; and apply plaster, of the powder of the mill with much salt or flour of sisament, after you have taken out the cerote; and put on the other light plaster, and if the plaster applies itself, and the disposition of the ill one does not change, leave it as long as it is healthy; many times is healthy in III weeks.
Et s’il i a brisure et plaie ensamble, rewarde se nule piece de l’os en est ostee; si subtilie de l’oster as estrumens covenaubles a ceu.	And if there is a fracture and wound together, cut off no piece of the bone in ostification; if subtle, use the appropriate instruments for this.
Et se li plaie est estroite, si l’eslarge a flaime selonc ta necessiteit.	And if the wound is tight, expand it with fire according to necessity.
Et quant tu avras ostees toutes ces pieces, et il n’i demore nule, si cout la plaie, s’ele est large, et met sus I des emplaustres covenaubles a ceu, por enjanrer char, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have all the pieces of bone together, and there is no delay, if the wound is wide, put on it plasters suitable for this, to prevent infection, until it is healed.
de la forcele	(Here comes the end)
Li forcele brise plusors fois devant, devers l’espaule, et li brisure si est selonc III manieres: ou elle est brisie et desevree en II, et i a pieces, et est li plus legiere a restorer; ou il i a brisure avec plaie.
