(Here comes the end)The force of the blow breaks it several times in front, around the shoulder, and this fracture is according to three ways: either it is broken and dislocated, and there are pieces, and it is easier to restore; or there is a fracture with a wound.
Et li ovraiges si est quant li brisure est sens plaie, que tu aies II ministres, si que li uns teigne l’ajutoire que sent la forcele brisie; et li autres estende lou col vers la partie; puis met igal la brisure a tes dois, si que li forme soit si com il covient, et n’i ait ne apparance ne chevement.	(Here comes the end)And if the fracture is without wound, you have two ministers: one to hold the shoulder joint so it does not move because of the force of the blow; and the other extends the neck towards the part; then make the fracture even on both sides, so that its shape is as it should be, and there is no appearance or hair growth.
Et se tu a mestier de plus estendre, si met desoz l’espaule au malaide une spere reonde de drap, ou de lainne, et soit grosse selonc ta necessiteit; et estent et lieve la forcele, et estraint le spere a ta main, si que tu mettes igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And if you have the skill to extend further, so put a large round spear of cloth or another fabric on the shoulder of the patient, and make it big according to your need; and hold it up and tighten it, and hold the spear in your hand, so that you put the break even, as is right.
Et se tu ne pues traire le chief de la forcele au defuer, por ceu qu’elle vient em parfont, si covient que li malaides gise sovin sus son hatereil, et met desoz l’espaule I oreillier moien, et boute li ministres l’espaule aval, tant que li os de la forcele soit levez.	And if you cannot pull the head of the spear out to the end, so that it comes completely off, it is appropriate for the patient to lie down on his back, and put the shoulder with the help of a minister, and hold the shoulder away, until the bone of the spear is raised.
Et puis adrece la brisure a tes dois, et se tu lou trueves debrisiet, si covient que tu fendes sus; et trai fuer les pieces legierement, et se li os ne puet joindre por aucun sormontement, si le cope a l’un des incisoires que tu as; mais que tu mettes desoz la forcele cest estrument, por warder lou syfac:	And then place the break on both sides, and if you find it difficult to split it, it is appropriate to split it; and pull the pieces apart lightly, and if the bone cannot be joined together by any means, so take away the instrument of the spear, to preserve the medicine:
et semble une cuiller, et n’est mie chevez, et soit ausi large com il lou covient, selonc la grandor de l’os et la possance de l’uevre; et ait II chiés, si com tu vois, et soit li uns larges, et li autres estrois, si com est li routure de la plaie que tu as fait quant tu as trait les os; et quant tu es asseurez d’aposteme chaut, si cout la plaie, et se li routure est petite, ou tu doutes aposteme chaut, si emple la plaie de drapelz et de tentes, selonc sa quantiteit.	and it looks like a spoon, and is not hair, and is also wide as it should be, according to the size of the bone and the strength of the work; and it has two heads, if you look at it, and one is wider, and the other is narrower, just like the break in the wound that you made when you broke the bone; and when you are sure that the abscess is hot, if there is a small break, or you doubt about it, then bandage the wound with linen and tents, according to its size.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si moille I drapel en oile roset et en aisil et en vin, et met sus.	And if hot abscesses come, if you moisten it with oil, honey, and wine, and put it on.
Li estrignement de l’os, quant il est sens plaies et sens tailleure, est que tu mettes sus l’os l’enplaustre de la poudre dou molin et d’aubun d’uef, et met estoupes legieres sus, et met une spere desoz l’assele, se tu en as mestier; puis pren une tres grant bende d’une palme de large, puis met I drapeil double sus estoupes, et l’emplaustre; puis pren une estele subtil de III dois de large et de lonc, et l’envoloupe entor celui bendeil, si que li chief dou bendeil soient pendant; et met l’estele sus la briseure, et torne le bendeil sus lou col, et desoz l’asselle sainne, et desoz l’asselle malaide; et la ramoinne de chescune partie, et quant tu vois ke li lieure tient la briseure avenanment, et tu vois clerement que li estele ne se muet desus l’os brisiet, si le rewarde chescun jor, et quant li liiens eslaiche, si lou restraint; et fai gesir lou malaide sus son dos, et li met quant il dort I petit orillier desoz l’assele, por lever l’ajutoire en haut; si aligera li brisure de la forcele par l’aligement de l’espaule, ou tu li lie lou bras au col, et ne lou desliier se malvais accidens n’i vient, jusc’a XX jors; puis rencomence l’emplaustre, se tu vois qu’il en ait mestier, et l’estraint et le laisse ensi, tant qu’il soit restorez; et elle est restoree au plus en XXVIII jors, et en moins a aucuns homes.	And for breaking the bone, when there are no wounds and no cuts, you must put the bone in plaster with powder from the mill and ashes of ash, and lightly put staples on it, and tie a small staff around it, if you need to; then take a very thick band about a palm wide, then put the linen double on the staples, and cover it with plaster; then take a thin stake three fingers wide and long, and wrap it tightly around that band, so that the head of the band is hanging down; and place the stake over the break, and turn the band back over the neck, and tie the staff to the joint; and let it rest like this for each day, and when you see that the limb holds together well, and you clearly see that the stake does not move around the bone, then release it slowly, day by day, until it is healed; and it will be healed in about twenty-eight days, and less for some men.
de la brisure de l’espaule	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Poc avient que li espaule brise ou large leu ne em mileu, et ne lou seit on fuers que par lou touchement; si l’apareille selonc la figure de la brisure, et la ramoinne selonc sa forme natureil, en toutes les manieres que tu pues; puis met sor le leu poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, et estoupes legieres, et met sus I drapeil double; puis met sus une estele large et subtil, un poc plus large de l’espaule, et se desoz l’estele est chevemens en aucun leu de l’espaule, si emple celle cheveure d’estoupes de lin, si que li estele siece igalment; et puis l’estraint a tout une grant bende fermement, si que li estele ne se mueve de son leu, et regarde le liien chescun jor; et toutes les fois k’il amolist, si l’estraint, et met igal l’estele s’elle est fuer de son leu, et gise li malaides sus son costeit; et li espaule est restouree en XX jors ou en xxv, Et quant cist nombres est acomplis, si le deslie, et soies seur, car ce n’est mie os qui se mette fuer legierement.	de la brisure de l’épaule
Et se une piece de l’os tent avant, et point desoz lou keur, si fent sus, et l’oste, et fai ceu que nos avons dit en la brisure de la forcele d’apaisier aposteme chaut.	If there is a piece of the bone forward, and don't remove it, if it heats, and the bone, and do as we said in the dislocation of the shoulder to soothe abscess heat.
de la brisure dou pis	of the break of the foot
Li peis est aucune fois brisiez em mileu, mais ce avient poc; mais il brise sovent au defuer.	The feet are not sometimes broken in the middle, but this does happen; but they often break at the end.
Et quant il est brisiez emmi, si decline au desoz, et sent li malaides grant dolor, et faute d’alainne, et toust, et par aventure vomist sanc, et apert li chevemens en l’os brisiés, et lou sent om bien.	And when they are broken in the middle, if they decline to the side, and the patient feels great pain, and there is a lack of support, and at times, and by chance he vomits blood, and opens the veins in the broken bone, and it smells bad.
Et li restoracion si est que li malaides gise sovin sus son dos, et li met I cussin entre les espaules, puis presse les espaules, et li assemble les costes des II costelz a tes mains, et subtilie dou mettre igal a toutes les manieres que tu pues, tant que li figure de l’os soit si com il covient; puis met sus emplaustres et estoupes desus l’estele subtil de salz, ou d’autre fust legier, et l’envoloupe en I drapeil, et la lie sus l’os brisiet, si qu’elle ne se mueve; et torne le liien reondement au dos, et l’estraint avenanment, et rewarde chescune houre la liure, et s’elle ramolist, si l’estraint; et s’il lou covient desliier, por corrosion ou por prurite que vient au leu, ou dolor ou aposteme, si te haste, et lou deslie, et raie l’emplaustre, et adresce ceu qui i est venus de manieres de cures; puis ramoinne l’emplaustre, et l’estraint tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is that the patient is made to lie on his back, and he places it between the shoulders, then presses the shoulders, and gathers the ribs of the II ribs with your hands, and gently puts it in place as much as possible, so that the shape of the bone is like this; then put it on plasters and wrap it around the thin board of salt, or other lighter thing, and wrap it in a cloth, and attach it to the broken bone, so that it does not move; and return the tie nicely to the back, and holds it fast, and releases it every hour, and if it relaxes, then hold it; and if he needs to be released, because of corrosion or itchiness that comes to the spot, or pain or abscess, if you hurry, and release it, and remove the plaster, and treat him in this way; then take off the plaster, and hold it fast until it is healed.
de la brisure des costes	of the rupture of the ribs
Saiches que li briseure des costes ne vient fuer que en leus gros aprés le dos, et au chief dedens, et ne ploient fuer que por ceu qu’eles sont glairouses; et le sent om bien a l’inquisition as dois.	I know that the rupture of the ribs does not come from anywhere except from the large ones behind the back, and at the top inside, and do not bend too much because they are thin; and feel very good to the touch.
Et li restoremens si est que tu met igal la brisure, si com il covient.	And restore them so that you make the rupture even, as it should be.
Et puis met l’emplaustre, et l’estraint d’une estele, se tu en as mestier.	And then put on plaster, and a splint from a stick if you need one.
Et se li brisure des costes est declinans au dedens, si sent li malaides tres grant dolor, et pointure, ausi com de pleuresin, car li os point la toile; et alaine a poinnes, et toust et vomist grant planteit de sanc, et c’est de grief santeit, et li ancien i ont mis grant engien.	And if the rupture of the ribs is declining inwardly, then the patient feels great pain and a sharp pain, as if he were crying out; for the bone does not spread; and it makes him nauseous and vomit a lot of blood, and this is a sign of bad health, and he has put up with a lot of trouble.
Et si a de ces qui dient qu’il le covient aministrer viandes qui enflent le ventre, por bouter la briseure au defuer.	And if any of these serve that it is necessary to administer meat that swells the belly, in order to push the rupture away.
Nos ne faisons mie ceu, que apostemes chaulz n’i viegne, s’il n’i est venus.	We must not do this, for if hot poultices are not brought, they will not come.
Et s’il i est venus, si le saine.	And if they have come, and the wound is healed.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on met ventouses sor le leu, por sucier forment, et c’est semblant a raison; toutevoie, doutance i a que li ventouse n’atraie les superfluitez au leu por la disposition de foiblece.	And they say that we should not put leeches on the spot, for sucking out the excess fluid, and this seems reasonable to us; nevertheless, there is doubt that the leeches will not attract the excesses to the spot due to their weakness.
Et dirent aucun d’ous c’on doit covrir le leu de lainne moillie en oile chaut, et met on tentes entre les costes por metre igal la lieure entor, puis soit curez de la cure de pleurisin, de viande et de medicine.	And they say that one should not cover the spot with another moist thing in oil, and put tents between the ribs to make the wound even, then it is cured with the cure for ulcers, meat, and medicine.
Et se li malaides sent grant dolor qu’il ne puet soffrir par l’os qui point la toile, et doutance est au malaide, si covient fendre sus lou leu de la coste brisie, et covient mettre desoz I estrument por warder lou syfac; et adonques doit on trenchier l’os, et traire legierement, et puis coudre les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, et le curez d’emplaustres, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the patient feels great pain so that he cannot bear the pressure of the towel on his back, then there is doubt in the patient; therefore, it is necessary to split the bone at the site of the broken rib, and to put a tool under it to hold it in place; and then one must trim the bone, and draw it gently, and then stitch the two sides of the wound together, if it is large, and treat it with ointments until it is healed.
Et se apostemes chaus vient, si met sus drapelz moilliez en oile roset, et met sus lou leu; et cure tandis le leu de ceu qu’il covient a aposteme, et soit gisans sovins sus lou costeit ou il doit, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if abscesses come up, then put oil on the drape and place it on the lump; and cure while waiting for the lump to heal, and give soothing drinks along the side where he needs it until he is well.
de la brisure dou col	of the break in the throat
Aucune fois vient briseure as os dou col, et poc avient k’il ploie; et ausi a l’espinee dou dos.	No time comes when the bones of the neck break, and there is no pain; and also at the spine of the back.
Et quant ce avient a aucun, et tu vues savoir s’il sera sanez ou non, si pren warde se tu vois ses mains mollifiies et enflees et mortes, et ne les puet movoir ne estendre, et quant tu les poins d’une aguille, si ne lou sent.	And when this has happened to anyone, and you do not know if he will be well or not, then take care that his hands are soft and swollen and dead, and cannot move them or stretch them out; and when you prick them with a pin, if he does not feel it.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz em plusors dispositions, et s’il les muet et sent bien quant on les estraint et point, saiches que li jointure de l’os est sauve, et que li malaides iert curez, s’on i met cure.	Know that it is fatal in many cases, and if he does not feel them when they are pricked and does not move them, know that the joint of the bone has been saved, and the disease has been cured, if one puts on a cure.
Et se semblans chose vient a l’espinee dou dos, et tu vues savoir s’il iert sanez ou non, si pren warde se li piez sont amollis, et se li accident i sont qui sont em mains, et sus lou dos saut ventositeit et egestion sens volonteit; et quant on l’a sovineit sus son ventre, si saut egestion sens volonteit.	And if there is a similar thing that comes to the spine of the back, and you know whether it is healthy or not, if its feet are soft, and if the accident that happened to it was with its hands, and on the back there is windiness and excretion without volition; and when it has been treated by being placed on its belly, if there is excretion without volition.
Et quant il est sovinez sus son dos et il vuet asseller, si ne puet.	And when it has been treated by being placed on its back and it cannot move, then it cannot.
Saiches qu’il est mortelz: si ne laboreir mie en sa cure.	Know that it is fatal: do not work at its cure.
Et se cist accident ne li vienent, si est li chose plus legiere.	And if this accident did not come to him, then this is the lightest thing.
Et li cure si est que tu rewardes s’il i a aposteme chaut, si met sus l’espinee oile roset ou oile de moieuf d’uef, tant qu’il soit apaisiez; puis met sus un des emplaustres confortans et sechans, et le lie d’un liien, et comande au malaide a reposer; et ne dorme mie sus celle partie ou il sent la dolor, tant k’il soit sanez.	And the cure is that you treat him if there is an abscess, put oil or butter of cows on the spine until it is relieved; then put one of the plasters conforting and drying, and tie it with a ligature, and order the patient to rest; and do not sleep on that side where he feels pain, until he is healthy.
Et se aucuns os se dessevre, si covient coper sus lou keur; et oste l’os, puis assemble les II levres de la plaie, s’elle est grans, a une costure, puis le cure d’oignement enjanrant char, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se li chiés de l’os est brisiez, ki est apelez li «chiés de la kowe», se i boute ton pouchet de ta main senestre, et le met igal a l’autre main a ton pooir, puis met l’emplaustre et l’estele sus, se tu en a mestier; puis l’estraint, et s’il i a os desevreit, si fent sus, et l’oste, et cure la plaie tant qu’elle soit sanee.	Et si certains os se dessèvelent, couvrez-les avec du kératine ; puis fixez l'os, puis assemblez les deux lèvres de la plaie, s'elle est grande, avec une couture, puis traitez-la avec des onguents en utilisant du charbon de bois, jusqu'à ce qu'elle guérisse ; et si le cheville de l'os est brisée, ce qui est appelé le "cheville de la cowe", si vous tenez un pot dans votre main gauche et le placez horizontalement par rapport à votre poignet gauche, puis placez-y l'emplastre et le bandage, si nécessaire ; puis l'appliquez, et si certains os se sont dessèvelés, couvrez-les, puis traitez la plaie jusqu'à ce qu'elle guérisse.
de la brisure de l’os de la hainche	For the fracture of the leg bone
Poc avient que li os de la hainche soit brisiez, et s’il avient, si n’avient fuer c’un poc d’amenuisement au chief; et fent dou lonc, et decline au pardedens, et vient au malaide dolor au leu, et pointure, et enfle ceu que brise.	If the hip joint is broken, and if so, there would be a little decrease in height at the top of the skull; let it grow long, and decline to the back, and comes to the patient pain at the site, and ache, and swelling that is broken.
Et li restoration si est que tu estendes ta main sus, tant que tu soies sus la briseure; et saiches quelz est li brisure et li figure de li; et se li brisure est au chief soulement, si met igal cele brisure, tant qu’ele soit a figure natureil.	And the rehabilitation is that you extend your hand above it as long as you are above the fracture; and know what is the fracture and its shape; and if the fracture is at the top, then make it equal to the natural shape as long as it exists.
Et se li brisure est dou lonc, ou elle decline au dedens, si fai gesir le malaide sus son ventre, tant que li restauration de cele brisure te soit aparillie.	And if the fracture is long, or it declines inward, then make the patient stand on his stomach as long as the rehabilitation of that fracture is arranged for him.
Et quant tu l’avras mise igal, si met sus l’emplaustre, puis met sus une estele de fust ou de keur, et estraint la briseure, si qu’ele ne se mueve; et emple le leu desoz les costes, tant que li lieure soit igalz.	And when you have made it equal, then put on the plaster, then put on a wooden or iron splint, and tighten the fracture so that it does not move; and employ the space between the ribs as long as the place is equal.
Et comande au malaide k’il dorme sus son costeit sain, ou sus son dos.	And command the patient to sleep on his side or back.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si n’i tochier, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez, et met sus ceu que nos avons devant dit; et puis revien a la restauration, et l’estraint si com il covient, s’il n’i a nul mavais accident; et c’est li maniere.	And when the abscess is hot, if it does not burst, as long as the abscess is warm, and put on what we have said before; and then return to restoration, and hold it as necessary, unless there is some bad accident; and that is the way.
de la brisure de l’ajutoire	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Li adjutoires est ceu qui est entre lou coute et lou chief de l’espaule, et s’il est brisiez, si le doit on restorer selonc l’une des II manieres: dont l’une est que tu pren I fust plain de moiene groissor, selonc ceste forme:	The adjutory is that which is between the neck and the head of the shoulder, and if it is broken, then should one restore according to one of the two ways: which one is that you take a pliable cloth, according to this form:
Et lie as II chiés II liens, et les pent en haut, et siece li malaide sus I siege; puis li giete som bras brisiet sus le fust, tant qu’il viegne a l’aissele, et ait em mi une corbeure de fust, puis pent sus aucune pesant chose ou li ministres l’estende aval; puis mette li mires la briseure igal a ses mains ensamble, tant que li briseure retorne si com il covient.	And lie down on two pillows and bend them up high, and tie the patient to a couch; then put the shoulder in place with a rope; then he will have to support his arm with something that goes under the armpit; then put the dislocated shoulder in line with his hand, as long as it returns as necessary; and that is how you should do it.
Et li autre maniere si est que on sovine le malaide sus son hatereil, et li lie la main a son col, puis comande a II ministres que li uns teigne ceu qui est sus la briseure a ses mains, et li autres teigne desoz a tout I liien, et estende chescuns a sa partie.	And another way is that one should let the patient rest on his back, and tie his hands to his neck, then order two ministers that one of them tie who is lying on the side with his hands, and the others pull him by all his body, and extend each to their part.
Et se tu vues que li estraction soit plus fors, si estraint I liien desoz la briseure, et sus la briseure, et estende chescuns des ministres a sa part.	And if you see that the extraction is too much, then tie the patient by all his body, and extend each minister to their part.
Et se li briseure est prochiene au chief de l’espaule, si covient que tu mettes I liien moien desoz l’assele, et I autre vers lou coute, desoz la briseure; et ausi se li briseure est devers lou coute, si i covient mettre I liien legierement, sens labor, tant que li briseure soit igalz sus lou leu, et sus lou coute; puis met igal la brisure, si com il covient, et l’estraint, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the fracture is near the shoulder head, then you must place the bandage over the shoulder as well as around the chest; and likewise, if the fracture is on the side of the neck, you must place the bandage slightly, without strain, until the fracture is even with its position, and then secure it, because with the posture of the patient in that position, there will be no injury.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si ne l’estraindre mie jusc’a VII jors, et met sus lainne moillie en aisil et en oile roset, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez; puis l’estraint, et li maniere de l’estraindre si est que tu mettes l’emplaustre sus la briseure, puis assemble le bras sus l’ajutoire, et met ta main sus l’espaule ou sus lou sein; et met le drapeil, et estraint sus l’ajutoire, et sus lou bras, si que li bras soit en leu d’esteles, s’aucune chose ne le te deffent, ou se li os n’est muez.	And if the abscess comes out, do not extract it until seven days have passed, and put plaster on it with milk and rosewater until the abscess is calm; then extract it, and the way to extract it is that you put the plastrice on the bruise, and then tighten the arm on the aid, and put your hand on the shoulder or the lap; and wrap the bandage around, and tighten on the aid and on the arm so that the arm is in place of the elbow, so that nothing hinders it or the bone does not break.
Et se tu doutes que li os ne se mueve, si use d’esteles, et met sus la brisure une estele plus large et plus fort des autres, et ait entre chescune estele I doi d’espaice, et soit chescune estele si grans qu’elle passe la briseure III dois de chescune part; puis estrain sus les esteles, ensi com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre sus la briseure, plus fort et moins en aloignant.	And if you doubt that the bone is moving, use a splint, and put a wider and stronger splint over the bruise than the others, and have two inches of space between each splint, and make each splint so large that it passes three inches on either side of the bruise; then pull on the splints as I said at the beginning of the chapter about the plaster on the bruise, more strongly and less by moving away.
Et se tu vois l’assise des esteles, et l’estrignement, si com nos avons dit, en l’oure que tu restoures le membre brisiet, et tu doutes l’aposteme chaut, si le laisse a liier jusc’a septime jor, si com nos avons dit; puis regarde chescuns III jors lou lien, que prurite ne enfleure n’i viegne au leu, ou li norrissemens ne puist venir au membre por ceu k’il est trop estrois.	And if you see the seat of the star and the incision, as we have said, in the hour that you restore the broken member, and you dub the apotheosis warm, let it remain tied until the seventh day, as we have said; then look at each of the three days to the knot, that itching does not flourish or come to the place, or that the re-setting cannot come to the member because it is too constricted.
Si l’adrece, si com nos avons dit.	And if you dub the apotheosis, as we have said.
Et se nulz telz accidens n’i vient, si ne lou desliier fuer que aprés III jors ou plus, et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ait ses mains sus son stomac; et met desoz l’ajutoire I cussin plain de laine igalment, et regarde chescune houre dou jor ou de la nut, que li figure dou membre brisiet ne se mueve, ou ne soit amollis li liiens; si l’adrece par la vertu de medicine, et li done la viande que nos avons devant mis, en teil maniere que li viande soit au premier subtilz; et quant il comance a reprendre, si soit grosse.	And if no such accident happens, and you only remove it after three or more days, and the patient sleeps on his back, and has his hands on his stomach; then stretch out the shoulder with one straight piece of linen, and look every hour during the day or night, that the figure of the broken member does not move, or become softer; if you reset it by the power of medicine, and give him meat that we have before mentioned, in such a way that the meat is at the first subtle layer; and when it begins to recover, let it be coarse.
Et est costume que li ajutoire et li jambe doient estre repris en XL jors dou tout; et adonques lou doit on desliier et aministrer bain et medicines d’oignemens por le leu adrecier.	And it is fitting that the shoulder and leg should be set again in 40 days after all; and then they must be separated and administered baths and medicinal ointments to the wound.
Et se li estricture est laide et emboee, si demore a desliier L jors ou II mois.	And if the stiffness is bad and blocked, it should not be separated after one or two months.
de la brisure du bras	of the break of the arm
Li bras est compos de II os, qui sont apelez li dui «foscile», de coi li uns est petis, et est cil qui enseut le pouchet; et li autres est grans, et est cil qui est desoz, devers lou petit doi; par aventure brise li grans foscile soulement, ou li petis, et par aventure andui ensamble.	The arm is composed of two bones, which are called the "foscile", one small and one large; the small is that which attaches to the hand, and the large is that which is joined to the shoulder; perhaps it will break only one of these, or both together.
Quant li petis fosciles est brisiez, li restaurations est legiere, et li sanations; et quant li grans est brisiez, si est li sanation male, et plus griés que quant il sont brisiez andui ensamble.	When the small "foscile" is broken, the restoration is light and the healing; and when the large one is broken, the healing is bad, and more painful than when it is broken together.
Se c’est li petis foscile qui est brisiez soulement, si le covient poc estendre legierement, et mettre igal.	If this small piece of wood has been broken by a slight blow, then it is necessary to extend it slightly and make it even.
Et se c’est li grans foscile, si le covient estraindre plus fort; et l’estende sus I cussin, et teigne le pouchet de la main plus haut des autres, et li petis dois plus bas des autres dois, et soit li malaides croisiez sus lui meisme, et I cussin devant lui plus haut, que li malaides ne soffre nule labor; puis estende li ministres som bras a la partie desoz a sa main, ou a I liien, et uns autres ministres a I autre au desus.	If the large piece of wood is broken, then it should be pulled out with force; and it is extended on one side, and the handle of the iron is held higher than the other handles, and the small pieces are placed lower than the other handles, and so that the patient does not feel any pain; then extend the arms of the minister to the affected part at his hand, or at his leg, and place other ministers on either side above.
Et puis le mette li mires igal, selonc sa millor forme.	Then make it even, according to its best form.
Et se en la brisure a pieces, si met chescune en son leu, et s’il en i a nule desevree ke poigne lou keur, et tu ne la pues restorer en son leu, si fent sus et l’oste, si com nos avons dit devant.	If the wood has broken into pieces, then place each piece in its proper place; and if one of them has become loose and does not fit, and you cannot restore it to its place, then fix it with iron and bone, as we have said above.
Et se avec la briseure a plaie, je en ai parleit au chapistre singuler; si pren la cure.	And if with the cautery there is an injury, I have spoken of it to the peculiar chapter; so take the cure.
Et se en l’encomencement dou restorement sorvient apostemes chaus, si glue I drapeil de cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire blainche, que ne soit mie ne trop durs ne trop molz; et lie I drapeil par sus subtilment, tant que li apostemes chaus soit apaisiez.	And if in the beginning of the restoration there are abscesses, then let me wrap them with a plaster made of oil and white wax, which is neither too hard nor too soft; and let me wrap them gently, until the abscesses are calm.
Et puis oste lou cerote, et i met l’emplaustre de la poudre dou molin avec abun d’uef, pues met les esteles, et soit li estele de la briseure adés plus fors, et un poc plus large que les autres; et saiches que il doit avoir VI esteles ou bras em plusors dispositions: soit que li briseure soit en l’un des os, soit en II; et estraint plus sus la briseure que autre part, et toz jors moins en aloignant, si com j’ai dit au comencement dou chapistre; et soient li drapelz que sont sus la briseure molz et moistes, et ne soient mie dur ne aspres; et soit li filz, dont il est estrains, de lin, ne trop gros ne trop menus, si com nos avons dit.	And then the bone is wrapped in the plaster, and I put the paste made from powder from the mill with a lot of ash, then put the splints, and let the splint of the fracture be closer to the shoulder than to the other; and know that there must be six splints or more: whether the fracture is in one bone or two; and pull it up above the fracture rather than down, always moving away as I said at the beginning of the chapter on plaster; and may the wrappings that are on the fracture be soft and moist, and not too hard nor too sharp; and let the thread with which it is pulled be made of linen, not too thick nor too thin, as we have said.
Et rewarde lou membre et lou liien aprés aucuns jors.	And wait for the member and the lien after a few days.
Et se aucuns mavais accidens vient au membre, si com prurite ki vient au membre, si covient que tu aroses lou membre d’aigue chaude, tant que cil prurites soit apaisiez; et laisse le membre ne mie estroit reposer.	And if some bad accident happens to the member, as when itch comes to the member, it is necessary that you dip the member in warm water until the itch is relieved; and let the member rest without constricting it.
Et puis rencomence l’estrignement, et se li liiens est amolis et li os desevrez, et semblant chose, si l’adresce.	And then begin again to draw out, and if the lien is softened and the bone exposed, and similar things, then address it.
Et se pren warde se li norrissemens ne puet venir au membre, por ceu qu’il est trop estrois, si covient que tu l’amollisses I poc, et laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant que li norrissemens i corre, et puis l’estraint.	And if it is necessary that the member not be moved again for a long time, because it is too stiff, then you must soften it slightly and leave it thus for some days, so that the movement begins again, and then draw it out.
Et se nules de ces choses que nos avons dit ne vient au malaide, si ne lou desliier jusc’a XX jors.	And if none of these things that we have said comes to the patient, let it not be dislocated until XX days.
ou enqui entor, puis li pent les mains a son col, et soit ses cols igalz, et se warde de movement et de degitement, et dorme sus son dos; et saiches que ceste briseure est restoree en XXX jors ou en XXXV, et par aventure en XX jors, selonc les compositions et les complexions des vertus.	Or, having entered the room, he puts his hands on his neck, and let his necks be even, and hold back from movement and turning, and sleeps on his back; and know that this healer is healed in XXX days or in XXXV, and by chance in XX days, according to the compositions and complexions of virtues.
de la brisure de la main	of the break in the hand
Saiches que au dos de la main et as nous des dois avient poc de briseures, et n’i vient mais que ploieure maintes fois.	are few fractures on the back of the hand, and there comes but little rain many times.
Et quant li plante de la main est brisie ou ploie, si covient que li malaides siece croisiet, et siet droitement devant lui igalement; puis met sa main sus la toie estendue, et estende li ministres les os brisiez, et les mete igalz li mires, tant qu’il soient bien joint; et met l’emplastre et les estoupes, se apostemes n’i vient, puis i met une estele selonc la quantiteit dou leu; et soit envoloupee en I drapeil de lin.	And when the plant of the hand is broken or wet, so that the patient crochets and sits up straight and even; then he lays his hand on a cloth spread out, and extends the broken bones, and makes them even by the mirror, until they are well joined; and puts plaster and staples, if there be an abscess, then he puts a stake according to the quantity of the place; and is wrapped up in one sheet of linen.
Et se li briseure est au pardedens entor lou ventre de la plante, si fai une spere de drapelz, et comande au malaide qu’il l’estrigne a sa plante brisie; et puis l’estrain d’un lonc drapeil, et soit li estele de keur souef ausi grans com li plante de la main, et l’estraint, si com il covient.	And if it breaks within the parka between the navel of the plant, then make a rope of canvas, and command the patient that he strangles at his broken plant; and then extract with a long rope, and let his steel be as great as the plant of his hand, and extract it, as it befits.
Et se li brisure est au defuer, si covient que tu mettes une estele sus, et une autre desoz en la plante, si que li mains soit overte et droite, puis le lie tot entor la main, et estanche lou liien entre les dois.	And if it breaks on the outside, then it is fitting that you put a stake above, and another one in the plant, so that the hands are open and straight, then tie it completely around the hand, and stop the blood flow between the two.
Et se li briseure vient a aucun des nous des dois, se c’est li pouchés, si le met igal, si com il covient; et l’estraint avec la plante, et se tu vues si met une estele droite petite por lever la briseure, et ne se mueve; et se li brisure est as autres dois, si com en l’indice ou l’un des autres, si le met igal, et lou lie avec lou doi sain qui est aprés; ou tu les lie toz en I tenant, que mues vaut, ou tu met sus une estele, si com ou pouchet; et pren warde en la restauration et en la disposition d’aposteme chaut, et secor ceu qui i vient, si com j’ai dit.	And if the break comes to either of the two hands, then he is pulled up, even as it befits; and it is extracted with the plant, and if you see that there is one above, then he puts it equal, even as it befits; and he extracts it with the healthy hand that is after; or you tie them all together holding, so that it does not hurt, or you put a stake on it, even as the poultice; and take care in the restoration and arrangement of the aposteme, and help those who come to it, even as I said.
de la cuixe brisie	of the broken chest
Li os de la cuixe est maintes fois brisiez, et bien le voit on quant elle torne devant et derrier; et li restauration si est c’on lie I liien desus la briseure, et I autre desoz.	The bones of the breast are often broken, and we can clearly see when they turn forward and backward; and the restoration is so that we bind them above the fracture, and another below.
Et li malaides gise sus sa faice, puis estende chescuns ministres son lien a sa part igalment; et c’est quant li brisure est emmi l’os.	And the patient lies on his face, then extends each minister his bond to his part equally; and it is when the fracture has been made thin.
Et se li brisure est prochiene a la racine de la cuixe, si soit li uns des liiens devers lou poignil, et li autres liiens desoz la briseure.	And if the fracture is near the root of the breast, then one of the bonds extends beyond the knuckle, and the other bond below the fracture.
Et ausi s’elle est prochiene au genoil, et adonques soit li liens delez lou genoil, et soit li extension aval; puis mette li mires l’os igal a ses II mains, tant qu’il soit selonc sa figure natureil, et puis met l’emplaustre, et lou lie, se apostemes chaz n’i vient.	And if it is near the knee, then one of the bonds extends beyond the knee, and the other below the fracture; then put the minister the bone equal to its natural shape with his two hands, and then put the plaster on, and bind it, so that there are no gaps in the aposteme.
Et s’il i a aposteme chaut, si le laisse apaisier puis revien a ton ovraige et a ta cure; li lieure est faite en teil maniere.	And if there is an abscess, let it be calmed then return to your work and your treatment; the time has come in some way.
Il covient que tu envoloupes sus la briseure I bendeil dur doublé en II ou III, et en demoure li superfluitez, puis torne la jambe tant que li talons veigne a la racine de la naige, et boute I fil lonc entre la cuixe et la jambe, delez lou genoil desoz, et veignent li chief dou fil au desus; puis torne sus la jambe et sus la cuixe le bendeil, puis met sus la briseure esteles, et met une estele sus l’os de la jambe; puis emple le leu vuit entre la jambe et la cuixe de drapelz souef por mettre igal l’estrignement, puis comence a liier forment III tors ou IIII sus la briseure; et quant plus vas en sus de la briseure, et moins l’estraint; puis enten as II chiés dou fil que tu as bouteit entre la jambe et la cuixe, et en lie III esteles que sont desus, puis revai au desoz au chief dou fil, tant que tu veignes delez le piet; et l’estraint, si qu’il ne se mueve de son leu, puis le laisse ensi, puis k’il n’i vient ne aposteme ne enfleure n’autre semblant.	And if there is an abscess, wrap it in a dry cloth with a hard strap double-knotted in II or III places, and let the excess fluid go; then turn the leg so that the heels come to the root of the heel, and fix the long thread between the thigh and the leg, release the knee joint, and bring the chief of the thread upward; then turn again on the leg and on the thigh, put on the strap, and put a strap on the bone of the leg; then employ the place where it is stretched with cloth to make the straining even; then begin to tie it in III or IV twists on the bandage; and as you go up on the bandage, let the straining be less; then put II or III straps that are above on it, and return to the release at the chief of the thread, until you come to the heel; and the straining, so that it does not move from its place, then leave it like this, and if there is no swelling, no abscess, or any other appearance.
Et s’il i avient, si le deslie, et adresce ceu que i vient, si com nos avons dit maintes fois; et se il i a pieces de l’os que poigne, si le covient ewer, s’om puet; et s’on ne puet, si covient fendre le leu, et traire fuer; et le cure si com nos avons dit, tant k’il soit sanez.	And if it should fall, and turn the other way, and take that which comes to it, as we have said many times; and if there are pieces of the bone that hold, then let them be held fast; and if they cannot be held fast, then let the place be split open and pulled out firmly; and heal it as we have said, until it is well.
Et aucune fois est brisie li cuixe ensi c’on i met esteles, si com en l’ajutoire et ou bras; toutevoie, en la restauration ensi faite ne cloche mie li malaides.	And in no way should the collarbone be broken when it is put back in place, as with the shoulder and arm; however, when restored in this way, the patient does not recover.
Et saiches que li cuixe est restoree en L jors, ou poc moins ou poc plus, selonc les diversitez des complexions.	And know that the collarbone is restored in a day or two or more, depending on the diversity of complexions.
de la ruelle dou genoil	of the knee
Saiches que en la ruelle dou genoil avient poc brisure, mais elle ploie maintes fois.	There is little breaking in the knee, but it swells many times.
Et s’elle brise, si n’est mais c’une fendure, ou I pertus, et avient a tout plaie, et sens plaie, et ce sent om bien.	And if it breaks, let there be only a split or a crack, and not all at once, and not too deep; and if it does not hurt, then let it be fixed in this way, so that it no longer hurts.
Et li restauration si est c’on mette igal ceu qui est rons a ses dois, tant qu’il soit assemblez mues c’on puet; puis met l’emplaustre, et i met une estele reonde, se tu en as mestier, et l’estraint si com il covient, puis rewarde toutes les dispositions que nos avons dit ens autres briseures, si com aposteme chaut et autre semblant; si met a chescun accident ceu k’il li covient, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And the restoration is such that one puts equal to the other what is long to its two, as far as it can be assembled; then put the plaster on, and put a round stake if you need one, and hold it as it should be held, then return all the dispositions that we have said in other breaking, such as an abscess and others; put on each accident what is appropriate to it, as long as it is healthy.
de la brisure de la jambe	regarding the break of the leg
Saiches que en la jambe ait II os, de coi li uns est apelez par droit non «mustelz», et li autres est apelez «foscile»; et avient tout auteil briseure com il vient au bras, et por ceu est li restauracion si com celle dou bras igalment, et li ovraiges est tout i. Et se li dui os sont brisiet ensamble, si torne li jambe de toutes pars.	I understand that in the leg there are two bones, one which is called "mustelz" by right and the other "foscile"; and it happens to each in the same way as with the arm, and for this reason the restoration is done in the same way as that of the arm; and if the two bones break together, the leg turns all around.
Et se li os subtilz est brisiez, si torne devant.	And if the thin bone is broken, then turn back.
Et se li gros os est brisiez, si sent on grant dolor, et le voit on bien; et torne desoz.	And if the large bone is broken, then one feels great pain and it is seen clearly; and turn aside.
Adonques amenistre extension, et le met igal, et lie les esteles igalement; mais toutevoie, il covient se li brisure est laide, et il i a plusors pieces, que li extension soit menor et plus legiere; et l’alige selonc ta vertu.	And then bring the body to an upright position, and make it even, and bind the joints evenly; but nevertheless, it is necessary that the fracture be ugly, and there are many pieces, so that the extension is smaller and lighter; and align according to your virtue.
Et quant tu as tout acomplit ton ovraige, si pren II faixes de fust chevees que porpreignent la jambe d’une part et d’autre, et soient dou lonc de la jambe des le genoil jusque desoz; puis envoloupe en II leus I bendeil desus et desoz, et le lie em mileu ausi, et a ceste lieure ne pora li jambe decliner a destre ne a senestre, et ensi est bien; et aucun i aministrent I bers dou lonc de la jambe, et s’est de fust, et i met on la jambe por warder de movement, et proprement fait on ceu en la brisure ou il a plaie; et remue chescun jor la jambe, por veoir s’il i a aposteme chaut n’autre accident; si le cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	And when you have finished your work, take two pieces of rope that purple the leg on one side and the other, and are long from the knee to the foot; then wrap them in two loops above and below, and tie this ligature firmly, so that the leg does not fall towards the right or the left, and so is good; and no one administers the ropes of the leg, and if it is wood, and one puts the leg to keep from moving, and properly he lays him on the fracture or wound; and moves each day the leg, to see if there is an abscess or some other accident; then cure as long as it is healthy.
de la brisure des os dou piet	of the break of the bones of the foot
A la cheville ne vient point de brisure, mais as os dou piet vient aucune fois brisure et as dois poc, et n’i avient fuer que quassure em plusor dispositions.	At the ankle there is no break, but at the foot there is a break in two cases and only one time; it has happened to me in more than one condition.
Et s’il avient as os dou piet brisure, et tu vois ces os sormonter l’un l’autre, si mette si malaides som piet sus la terre, ausi com s’il voloit aler, et puis met maintenant ton piet sus lou sien, lai ou li os sont levez, puis le presse tant k’il reveignent en lor leus; puis met l’emplaustre et estoupes sus, et met desoz lou ventre dou piet une petite tauble a II chiés plains, puis l’estraint au piet avenanment, puis que tu as envoloupez drapelz entor, et autres choses dont tu as mestier.	If there is a break in the foot bone, and you see these bones overlap each other, then put this man down on the ground as if he wanted to walk, and then now put your foot on its side, lifting up the bones as they go back into their places; then apply plaster and wrap it up, and tie with rope around the navel of the foot, and also put a flat stone on top of the foot, and then fasten him to the foot in this way, and then you have wrapped sheets around him, and other things that you need.
Et quant III jors ou IIII seront passez, si deslie lou liien, car tu troveras les os igalz, soient brisiez, soient desaluez.	And when three days or four are passed, then unclasp him, because you will find the bones even if they are broken or out of place.
Et s’il i a aucuns des dois brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as dois de la main; puis met au doi brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou doi, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a II ou III, ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun doi une estele selonc sa quantiteit, envoloupee en I drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.	Et s’il i a aucuns des deux brisiez, si les restoure, si com nos avons dit as deux de la main; puis met au deux brisiet une estele selonc la longesce dou deux, et soit un poc plus large, puis met desoz le piet celle tauble que j’ai dit, et l’estrain avenanment; et s’il en i a II ou III, ou plus, brisiez, si met sus chescun deux une estele selonc sa quantitude, envoloupee en I drapeil de lin, et estraint la tauble desoz lou piet; et soit estans sus lou chief de la tauble defuer lou ventre dou piet, si qu’il le teigne bien.
Et covient que tu n’oblier mie les autres choses que j’ai dit as autres briseures, des que nos avons dit; et secor chescun accident si com il covient.	And it is necessary that you do not forget the other things that I have said about other breakers, as we have said; and assist each accident as it should be.
de la brisure de l’os dou poignil	of the break of the bone with a blunt knuckle
Quant li os de la nature la femme est brisiez, si la fai seoir enlargie, puis l’encline a la partie dou dos, et soit tenue par derrier; puis emplisse li baile la nature de la malaide de couton, et en i mette ausi gros com I sto; puis deboute la femme, et lieve lou dos poc et poc, et adonques saut li coton, tant qu’il vient a l’entree de la nature, et revient li os avec lou sto; et quant elle vuet pissier, si oste lou coton, et quant elle a pissiet, se li remette, et ensi faice VII jors ou entor: si sera restoree li brisure, et se tu vues, pren une vessie de berbis, et lie au pertus une cainne, et boute toute la vessie en la nature; puis soffle en la cainne forment, tant que li vessie soit enflee dedens: la nature si revenra li brisure; puis soit emplie de coton, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit sanez.	When the bone of nature is broken in two, then if the woman is set down enlarged, then she is inclined to the part of the back, and held behind; then the bail is filled with cotton of the disease, and as much as it stands, then she is turned on her back, and little by little pulls at the cotton until it comes into the entry of nature, and brings the bone with it; and when she urinates, if she holds the cotton, and when she has finished urinating, then let it be put away, and so do for seven days or more: so will the break be healed, and death will be prevented. Take a bladder of goat, and tie a cord to the navel, and squeeze all the bladder into nature; then blow into the cord forming, until the bladder is gone inside: nature will then return the break; then let it be filled with cotton, and left like that for several days, until it is healed.
Et quant li os dou poignil de l’ome est brisiez, ou de la femme, si le restoure ensi com nos avons dit en l’os de la hainche; et ne sont mie occultees ces briseures prochienes a celui qui i met son estude et son us, et entent mon livre.	And when the jaw of the man or woman is broken, if it is set back in the same way as we have described for the hip bone; and these breaks are not hidden from him who sets them and uses them, and hears my book.
Car li brisure li signifie em plusors dispositions la droite voie de la restauration: enten le donques.	For the break means many things in the right way of restoration: hear it then.
En la verge, quant elle est brisie, pren une gorge d’oie et i boute la verge; puis envoloupe drapelz entor, et le laisse III jors ou enqui entor, et il sera sanez hastanment.	In the throat, when it is broken, take an goose's neck and pour the juice of the throat; then wrap up drapels around, and leave them for three days or so, and they will be healed without surgery.
de brisure avec plaie	with break with wound
Il covient a celui qui a brisure avec plaie, meismement s’elle est grans, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire ou semblant, qu’il soit sainiez maintenant, si que les sainies que nos avons dit le tesmoignent.	It is appropriate for the one who has broken with a wound, even if it is great, as with the hip bone or shoulder blade or similar, that he be healed now, so that the healers that we have described testify to this.
Et se li plaie saine, si la restainche de vitriole, se tu n’as autre chose, puis rencomence a restorer la briseure en cele meisme houre, ou celui jor, se apostemes chaus n’i vient.	And if the wound heals well, if the vitriol scar remains, then you should continue to restore the rupture in that very same hour, or else the blisters will come on that day.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si laisse la restauration jusc’a nuevime jor, tant que li apostemes soit apaisiez, et n’i touchier ne au tier jor ne au quart, car tu i feroies venir malvais accident.	And if the blisters come on, and you postpone the restoration until the next day, as long as the blisters are calm, and do not touch them either on the third or fourth day, for you will bring about a bad accident.
Et se li os brisiez est aparans sus lou keur descovert, si covient que tu lou mettes a point legierement a tes mains, a extension petite.	And if the broken bone is protruding through the skin, it is necessary that you bring the bone to a standstill lightly with your hands, with a small extension.
Et se li extensions ne t’est apareillie por mettre igal a tes mains, si le ramoine a cest estrument qui est de fer, qui a VII dois ou VIII de lonc, et li largesce est selonc la quantiteit de la plaie; et por ceu est mestier au mire qu’il empreigne III ou IIII, selonc ceu qu’il en ait mestier en chescune cure de briseure; et soit rons et un poc gros, k’il ne ploie mie a la compression sus lou membre a ton ovraige, et soit agus devant, et gros des le mileu en avant, ensi:	And if the extensions are not equal to your hands, take this tool made of iron, which has seven or eight inches in length, and its width is according to the quantity of the wound; and for as much as it is necessary to employ the more or less according to each cure of the rupture; and be round and a little thick, so that it does not press on the member at your work, and be sharp in front and thick in the middle, thus:
Et est apelez «palainche», por coi il covient que li chiés corbes soit mis sus lou chief de l’os apparent; et le boute a une fois, tant k’il reviegne, et soit igalz l’un encontre l’autre.	And is called "palanquin", because it is necessary that the curved shoulders be placed on top of the head of the bone that appears; and is turned over once, as long as it comes back, and is equal on one side to the other.
Et se li brisure est subtilz, et li estrumens ne puet bien prendre l’os, si covient que tu copes lou chief de l’os, tant que li estrumens en ait possance.	And if the fracture is subtle and the tool cannot take the bone well, it is necessary that you cope with the head of the bone as long as the instrument has the ability to do so.
Et se tu ne pues ramener l’os, si com nos avons dit, si lou cope d’un estrument covenable a ceu, ou incisoire ou soieure, a ton pooir; puis reis ceu qui est demorez en l’os d’aspreteit et de menues escorces.	And if you cannot bring back the bone as we have said, if the coping of an appropriate tool, or chisel or file, is beyond your power; then resect what remains of the bone with roughness and small scrapings.
Et quant li os est ramenez, et li malaides sent grant dolor aprés, saiches qu’il n’est mie en son leu natureil.	And when the bone is brought back and the patient feels great pain afterwards, know that it is not in its natural position.
Si fai tant qu’il soit en son leu, puis moille I drapeil en vin stiptique noir, et proprement se c’est en esteit; et ne mettre mie sus la plaie cerote ne autre chose ou il ait oile, qu’il n’i faice venir porriture et corruption; puis aministre esteles quant tu as restoreit l’os, et laisse la plaie descoverte, et cope la coverture tout entor, selonc la quantiteit de la plaie, et te done bien en garde que li plaie ne soit estrainte avec la brisure; et maintes fois ont ce fait li fol mire, et ont fait venir sus le malaide ou mort ou corrodent aucune fois; et soit li estrignemens plus molz et plus souef des autres brisures.	If it is still in its place, then moisten the wound with wine-based black tar and keep it clean; do not put on any ointment or other oil on it, lest it cause pus and corruption; then administer salves when you have restored the bone, leaving the wound uncovered, and cover it all around with a covering according to the size of the wound, and be sure that the wound is not constricted with the break; and many times this has happened, and has brought about death or corruption in the patient, and these injuries are softer and less painful than those from other breaks.
Et se li plaie est male ou grans, et tu doutes que mavais accidens n’i veigne, si com nos avons dit, et tu trueves dolor au leu, si n’i covient mie mettre sus esteles; mais envoloupe entor, en leu d’esteles, drapelz durs, et les lie.	If the wound is bad or large and you doubt that a good accident will not come, as we have said, and you feel pain in the place, then it is not good to put on stitches; but wrap it tightly, instead of stitches, with hard cloths, and tie them.
Et quant tu vois aprés I jor ou II enjanrer bowe a la plaie, si oste ceu que tu as mis sus a tout vin, et i met oignement sanant plaies, si com oignement tetrafarmaçon et semblans.	And when you see after one or two days to have been infected the wound, if he is there that you put on top of all water, and I put poultices healing wounds, so as poultice tetrafarmacion and similar.
Et covient que tu deslies lou membre II fois le jor, lou matin et au vespre, tant qu’il soit soudez et sanez.	And it is necessary that you dislocate the limb twice a day, in the morning and in the evening, until it is healed and sound.
Et covient que li membres soit aparilliez en teil maniere que li bowe corre aval legierement.	And it is necessary that the limbs are moved so that the wound runs down lightly.
Et se maint jor trespassent, et il ne puet souder mais rent adés bowe, saiches k’il i a petites pieces d’os, por coi il covient que tu quieres la plaie avec tente, et oste toutes ces pieces desevrees que font venir celle dolor.	And if every day passes, and it cannot be joined but runs together again, knowing that there are small pieces of bone; because it is necessary that you wash the wound with water, and all these troublesome pieces that bring about pain.
Et se fistule vient au leu, ou autre maniere de corruption, si covient que tu le cures, selonc ceu qu’il dist en son chapistre ci devant.	And if a fistula comes to light, or any other kind of corruption, it is necessary that you cure it, according to what he says in his chapter above.
Et quant li os est brisiez, et apert sus lou membre, si com li os de la cuixe ou de l’ajutoire, et autres semblans des grans membres, si ne le traire mie, car maintes fois en vient li mors, mais le laisse tant qu’il porrisse; par aventure cherra par lui aprés XX jors ou XXX, puis cure la plaie, se tu pues; et se tu ne pues, si la laisse.	And when the jaw is broken and opened up on the side of the member, as the jawbone of a cow or a shoulder, and other large members, do not pull it out, for many times death comes, but leave it until it putrids; perhaps after twenty days or thirty, then cure the wound, if you can; and if you cannot, then leave it.
des brus qui vienent sor la sodure	the bruses that come from the sudore
Nous vienent maintes fois aprés la santeit de la briseure, meismement quant c’est pres de la jointure, et laide chose est a veoir li figure dou membre; et par aventure ne puet faire li membres ses ovraiges naturelz.	come often after the health of the break, especially when it is near the joint, and it is an ugly sight to see the member's form; and perhaps cannot make the member's natural movements.
Pren warde donques se li nous est fres: si li aministre medicines stiptiques, si com aloes, encens, et mirre, et sarcocolle, acaice, et semblans autres, ensi que tu preignes aucune de ces choses, ou toutes ensamble, et les confit avec vin stiptique ou avec abun d’uef ou avec aisil; et les met sus le nout en estoupes, et l’estraint bien, et ne la desliier en mains jors; et puis la desloie, et rencomence une autre, tant que li nodations soit ostee; ou tu estrain sus une piece de plonc bien faite; car li proprietez dou plonc si est qu’il oste toutes les enfleures desus les membres; et se li nodation est ja convertie en durteit ausi com piere, et il est besoing de l’oster, si la cope desus, et fent la superfluiteit apparent; ou tu la reis a aucun raseur, tant qu’ele soit ostee, et la cure tant qu’ele soit sanee.	Take care then if we are broken: if we administer stipitive medicines, as aloes, incense, myrrh, and sarcacoll, ash, and others; so that you do not use any of these things, or all together, and confound them with wine of stippet, or with much urine or with honey; and put them on the wound in piles, and bind them well, and do not remove them for many days; and then loosen them, and begin again, as long as the nodules are hard; or you tie them to a piece of linen well made; for the property of linen is that it hardens all swelling on the limbs; and if the nodule has become hard like stone, it needs to be cut off, if the excess is removed, and the appearance made apparent; or you take it to any barber, as long as it is hard, and cure it until it is well.
dou membre qui est foibles aprés la garison	the member which is weak after the garrison
Quant li brisure de l’os est restoree, et demoure aprés li membres foibles et subtilz, si avient por mout de causes: de coi l’une est por ceu qu’il fut liiez trop estroit, et ne fut mie liiez si com il covenoit; ou por ceu qu’il i ot trop de liiens, et ne pooit venir li norrissemens au membre; ou por multitude d’arosement; ou por trop grans movements, ne mie en son houre; ou por ceu qu’il a poc de sanc en son cors, si est foibles.	When the fracture of the bone is healed, and there remains after the weak and thin limbs, for many reasons: because one is too tightly bound, and was not bound as it should be; or because he had too many ties, and could not bring the member's movements into line; or because of many inflammations; or because of great movements, not at the right time; or because he has little blood in his body, so is weak.
Et li cure si est que tu faices mengier le malaide, et faire le cors tendre, tant que li sans soit multipliiez en lui; et li aministre bain, et li done joie et liesce; puis met poix sus le membre, si que li poix atraie a li grant norrissement, et l’arose sovent d’aigue tede, tant que li norrissement corre au membre; et reviegne a sa figure natureil.	And the cure is that you make the patient eat, and make the body flexible, so that the blood increases within him; and give him baths, and give him pleasure and rest; then put poultice on the member, so that the poultice attracts a lot of moisture, and rinse it often with warm water, until the moisture corrects the limb's movement; and return it to its natural shape.
dou membre tort aprés la santeit	two injured limbs after surgery
Quant li membres est tors aprés la restauration, et li os brisiez apert, et li forme dou membre est laide, toutevoie ne pert mie son ovraige natureil: si ne croire mie les folz qui dient c’on doit brisier lou membre tout de noveil, et maint fol mire ont ce fait en nostre terre; et cist ovraiges est blamez, et en vient grans malz, et par aventure li mors; toutevoie, se li nodations et li torture sont fres, si covient k’il soient arosez d’aigue chaude, ou herbes mollifians soient cuites, si com foilles de vismalve, et racines, et mellilote, et semblans choses; et li fai I emplaustre mollificatif, si com dyaquilon bien fait, et tu pren le muscillaige de vismalve, et la confit avec graisse de geline ou oile de sisament, et fai emplaustre sus; ou tu pren figues graisses, et les broie avec fien de colon, et semblans medicines que amenuisent le soudement.	When the limbs are twisted after restoration, and the bone is broken open, and the form of the limb is ugly, nevertheless it does not lose its natural function: do not believe the foolish who say that the limb must be broken again from new, and many foolish people have done this in our land; and these practices are blamed, and great harm and perhaps death result; however, if the nodules and torments are fresh, it is good that they be soaked in warm water, or cooked herbs are softened, as foils of whale blubber, and roots, and melilot, and similar things; and the mold with a softening substance, such as well-made dye, and you take musk from whale blubber, and confound it with linseed oil or sesame oil, and make a mold; or you take fatty figs, and grind them with hay of colza, and similar medicines that soften the stiffness.
Et aucune fois est ostee li nodacion por froter continuelment et longement a mains moistes.	And never is the osteum rubbed constantly and lengthily with moist hands.
Et soit amenistrez movement au membre chescune houre.	So that each limb is moved every hour.
Et se li tortuositez est enveillie et endurcie, ausi com piere, et besoins est de l’oster au fer, si la covient coper jusc’a l’os, a l’incisoire subtil legierement; et mettre cusenson et estude en la cure.	And if the limb becomes twisted and hardened, as in stone, then it must be sharpened with a sharp edge, covering the bone, cutting with a slight stroke; and put on ointment and study for the cure.
Ci encomence li livres des dislocations	Here begins the book of dislocations:
Dislocations est issue d’aucune jointe de son leu, por coi il ne se puet muevre, et est li membres mal figurez, et sent li malaides grant dolor et grant lesion.	Dislocation occurs when a joint moves out of its place, which prevents it from moving, and the limb is misaligned, causing the patient great pain and injury.
Quant dislocation vient a aucun, si le covient maintenant ramener sens targier.	When dislocation comes to anyone, if it is now brought back gently.
Car s’on tarde, si enfle li leus, et par aventure si le remet on a poines au leu; por ceu ne covient mie c’on le mueve a l’oure k’il est enflez: maintes fois fait venir spame et autres dolors; toutevoie, quant ce avenra, si fai sainier lou malaide, puis le laisse, tant que li apostemes chas soit apaisiez; puis arose le membre d’aigue chaude et d’oile, puis le ramoinne legierement, et cure chescun membre si com li cure venra en son leu.	For if one is delayed, and the joints swell, and perhaps he is again put in place at his joint; for thus it will not move when taken out: many times causes swelling and other pains; however, when this has come, if one makes the patient well, then leave him, until the abscesses are calmed; then raise the member with warm water and oil, then gently move it again, and cure each member as the cure comes.
Et j’ai ordenez les chapistres des dislocations des lou chief jusc’a piez.	And I have ordered the potions for the dislocations of the shoulders just up to the height of the piez.
des mandibules	of the mandible
Poc avient que les mandibules soient desaluees andous, et li dislocations d’ambedous est selonc II manieres: ou elles sont un poc ostees de lor leus, et mollifies un poc; ou elles sont desaluees entierement, et pendent vers lou pis, et cort li salive de la bouche qu’il ne la puet tenir, ne ne puet clore sa bouche, et envoloupe sa langue avec la parole.	and dislocations of both are according to two ways: where they are a little out of place and stiff; or where they are completely dislocated, hanging down toward the loins, and the saliva of the mouth flows off because he cannot hold it, nor can he close his mouth, and wraps his tongue with speech.
Quant li dislocations est petite, si revient par li em plusors disposicions.	When the dislocation is small, return by means of these four dispositions.
Et s’elle est entiere et acomplie, si covient que tu la ramoinne hastanment, et ne targier mie; et en tel maniere que li ministres teigne le chief dou malaide, et boute li mires som pochet de l’une de ses mains en la racine de la dislocation de la mandibule dedens la bouche, se li dislocations est de II pars; et li autre doi des mains soient defuer, por mettre igal; et comande au malaide qu’il les amollisse, ses mandibules, et les mueve de toutes pars.	And if it is whole and complete, then you must reset it promptly, without procrastination; and in such a way that the minister holding the head of the sick person, pours a little potion from one of his hands at the root of the dislocation of the jaw inside the mouth, this dislocation being of two parts; and the other two hands should be away, so as to make it even; and command to the patient that he softens his mandibles, and moves them in all directions.
Et li mires la mete igal, tant qu’elle reveigne en son leu.	And let the wound heal evenly, until it returns to its place.
Et se li ramener est griés, meismement se ce sont les II mandibules ensamble, si les arose d’aigue chaude et d’oile, tant que les ramoinnes legierement; ne ne targier mie dou ramener, si com nos avons dit.	And let them be brought together gently, especially if the two mandibles are separated; then let them be ramined with hot water and oil, lightly at first; do not tarry in bringing them together, as we have said.
Et quant elles sont ramenees igalment, et li bouche dou malaide clot bien sens mollifiier, si met sus drapelz moilliez en cerote fait d’oile roset et de cire, puis le lie legierement de molz liiens; et dorme li malaides sus son dos, et ses chiés soit estans entre II cussins, si qu’il ne lou mueve ne a destre ne a senestre, ne ne s’efforce mie de maixier, mais preigne legiere viande, tant que les dolors soient ostees, et soient noees les mandibules; et puis menjuce ce qu’il vuet legierement, et ne se travaille mie d’ovrir la bouche au mengier et au boivre, tant que li mandibule soit bien noee et sanee.	And when they have been brought together evenly, and the mouth of the sick person is closed well with a softening agent, put it on drapings wetted with an ointment made of oil and wax, then gently bind them; and let the patient lie on his back, and his cheeks be placed between two pillows so that he cannot move or force himself to open or close his mouth, but eat lightly, until the pains are relieved and the mandibles are healed and sound. And then allow him to eat and drink easily, and do not worry about opening the mouth for eating or drinking, unless the mandible is well healed and sound.
Et se les II mandibules ne pueent estre remises a point a une houre, et ne sont mie converties a lor leus, si en vient fievres et sode acostumees, et par aventure solution de ventre, et par aventure vomist cole pure.	And if the two jaws cannot be put back in place within an hour and do not return to their places, then fever and abnormal sweating will come, and by chance there will be a solution of the stomach, and by chance vomiting of clear bile.
Et quant tu verras ceu, adonc saiches que c’est perdicions; et maintes fois muert cil cui il avient, en VIIII jors.	And when you see this, then know that it is a loss; and many times he who has it dies in nine days.
de la forcelle	of the fork
Li forcele ne puet desaluer dou costeit dedens la continuation de li et dou pis, et est desaluee aucune fois au defuer, et bien le sent on.	does not release from the coast within the extension of the thread inside it, and is dislocated only once at the back, and one feels it well.
Et li restauration si est que li malaides gise sovin sor son dos, et estende ses bras; et puis presse le leu forment a ta palme, et elle revenra; puis met sus l’emplaustre et lou bendeil, et l’estraint; et li chiez qui est devers lou coute ne puet desaluer; se poc non, et se il desalue aucune fois, si le ramoinne a son leu, si com nos avons dit; puis met sus l’emplaustre et le bendeil, et l’estraint, et coumande au malaide qu’il se repose tant qu’il soit sanez; et ensi meisme est ramenez li chiés de l’espale, quant il est desevrez de son leu.	And the restoration is such that the patient lies down on his back, and extends his arms; then press the head in your palm, and it will return; then put on plaster and bandage, and bind it; and the chin, which is toward his head, cannot be released; if not, and if it is dislocated once, then you bring it back to its place as we have said; then put on plaster and bandage, and bind it, and order the patient to rest until he is well; and thus is brought back the head of the shoulder when it has been dislocated from its place.
de la dislocation de l’espaule	of the dislocation of the shoulder
Saiches que li espaule n’est desaluee fuer que selonc III manieres: de coi l’une est qu’ele desalue a la partie de l’assele au desoz; et li seconde est a la partie dou pis; et par aventure desalue a la partie desus, et ceu avient poc; et ne desalue mie derrier por l’espaule, et ne desalue mie dedens por les ners; et plusors fois desalue desoz vers l’assele, meismement a ces qui ont poc de char, car a ces saut ele fuer hastanment; a ces qui ont assez char, saut ele a poines, et rentre a poines.	Because we know that the shoulder can only be dislocated in three ways: either it is pushed out of its axis; or to the side of the breastbone; and perhaps it can also be pushed from above, and this happens rarely; nor should it ever be pushed behind the shoulder, or into the back, because many times it will require hospitalization if done so; but those who have enough strength, they push them a little and let them go.
Et par aventure avient a aucuns homes percussion ou casseure, et enfle li espaule d’un aposteme chaut, et cuide qu’elle est desaluee par ceu.	And perhaps it happens to some men that they beat or break, and the shoulder is heated by a hot abscess, and they think that it has been dislocated.
Il covient donques que tu l’esprueves, tant que tu en soies certains; et adonques encomence la cure.	So you must first test this out, until you are certain of it; and then begin the treatment.
Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desaluee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.	Et est conue li dislocations quant il est aval vers l’assele, et met difference entre l’espaule malade et la saine, et tu troveras entre lor diversiteit manifeste; et troveras au chief de l’espaule une fosse, et desoz l’assele au tochier le chief de l’espaule, ausi com se ce soit uns oes; et ne puet li malaides ramener sa main a son neis, ne movoir de nulz movemens; et ausi, s’elle est desalee en haut, si n’est mie occultee, car tu le trueves manifestement au tochier; et ceste maniere de dislocation n’est mie fors a ramener, quant elle est novele, ou se li enfes est malaides.
Et li maniere est que li ministres lieve la main dou malaide en haut, puis met tes peuchas desoz l’assele, et lieve la jointure a force en haut au leu; et li ministres lieve la main, et l’estende en haut, pues le mette desoz; si venra hastanment.	And the manner is that the ministers lift up the sick hand upwards, then put on the splint, and fit the joint firmly upwards to its place; and the ministers lift up the hand, and extend it upwards, and put it back; so comes about soon.
Et s’elle ne vient si com nos avons dit em mains jors aprés, si covient ke li malaides soit baigniez en aigue chaude; et li amenistre arosement mollifiant et assouajant, si com decoction de altee et de fenugrec et de mellilote en aigue, et soit amenistree; puis soit sovinez li malaides sus son dos, et mette on desoz l’assele un sto de lainne igal, ne trop mol ne trop dur, puis mette li mires son talon sus le sto, et lieve le chief de l’espaule vertuousement, et traie la main dou malaide; et uns autres ministres teigne lou chief dou malaide, si qu’il ne se mueve aval; celle espaule revient tout maintenant, et se tu vues si le ramoinne selonc ceste maniere: et est que tu faices estre present I home qui soit plus grans que li malaides; et soit drois devers lou costeit, et boute s’espaule desoz l’assele dou malaide, et lieve l’assele en haut, si que li malaides pende en l’ar; et uns autres ministres traie la main dou malaide aval devers lou ventre.	And if it does not come as we have said, on the days of your hands after, it is appropriate that the patient be bathed in warm water; and provide softening and soothing poultices, as with decoction of althaea and fenugreek and melilote in water, and are applied; then let the patient be supported on his back, and take off the shoulder rest one by another leg like this, not too soft or too hard, then put the mirror his heel on the rest, and gently lift the shoulder with care, and pull the hand of the patient; and provide other ministers to dye the head of the patient, so that it does not move down; that shoulder returns now, and you will see if you bring it back this way: and it is that you make a present of a man who is greater than the patient; and stand face-to-face with his side, and bottle should the shoulder rest of the patient, and lift the rest up, so that the patient hangs in the air; and provide other ministers to pull the hand of the patient down towards his belly.
Et se li malaides est trop legiers, si pent avec lui aucune chose pesant, et li dislocation revient maintenant.	And if the patient is too light, then with him put something heavy, so that the dislocation comes back now.
Et le ramoinne on ausi en autre maniere: et est c’on fiche I lonc tison en terre, dont li chiés soit ausi reons com I pistal, et ne soit ne trop gros ne trop graile; puis soit mis desoz lou malaide, mais k’il ait drapelz souef sus, et li malaides soit estans dou lonc dou fust; puis soit estendue sa main aval d’autre part forment, et li jointure revenra en son leu hastanment; et s’elle ne vuet revenir por toutes ces choses que nos avons dit, si fai ceste cure: pren I tison de II bras de grant et IIII dois de large, qui ait le chief reont por mues entrer em parfont desoz l’assele, selonc ceste forme:	And let it be that if the patient is too light, then with him put something heavy, so that the dislocation comes back now. And the way to do this is: and let there be placed a long piece of wood in the earth, whose shoulder is also reason as a pistol, and is not too large or too small; then the dislocated person should lie on the long pole's head; then let his hand be extended down from another part forming, and the joint will return to its place safely; and if it does not come back because of all these things that we have said, then do this cure: take a piece of wood of II arms of great and IIII fingers wide, which has the head reont so as to perfectly enter into the assembly, according to this form:
puis lie sus le chief dou fust drapelz souez, que li fust ne blece lou malaide, puis le met desoz l’assele dou malaide; et estende som bras sus le fust dou lonc, et lie l’ajutoire sus le fust, et lou bras au chief de la main, puis met le bras sus I eschillon d’une eschiele dou large, et soit estendue li mains aval, et soit laissiez li cors pendans d’autre part: li jointure reva ens maintenant.	Then lie on the chest down windless furrows, so that the patient does not hurt himself, then put it in order the apparatus of the patient; and extends his arms on the bar long, and puts the aid on the bar, and his arm at the head of the hand, then places the arm on a grindstone of a wheel large, and let be extended hands down, and let hang the body from the other part: the jointure has now come.
Et quant elle est ens, en quel maniere que ce soit, si covient que tu mettes desoz l’assele une spere de laine igal, puis met l’emplaustre aparilliet de poudre dou molin, avec encens et aubun d’uef, sus toute l’espaule et entor, puis l’estrain desoz l’assele avenanment, et torne le liien sus l’emplaustre, et embraice la main a son col, et soit li mains demorans ensi.
