Then when it is in place, in whatever way it may be, you must put an even woolen needle, then set the plaster ready with powder from the mill, with incense and amber, on the whole shoulder and innards, then draw it away forward, and tie it to the plaster, and embrace the hand at its neck, and let your hands remain in this way.
Et covient qu’il menjuce poc, tant que li membres soit confortez, car il sanera plus tost; et puis menjuce plus aprés V jors ou VII, et le mueve; et s’il est fermeis et il n’est mollifiez, si est sanez.	And it is necessary that he drink a little while the members are comfortable, for he will heal faster; and then drink more after 5 or 7 days and move them; and if they are hard and have not become softened, then they are healed.
Et se li jointure est fuer de leu por moistor que i est venue, ou por autre cause, si covient que tu i aministres cauteres a III pertus, si com il est mis devant ou chapistre des cauteres.	And if the joint has come out of its place due to moisture that has come or due to some other cause, you must apply cauterization three times, as it is done with the paste of cauterization.
Et se tu fais tout ceu, et il deslie aprés VII jors, et li jointure ne se tient, et ne puet lever som bras amont, adonc saiches que li nerf au chief de l’espaule sont copeit ou estendut ou amollis; et saiches que li jointure n’iert jamais fichie en son leu.	And if you do all this, and it slides after 7 days, and the joint does not hold, and cannot raise its arm upward, then know that the nerve in the shoulder is torn or stretched or softened; and know that the joint has never been put back in its place.
Li dislocation qui est devers lou pis, et les mameles, ou derrier, si est faite par impulsion, et estendement de mains, et i aministre on autre lieure; et cure tant qu’il soit sanez.	The dislocation that is near the loins and the breasts, or behind, is done by impact, and by spreading of the hands, and I apply another place; and I treat as long as it is healed.
Et se aprés la sanation vient grietez au membre, et tardemens em movement, si use li malaides bain maintes fois, tant que celle grietez soit alegie, et reviegne a sa premiere nature.	And if after healing comes to the limb greasiness, and slowly moving, then the patient often bathes, until that greasiness is gone, and returns to its first nature.
de la dislocation dou coute	of the dislocation of the head
Saiches que li jointure dou coute est desaluee a poinnes, et a poinnes revient; et s’est desaluee de toutes pars, et meismement devant et derrier, et li dislocations n’est mie reponue, car on la voit bien et sent bien; et desalue selonc chescune figure.	I understand that the joint of the shoulder is dislocated to such an extent that it returns to its original position again and again; and if it is dislocated from all sides, especially in front and behind, and the dislocation is not reset, for we can see it and feel it clearly; and let it be dislocated according to each figure.
Et quant tu joins le coute malaide avec lou sain, si le pues veoir apertement.	And when you join the dislocated shoulder with good health, if you can see it openly.
Car li jointure est chevee, et ne puet ploier lou bras, ne touchier son espaule a tout.	For the joint is deformed, and cannot bend the arm, nor touch its shoulder at all.
Et covient que tu le ramoinnes ainsois que apostemes chaus i viegne, car se apostemes chaus i venoit, si seroit grief li ramener; et par aventure ne puet estre ramenez dou tout en tout, meismement quant ele est au derrier; si vaut pis que les autres dislocations, et est de plus grant dolor, et par aventure i vient li mors.	And it is necessary that you reset it as if an abscess were coming out, because if an abscess comes out, then it would be painful to bring it back; and perhaps it cannot be brought back from all sides at all, especially in the rear; so much so that it is more painful than other dislocations, and sometimes leads to death.
Et li restauration si est, quant elle est telz c’on la puet ramener, que tu li estendes sa main a tes II mains; et ses bras soit espandus, et les mains dou mire selonc le coute entor, desor et desoz, et boute la jointure a ses peuchas ensamble, ou a la racine de sa palme, tant qu’ele reviegne a son leu.	And the recovery is, when it is such that one can bring it back, that you extend its hand to your two hands; and let its arms be spread out, and the hands reach along the wrist, behind and before, and pull the joint together with its little fingers, or at the root of its palm, until it regains its place.
Et se li dislocations est au devant, si revient quant il double sa main a sa main, et fier de la racine de la palme lou coute qui est desaluez.	And if the dislocations are in front, so that when it doubles its hand to its other hand, and raises its wrist, it returns to its place.
Et s’il ne vuet revenir au leu, si aministre fort extension; et est que dui ministre estendent le bras, et le teignent dui ministre, si qu’il ne se mueve a l’estension; puis torne le bras de chescune part, puis que tu as envoloupeit un drapeil double lonc et large; et quant li mires a jointe la jointure a sa main, si l’oigne d’aucun oile por amolir la jointure, puis boute la jointure forment, tant qu’ele reviegne; et quant elle est au leu, si met sus emplaustre sec avec aubun d’uef, et l’estrain forment, et pent le bras au col dou malaide, et le laisse aucuns jors, puis le deslie.	And if it does not return to its place, so that you administer a strong extension; and it is that the two extend the arm, and tie them together, so that it does not move with the extension; then turn the arm of each part, then that you have wrapped a double long and wide cloth; and when you see the joint joined to its hand, so that you rub it with any oil to soften the joint, then pull the joint in shape, until it regains its place; and when it is in place, put it on dry plaster with a bit of ointment, and strain it firmly, and bend the arm at the neck of the patient, and leave it for some days, then release it.
Et se li jointure est ferme en son leu, si deslie lou liien, et le laisse; et se tu vois que li jointure n’estrigne bien, si rencomence l’emplaustre et lou lien, et le laisse ensi aucuns jors, tant qu’il soit fermement mis; puis le deslie.	And if the joint is secure in its place and loosens it and lets it be; and if you see that the joint is not well set, then re-cast the plaster and the bond and let it be for some days, as long as it is securely placed; then remove it.
Et se il sent grieteit aprés le ramenement de la jointe, et elle se muet, si le baigne et frote bellement, et presse tant qu’il soit assouagiez; ou tu met sus la jointure une naige de mouton grasse, puis la laisse I jor et une nuit, puis l’oste, et lou fai entrer ou bain; et quant il sue, se li frote la jointure tempreement, puis remet la naige sus, et puis entre ou bain; et ensi fai II fois ou III, tant qu’il soit sanez; et se tu vues, si met sus fien de vaiche moiste chaufeit avec burre, et l’estrain sus; si revenra a sa disposition.	And if he feels pain after the resetting of the joint, and it moves, then bathe and gently rub, and press until it is relieved; or put on the joint a thin layer of greasy sheep's wool, then leave it for a day and a night, then remove it, and let it enter or bathe; and when it sweats, gently rub the joint, then put the wool back on, and then go in or bathe; and do this twice or three times until it is well; and if you see, put on a thin layer of hot sheep's wool, and draw it on; then return to its position.
li dislocation de la main	the dislocation of the hand
Li jointure de la main desalue, et li revenue est legiere, plus que les autres jointures Toutevoie, il la covient ramener au leu hastanment, en l’oure meisme qu’ele est desaluee, ainsois que li leus soit enflez, ou qu’il i viegne aposteme chaut.	the dislocation of the hand is released, and its return is lighter than that of other joints However, it is necessary to bring it back to its place as soon as it is released, so that the joint is swollen or there comes an abscess.
Et li ramenemens si est que tu mettes la main malaide sus une tauble, et estende li ministres la main, et li mires la mette igal, ensi que il mette sa paume sus l’aparance de la jointure, et la boute tant qu’elle reviegne Toutevoie, il covient que vos regardez s’il est bien a leu; adonc mette li malaides lou dos de sa main sus une tauble a l’estension et au ramenement.	And when you bring it back, put the sick hand on a table, and spread out the fingers, and make it equal, so that its palm faces the joint, and hold it like this until it comes back into place; then look to see if it is well in place: then put the patient's hand flat on the table at rest and at return.
Et se li dislocations est au dos de la main, si mette li malaides son dos de sa main sus la tauble, et li mires mette sa main sus cele apparance de la jointure.	If the dislocation is at the back of the hand, then put the patient's hand flat on the table and bring it to rest: then look to see if it is well in place;
S’elle revient maintenant, c’est bien Se ce non, si l’estrain d’emplaustres apaisans apostemes chaus, et lou laisse ensi sens rencomencier.	If it returns now, that is good; but if not, if the extraction of pus from abscesses is painful, and he leaves in this way with pain.
Et s’il ne le puet soffrir, et tu ne la pues mettre au leu aprés aucuns jors, si demore li jointure torte; et ne nuist niant au malaide fuer que tant que li mains est amoillie, et ne puet estraindre aucune chose a tout: adonc saiches que li nerf sont copez, ou li artere; si n’i a autre engien fuer que d’estraindre par cautere delez le cas, et par aventure n’i vaut autre chose.	If he cannot bear it, and you cannot put it back in place after some days, if the joint is twisted; and there is no benefit to the patient except that his hands are wet, and he cannot extract anything at all: then you know that the nerves are cut, or an artery; otherwise, you have only the option of extracting by a fire cautery, and perhaps there is nothing else.
Et quant li mains est au leu, si met sus l’emplaustre que nos avons dit, puis l’estrain et le laisse V jors, puis le deslie et laisse ensi.	When the hand is in place, put on the poultice that we have said, then extract it and leave it for V days, then take it off and leave it like this.
Et s’il ne la puet bien movoir, et il i a aucune grieteit, si la moille d’aigue chaude, et le frote tant qu’il soit sanez.	If he cannot move it well, and there is no crack, if the wet warm water, and rub until he is cured.
de la dislocation des dois de la main	of the dislocation of the two bones of the hand
Aucune fois sont desaluez li doi de la main a chescune part, aucune fois au dos de la palme ou au ventre; adonques estent le doi, et boute la dislocation a tes pouchés tant qu’il reviegne, puis sostien lou chief dou doi, et le pent vers la partie ou il est desjoins; et le laisse II jors, et puis le met igal celui jor; et de nut le lie, si com nos avons dit, et lou deslie de jor, et lou fai movoir, et le relie la nut; et fai ce sovent, tant qu’il soit estroit, et tout ausi fai, se il est desaluez au ventre de la main, et fai si com tu as fait ci devant, tant qu’il soit sanez; et tout ausi fai, quant il est desaluez d’autre part.	of the dislocation of the two bones of the hand are not dislocated at each end, nor on the back of the palm or abdomen; so they are put together, and release the dislocation to the pockets until it revives, then support the head of the two, and bend it towards the part where it is joined; and leave it there for a day, and then make it even that day; and from there he takes it off, if he has taken it off in the palm of the hand, and does so as you have done before, until it is well; and do the same thing, if it is dislocated on the other side.
dou desaluement de l’eschinee dou dos	the dislocation of the spine of the neck
Quant l’eschinee dou dos ou dou col est desaluee, ou il en i a plusors desaluees, si n’i a point de cure, car li mors haste le malaide.	When the spine or neck is dislocated, or there are several dislocations, there will be no cure, for it quickly kills the patient.
Et li signes si est que li egestions saut fuer sens volunteit, ne ne la puet tenir, et maintes fois sont mollifiez aucun membre, ou les II cuixes ou li dui bras ou I Et maintes fois se muet li eschinee a IIII pars; celle qui se muet au derrier si est apelee «gilbositez»: li cure si est que tu rewarde se li gilbositez est venue d’enfance: si n’i ait point de cure ne de sanation dou tot.	And the signs are that the injections have gone without a trace, they cannot be held, and many times the members are softened, or the II legs or the II arms or I And many times the eschinaire mutates to IIII parts; this which mutates behind is called "gilbositez": the cure is that you reward if the gilbositez has come from childhood: if there is no cure or recovery from all.
Et celle que vient de cheoir ou de percussions ou de semblans choses, dirent li ancien manieres de cures par grans paroles, ou il n’a mie en toutes grant profit; mais je l’ai abregiet selonc mon entention, et ai formez estrumens en diverses manieres.	And that which comes from sitting or percussion or similar things, the ancient ways of cure were spoken of in great words, which did not bring much good to all; but I have shortened it according to my understanding, and have formed instruments in various ways.
Je dis que en la gilbositeit que vient au pis devant, nen a engien ne santeit; et ausi cele que vient droitement en II costez, et ne puet on curer fuers que celi proprement qui vient au dos, si com je dis; et est que li malaides soit estendus sus sa faice en I leu igal, et ait de l’estrain desoz lui, qu’il ne se blece; puis fiche I tison au chief en terre forment, et I autre as piez, et lie un liien pardesoz les asseles dou malaide, et I autre as hainches, et as genous, et as chevilles; et dui ministre saichent les liiens, li uns au chief et li autres as piez, parmi les II tisons; et soient bien fermez, li tison si com nos avons dit, et li mires mette ses paumes sus l’espinee forment, tant qu’ele reviegne.	I say that in the gimblet which comes to the back of the foot before, no cure or health has been found; and also that which comes directly on both sides, and cannot be cured except properly, as I have said; it is that the sick person be laid face down in one equal place, and that there be an extraction of fluid from him so that he does not bleed; then put a piece of fire at the head in the form of a stick, and another between the toes, and tie a string behind the foot of the sick person, and another between the knees, and between the ankles; and let the two ministers tie the strings to the head and between the toes, among the two pieces of wood; and let them be well tied, the string as we have said before, and the mirror put his palms on the spine in the form, until he recovers.
Et s’elle ne revient par ceste cure, si pren une tauble de III bras de lonc, et chevé desoz la paroit, et li malaides soit en costé, et boute le chief de la tauble desoz la paroit, puis met le mileu de la tauble sus l’espinee; et mette li mires ses piez sus l’autre chief de la tauble, et presse bien, tant qu’il reviegne au leu; et se tu vues, si le fai au tornet qui torne a la main.	And if it does not return with this cure, take a table of three arms long, and shave the side, and let the patient lie down on his side, and bottle the head of the table in, then put the middle of the table on the spine; and place the fingers of the hand on the other head of the table, and press hard until it returns to its place; and if you see it, do it with a turn that comes to the hand.
Et est que tu fiches II tisons au chief dou malaide d’un bras de grant, et devers les piez II autres, et ait entre chescun tison, desoure et desoz, une paume d’espaice de lonc; et ait en chescun tison I pertus, ou li tornet corre, et soient li tison fermement en terre, si qu’il ne se muevent; et entre chescuns II tisons ait I tison tornant, sor coi li liien tornent, et ait en II tornans II petis tisons d’une paume de lonc, por torner le tornet; et puis lie lou lien qui est parmi les asseles au tornet devers le chief, et l’autre liien devers les piez a l’autre tornet, et chescuns des ministres torne son tornet a tout le liien, et li maistres mette l’espinee igal si com nos avons dit.	And this is that you fix two torches at the head of the sick person with an arm long, and place the fingers two others, and have between each torch, behind and shave, a palm of space long; and have in each torch a perforation where the twist runs, and let the torch firmly in the ground so that it does not move; and between each pair of torches have a small torch turning, so that the link turns, and have two twists with two small torches a palm long, to turn the twist; then lie down the link that is among the ashes to the twist at the head, and the other link toward the fingers on the other twist, and each minister turns his twist on all the link, and the master puts the spine even as we have said.
Et quant elle est igalz, si met sus emplaustre desiccatif avec abun d’uef, et puis les estoupes, et puis l’estele d’une tablete de III dois de lonc, que porpreigne lou leu de la gilbositeit et la partie de l’espondile sainne, puis le lie d’un liien, si com nos avons dit, et use li malaides de norrissement subtil, tant qu’il soit sanez; et s’aucune chose vient en la fin de la santez, si covient aministrer medicines amollissans et asouajans, avec l’estele que nos avons dit ci devant; et aucune fois i aministre on une piece de plonc, et aucune fois vient li apparance en la derriere spondile dou dos, et cuide on que ce soit dislocations; et c’est li os qui apert, por coi on n’i doit mie avoir presumption: par aventure feroit venir la mort.	And when it is even, put on a desiccant plaster with plenty of wax, and then the props, and then the stake of a tablet of III inches long, that redoubles his place in the gleba and the part of the spine healthy, and then the knot of a cord, as we have said, and use the patient subtlety of nutriment until he is well; and if anything comes at the end of health, then administer medicines softening and soothing, with the stake that we have said above; and never administer one piece of lead, and never does an appearance come in the posterior spine of the back, and think that this is dislocations; and that is the bone that opens, for one should not have presumption: perhaps it would bring death.
des dislocations de la hainche	Here is the translation of the text: 
Saiches que as jointures de la hainche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hainche est desaluee selonc IIII parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.	Saiches que as jointures de la hanche et as jointures de l’espaule ne vient fuers que dislocacions soulement, ne n’i vient mie si com as autres jointures; et li jointure de la hanche est desaluee selonc IIII parties: dedens et defuer ,et devant et derrier; et plus dedens c’aillors, et poc desalue devant et derrier.
Et li conoissance de sa dislocations dedens si est que quant on joint la jambe malaide avec la sainne, si est plus longe, et apert plus li malaides genous que li sains, et ne puet li malaides doubler son genoil au feu; et est li leus qui est delez enflez d’aposteme chaut, por ceu que li chiés de la cuixe vient lai.	Saiches that the hip and shoulder joints come only from dislocations, not like the other joints; and the hip joint is dislocated according to IV parts: inside and outside, and front and back; and more inside there, and a little dislocated in front and behind. And the knowledge of its dislocation inside is that when you join the leg with the pain with the healthy one, it is farther away, and more than the patient's knees than the healthy ones, and the patient cannot double his knee on fire; and this is the joint which is swollen by an abscess, for that the head of the thigh comes there.
Et li signe de celui cui il vient au defuer, si est que cist accident sont contraire a ces devant.	And the sign of him to whom it comes at death, if this accident is opposite to these before.
Et li signes de celui cui avient au devant, si est qu’il estent bien sa jambe selonc l’acomplissement; toutevoie, ne double mie le genoil sens dolor, et s’on le vuet faire aler, si ne puet avant, et retient son urine, et enfle li angre, et quant il vait, si passe sus le talon.	And the sign of him to whom it comes in front, if his leg is well according to the completion; however, do not double the knee with pain, and if you make it walk, it cannot go before, and holds back its urine, and swells the ankle, and when he walks, he goes on the heel.
Et li signes de celui cui il avient derrier, si est qu’il ne puet espandre son genoil, ne doubler, et est celle jambe plus torte de l’autre, et li angre est mollifié, et est li chiés de la cuixe au leu desoz les costes.	And the sign of him to whom it comes behind, if he cannot spread his knee, nor double it, and this leg is more twisted than the other, and the ankle is softened, and the head of the thigh is in its place between the ribs.
Li ramenemens de ceste semblance de dislocation si est que tu rewarde se li dislocations est anciainne, et elle demore selonc sa disposition, si n’i a nule cure; et n’i covient mie qu’il ait presumption.	The remendations for this dislocation if it is old, and it does not remain according to its disposition, so there is no cure; and it does not come that he has presumptiousness.
Et en celi dont li dislocation est fresche, et c’est des IIII manieres de dislocation, si te haste que tu tornes la jointe, et l’esten dedens et defuer, et la muef a destre et senestre; par aventure si revenra, et n’a mestier d’autre cure.	And in that which the dislocation is fresh, and this is of four ways that dislocation can happen, so you hurry to turn the joint, and it moves back inside and out, and turns to the right and left; by chance if it comes back, and there is no need for other treatment.
Et s’il ne revient en ceste maniere, si covient que tu apareilles I ministre fort, et esten la jambe fort a II mains, ou a I liien que soit liiez sus lou genoil; et uns autres ministres estende sa main desus en teil maniere qu’il boute ses mains desoz ses asseles, puis l’estrigne d’un souef liien sus la cuixe; et uns autres tigne lou chief dou liien; et estendent amont et aval tuit a une fois, tant que li malaide soit levez de terre a une fois, et demoure pendans.	And if it does not return in this way, then you must prepare a very strong minister, and hold the leg firmly with two hands, or tie it to a mat that is placed under the knee; and another minister extends his hand above and below at the same time, until the patient is raised from the ground once, and remains so for a while;
Ceste maniere d’estension si est commune as IIII semblances, et se li dislocation est revenue, si com nos avons dit, c’est bien.	This method of extension is common in four appearances, and if the dislocation has returned, as we have said, it is good.
Se ceu non, si covient mettre cure a sa semblance Quant li dislocations est au pardedens, si covient que tu sovines le malaide sus son costeit sain, puis met le liien sus la racine de la cuixe, et le leu qui est desoz l’angre, puis estent le liien en haut devers l’angre, et devers la forcele; puis preigne uns autres ministres ses bras, et embraice le gros leu de la cuixe malaide, et l’estende au defuer forment: si revenra a son leu maintenant; et ceste maniere de dislocation est plus legiere des autres.	If so, if it is necessary to apply cure for its appearance When the dislocations are in the garden, if you need to place the patient on their back comfortably, then put the bandage over the root of the hip, and the strap that is loosed from the ankle, then place the bandage above the ankle, and towards the forceps; then ask others to help with its arms, and embrace the large strap of the hip, and extend it to the side: now it will return to its position; and this way of dislocation is easier than the other.
Et se tu ne la pues serrer en ceste maniere que nos avons dit, si covient que tu lies les II piés dou malaide ensamble d’un fort liien souef sus les II talons, et sus les II genous, et soit li jambe malaide estendue II dois plus que li autres; puis soit pendus sus le chief d’un fust, et soit en sus de terre II bras de lonc; puis comande a I ministre qu’il embraice le chief de la cuixe, et soit uns autres ministres pendans avec le malaide, qui embraice forment la cuixe, car li jointure revient maintenant hastanment.	And if you cannot do it in this way that we have said, if you need to tie the patient's two feet together with a strong rope under their heels, and on their knees, so that the affected leg is extended more than the other; then hang them by the head from a beam, and their long arms above the ground; then order one of the ministers to embrace the root of the hip, and others to hang with the patient, who embraces the hip firmly, for the joint will now heal gradually.
Et quant li dislocations est au defuer, si gise li malaides, si com nos avons dit en celui qui a gilbositeit, et estraigne I liien sus la jambe malaide proprement, et sus le peis ausi; puis met II tisons, I au chief et I autre as piez, puis fiche I tison entre les cuixes au malaide emmi la forme; et ait plantei de drapelz moistes entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide, puis estende chescuns ministre devers lui, et li mires mette igal a sa main la dislocation.	Et when the dislocations are far away, if the patient lies down, as we have said in that which concerns giddyness, and he draws the reins properly upon the sick leg, and also upon the foot; then put two torches, one at the head and another at the feet, then place one torch between the thighs of the patient, under the form; and plant therewith wet towels around him, so that he does not burn himself, then spread out each minister on either side of him, and let the doctor put his hand like a bridge over the dislocation.
S’elle revient, c’est boin.	If it returns, it is good.
Se ce non, met sus .ie. table, et le presse ensi com nos avons dit en la gilbositeit, et gise li malaides sus le sain costeit.	If not, put him on a table, and press him as we have said in gibbosity, and make the patient lie on his sound side.
Et quant li dislocations est devant, si covient estendre la jambe malaide hastanment, et selonc ce que j’ai dit; et mette li mires sa paine d’estre sus l’angre malaide, puis presse a l’autre main, et l’estent aval devers lou genoil.	And when the dislocations are in front, if it is necessary to extend the sick leg far away, and according to what I have said; and let the doctor put his pain on the sick ankle, then press with the other hand, and draw him forward towards the knee.
Et se li dislocations est au defuer, si ne covient pas estendre le malaide aval, ne lever sus la terre, ains covient qu’il soit ausi com se li hainche estoit desaluee au defuer, si com nos avons dit dou couchement sus les II hainches; et soit sus sa faice, et li lien estendut si com nos avons dit ci devant, et doit om presser sus la jointure a la table; et sera a point quant li malaides estendra ses jambes, et elles seront igalz; adonques ajoste les cuixes, et met l’emplaustre, et l’estrain d’un bendeil, si que li hainche ne se mueve; et se repose III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie, et met l’emplaustre sus; et se tu vois qu’elles soient igalz, si l’estrain, si com devant, et le laisse III jors; puis le deslie, et lou fai aler belement, tant que li membres soit confortez.	Et s'il est disloqué au loin, il ne convient pas de l'étendre vers l'avant, de le soulever sur la terre, mais qu'il soit plutôt comme s'il était au loin, comme nous l'avons dit pour le coucher sur les deux hanches ; et qu'il soit sur son visage, et que la jambe soit étendue comme nous l'avons dit ci-dessus, et qu'il appuie sur la jointure à la table; et il sera fait quand le patient étendra ses jambes, et elles seront longues; alors posez les cuisses, et mettez l'ampoule, et l'extraction d'un bandage, de sorte que la hanche ne bouge pas; et qu'il se repose trois jours ou quatre, puis le déboulonne, et met l'ampoule dessus; et si tu vois qu'elles sont longues, alors le pinceau, comme avant, et il le laisse trois jours; puis il le déboulonne, et fait-le cracher fort, jusqu'à ce que les membres soient confortés.
de la dislocation dou genoil	of the dislocation of the knee joint
Li genous est desaluez selonc III manieres: c’est a savoir, dedens et defuer, et derrier; et ne desalue point devant.	The genoux is dislocated according to three ways: that is to say, inside and outside, and behind; and does not dislocate in front.
Et li signes si est que tu comande au malaide qu’il plie sa jambe a sa cuixe, et s’ele ne s’aert a sa cuixe, saiches qu’il est desaluez; et li restauration de toutes si est que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et estende sa jambe s’il puet, et li met ton dos sus sa faice, et met son piet sus tes piez; puis pren son genoil a tes paumes, et retrai entre tes dois, puis plie les II costez dou genoil forment; et uns autres ministres estende son piet, tant que li genous reviegne a son leu, et li signes est qu’il aert bien sa jambe a sa cuixe legierement; et met l’emplastre sus, et fai aerdre la jambe a la cuixe, et les loie ensamble fort III jors ou IIII, puis le deslie; et ne se travaille mie li malaides d’aler, tant que li membres soit confortez.	And the signs are that you command the patient to bend his knee at the kneecap, and if he does not bend it at the kneecap, knowing that it is dislocated; and the restoration of all is that you make the patient sit upright, and extend his leg if he can, and put your back on his face, and place his foot on your feet; then take the genoux with your palms, and withdraw between the two, then bend the II costez of the genoux formed; and other ministers extend the foot, until the genoux returns to its place, and the signs are that he bends his leg well at the kneecap lightly; and put the plaster on, and make the leg move towards the kneecap, and join them firmly together for III days or IV, then release it; and do not work with the patient to walk, until the members are comfortable.
Et se li membres n’est a point, si aministre estendement fort, si com nos avons dit en la cure de la hainche, tant qu’il soit sanez	And if the limbs are not in place, then give a strong extension, as we have said in the treatment of the hip, until they are healthy.
de la dislocation dou talon	of the dislocation at the heel
Li talons est aucune fois esmeus, et aucune fois desaluez plenement, et dedens et defuer.	The heels are never dislocated and never fully displaced, both inside and out.
Et li signes si est que li cheville est enflee, et tent avant a la partie ou elle est desaluee: li ramenemens si est legier, et le doit on estendre legierement a ses mains quant il est esmeus soulement.	And the signs are that the ankle is dislocated, and the approach to the part where it is displaced is this: you should bring it lightly to your hands when it is only slightly dislocated.
Et quant il est desaluez dou tot, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide droit, et le tigne I ministres fors par la jambe, desus la cheville; puis trai le piet a toi a ta main destre, et puis a la senestre II fois, puis l’estent en haut, et boute bellement lou piet en haut; et fai ce II fois, si com nos avons dit, em boutant et en traiant lou piet; s’elle revient, c’est bien; se ce non, si rencomence l’ovraige, car il revient; et s’il ne puet revenir ensi, si fai gesir lou malaide sor son dos sus terre, et fiche I passeil fermement en terre entre ses cuixes, et lie drapelz entor, qu’il ne blece lou malaide; puis teigne li ministres la cuixe, et uns autres ministres estende lou piet a ses mains ou a I liien, k’il lie sus le col dou piet; puis estende chescuns ministres igalment, et li passelz soit adés entre les cuixes dou malaide por retenir le malaide quant on l’estent; puis mette li mires igal la dislocation a ses mains, et uns autres ministres teigne la jambe sainne au desoz, et li dislocation revenra hastanment.	And when it is dislocated from the top, you should make the patient lie down and extend his leg by the ankle; then bring the foot to your right hand, and then to your left twice, and then raise it up, and press it strongly upwards; and do this twice, as we have said, pushing and pulling the foot; if it returns, it is good; if not, begin again with the treatment, for it will return; and if it does not return in this way, make the patient lie on his back on the ground, and place a staff firmly between his knees, and tie blankets around it, so that he does not fall; then make the minister extend the healthy leg by the ankle, and others extend the foot to their hands or the bandage, that he may be held firm; then put the mirror equal to the dislocation in their hands, and others extend the healthy leg by the ankle, and the dislocation will certainly return.
Et quant elle iert a point, si met l’emplastre et estoupes sus, et l’estrain forment, et lie lou piet a la jambe, et warde les ners qui sont sus la cheville derrier, que li liiens ne soit trop estrois; puis le laisse II jors ou III, et se li liiens amolist, si l’estrain; puis le deslie au tier jor ou au quart, et deffent a aler lou malaide par IIII jors; et s’il va devant cel termine, ce n’est mie seurtez qu’il ne desalue encor.	Et when it is done, so put on the plaster and press down on it, and form the splint, and fasten the foot to the leg, and guard the tendons that are behind the ankle, lest the bonds be too tight; then leave it for two days or three, and let the bonds come loose if they do not hold fast, so take them off after three days or four, and let the patient go on his way. And if he goes before this term is up, there is no danger that he will dislocate again.
Et se apostemes chaus i vient, si covient que tu l’apaises, si com nos avons dit autre part, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if abscesses come to the foot, so that you calm them down, as we have said elsewhere, until they are well.
des dois	the two
Quant li doi sont desaluez, si les covient bellement estendre sens travail, et c’est legiere chose.	When the two are dislocated, so it is best to gently extend them without work, and this is a light thing.
Et se li dislocations est en aucun nout dou dos dou piet, si covient que tu faices seoir le malaide sus I leu plain ou sus .ie. table tot droit, et met ton piet sus ce qui apert de ces jointures, puis presse a ton piet forment, tant qu’il reviegne; et quant il est igalz, et il n’i apert nient, si met desoz la plante dou piet une table a II chiés, puis l’estrain forment, et le laisse III jors, puis le deslie; et le fai reposer, tant qu’il soit sanez.	And if the dislocations are in no way from the back of the foot, so it is necessary that you make the patient sit on a flat surface or a table, straight up, and put your foot on what opens up from these joints, then press down on your foot forming it, until it is right again; and when it is even, and there is no opening, so take off the splint from the back of the foot, then form the splint, and leave it for three days, then take it off; and let the patient rest, until he is well.
de plaie et de dislocation ensamble	of wound and dislocation together
Quant plaie vient avec la dislocation, et on la vuet restorer, maintes fois avient que li malaides muert: si ne soies mie presumptuous en la cure, se tu n’es saiges en l’art et tu ne l’as useit longement, et se tu n’es pitous et misericors et tardis, ne mie hardis; et use au comencement de choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et laisse le malaide en la main Deu, se tu n’i vois esperance de santeit; et quant tu i vois esperance, si ramoinne maintenant le membre au leu, ainsois que li apostemes chaus i viegne; et quant li membres est a leu, si aministre choses apaisans aposteme chaut, et cure la plaie, si com il covient, d’oignemens desiccatis; et se avec la dislocation a brisure, et os menus desevrez, si les oste, et fai ce que nos avons dit en maladies simples; et te garde d’entrer en voie de paour, selonc ce que j’ai dit, car ce te vaut mues selonc ton Creator, et por la saveteit de t’arme et de ton cors.	When a wound comes with dislocation, and you want to restore it, many times the patient dies: do not be presumptuous in the cure, lest you be unwise in this art, and have not used it long; and be not hasty, but use at the beginning calming things for an abscess, and leave the patient in God's hands, unless you see a chance of health; and when you see a chance, now put the member back into place, so that the abscesses come to light; and when the member is back into place, administer drying ointments, and if there is a fracture with small bones out of place, so mend them, and do as we have said for simple illnesses; and guard against entering a path of fear, according to what I have said, because this will harm you before your Creator, and for the sake of arming yourself and your body.
Amen	Amen
